赞扬 Janna Levin 的《图灵机

的狂人梦》

Praise for Janna Levin's

A MADMAN DREAMS OF Turing Machines

“闪闪发光的清晰散文。……对天才和疯狂的令人眼花缭乱的探究。”

“Sparklingly clear prose. … A dazzling investigation of genius and insanity.”

—寺庙新闻

—Temple News

“无可否认，这本书引人入胜……这是对数学和哲学领域两位杰出人物的详细而深刻的性格研究。”

“Undeniably compelling. … A detailed, intensely felt character study of two striking figures in the realms of mathematics and philosophy.”

—里士满时报快讯

—Richmond Times-Dispatch

“詹娜·莱文的引人入胜的叙述巧妙地跨越了虚构和非虚构的领域，让我们真切地体验到两位杰出智力者——哥德尔和图灵——痛苦的一生，同时了解他们各自如何以自己的方式在人类思想上留下了深刻的印记。”

“Janna Levin's compelling narrative artfully straddles the realms of fiction and nonfiction, allowing us to viscerally experience the tortured lives of two towering intellects— Gödel and Turing—while learning how each, in his own way, left a profound imprint on human thought.”

—布莱恩·格林， 《优雅的宇宙》作者

—Brain Greene, author of The Elegant Universe

“一部富有启发性的智力小说。”

“A brainy novel rich in revelation.”

—彭博新闻

—Bloomberg News

“充满诗意的语言……咒语般的散文和风格化的形而上学对话……清楚地表明，莱文的小说不仅仅是传记抄录的集合。”

“The poetically heightened language … the incantatory prose and the stylized metaphysical colloquy … make it clear that Levin's novel is no mere assemblage of biographical transcriptions.”

— 《纽约时报书评》

—The New York Times Book Review

“我喜欢图灵的机械化世界观与哥德尔更开放的‘不完备性’之间的对比。《狂人梦见图灵机》是一本想象力丰富的书。”

“I love the contrast of Turing's mechanized view of the world with Gödel's more open-ended ‘incompleteness.’ A Madman Dreams of Turing Machines is a wonderfully imagined book.”

—艾伦·莱特曼， 《爱因斯坦的梦想》作者

—Alan Lightman, author of Einstein's Dreams

“极度令人上瘾。……一个悖论：一部本质上真实的虚构作品。”

“Wildly addictive. … A paradox: a work of fiction that is essentially true.”

—页面

—Pages

“詹娜·莱文是一位天才的文体家，凭借这本引人入胜的书，她超越了写书的科学家的范畴，成为我们最有趣的当代作家之一。”

“Janna Levin is a gifted stylist, and with this compelling book she has transcended the category of scientists who write books to become simply one of our most interesting contemporary writers.”



——李·斯莫林， 《宇宙的生命》和《通向量子引力的三条道路》的作者

—Lee Smolin, author of

The Life of the Cosmos and Three Roads to Quantum Gravity

“莱文构建了一个引人入胜的故事……最令人印象深刻的是莱文以优雅和同情心创造了一个虚构的世界，这个世界容纳了这些人的数学原理，同时还绘制了一个虚构可以蓬勃发展的数学世界。”

“Levin constructs a fascinating tale… . What's most impressive here is the elegance and sympathy with which Levin creates the fictional universe that accommodates these men's mathematical principles, while at the same time mapping a mathematical universe in which fiction can thrive.”

— 《巴尔的摩太阳报》

Janna Levin

一个疯狂的人梦想着

图灵机

Janna Levin

A MADMAN DREAMS OF

Turing Machines

詹娜·莱文 (Janna Levin) 是哥伦比亚大学巴纳德学院的物理学和天文学教授。她住在纽约市。

Janna Levin is a professor of physics and astronomy at Barnard College of Columbia University. She lives in New York City.

www.jannalevin.com

www.jannalevin.com

JANNA LEVIN 的其他作品

ALSO BY JANNA LEVIN

宇宙是如何形成斑点的：

有限空间中有限时间的日记

How the Universe Got Its Spots:

Diary of a Finite Time in a Finite Space

献给我的父亲

To my father

没有开始。我曾试图编造一个开始，但那是一个谎言，我不想撒谎。这个故事的结局将回到开始的地方，也就是故事的中间。一个三角形或一个圆圈。一个由三个点组成的闭环。

There is no beginning. I’ve tried to invent one but it was a lie and I don’t want to be a liar. This story will end where it began, in the middle. A triangle or a circle. A closed loop with three points.

一个顶点是偏执狂，另一个顶点是孤独的弃儿：库尔特·哥德尔，几个世纪以来最伟大的逻辑学家；艾伦·图灵，才华横溢的密码破译者和数学家。他们的天才证明了我们自身的价值，是无足轻重的解药；他们身上的缺陷虽然不幸，但似乎是自然的补充，仿佛伟大只能与同等程度的弱点相得益彰。

At one apex is a paranoid lunatic, at another is a lonesome outcast: Kurt Gödel, the greatest logician of many centuries; and Alan Turing, the brilliant code breaker and mathematician. Their genius is a testament to our own worth, an antidote to insignificance; and their bounteous flaws are luckless but seemingly natural complements, as though greatness can be doled out only with an equal measure of weakness.

这两个人在历史中趋同，在信仰上却大相径庭。他们演绎着彼此之间毫无关联的人生和注定要发生的死亡，是颠倒的倒影。他们都是才华横溢的独创者，也是局外人。他们都忠于理性和真理。他们都痴迷于数学。但尽管他们如此热心，数学却无动于衷，他们的任何戏剧性事件——哥德尔的精神病妄想、图灵的性取向——都不会改变数学。一加一永远等于二。他们破碎的生活只是他们发现边缘的轶事。但他们的发现是我们目标的证据，他们的生活是自由意志的寓言。为了对抗冷漠，我想讲述他们的故事。

These two people converge in history and diverge in belief. They act out lives that are only tangentially related and deaths that are written for each other, inverted reflections. They are both brilliantly original and outsiders. They are both loyal to reason and to truth. They are both besotted with mathematics. But for all their devotion, mathematics is indifferent, unaltered by any of their dramas—Gödel's psychotic delusions, Turing's sexuality. One plus one will always be two. Their broken lives are mere anecdotes in the margins of their discoveries. But then their discoveries are evidence of our purpose, and their lives are parables on free will. Against indifference, I want to tell their stories.

难道我们的故事不重要吗？

Don’t our stories matter?

我本不该在这里，但有些事情你只能用最尴尬的方式才能得到。即使我试图隐瞒，撒谎，事实仍然是我在讲述这个故事。未经分类的传记事实目录没有故事，故事有缺陷和遗漏，有时甚至彻头彻尾的谎言，以创造意义，而这些意义永远不会从未拼凑的事实的碎片中浮现出来。因为有些真理永远无法通过遵守规则来证明。所以关于真相的整个故事都是谎言。骗子说，这是谎言。

I shouldn’t even be here but some things you can only get to in the most awkward ways. Even if I tried to hide it, to lie, the truth is it's still me telling this story. The unsorted catalogue of biographical facts provides nothing without stories with their dents and omissions and sometimes outright lies to create meaning that just won’t emerge from the debris of unassembled facts. Because some truths can never be proven by adhering to the rules. So this whole story about Truth is a Lie. The liar says, This is a lie.

我就是那个撒谎者，是三角形的第三点也是最后一点，是薄弱环节，是摇晃的铰链，是错位的顶点。我本应从上一点继续，然后交接给下一点。但我不知道从哪里开始。我站在城市的街道上。我要赶火车。四面八方的人潮涌动，还有一位老妇人在散步。我们当中有人会被记住吗？我们当中有人重要吗？

I am that liar, the third and final point on the triangle, the weak link, the wobbling hinge, the misaligned vertex. I am meant to carry on from the previous point and give over to the next. But I don’t know where to begin. I am standing on a street, in a city. I’m going to catch a train. There are people streaming in all directions and one old woman strolling. Will any of us be remembered? Do any of us matter?

这个关于真理和逻辑的故事导致了无神论和神秘主义。导致了绝望和自杀。导致了未来，导致了我们的过去。导致了现在。所以这是一个任意的起点，因为逻辑不会随着时间而展开。它永远存在于过去，决定着宇宙是如何开始的；永远存在于未来，决定着我们的命运已经被不可避免的逻辑规则所写成。我们可以强制执行时间顺序，因为时间的线性有助于我们；它给了我们剧本中的角色，一个开始和结束的地方。所以我从这里开始。在维也纳。那是 1931 年。这个地方和任何时候一样好，这一次和任何时候一样好。

This story about truth and logic leads to atheism and mysticism. To despair and suicide. To the future, our past. To the present. So here's a starting point as arbitrary as any because logic does not unfold in time. It exists forever into the past, dictating how the universe began; and forever into the future, our fate already written by the inescapable rules of logic. We can enforce chronology because the linearity of time helps; it gives us roles in the script, a place to start and to end. So here I start. In Vienna. It is the year 1931. This place is as good a place, this time as good a time, as any.

奥地利维也纳，1931 年

VIENNA, AUSTRIA. 1931

场景是一家咖啡馆。约瑟夫咖啡馆首先是一种气味，一种刺鼻的土耳其烤豆气味，太浓了，无法在空气中飘散，所以只能等待更强大的蒸汽从沸腾的碟子表面吹出，发酵成咖啡。顾客们只是从空气中吸出蒸汽，就变得过度兴奋。咖啡馆首先以这种美味、浑浊的气味出现在大脑中，其次唤醒了对镜子房间的记忆——这个记忆几乎和房间的实际景象一样充满活力，而房间的实际景象只出现在脑海中的第三个。咖啡是激发思想的燃料。是焦急希望的燃料，希望艺术、文字和逻辑的收获将是最丰收的，因为只有最丰收的季节才能让他们度过这个可怕的冬天和那场可怕的战争的围困。名字被创造出来，又被遗忘。著名的台词被写下来，也有不那么著名的台词。艺术家们用作品来偿还他们的债务，这些作品给一些墙壁增添了色彩，而其他墙壁则倒塌了迷人的老旧。外面，维也纳在一片片的斑驳中衰败又焕发活力，就像一个杂乱无章、无人照管的花园。从这里看，咖啡馆的窗户似乎保护着里面的人群免受风吹雨打和一天的乏味。在里面，他们笑着、抽烟、喊叫、争吵、盯着看、吹着口哨，牛奶般的咖啡变硬，沿着杯口流淌。

The scene is a coffeehouse. The Café Josephinum is a smell first, a stinging smell of roasted Turkish beans too heavy to waft on air and so waiting instead for the more powerful current of steam blown off the surface of boiling saucers fomenting to coffee. By merely snorting the vapors out of the air, patrons become overstimulated. The café appears in the brain as this delicious, muddy scent first, awaking a memory of the shifting room of mirrors second—the memory nearly as energetic as the actual sight of the room, which appears in the mind only third. The coffee is a fuel to power ideas. A fuel for the anxious hope that the harvest of art and words and logic will be the richest ever because only the most fecund season will see them through the siege of this terrible winter and the siege of that terrible war. Names are made and forgotten. Famous lines are penned, along with not so famous lines. Artists pay their debt with work that colors some walls while other walls fall into an appealing decrepitude. Outside, Vienna deteriorates and rejuvenates in swatches, a motley, poorly tended garden. From out here, the windows of the coffeehouse seem to protect the crowd inside from the elements and the tedium of any given day. Inside, they laugh and smoke and shout and argue and stare and whistle as the milky brew hardens to lace along the lip of their cups.

一群来自大学的科学家开始会面，将他们的想法与艺术家、小说家和幻想家的想法混合在一起，这些人从国家战败后的萧条中恢复过来，疯狂起来。少数人通过邀请才得以增加人数。慢慢地，他们的成员逐渐增加，概念从思想之汤中凝结并成形，直到这汤值得命名，因此他们在欧洲各地，甚至在美国被称为维也纳学派。

A group of scientists from the university begin to meet and throw their ideas into the mix with those of artists and novelists and visionaries who rebounded with mania from the depression that follows a nation's defeat. The few grow in number through invitation only. Slowly their members accumulate and concepts clump from the soup of ideas and take shape until the soup deserves a name, so they are called around Europe, and even as far as the United States, the Vienna Circle.

圆圈的中心是一个圆圈：干净、圆润、白色的大理石桌面。他们为这张桌子选择了约瑟夫咖啡馆。一支笔逆时针传递。第一个标记是直接在桌面上写一个方程式，在大理石上划出一道黑色墨水线，在飞溅的墨水中写出一个数学句子。他们都读着方程式，在杂乱的墨水滴中寻找其含义。数学是视觉的，不是听觉的。他们用声音争论，但用笔争论得更尖锐。他们用几乎可以洗掉的多汁黑色颜料，将符号逻辑的光线染在大理石上。

At the center of the Circle is a circle: a clean, round, white marble tabletop. They select the Café Josephinum precisely for this table. A pen is passed counterclockwise. The first mark is made, an equation applied directly to the tabletop, a slash of black ink across the marble, a mathematical sentence amid the splatters. They all read the equation, homing in on the meaning amid the disordered drops. Mathematics is visual not auditory. They argue with their voices but more pointedly with their pens. They stain the marble with rays of symbolic logic in juicy black pigment that very nearly washes away.

他们每周四晚上都会聚集在这里，提炼自己的观点——区分科学和迷信。事关一切。现实。意义。他们的生命。他们已经失去了任何宽容他们反对无效和虚伪的态度，反对神秘主义或形而上学。这样说太不客观了。他们憎恨神秘主义和形而上学、宗教和信仰。他们厌恶它们。他们想分离出真理。我想，他们感觉到近乎歇斯底里的感觉，就在那里，就在他们伸直双臂的手指末端。

They collect here every Thursday evening to distill their ideas—to distinguish science from superstition. At stake is Everything. Reality. Meaning. Their lives. They have lost any tolerance for ineffectual and embroidered attitudes, for mysticism or metaphysics. That is putting it too dispassionately. They hate mysticism and metaphysics, religion and faith. They loathe them. They want to separate out truth. They feel, I imagine, the near hysteria of sensing it just there, just beyond the nub of their fingers at the end of arms stretched to their limits.

我站在那里，环顾桌子四周。他们中的一些人比其他人更加引人注目。他们向前走去，宣布自己的身份。数学家奥尔加·哈恩-诺伊拉特在场。她和她的丈夫奥托·诺伊拉特（一位大牌社会主义者）在这个剧本中扮演着一个虽小但很有价值的角色。最重要的是，莫里茨·石里克在这里，构成了圈子的顶峰和源头。奥尔加因感染而失明，她抽着雪茄，而奥托喝着致命剂量的咖啡因，莫里茨用刷子刷着他的衣领。今天在场的其他人的参与并不那么重要。一个圈子可以用少数几个离散点来近似，其他的将不予计算。多年来，圈子里也许有更重要的成员，但这些人在我那粒状的黑白历史形象中闪闪发光。这是一幅粒状、破旧、分辨率低、单色的静止场景图片。如果我仔细观察这张照片，就能看出细节。外面，一阵冻结在时间里的风灼烧着偶然经过的行人的模糊面孔。男人们用戴着风吹日晒的手套的手把帽子固定在头上。里面有一面大镜子，里面是一块活生生的玻璃，里面是窗户上的影像。

I’m standing there, looking 360 degrees around the table. Some of them stand out brighter than the others. They press forward and announce themselves. The mathematician Olga Hahn-Neurath is here. She has a small but valuable part to play in this script as does her husband, Otto Neurath, the oversized socialist. Most important, Moritz Schlick is here to form the acme and source of the Circle. Olga, whose blindness descended with the conclusion of an infection, smokes her cigar while Otto drinks lethal doses of caffeine and Moritz settles himself with a brush of his lapels. The participation of the others present today is less imperative. A circle can be approximated by a handful of discrete points and the others will not be counted. There are perhaps more significant members of the Circle over the years, but these are the people who glow in color against my grainy black-and-white image of history. A grainy, worn, poorly resolved, monochromatic picture of a still scene. I can make out details if I look the shot over carefully. Outside, a wind frozen in time burns the blurred faces of incidental pedestrians. Men pin their hats to their heads with hands gloved by wind-worn skin. Inside a grand mirror traps the window's images, a chunk of animated glass.

在靠近墙壁的一张朴素的深色木椅上，几乎被隐藏起来库尔特·哥德尔 (Kurt Gödel) 站在铺满花饰的软垫摊位的扶手后面，仿佛身处沙尘暴之中，沉浸在那个充满希望的时代的活力与热情之中。

In a plain, dark wooden chair near the wall, almost hidden behind the floral arm of an upholstered booth, caught in the energy and enthusiasm of that hopeful time as though caught in a sandstorm, is Kurt Gödel.

1931 年，他是一个 25 岁的年轻人，他最敏锐的锋芒仍隐藏在青春的柔软肌肤之下。他刚刚发现了自己的定理。他带着骄傲和焦虑带来了这一发现。他那几乎、不完全是悖论的、扭曲的理性循环，将成为他永生的保证。是灵魂的永生，还是仅仅是他的名字的永生？这个问题将成为他疯狂的主题。我能断言超人的长寿只适用于他的名字吗？甚至连这一点都很难说。即使现在我们生活在他的发现的阴影之下，他的名字也几乎不为人所知。他的名字代表着一条定理；他是一个首字母，而不是一个人。只有他在这里，一个捍卫灵魂、捍卫真理的人，随时准备改变他的朋友们在这张大理石桌上形成的现实观。他加入圈子是为了告诉成员们他们错了，他可以证明这一点。

In 1931 he is a young man of twenty-five, his sharpest edges still hidden beneath the soft pulp of youth. He has just discovered his theorems. With pride and anxiety he brings with him this discovery. His almost, not-quite paradox, his twisted loop of reason, will be his assurance of immortality. An immortality of his soul or just his name? This question will be the subject of his madness. Can I assert that suprahuman longevity will apply only to his name? And barely even that. Even now that we live under the shadow of his discovery, his name is hardly known. His appellation denotes a theorem; he's an initial, not a man. Only here he is, a man in defense of his soul, in defense of truth, ready to alter the view of reality his friends have formulated on this marble table. He joins the Circle to tell the members that they are wrong, and he can prove it.

哥德尔沉默寡言，即使在人群中也孤身一人，背靠墙，像在电影院里一样在黑暗中向外张望。他沉默寡言，但并不令人讨厌。他光滑的头发梳在脑后，远离脸部，涂上发油，精心打理，这暗示着他除了数学之外最感兴趣的是女人。他的努力常常有成果，这只会给他周围的许多数学家增添神秘感。虽然人们都知道他炫耀过一两个女朋友，但他对自己的真爱却讳莫如深。他受伤的苹果，他甜美的阿黛尔。

Gödel is taciturn, alone even in a crowd, back against the wall, looking out as though in the dark at the cinema. He is reticent but not unlikable. The attention with which his smooth hair, brushed back over his head away from his face, is creamed and tended hints at his strongest interest next to mathematics, namely women. His efforts often come to fruition, only adding to his mystery for a great many of the mathematicians around him. And while he has been known to show off a girlfriend or two, he keeps his real love a secret. His bruised apple, his sweet Adele.

他的脸上也有一些甜美的东西，隐藏在厚边护目镜和倒置的双筒望远镜后面，所以那些被他吸引去讨论数学的人会感觉自己仿佛凝视着模糊的遥远地平线。全圆的黑色镜框和厚厚的鼻托突出了他的眼睛，或者用卡通眼球代替了它们——这是伟大隐喻视野的物理表现。他们给任何看的人留下这样的印象：所有的注意力都应该放在那些悲伤的窗户上，或者更重要的是，放在双筒望远镜焦点之外的广阔的知识世界里。

There is something sweet about his face too, hidden as it is behind thick-rimmed goggle glasses, inverted binoculars, so that those who are drawn into a discussion of mathematics with him feel as though they are peering into a blurry distant horizon. The completely round black frames with a thick nosepiece have the effect of accentuating his eyes or replacing them with cartoon orbs—a physical manifestation of great metaphorical vision. They leave the suggestion, with anyone looking in, that all emphasis should be placed there on those sad windows or, more important, on the vast intellectual world that lies just beyond the focus of the binocular lenses.

他只在别人问他问题时才会开口，而且只谈论数学。但他的回答直截了当、优美动人，能与他沟通的极少数人都觉得自己发现了无价之宝。他简洁的建议受到追捧和推崇。这是一个才华横溢、实力令人生畏的年轻人。这也是一个性格怪异、软弱得令人生畏的年轻人。也许他的弱点并不比我们其他人多，但他的所有弱点似乎都很极端——疑病症、偏执狂、精神分裂症。与他令人难以置信的精神力量相比，这些弱点更加明显。它们看起来像巨大的黑色空洞，是从一颗闪耀的恒星上切下来的碎片。

He speaks only when spoken to and then only about mathematics. But his responses are stark and beautiful and the very few able to connect with him feel they have discovered an invaluable treasure. His sparse counsel is sought after and esteemed. This is a youth of impressive talent and intimidating strength. This is also a youth of impressive strangeness and intimidating weakness. Maybe he has no more weaknesses than the rest of us harbor, but his all seem so extreme— hypochondria, paranoia, schizophrenia. They are even more pronounced when laid alongside his incredible mental strengths. They appear as huge black voids, chunks taken out of an intensely shining star.

他仍有潜力。有潜力成为伟人，也有潜力成为疯子。他将出色地实现这两点。

He is still all potential. The potential to be great, the potential to be mad. He will achieve both magnificently.

周四聚集在一起的每个人，轮流发言的人数约有三十人，都从内心深处相信数学是坚不可摧的。哥德尔今晚来打破他们的信念，直到他们只剩下令人信服的碎片，这些碎片组装起来后将为数学树立起一座强大的纪念碑，但不是坚不可摧的——至少不是完整的。哥德尔将证明，有些真理存在于逻辑之外，我们无法从这里到达那里。有些人——可能不信任数学的人——很快就声称他们一直都知道有些真理超越数学。但他们就是不知道。他们没有证明这一点。

Everyone gathered on this Thursday, the rotating numbers accounting for some three dozen, believe in their very hearts that mathematics is unassailable. Gödel has come tonight to shatter their belief until all that is left are convincing pieces that when assembled erect a powerful monument to mathematics, but not an unassailable one—or at least not a complete one. Gödel will prove that some truths live outside of logic and that we can’t get there from here. Some people—people who probably distrust mathematics—are quick to claim that they knew all along that some truths are beyond mathematics. But they just didn’t. They didn’t know it. They didn’t prove it.

哥德尔不相信真理会躲避我们。他证明了真理会躲避我们。他没有编造一个符合他对世界的偏见的神话——至少在数学方面没有。他发现他的定理就像他从地里挖出一块石头一样确定。他可以在桌子上传递它，它和那块石头一样真实。如果有人愿意，他们可以在他埋葬它的地方挖出来，同样能找到它。寻找它，你会在他所说的地方找到它，就在你凝视的地方的中心之外。夜空中有一些微弱的星星，你可以看到，但只有当你看它们发光的一侧时才能看到。它们太弱或太远，即使你盯着看也无法直接看到。但你可以用眼角余光看到它们，因为你视网膜边缘的细胞对光更敏感。也许真理就是这样。你可以看到它，但只能用眼角余光。

Gödel didn’t believe that truth would elude us. He proved that it would. He didn’t invent a myth to conform to his prejudice of the world—at least not when it came to mathematics. He discovered his theorem as surely as if it was a rock he had dug up from the ground. He could pass it around the table and it would be as real as that rock. If anyone cared to, they could dig it up where he buried it and find it just the same. Look for it and you’ll find it where he said it is, just off center from where you’re staring. There are faint stars in the night sky that you can see, but only if you look to the side of where they shine. They burn too weakly or are too far away to be seen directly, even if you stare. But you can see them out of the corner of your eye because the cells on the periphery of your retina are more sensitive to light. Maybe truth is just like that. You can see it, but only out of the corner of your eye.

英国多塞特郡，1928 年

DORSET, ENGLAND. 1928

场景是多塞特郡舍伯恩男子寄宿学校。一名 16 岁的男孩躺在韦斯科特之家日间教室地板下粗糙未完工的地基旁的沙砾和锯末中。地板下的男孩是艾伦·图灵。

The scene is Sherborne boarding school for boys in Dorset. A sixteen-year-old boy lies in the grit and sawdust against the rough unfinished foundation below the floorboards of the dayroom at Westcott House. The boy under the floor is Alan Turing.

他不是自愿待在这里的。自从那次突然的推搡和乱抓之后，已经过去了一段时间，四周一片漆黑。木板被插好。发出清脆的、不祥的叮当声。临时棺材的盖子沉重而合身。图灵被活埋了。这是一个显而易见的观察，但孩子们总是低估了他们武器的威胁。

He isn’t there by choice. It has already been a while since the sudden shoving and scrabbling and it went dark. The wooden boards slotted into place. The clean ominous clink. The weighty, fitted lid of a makeshift coffin. Turing buried alive. It's a transparent observation, but children always underestimate the menace of their weapons.

时间上有一个窗口，不长不短，几股精巧的气流吹散了笨拙地粘在地板底面上的灰尘，然后木板随着他的挣扎移动了一毫米。几条纠缠在一起的手臂向下推的力量减去一个男孩推的力量向上。图灵，他并不完全虚弱。他身材瘦削，肌肉发达。他用力推挤，直到绝望的吼叫声从他身上发出来，声音比他平时的声音要低沉。虽然这声音有点恐怖，让一些人感到焦虑，但没有一个男孩有权阻止其他人，所以，他们内心深处埋藏着一丝恐惧，他们合作把沉重的旧橡木桌子拖到位，两条腿放在松散的木板上，另外两条腿牢牢地固定在更坚固的板条上。

There is a window in time, no longer than it takes for a few wrought puffs of air to loosen dust clinging awkwardly to the underside of the floorboard, when the wood shifts a millimeter in response to his struggling. The force of several tangled arms pushing downward minus the force of one boy pushing upward. He isn’t entirely weak, Turing. He is wiry and strong, with a sinewy musculature. He strains and shoves until desperation bellows out of him in a deeper register than his voice can ordinarily reach. While the sound, a bit of a horror really, makes some of them anxious, no one of the boys has the authority to stop the others and so, with a small pit of dread planted deep in the lining at the tops of their stomachs, they collaborate to drag the heavy old oak table into place, two legs on the loose board, two well anchored on firmer slats.

也许这是一场成人礼。他乐观地​​抓住了这种可能性。他没有讽刺的意思。他的意思不是象征性地将一个男孩变成男人。他既不使用也不理解隐喻。他指的是字面意思。这种误解是有先例的。1925 年，在他到舍伯恩的第一周，有一个正式的仪式，最后年龄较大的男孩们粗暴地把他的胳膊和腿收起来，让他与地面分离，然后把他折叠起来，直到他舒适地塞进一个桶里。然后他被踢到走廊尽头。虽然打击是间接的，但羞辱却更直接。不知道还能做什么，他只好全心投入这件事。他蹦蹦跳跳地走着——总的来说，他很和蔼——眼睛盯着扣好的木带之间的一小块空隙。但他认为这很愚蠢。他认为这很可能真的很愚蠢。

Maybe this is an initiation ceremony. He grasps at the possibility optimistically. He means no irony. He does not mean a symbolic initiation of a boy into manhood. He neither uses nor understands metaphors. He means literally. There is a precedent for this miscomprehension. During his first week at Sherborne in 1925, there was an official ceremony that culminated in the older boys roughly collecting his arms and legs so that he was disconnected from the ground and folded up until he fit snugly into a barrel. He was then kicked down the hall. Although the blows were delivered indirectly, the humiliation was delivered rather more directly. Not knowing what else to do, he gave himself over to the incident. He bounced along—quite good-naturedly all in all—with eyes focused on a sliver of space between buckled wooden bands. But he thought it was stupid. He thought it was probably really stupid.

这也太蠢了。他知道这很蠢。他想尖叫，想咒骂他们，但骂声堵在喉咙里，像刺鱼一样粗鲁。木板残忍地把他的脸压向右边，压碎了他的脸颊、手臂和大腿，所以每次被阻止的动作都是一种痛苦。黑暗是另一场失败。

This is stupid too. He knows it is. He wants to shriek, to curse them, but the epithets catch in his throat, rough as sticklebacks. The boards brutally press his face to the right, mashing his cheek, his arms, and his thighs, so every arrested move is agony. The blackness an additional defeat.

他惊慌失措。他被自己的唾液呛到。他扭动着身子。他蜷缩着脚趾。他夹紧双腿。他尖叫起来——一声尖叫，音调越来越高，最后变成了无水的呜咽。挣扎让情况变得更糟。这是幽闭恐惧症。这是谵妄。痴呆。就在他干呕和呕吐的时候，他想屈服。但他无法放松、软化、屈服于这件事，被装在木桶里踢出走廊。虽然他知道他们很蠢，虽然他知道他们是骗子，但他也承认世界上有很多事情他不明白，有时，承认自己对世界的无知总比承认自己对世界的无知要好。在这种情况下，最好接受被困在韦斯科特之家休息室松散的木板下面的事实。但他做不到。

He panics. He chokes on his own saliva. He twists. He knots his toes. He clamps his legs. He shrieks—a squeal that reaches up high in pitch as it mounts into a waterless sob. Struggling is making it worse. This is claustrophobia. This is delirium. Dementia. Even as he gags and spits vomit, he wants to yield. But he can’t relax, soften, surrender to the incident, be kicked down the hall in a wooden barrel. While he knows they are stupid, while he knows they are phonies, he also admits there are many things in the world he does not understand and, on occasion, it is better to confess this lack of knowledge of the world. On these occasions it is better to accept being trapped beneath the loose boards of Westcott House dayroom. But he can’t.

他的膝盖磨得生疼，脚趾扭伤。他的背僵硬，他像鬣狗一样大笑着向后退去——这对图灵来说并不完全是不寻常的——这么奇怪的讲话配得上一声笑声——但却是夸张的、尖锐而锯齿状的笑声。艾伦的整个声音器官都无法控制。这是一种听觉畸形，其根源无疑是这位高功能自闭症患者大脑中的极端化学反应。他的声音轰隆隆、时断时续。他调整了音调，但从不调整节奏或声调。他缺乏语调语言。缺乏使声音可以忍受并产生意义的节奏。他的讲话就像小孩用勺子敲击硬表面发出的刺耳声音。

His knees grind. His toes kink. His back seizes and he recoils with a hyena's laugh—not altogether uncharacteristic for Turing—such strange speech deserves a complementary laugh—but exaggerated, a high and serrated scream of a laugh. Alan's entire vocal instrumentation is unmanageable. It is a kind of aural deformity whose source is no doubt the extreme brain chemistry of the highly functioning autistic. His voice booms and bangs and halts and stalls. He modulates the pitch but never the rhythm or the tone. The language of intonation is missing. The cadence that makes a voice bearable and creates meaning is missing. His speech is the grating clatter of a child's spoon on a hard surface.

他过于热情的音量和奇怪的口才有时会让人觉得很开心。这种缺陷，加上他退缩的倾向，让学校的老师们对他是否快乐感到矛盾。当他们与图灵夫人通信时，他们试图组织对她儿子的观察得出了一个令人心酸的结论，但却搞砸了。他们无法抑制自己的沮丧，最终脱口而出：“不可否认，他不是一个普通的男孩。”她知道的就这么多。

His overzealous volume and peculiar elocution sometimes come off as cheerful. This malfunction, along with the tendency to withdraw, leaves the masters of the school conflicted as to whether or not he is happy. When they correspond with Mrs. Turing, they try to structure their observations of her son into a poignant conclusion but bungle the job. Unable to temper their frustration they ultimately blurt, “Undeniably, he is not a normal boy.” This much she knew.

地板上方，房间变成了一个空洞，将他尖锐的笑声困在里面，直到它不祥地消失。男孩们试图通过忽略刺耳的咯咯颤音来炫耀他们的冷酷无情。当他们继续玩一场异常安静的游戏时，恐惧的深渊被推挤并深深地落入肥沃的胃肠道土壤中，在那里它开始了生命周期。它会像溃疡一样溃烂，还是会变成腐烂的异常细胞？这取决于每个人选择如何照料这个杂乱的花园。

Above the floorboards, the room becomes a cavity trapping his shrieking laughter until it dies off ominously. The boys try to show off their callousness by ignoring the cackling vibrato slicing their ears. While they continue to play an anomalously quiet game, the pit of dread is jostled and falls deep into the fertile gastrointestinal soil where it begins its life cycle. Will it fester as an ulcer, or blossom into rancid abnormal cells? That depends on how each chooses to tend that messy garden.

图灵无法看透黑暗。黑暗笼罩着他睁开的眼睛，还有大块的盐粒，让他的眼睛灼痛、流泪，但严格来说，这并不算是哭泣。那是在他后来的磨难结束后的事。或者至少是他一生磨难中的一次小冲突——孤独、迫害和沮丧的生活，夹杂着孩子般的快乐。但总的来说，这不会是糟糕的生活，它将充满成就和意义，甚至连他自己都从未意识到。

Turing can’t see through the darkness. The blackness coats his open eyes, as do large salty dust grains so that his eyes burn and water but technically it doesn’t amount to crying. That comes later, when his ordeal is over. Or at least this one skirmish in his lifelong ordeal—a life of loneliness, persecution, and depression, lightly salted with childish bouts of happiness. But it won’t be a bad life all told and it will come to be laden with achievement and significance so great that even he never recognizes it.

这不是入会仪式。这是惩罚。对看透他们、看透他们内心的惩罚。

This isn’t an initiation ceremony. It is punishment. Punishment for looking right through them, for looking right inside them.

世界上有发光的闪电。坚硬、明亮的糖果像珠宝一样噼啪作响，在灰色的风景中散开尖锐的金色光线。有时艾伦可以不借助工具就看到这些光辉。他在树林里找到它们，或者在天空中看到它们。有时他必须用笨拙的化学实验从普通岩石中提取它们，而他自己做得很差他虽然在房间里，但他像炼金术士一样全神贯注地寻找，直到找到金子、碘或其他元素周期表中应有的元素。有时，他会用自己的头脑发现它们，就像他设法用无限的更简单的代数形式表达的反三角函数一样。这些是他大脑不懈、系统性探索的精华，是耀眼的宝石。化学物质的气味和煽动性的威胁并没有阻止他，但其他人却对混乱感到恼火并抱怨。他的纯数学发现具有隐私的优势——真理的碎片突破了混乱的表皮，被只有他才能看到的深红色包围着。

There are bolts of luminescence in the world. Hard, brilliant candies that crackle like jewels, fanning pointed rays of gold through an otherwise gray landscape. Sometimes Alan can see these splendors unaided. He finds them in the woods or sees them in the sky. Sometimes he has to distill them from ordinary rock with clumsy chemical experiments he executes poorly in his room but pursues with the devotion of an alchemist until they yield gold, or just iodine, or some other element with a rightful place in the periodic table. Sometimes he discovers them with his mind like the inverse trigonometric function that he managed to express as an infinite series of simpler algebraic forms. These are the best, these dazzling gems of his brain's relentless, systematic expeditions. The smells of his chemicals and their incendiary threat don’t deter him, but others are irritated by the mess and complain. His pure mathematical discoveries have the advantage of privacy—splinters of truth broken through the skin of confusion, framed by pools of crimson that only he can see.

对艾伦来说，这就是世界：闪闪发光的巨石，一串珍贵的宝石。他从一个世界跳到另一个世界，勉强能在虚假和骗子的浑浊海洋上保持平衡。他们的世界充满了面部表情和虚假的步伐，社会规范。他们间接、乏味的不诚实、竞争和虚伪的世界。

To Alan, this is the world: luminous boulders, a string of precious stones. He jumps from one to the next just barely able to balance above the murky sea of fakes and phonies. Their world of facial signals and false strides, social norms. Their indirect, dull universe of dishonesty and contests and artifice.

其他男孩正在学习的那些错综复杂、妙趣横生的对话让他困惑不已，迷失了方向——这些机制以中产阶级的繁荣来逃避坦诚。在人类行为的碎片漩涡中，他摸索着寻找真理；如果他找到了真理，他就会忠实地盯着真理的闪光，而这种忠诚会冒犯其他人。他们恼怒、怨恨，把石头踢到他脸上，不知道他为什么盯着看。

He is baffled and lost in the tangled, witty exchanges the other boys are learning—mechanisms that evade candor with the flourish of the middle class. Through the swirl of debris of human behavior, he gropes for truth; and if he finds it, he stares at truth's sparkle with a fidelity that offends the others. Annoyed, resentful, they kick the rocks up in his face, not knowing why he stares.

多塞特，1928 年

DORSET, 1928

他的房间从来没打扫过，这让他的母亲很沮丧。她试图向他展示，示范：“听着，艾伦。把你的衬衫整理得井井有条。”她还给了他指示。“仔细清洁墙壁和地板的接缝处，否则疏忽大意会积满毛茸茸的灰尘。”她拍打着他的夹克，寻找脏兮兮的手帕，就像母亲在孩子的口袋里寻找违禁品一样绝望。脏衣服总是那么多，甚至当她伸手去拿埋得最深、因此也是最古老的衣服时，她都恶心得打嗝。她舔了舔手掌，试图梳理他的头发，擦去他黝黑的肤色。艾伦是她的事业，她以耐心和偶尔动摇的信心忍受着挫折。

His room has never been clean, much to his mother's frustration. She tries to show him, to demonstrate: “Look, Alan. Arrange your shirts in an orderly fashion.” And there are instructions too. “Clean carefully at the join of the wall and the floor or neglect will yield a rich harvest of furry dust.” She pats his jackets down in search of filthy handkerchiefs with the desperation of a mother searching her child's pockets for contraband. There are always so many dirty cloths that even she belches with disgust as she reaches in for those buried deepest, hence oldest. With a lick of her palm, she tries to train his hair and wipe down his dark complexion. Alan is her cause and she endures her frustration with patience and a confidence that falters only occasionally.

要么他不懂如何打扫，要么他不在乎，或者，最令人高兴的解释是，他太专注于深刻而复杂的干扰，太专注于数学是深奥的真理，完全不受人类污点的影响，即使他笨拙的方法也无法玷污它的光彩。也许他只是不明白干净意味着什么，无论是个人卫生还是社会成功。所以休息室地板上的灰尘味道对他来说很熟悉，只是他更专注而已。

Either he doesn’t understand how to clean or he doesn’t care or, most flattering of all interpretations, he is too preoccupied with deep and complex distractions, the sanctity and purity of mathematics, the profound truth so completely immune to human stains that even his clumsy approach can’t tarnish its luster. Probably he just does not understand what it means to be clean, both for personal hygiene and for social success. And so the dusty taste of the dayroom floor is familiar to him, if more intense in concentration.

图灵今年夏天满 16 岁，最近发现了荷尔蒙。荷尔蒙对他的高音毫无作用，使它充满了成人的力量，但他无法将其调到较低的音域。因此，他那奇怪、犹豫、不太结巴的声音不但没有减弱，反而增强了力量。青春期生物化学反应的开始使他对腋窝黑暗角落里长出的硬毛更加敏感。仿佛是为了让他感到尴尬，并让他一眼就能看到隐藏在他最私密部位的东西，这些毛发稀疏地爬上他油腻的下巴——脸上就有一些肮脏和性感的东西。但他不知道该如何打理和整理这新生的男子气概，就像他不知道该如何梳理头顶上顽固地向前垂下的头发，一缕深黑色的刘海，也不知道该如何将他那件永远歪斜的外套上的纽扣与扣眼对齐一样。外套遮住了他半露在外面的衬衫和松垮的领带，领带上系着一个男孩子气的绳子，领子上沾满了墨水。他一团糟。一团糟。

Turing reached sixteen this summer and recently discovered hormones. The hormones do nothing for his high voice, filling it with adult strength but he's unable to retune it to a lower register. So his odd, hesitant, not-quite-stammer gains power instead of abating. The onset of his adolescent biochemistry heightens his sensitivity to the bristle of stiff hairs that climb in dark corners of his armpits. As if to embarrass him and reveal at a glance what lurks in his most private of areas, the hairs sparsely grass his greasy jaw—something dirty and sexual right there on his face. But he no more knows how to groom and organize this new manly growth than he knows how to groom the hair atop his head that stubbornly flops forward, a deep black fringe, or than he knows how to align the buttons with the buttonholes on his perpetually askew coat that covers his partially untucked shirt and loose off-kilter tie, a man-child's poorly tied noose around an ink-stained collar. He is a mess. A dirty mess.

肮脏萦绕在他身边，就像一股略带刺鼻的气味钻进人们的鼻子，直到“肮脏”这个词出现在他们的脑海中——同时也出现在他自己的脑海中——提醒着他其他人已忙于忘记的青春期性行为。

Dirtiness hangs about him like a slightly sharp smell rising up people's noses until the word “dirty” rises in their minds—as it simultaneously rises in his own—a reminder of the adolescent sexuality that the others are already busy forgetting.

舍伯恩男子学校的性紧张程度是可以控制的。淫秽的评论和激烈的摔跤是只要调节好那种紧张感，他们的工作就足够了——不是完美，但还行，就是还行。男孩们都挺过来了。他们中的大多数人都渴望女孩，渴望柔软的身体，他们有着前所未有的最基本的迫切感，这种欲望一生都不会平息。他们永远无法满足那种青春期的欲望，因为他们再也无法唤起同样的绝望。但他们还是做到了，即使他们很紧张。还有图灵。他永远不知道怎么站，怎么说话，看哪里，说什么。他的暗示，他淫荡的目光。该死的图灵。就像一个俯身低语，当你俯身时，他却舔你的耳朵。那就是图灵，永远想舔你的耳朵。

The sexual tension of Sherborne School for boys is manageable. Smutty comments and explosive wrestling are valves to regulate that tension and they work well enough—not perfectly, but fine, just fine. The boys get through. Most of them yearn for girls, long for soft downy bodies with the basest form of urgency they are ever to experience, and the desire will never be quenched in their lifetimes. They can never satiate that adolescent lust since they can never again conjure up quite the same desperation. But they manage, even if they are tightly wound. Then there's Turing. He never understands how to stand, how to talk, where to look, what to say. His innuendos, his leering stares. Bloody Turing. Like someone who leans over to whisper and when you lean in, licks your ear instead. That's Turing, forever trying to lick your ear.

他把今天的困境归咎于西兰花。餐厅里盘子里的西兰花让他非常焦躁。它味道辛辣，质地像小灌木丛一样不规则。他喜欢口感顺滑的食物。块状或随机的质地会让他焦虑不安。而且，酸酸的黄绿色与豌豆汤的颜色非常相似。汤还可以，因为它像茶一样顺滑稀薄——这个国家的烹饪习惯受到了第一次世界大战期间严格配给制的启发。这很适合他。他喜欢淡而无味的食物。味道均匀，种类有限。颜色混淆是一种特别恶劣的伎俩。如果食物要具有相同的颜色，那么它们的味道就必须相同。但是西兰花的味道一点也不像汤，尽管它们都很淡。西兰花软而糊状，但形状很好。这个想法就令人作呕。

He blames the broccoli for today's predicament. The broccoli on his plate put him in a state of great agitation in the dining hall. It was pungent and fractal with the texture of a small bush. He likes his food smooth. Lumpiness or random texture plunge him into anxiety. Plus the sour yellow green was very similar to the color of the pea soup. The soup was okay because it was smooth and thin as tea—the country's culinary habits have been inspired by the stringent rationing imposed during the Great War. This suits him. He likes his food diluted and weak. Uniform in flavor and limited in variety. Color confusion is an especially foul trick. If foods are to have the same color, they must taste the same. But the broccoli tasted nothing like the soup, though they were both bland. The broccoli was soft and mushy but shapely. The very thought revolting.

他真正想要的是苹果。稀薄的茶豌豆汤，然后是苹果。苹果不光滑，但它是红色的，一点也不像酸酸的黄绿色，这是它的优势。苹果也是圆的。有些苹果圆得像球体，可爱又有几何感，对称性被茎刺穿，使果实朝向北方。他喜欢苹果。

What he really wanted was an apple. The thin tea-pea soup followed by an apple. An apple is not smooth, but it is red, nowhere near sour yellow green, and it has this in its favor. An apple is also round. Some apples are as round as globes, lovely and geometric, the symmetry pierced by the stem, orienting the fruit to the north. He loves apples.

他想不出一个好办法来处理西兰花。它被他放在盘子里，冷得像老鱼一样，没人要。把煮熟的蔬菜扔掉可不是件容易的事。老师们不容忍浪费，级长们肯定会注意到的。所以当他坐下来吃饭时，他已经处于非常不利的地位。

He could not invent a happy resolution to the broccoli. It sat unwanted on his plate, cold as old fish. Discarding the boiled veg uneaten wasn’t easy. The masters were intolerant of wastefulness and the prefects would surely notice. So he was already at a great disadvantage when he sat down to dinner.

他从来不知道要把盘子放在哪儿。他喜欢早到或晚到。如果他早到，他就可以私下整理盘子里的食物。对颜色和稠度进行分类，并隐藏任何真正有问题的食物，以便稍后处理。如果有人和他一起，他会选择这样做，他可能是一个不错的晚餐伙伴。不是每个人都讨厌他。没有人讨厌他。有些男孩就是受不了他，这完全是两码事。他们常常私下后悔袭击老图灵，但下次仍然难以抗拒这种冲动。如果他迟到了，提供的食物就会少一些，他的盘子会自动精简。由于不需要分类，他可以一个人快速吃饭。

He never knew where to accompany his tray. He preferred to arrive early or late. If he was early then he could likely arrange the food on his plate in private. Sorting the hues and consistencies and hiding any real offenders to be disposed of later. If anyone joined him he would do so by choice and he would probably be an all right dinner companion. Not everyone hates him. Nobody hates him. Some of the boys just can’t bear him, which is not at all the same thing. They often privately regret their assaults on old Turing but still find the urge hard to resist the next time around. If he arrived late, there would be less food on offer, his plate automatically streamlined. With less sorting required, he could eat quickly and alone.

今天可供选择的座位不多，而且没有一个是孤立的。这就像一场轮盘赌。该选哪个座位？有时所有的男孩看起来都一样，每个人都带着定量的肉粉色脸。只有当他惊慌失措时才会发生这种情况——他无法将脸与名字和角色联系起来。于是他像扔一先令一样把自己扔进一个空座位，听天由命。

Today there were few seats to choose from and none of those were isolated. It was a game of roulette. Which seat to choose? Sometimes all the boys looked the same, each wearing a rationed fleshy-pink face. This happened only when he panicked—he couldn’t put face to name to character. And so he tossed himself into an empty seat as though tossing a shilling, leaving it to chance.

一开始还不算太糟。他专心致志地看着托盘，继续处理西兰花，桌上一片嘈杂。危机。在艾伦独特的内心世界里，他想象自己是隐形的，完全不会被注意到。但对餐桌旁的男孩们来说，不把注意力集中在他身上是不可能的。他焦躁地看着蔬菜，动作生硬，而他自己的头皮屑也弄脏了汤。他们一个接一个地停止了说话，停止了微笑。整整一分钟，小桌子旁的几个男孩放下他们的工具，看着艾伦毫无知觉地为即将发生的事故做准备。后来，他们中没有人能记得他们中的哪一个人先用克里斯的名字刺伤了艾伦。但就这样，冲突开始了，艾伦被迫放弃解决食物组的问题，寻找他们的眼睛。

It wasn’t too bad at first. The table was noisy with chatter as he concentrated on his tray and continued to deal with the broccoli crisis. In Alan's unique inner world, he imagined himself to be invisible, entirely unnoticeable. But to the boys at the table, it was impossible not to focus on him. He fretted over his vegetables with jerky movements while his own dandruff salted his soup. One by one they stopped talking and stopped smiling. For a full minute the few boys at the small table put down their implements and watched Alan's oblivious preparations for the accident about to happen. Later, none of them would be able to remember which one of them first stabbed Alan with Chris's name. But just like that, the collision began as Alan was forced to abandon the solution to the food groups and search for their eyes.

这并不是说图灵不知道该看哪里。他不知道该怎么看。他目瞪口呆。他盯着看。他的眼睛睁大了，似乎从同学身上吸取了一些精华。感觉好像他能看穿他们。感觉好像他能看进他们里面。他们对他蓝眼睛的凝视比对他的无知更反感，他们用这个名字嘲笑他。这是一句单调的指控、抱怨和嘲讽：克里斯托弗·莫尔科姆。

It's not exactly that Turing didn’t know where to look. He didn’t know how to look. He gawped. He stared. His eyes dilated and seemed to draw some essence out of his classmates. It felt as though he could look right through them. It felt as though he could look right into them. Even more offended by his blue-eyed gaze than they were by his obliviousness, they mocked him with the name. It was a sing-song accusation, a whine and a taunt: Christopher Morcom.

克里斯是艾伦第一个、最伟大、最纯洁、完全单恋的对象。他在学校比艾伦高一个年级，来自另一个学院。虽然他比艾伦大一岁，但他身材瘦小，五官清秀，艾伦喜欢偷偷地研究他的五官，祈祷克里斯不会注意到。这种苗条的美貌至少部分可以归咎于慢性病引起的虚弱，而慢性病又是由一杯厚厚的白色浓牛奶引起的，一杯令人满意的半品脱牛奶上面有一层可爱的热泡沫，如果不是被牛结核病污染的话，这杯牛奶似乎很普通。没有什么倒牛奶那天，他感到很特别。他手握的玻璃杯没有什么特别之处，只是手掌上凝结的一层水汽让他感到有点不舒服的寒意。这种寒意远不足以让他远离有毒的饮料，它顺着他的喉咙滑下去，无意间覆盖了他的上唇，却不那么无意地覆盖了他的肠子。咳嗽迅速发展，给他年轻的声音增添了音色，并让他产生粗糙的痰液。从那时起，细菌就一直拖延，只是因为懒惰而维持着宿主。克里斯对自己的病情保密，让艾伦猜测他身材矮小、外表娇弱的原因。

Chris is Alan's first, greatest, purest, entirely unrequited love. He is a class ahead of Alan in school and from another house. Although a year older he is slight of frame, with thin, delicate features that Alan loves to study furtively, praying Chris won’t notice. This slender prettiness can be blamed, at least in part, on a frailty induced by chronic illness, induced in turn by a heavy white glass of thick cow's milk, a satisfying half-pint of milk crowned by a lovely warm froth, seemingly ordinary were it not for the contamination of bovine tuberculosis. There was nothing special about the day the milk was poured. There was nothing special about the glass his hands encircled, except a mildly unpleasant chill from a layer of condensation that struck his palms. The chill nowhere near shocking enough to ward him off the poisoned drink, and down his throat it slid, coating his upper lip innocently and his bowels rather less innocently. The cough developed quickly, adding timbre to his young voice and plaguing him with a coarse production of phlegm. Since then, the bacteria have procrastinated, sustaining the host out of simple laziness. Chris keeps his illness secret, leaving Alan to speculate as to the cause of his small frame and delicate appearance.

克里斯是艾伦摆脱孤独的唯一出口。他是一个金发碧眼的帅哥，拥有图灵所没有的一切。他成功来之不易，天生迷人，举止优雅，可爱迷人。艾伦可能会嫉妒克里斯的科学天赋、熟练的物理化学实验、天文学知识、高级望远镜，以及家人培养的科学素养和艺术造诣。但他选择了另一条路——他爱他。他从未直接表白过，尽管克里斯一定知道这个奇怪的同学爱他。但克里斯很容易被爱，他也一定知道这一点。

Chris offers Alan the only respite from his loneliness. A pretty blond boy, he is everything Turing is not. An easy success, naturally winning, polished, and lovely. Alan could be jealous of his scientific aptitude, his adept physical chemistry experiments, his knowledge of astronomy, his superior telescope, and his family's cultivation of scientific literacy as well as a sophistication in the arts. But instead he takes the only other route available—he loves him. He never confesses his love outright, although Chris must know that this odd classmate loves him. But then Chris is easy to love and he must know that too.

艾伦正在推着一棵棵纤维状的西兰花，不确定他的晚餐同伴是谁，无法分辨他们的脸，不知道谁是他的盟友，谁是他的敌人。当嘲讽落下时，他没有抗议，没有为自己辩护，也没有反感这种暗示。他咧嘴一笑。对这种肮脏的暗示，他露出了宽容的笑容。该死的图灵。

There was Alan, pushing at the fibrous trees of broccoli, unsure as to the identity of his dinner companions, unable to resolve their faces, not knowing who was with him or who was against him. When the taunt landed, he didn’t protest, didn’t defend himself, didn’t resent the implication. He grinned. A grin of indulgence at the dirty allusion. Bloody Turing.

尽管盘子破碎让他很震惊，但看到西兰花被吃掉他还是松了一口气。

Although the shattering of his plate shocked him, he was relieved to see the broccoli go.

在地板下，他有时间在晚餐时反思自己的失态行为。时间一分一秒地过去，他鼻子和嘴巴的蒸汽中积聚了粉尘。虽然他能辨认出事件发生的顺序——煮熟的蔬菜、椅子、名字、笑容、破碎的盘子——但他仍然不太确定到底出了什么问题。

Under the floorboards, he is given time to consider his gaffe over dinner. As the minutes pass, powdery dust clumps in the steam of his nose and mouth. Although he can identify the sequence of events—the boiled veg, the chair, the name, the grin, the broken plate—he's still not quite sure what went wrong.

舍监奥汉隆先生看到四个男孩一起挤进图灵的房间——或者可能有三个。他们四肢的疯狂动作有时让人觉得某个地方的男孩数量是图灵的两倍，而且他们蓝色制服的款式相似，让人很难准确统计出人数。

The housemaster, Mr. O’Hanlon, saw the four boys push together into Turing's room—or maybe there were three. The frenzied energy of their limbs sometimes made it seem as if there were double the number of boys in a given spot, and the similarity of the fit of their blue uniforms made it hard to get a clear count.

他也正要去图灵的房间，因为他在韦斯科特屋外的象限里看到了图灵空荡荡的窗台上方闪烁着光芒。“图灵又在熬制巫婆的药水了，”他心想，把肩膀伸向楼梯门，决心要拆开图灵的另一个简陋的炼金实验室。

He was also on his way to Turing's room, having spotted a flicker above his barren windowsill from the quadrant outside Westcott House. “Turing's boiling up another witch's brew,” he thought to himself and aimed his shoulders at the stairwell door, determined to disassemble yet another of Turing's crude alchemical laboratories.

上个月，一支蜡烛的火焰尖端被标准窗帘所遮住，这支蜡烛原本是用来加热勺子里的结晶体的，这是一个至关重要的实验程序。从那以后，艾伦家的窗台和窗框都没有装饰。图灵欣赏着蜡烛油蒸发、燃烧并凝结成烟时，蓝色、红色和黄色的瞬间丝带蜿蜒穿过最热的火焰中心。当窗帘卷成一团泥泞的水平黄色火焰时，这是一个辉煌的高潮，他忍不住停下来观看了一会儿，然后紧张地用自己夹克的领口和肩膀扑灭了火。从那以后，窗户就没再装饰过。

Alan's windowsill is undecorated, as is the window frame, after last month when the standard-issue curtains caught the pointy tip of flame from a candle intended to heat the crystallized contents of a spoon, a crucial experimental procedure. Turing admired the transient ribbons of blue, red, and yellow winding through the hottest core of flame as the candle grease vaporized and burned and curdled to smoke. When the curtains curled into a muddy horizontal yellow conflagration it was a glorious crescendo and he couldn’t help but stop and watch for a bit before he nervously snuffed out the fire with the neck and shoulders of his own jacket. Ever since, the window has been left undressed.

今天早上，奥汉隆先生不得不安抚图灵的另一位老师。班主任罗斯先生把那些令人反感的纸扇到舍监面前，拿出了图灵行为不当的明确证据。“宗教课上教代数。他在宗教课上教代数！”所有教职员工都不知道该怎么对待这个奇怪的孩子，如何改掉他的坏习惯，如何调整他高亢的嗓音，如何让他符合学校的规定和要求。几位老师的挫败感被某种程度的喜爱所抵消，他们慢慢地接受了其他人的讽刺和批评。正是这种谦逊的幽默和不加掩饰的微笑，以及他能展现的科学数据中偶尔出现的有趣事实，为他赢得了这种偶尔的善意。但今天，班主任有些疲惫，感到道德上的束缚，于是恳求道：“我无法原谅他对《新约》的理智讨论的愚蠢态度。”舍监不能完全不同意。于是，决定让图灵继续留在他的课程中。

This morning Mr. O’Hanlon had to soothe the sensibilities of another of Turing's instructors. Fanning the offending papers in the housemaster's face, Mr. Ross, the form-master, thrust forth the unambiguous evidence of Turing's misbehavior. “Algebra during religious instruction. He does algebra during religious instruction!” None of the staff quite know what to do with the peculiar child, how to reform his filthy habits, rescale the high pitch of his voice, align him with the codes and expectations of the school. Their frustration blunted by a measure of fondness, a few instructors ease his way through the jabs and criticisms of the others. It is the self-effacing humor and ungauged smile that earn him this occasional kindness, as well as the periodically intriguing facts that stick out from the litany of scientific data that he can unfurl. But today, somewhat exhausted and feeling morally bound, his form-master implored, “I cannot forgive the stupidity of his attitude towards sane discussion on the New Testament.” The housemaster couldn’t entirely disagree. And with that the decision to keep Turing back in his courses was made.

奥汉隆对自己对这个无可救药的不合群的人的一点点好感感到恼火，他从大厅的尽头悄悄地看着四个男孩，但可能只有三个，为他拆开了化学装置。他听到了迹象：最初的沉闷的砰砰声，玻璃的碎裂声，然后是围绕着对峙而积累的紧张的沉默。他听到了他们抓住艾伦所花的力气，他们紧紧抓住他挣扎的胳膊和腿，熟练地把他带进了休息室，他面无表情地站着。

O’Hanlon, annoyed at his own twinge of affection for this hopeless misfit, watches unnoticed from the end of the hall as four boys, but maybe it is only three, disassemble the chemistry set for him. He hears the signs: the initial dull thud, the crush of glass, and then the tense quiet that accumulates around a confrontation. He hears the effort it takes for them to grab Alan, and stands impassively as they clench his struggling arms and legs and deftly usher him into the dayroom.

“也许他们可以向他展示一些我们不能看到的东西，”他想，又停顿了一会儿，听着桌子落在松散的地板上，共振被图灵身体的隔热材料减弱，然后奥汉隆沿着他进来的路离开了大厅。

“Maybe they can show him something we cannot,” he thinks, and pauses another moment to hear the table land on the loose floorboards, the resonance dampened by the insulation of Turing's body before O’Hanlon leaves the hall the way he entered.

确实，图灵在宗教教育期间学习过代数，但他们低估了他的信仰力量。他思考的是上帝，以及灵魂，虽然这听起来有些陈词滥调。1 + 1 = 2 中的上帝在哪里？

It's true Turing was doing algebra during religious instruction, but they underestimate the strength of his faith. He was thinking about God and, clichéd as it sounds, about the soul. Where is God in 1 + 1 = 2?

上帝在哪里？

Where is God?

如果他将玻璃杯悬在火焰上方，那么直到一种化学物质与另一种化学物质相互作用，混合物才会发出嘶嘶声。每次发生碰撞时，混合物都会发出嘶嘶声。分子以更高的能量发生碰撞，其行为受物理定律支配。受物理定律支配。每个物质对象的未来、现在和过去都受物理定律支配。每个天体的轨道，每一滴雨的降落。他自己的身体是分子的集合。他的欲望是一锅激素，其化学成分刚刚得到科学证明。他的大脑是物质、血液和骨骼的集合。

If he suspends the glass above the flame, the brew will sizzle until one chemical interacts with another. The concoction will sizzle every time. Molecules colliding with increased energy, their behavior ruled by the laws of physics. Ruled by the laws of physics. The future, present, and past of every material object is subject to the laws of physics. The orbit of every celestial body, the fall of every drop of rain. His own body a collection of molecules. His desire a cauldron of hormones whose chemistry has just been scientifically documented. His brain a case of matter, blood, and bone.

但他能直接感受到自己的灵魂、自己的精神。他无法接受，作为肉体的集合体、物质的集合体，他的未来、过去和现在已经被物理定律。他无法压抑直觉，他做出选择，用他的思想和精神影响世界。他无法压抑他对上帝的信仰。

But he feels direct experience of his own soul, his spirit. He cannot accept that as an aggregate of flesh, a clump of matter, that his future, past, and present are already determined by the laws of physics. He cannot crush out the intuition that he makes choices, influences the world with his mind and spirit. He cannot crush out his belief in God.

但他心里很纠结。1+1 的精神在哪里呢？

But it gnaws at him. Where is the spirit in 1 + 1?

他设计了一个范式，将他对精神的信仰与他坚定的唯物主义结合在一起。这是痛苦和有缺陷的，他开始对这种融合感到尴尬。这种结合不会持久。

He designs a paradigm that welds his belief in the spirit to his firm materialism. It is painful and flawed and he comes to regard the fusion with embarrassment. The bond won’t hold.

物质主义的光辉与精神主义的诱惑。谁会赢？两者都有诱惑他的力量。即使在今天，当真相从混乱中浮现出来时，他仍然被催眠了。当他听到其他人来了，他们蜂拥而至，宣告他们的敌对意图，内心深处意识到他因今晚的下流言论而受到惩罚，即使在那时，他还是忍不住停下来欣赏蓝色、红色和黄色的丝带，因为蜡烛油蒸发并凝结成烟。

The sparkle of his materialism versus the enticement of his spirituality. Which will win? Both have the power to beguile him. Even today he was hypnotized when nuggets of truth protruded from the mess. When he heard the others coming, the stampede a declaration of their hostile intent, deep down recognizing his punishment for this evening's dirty talk, even then, he couldn’t help but stop and admire the ribbons of blue, red, and yellow as the candle grease vaporized and curdled to smoke.

克里斯向他展示了碘酸盐和亚硫酸盐溶液之间的反应。他将混合物放在靠近脸的透明烧杯中，观察艾伦的反应，溶液变成了鲜艳的蓝色，染上了克里斯托弗的头发，加深了他眼睛的色调。对艾伦来说，情况似乎正好相反，好像克里斯美丽的眼睛把烧杯染成了蓝色。几乎与试管中的离子产生共鸣，这是一种化学连锁反应，图灵的肤色先是变粉红，然后又变成了不均匀的红色。这并不是克里斯所期望的反应，但如果他知道艾伦脸红的原因，他就不会表现出这种感觉。他通过把注意力引向计算离子复合率的理论问题来消除尴尬。艾伦抓住了这条防线，并在接下来的几周里着手设计自己的理论。

Chris had shown him the reaction between solutions of iodates and sulfites. Holding the mixture in a clear beaker near his face, he watched Alan's response as the solution turned a bold blue, tinting Christopher's hair and deepening the hue of his eyes. To Alan it seemed the other way around, as though Chris's beautiful eyes had stained the beaker blue. Almost in sympathy with the ions in the tube, a chemical chain reaction, Turing's skin tone changed to pink and then an uneven red. Not exactly the response Chris had expected but if he knew the source of Alan's blushing, he spared his feelings. He dispersed any awkwardness by drawing attention to the theoretical problem of computing the rate of recombination of the ions. Alan seized on this line of defense and set about devising his own theory in the following weeks.

他经常试图重现克里斯的灵魂从他眼睛的入口渗出并注入房间的那一刻，他的灵魂被困在烧杯中的靛蓝液体中，他的灵魂以惊人的专注力凝结。他知道化学物质的简单形式及其组合规则，但他无法摆脱克里斯给他留下的印象。他不能将这种体验局限于普通物质的范围。在自己房间里，他重新进行了实验，等待了三十秒，色彩突然冲破液体。虽然这个过程增强了他对那一刻的记忆，但颜色从未达到克里斯把管子悬在眼睛附近时达到的峰值色调。人类细胞、化学物质和玻璃中的灵魂在哪里？

He often tries to re-create the moment when Chris's spirit seeped out of the portals of his eyes and infused the room, a stunning concentration of his soul trapped in the indigo liquid in the beaker. He knows the simple form of the chemicals and the rules of their combination, but he can’t shake the force of the impression that Chris makes on him. He can’t limit the experience to the confines of ordinary matter. In the privacy of his room, he re-creates the experiment, waiting for thirty seconds before the sudden rush of color tears through the fluid. While the process enhances the vibrancy of his memory of that moment, the color never quite strikes the peak hue it reached the time Chris held the tube suspended near his eyes. Where is the spirit in human cells and chemicals and glass?

虽然被困在木板下面，但他还是在思考这些问题，集中注意力的努力稍微抑制了他的歇斯底里。艾伦的左手食指在打斗中被碎玻璃割伤。看到自己那一股细小的血流，他跪了下来。其他人在这几乎昏厥的交界处占了上风，而他现在躺在地板下，呼吸着，用拇指按着手指外侧皮肤上的细小裂缝。几滴失血中灵魂在哪里？他也失去了一些灵魂吗？

Trapped as he is beneath wooden planks, he considers such questions and the effort to concentrate curbs his hysteria just slightly. Alan's left index finger was cut by broken glass in the scuffle. His knees bowed at the sight of the weak rivulet of his own blood. The others got the upper hand at the junction of this near faint and here he is under the floor, circulating his breath and thumbing the thin split in the skin along the outside of his finger. Where is the spirit in a few drops of lost blood? Did he lose some of his soul too?

尽管耳边传来刺耳的震颤声，但他走进休息室时，仍能清晰地听到克里斯的声音，透过地板的木板传来。即使在他目前荒谬的处境下，他还是被这声音所鼓舞，对着烟灰露出灿烂的笑容。他更加用力地扭动着身体，但同样徒劳无功，并抵制住明显的嫉妒之情。艾伦的嫉妒之情永远是天真的，永远不会变成蔑视。这种感觉只会让他第一次后悔自己的邋遢。他在克里斯身上看到了他不该有的从未想象过。他看到一个在世界上正常运作的人，他不是骗子。他感到敬畏和困惑，一个能够认识到木星卫星运动可预测性的人也能洞察谢尔本学校的社会规则。他研究了克里斯温柔的微笑和与生俱来的优雅，它们给了他一个新的标准来考虑。

Despite the blaring throb in his ears, he can catch the unmistakable lilt of Chris's voice, smothered through the planks of the floor, as he enters the dayroom. Even in his current ridiculous circumstances, he is gladdened by the sound and smiles broadly into the soot. He squirms more energetically but just as uselessly, and resists a rush of patent jealousy. In the natural preserves of his permanent innocence, Alan's jealousy never sours to contempt. This feeling only causes him to regret his slovenliness for the first time. He sees in Chris something he never imagined possible. He sees a person functioning in the world who is not a phony. He is awed and mystified that someone who can recognize the predictability of the motions of Jupiter's moons can also penetrate the social rules of Sherborne School. He has studied Chris's gently placed smile and inherent grace, and they have given him a new standard to consider.

艾伦的脏兮兮的论文，脏得难以辨认，只是他小小的反抗行为。在他的脑海中，他拥有令人惊叹的真理珍宝，这些珍宝被逻辑规则完美地切割出来。将这些珍宝抄录下来供他的导师参考是毫无意义的苦差事。但通过克里斯，他看到了另一种可能性。一种他永远无法实现的可能性。技能与文化魅力相结合。洞察力与完美执行相结合。

Alan's filthy papers, soiled and illegible, are a minor act of defiance. He holds in his mind's eye stunning jewels of truth, cut flawlessly by logic's rules. To transcribe these gems for the benefit of his instructors is a pointless chore. But through Chris he sees another possibility. One he will never achieve. Skill combined with cultured charm. Insight merged with polished execution.

当他们靠在艾伦上方的桌子上时，克里斯和另一个男孩之间发生了对话。艾伦想从木头和钉子中钻出来，看看克里斯是否愿意下棋。如果他能的话，满身泥土和一点点血迹的图灵会很乐意从地板上爬出来，不会解释他进来的特殊情况，也不会心怀怨恨，并恳求克里斯下一场深思熟虑的棋局。

As they lean on the table above Alan, there is an exchange between Chris and one of the other boys. Alan wants to claw his way through the wood and nails and see if Chris is up for a game of chess. If only he could, Turing, covered in dirt and a very little bit of blood, would gladly clamber out of the floor without explaining the peculiar circumstances of his entrance, without resentment, and plead with Chris for a thoughtful game of chess.

在他们上一场比赛中，图灵以糟糕的走法迅速输掉了比赛。他正在寻找一种确保控制棋盘的算法，而不是坚持当时的策略。当克里斯执行一步，决定车时，图灵充满了一种安慰的感觉——就像是克里斯选择的保证。他行使了自己的自由意志，消灭了图灵的骑士，艾伦亲眼看到他自由了。这种意志的来源是图灵知道，科学实在论的真正面貌只能是灵魂，只能是上帝的表现。1+1=2 中的上帝在哪里？上帝就在我们的头脑中，即 1+1=2。

During their last game Turing lost swiftly with an abysmal sequence of moves. He was searching for an algorithm to ensure board domination instead of adhering to the strategy of the moment. When Chris executed a move, deciding on the rook, Turing was flooded with a feeling of comfort— something like assurance because Chris chose. He exercised his free will and eliminated Turing's knight and Alan could see with his own eyes that he was free. The source of this will in the face of a scientific realism Turing knew to be true could only be the soul, could only be a manifestation of God. Where is God in 1+1=2? God is in our mind's recognition that 1 + 1=2.

但就在他感受到这个启示的温暖时，他的脑海里却有一些东西挥之不去。克里斯正在遵循一些指示。他把车向前移动了四格，尊重左右两边的棋子，尊重游戏规则。他遵守规则。

But even as he felt the warmth of this revelation, something stuck in his head. Chris was following some instructions. He moved the rook forward four squares, respecting the pieces to the left and to the right, respecting the rules of the game. He followed rules.

在谢伯恩男子学校的地板下，艾伦考虑着另一种可能性——他并不自由。把他困在那里的男孩们也不自由。克里斯也不自由。尽管艾伦很快打破了逻辑，转而遵循他的宗教信仰，但他有缺陷的信仰并不能真正安慰他。每一秒、每一次心跳、每一次呼吸都带来痛苦。这个有毒时刻的残酷将使他的身心陷入极度沮丧，以至于他不确定自己是否能完全恢复。有一段时间，他的氰化物实验被一种创造性自杀尝试的原型所取代——精心设计的装置，包括苹果、漂亮的圆红苹果和一根细细的导电电线。

Under the floor of Sherborne School for boys, Alan considers an alternative possibility—that he is not free. That the boys who trap him there are not free. That Chris is not free. Although he quickly breaks the trail of logic to follow instead his religious conviction, Alan's flawed faith cannot truly comfort him. Every second, every heartbeat, every breath brings anguish. The brutality of this poisonous hour will precipitate a depression of his mind and body so grave that he can’t be sure he will ever fully rebound. For a time his cyanide experiments are replaced with prototypes for an inventively devised suicide attempt—elaborate contraptions involving apples, lovely round red apples, and a delicate sliver of wire to conduct electricity.

他确实为克里斯而活。他破碎的信念也确实帮助他度过了难关。但怀疑的种子已经种下，恐惧的种子也种在了欺负他的人中间。这颗种子如何传播将取决于他如何照料那片杂乱的花园。与此同时，他努力保护自己的信仰不受现实的脆弱石头的伤害，听到桌子被拖回原位的声音，听到地板底面被他扭曲的脸、手推开，他感到疯狂，和肩膀。克里斯已经谈妥了释放事宜。他疯狂地从黑洞里跳出来，一边干呕、喘息，一边眯着眼睛适应光线，一边从地板上爬出来，看着同学们的脚步声渐渐远去。

He does live for Chris. And his damaged beliefs do patch him through. But a germ of doubt is planted, as a seed of dread is planted among his bullies. How that germ spreads will depend on how he tends that messy garden. In the meantime, he struggles to protect his faith from the brittle stones of reality, frantic at the sound of the desk as it is dragged back to its rightful place, frantic at the feel of the underside of the floorboards as they lift in response to the pushing of his twisted face, hands, and shoulders. Chris has negotiated his release. Wildly springing from the dark hole, he retches and pants and squints as he acclimates to the light and watches the receding heels of his classmates as he emerges from the floor.

在痛苦和困惑中，他回到自己的房间，收集他认为是灵魂永恒品质最关键的数据。他心中充满了一种可怕的预感，一种克里斯死亡的可怕预感，但他看到的只有这一幕：在他空荡荡的窗户下，一滩蓝色的水里有一个破碎的玻璃烧杯。

In his distress and confusion, he returns to his room, where he then collects what he trusts to be the most decisive data for the atemporal quality of the soul. He is filled with a terrifying experience of foreboding, a terrible presentiment of Chris's death, when all he sees is this: beneath his bare window a shattered glass beaker in a puddle of blue.

维也纳，1931 年

VIENNA, 1931

今天早上，库尔特公寓的三个大房间里挤满了寒冷的空气，但几乎没有家具，尽管他拥有的家具都很好，反映了他母亲的精致品味，而他并没有继承这种品味。他的母亲玛丽安来到维也纳照顾她的库尔特勒，为他安排一个家，并监督他吃饭。他的饮食很糟糕。他对每一口食物都抱怨不已，好像她让他吃沙子一样。但他一直是一个娇弱的男孩，有着可爱的月亮脸，像猫头鹰一样漂亮，眼睛周围有悲伤的蓝色眼圈。他不是这个世界的人，是她最小的儿子。他的聪明才智甚至让她感到害怕，当时他还那么小，本应该在和哥哥玩追逐游戏时擦伤膝盖，但他却躲在家里光线最暗的房间深处。虽然她无比爱他，但她常常不知道如何与他互动。所以她拥抱他，喂他，用她所有的一切来照顾他。

The three large rooms of Kurt's apartment were crowded with frigid air this morning but nearly empty of furniture, though what he owns is fine and reflects his mother's delicate taste, a palate he has not inherited. His mother, Marianne, came to Vienna to care for her Kurtele, to fix him a home and see that he ate. His diet was appalling. He complained about every morsel as though she were making him eat sand. But then he had always been a delicate boy with a lovely moon face, pretty like an owl, with sad blue rings around his eyes. He was not of this world, her youngest boy. His cleverness intimidated even her when he was so young he should have been skinning his knees in a game of chase with his brother but instead he skulked deep in the rooms of their home where the attrition of light was worst. And though she loved him beyond reason, she often didn’t know how to engage him. So she cuddled him and fed him and mothered him with all she had.

小时候，库尔特要么焦急地依偎在母亲身边，要么毫不费力地孤僻。他玩儿时的游戏时会全神贯注，比如堆砖头和摆放模型火车。偶尔，他会用一些令人困惑但又巧妙的棋盘游戏引起哥哥的兴趣。如果说当时有什么奇怪的，那就是两个男孩玩耍时那种奇怪的沉默。库尔特一个人玩得那么心满意足、那么安静，这让他哥哥很恼火。他深深沉浸在孤独的幻想中，而他真正的家人就像想象中的朋友一样，在他虚构的现实中进进出出。

As a child, Kurt was either anxiously clinging to his mother or effortlessly withdrawn. He played childhood games with intense concentration, stacking bricks and arranging model trains. Occasionally he caught his older brother's interest in board games with confusing moves that proved ingenious. If anything seemed odd then, it was only the peculiar silence of the two boys playing. It irritated his brother that Kurt would play alone just as contentedly and just as silently. He was deeply embedded in solitary fantasies while his real family drifted in and out of his invented reality, as easily as imaginary friends.

玛丽安娜用一些得体的家具布置了他维也纳公寓的房间，解决了一些建筑布局问题。和往常一样，他会假装忙于处理一些普通的事情，比如报纸或书籍，一杯没动过的咖啡，他把它当作道具，离他的手太远了，让人难以相信。她知道他是为了她而假装的，经常看到他坐在一把她希望他扔掉的木椅上，一动不动，就像一个小雕像。他会永远需要她，她珍贵的库尔特勒。虽然她回布尔诺的日期在她完成室内装饰之前就到了，但她还是设法确定了一些定义房间的关键点。

Marianne structured the rooms of his Viennese apartment with decent pieces, solving certain problems of the building's arrangement. Just as always, he would pretend to occupy himself with ordinary things, a newspaper or a book, an untouched coffee he placed like a prop, too far from his hand to be believable. She knew he was pretending for her sake and often watched him sitting in a wooden chair she wished he would discard, static as a figurine. He would need her forever, her precious Kurtele. Although the date of her return home to Brno arrived before she could complete the interior, she managed to establish a few key points that defined the rooms.

昨晚，在他母亲不在的时候，阿黛尔用她那异常温暖的手温暖他的手指，揉捏着他关节上冻僵的疼痛。她用一条粗糙的毯子裹住他，暂时离开了他，走下许多楼梯，进入石窖，这是连接街区几栋建筑的地下走廊网络的一个分支。她靠在昏暗的那个凹室就是他公寓的门牌号，就在洞口上方的墙上。她假装毫不体贴，一只手倒在煤灰里，另一只手抓着煤块，把黑色的煤块扔进一个脏兮兮的袋子里，直到对收集到的煤块的重量感到满意。她用双手捶打，把手指间最厚的炭灰敲掉，然后粗暴地在袋子粗糙的外面擦了擦，再在裙子前面轻轻地弹了弹。她一只胳膊扛着那块煤，从黑暗的地下室里走出了。

Last night, in his mother's absence, Adele warmed his fingers in her impossibly hot hands, kneading the frozen ache out of his knuckles. Wrapping him in a scratchy blanket, she left him momentarily to descend the many stairs into the stone cellar, a branch off a network of underground hallways connecting several buildings along the block. She leaned into the dingy alcove identified by his apartment number on the wall just above the opening. She pretended no delicacy as she fell onto one hand in the soot and grabbed at hunks of coal with the other, tossing the black blocks into a filthy sack until satisfied by the weight of the collection. She pounded her hands together to knock free the worst of the charcoal dust from between her fingers and then wiped them roughly on the coarse outside of the sack before flicking superficially at the front of her dress. Carrying the heft of coal in one arm, she found her way out of the dark hollow of the cellar.

阿黛尔·图斯内尔达·波克特。这是她父母给她起的名字，她一直用这个名字来表演舞台。她曾经梦想着跳芭蕾舞，从童年到青春期，再到成年。她的表演既有力又有活力，但也有些沉重，笨拙，让人想起她的名字。她看着女孩们优雅的舞姿，她们的脚趾尖尖的，骨头被塑造成粉色缎子鞋的形状。她们用长长的拱形脖子悬在空中，直到舞台再次轻轻地把她们带走。她们自由自在，飞翔着，非常漂亮。她会绝望地排练跳跃，一只脚愤怒地撞在地板上，用很大的力气却无法与地面脱离片刻，她的前腿落地很久之后，她才设法抬起后背。最后，她无法摆脱地球或阶级的重量。她的脚趾被粉色缎鞋外表看似精致的鞋带残忍地绑住，弯曲着，看起来可怕又疼痛，她的四肢却显得粗壮而性感她把它们发挥到了极致。她从来没有跳过芭蕾舞。但她确实跳了舞——在维也纳的一家夜总会 Der Nachtfalter。

Adele Thusnelda Porkert. That is the name her parents gave her, one she continues to use for the stage. She used to dream of dancing in the ballet and dance she did, past childhood and adolescence and on into years of definite adulthood. Her performances had strength and energy but a heaviness too, a clumsiness reminiscent of her name. She watched the elegance of girls with toes chiseled to points, their bones molded prettily into the shape of a pink satin shoe. They hung in the air with long, arched necks until the stage softly carried them along again. They were free and in flight and so, so pretty. She would rehearse the leaps in despair, banging one angry foot on the floor and with great force only to get less than a moment's disconnect from the ground, her front leg landing eons before she managed the lift of the back. In the end, she wasn’t able to float free of the weight of the earth or of her class. Her own toes were buckled and knobbed by the cruel binding inside the deceptively delicate facade of the pink satin shoe. They looked horrid and arthritic and her limbs felt stocky and sexual as she spread them to their limits. She never did dance for the ballet. But dance she does—for a Viennese nightclub, Der Nachtfalter.

芭蕾舞演员的名声和妓女差不多，阿黛尔对此心怀怨恨。人们经常开玩笑说，任何男人只要花几百克朗就能陪一个芭蕾舞演员。骗子。然而，夜总会更难辩护，因为其他女孩并不完全贞洁或端庄。如果她们结婚，她们更有可能把性病传染给丈夫，而不是生孩子。如果被迫坦白，她可能也不是那么纯洁。毕竟，她和库尔特有什么关系？但很难不享受你如此擅长的事情，她非常擅长照顾他。作为自遇到他以来的悔恨，她努力克制自己表演的性感，只为他而燃起激情。观众的掌声被这一声的沉默所取代。

Ballet dancers have reputations little better than whores and Adele carries a bitter resentment for this on their behalf. It has often been quipped that any man could keep a ballerina's company for a couple of hundred crowns. Liars. The nightclub, however, is harder to defend, as the other girls aren’t exactly chaste or demure. If they ever marry they are more likely to give a husband venereal disease than a child. Maybe she isn’t so pure either, if forced to confess. After all, what business does she have here with Kurt? But it is hard not to enjoy something you are so good at, and she is very good at caring for him. As penitence since she met him, she fights the sexiness of her own performance, turning it alight only for him. The applause of the crowd replaced with the silence of this one.

阿黛尔是这样认识年轻的哥德尔先生的：他和她以及她的丈夫住在同一条街上。她几乎每天都会和他擦肩而过，尽管他们几乎交换了一下眼神（一个人转过头去，另一个人却瞥了他一眼），但她并没有多想他。在一个普通的星期一，她在大街上扔了一堆钞票，库尔特在那里收拾了一堆信封，并邀请她喝咖啡。阿黛尔通常不会同意。每当她讲述他们相遇的故事时，她都会非常防御这一点。她总是对在夜总会接近她的那些男人的傲慢感到不快。但库尔特的邀请完全是另一回事。他谦逊而温和。他的笑容很慷慨并且富有感染力，他身上有一种明显的优雅。他的衣服很帅气，帽子也戴得很好，是真正的绅士的标志。他是如此的优雅，甚至谦逊，拒绝会让人觉得很粗鲁。更重要的是，她担心拒绝会显得很下流，就像拒绝让人开门一样。当他继续把她的邮件送到目的地时，他似乎很专注，甚至可能很崇拜。他立刻让她觉得——当她说出这句话时，她不愿意加上这个观察结果——更加优雅。

This is how Adele made the young Mr. Gödel's acquaintance: He lived on the same street as she and her husband. She passed him most days and though they almost exchanged looks (one would turn away before the other glanced) she hadn’t given him much thought. When, on an otherwise average Monday, she dropped a collection of bills on the Strasse, Kurt was there to collect the fan of envelopes and ask her to coffee. Adele would not ordinarily have agreed. She's very defensive on this point whenever she recounts the story of their meeting. She is always offended by the presumption of men who approach her at the nightclub. But Kurt's invitation was something else entirely. He was unassuming and gentle. His smile was generous and contagious and he had a decided elegance about him. His clothes were handsome and he wore a hat well, marks of a real gentleman. He was so gracious, even humble, that it would have felt rude to refuse. More than this, she worried it would have seemed lower-class to refuse, like refusing to have a door held open. As he continued to carry her post to their destination he seemed attentive, potentially even adoring. He immediately made her feel—she's reluctant to add this observation when she tells it—more refined.

在茶杯和碟子、碎蛋糕和咖啡馆的喧闹声中，他总是热情而有趣，不时地插话，语气恰到好处；而她则用滔滔不绝的话语填满了他们第一次约会的一个小时。

Over the cups and saucers, the crumbling cake, and the din of the café, he was warm and funny, interjecting now and again with just the right emphasis, while she filled the hour of their first assignation with her copious chatter.

她开始和她们交往，所以她打算继续交往下去。昨晚，她用脑子里第一个冒出的想法刺破了任何偶然飘过的安静泡沫。攻击之后很快又出现了一连串的重复、重复和强化。她八卦了 Der Nachtfalter 的其他女孩，尤其津津乐道那个陷入困境的新女孩的故事。她一边说着，一边在主炉子里堆了一个形状优美的煤堆，上面放着一大把皱巴巴的泛黄纸，然后点燃了它。

As she began their relationship, so she intended to go on. Last night, she punctured any bubble of quiet that happened to drift by with the sharp end of the first thing that came into her head. The assault was quickly followed by a volley of reiterations, redundancies, and reinforcements. She gossiped about the other girls at Der Nachtfalter, savoring in particular the tale of the new girl with a predicament gestating As she talked, she built a shapely mound of coals topped with generous handfuls of crinkled yellowed paper in the main oven and set the structure alight.

“阿黛尔，拜托，”他在厨房的座位上哀求道，“你在做什么？”

“Adele, please,” he whined from his seat in the kitchen, “what are you doing?”

“让您舒服。”

“Making you comfortable.”

“有毒气体让我很不舒服。胸腔里充满烟雾会导致肺部发炎，导致窒息。其中的金属成分会产生水泡并损害心脏组织。”

“Toxic gas makes me rather uncomfortable. A chest full of smoke can cause inflammation of the lungs resulting in suffocation. The metal content produces blisters and damages the heart tissues.”

“嘘。别傻了。这煤够纯净了。烟囱里没有异物。我亲自检查过了。”她的固执并不罕见。他的固执也一样。

“Shush. Don’t be silly. This coal is pure enough. The chimney is clear. I checked it myself.” Her stubbornness was not unusual. Neither was his.

她知道他讨厌碰煤。他宁愿冻死也不愿点燃公寓里的内置烤箱取暖。如果不是她，他不仅会冻死，还会饿死。她会在这里找到他，一具裹着羊毛的脆冰骨架。霜冻要花几个小时才能蒸发，这个地方才有机会变暖，但在她离开家，回到令她失望的丈夫身边之前，她会筛煤、测试煤条，清理边缘聚集的任何烟灰。到午夜，他应该会完全暖和起来。如果她不能在这里让他醒来，给他做早餐，至少她可以保护他免受清晨无情的寒冷的侵袭。

She knew he hated to touch the coals. He would rather freeze to death than light the built-in ovens that heated his apartment. If it weren’t for her, he’d not only freeze, he’d starve. She’d find him here, a skeleton of crisp ice wrapped in wool. It would take hours for the frost to evaporate and for the place to have a chance at warmth, but before she would leave for her own home and the disappointment that was her husband, she would sift the coals, test the shoots, and clean any soot that gathered near the edges. By midnight he should be outright warm. If she couldn’t be here to ease his waking and cook him breakfast, at the least she could protect him from the deep bite of the soulless cold of morning.

当她徒手堆放有毒的砷、铅和汞时，他想到她可能会杀死他。也许是意外，也许是故意。燃烧燃料产生的蓝色烟雾可能扼杀了公寓里的生命，并渗入肉汤，将苹果烤熟，使果肉中充满有毒矿物质。烟雾会软化骨头，然后扭曲骨头，使他残疾，牙齿变黄，眼睛刺痛失明。他尽量不深吸一口气，专注于短促而急促的呼气。他不可能独自在那里度过这一夜，被滚滚黑烟窒息而死。砖炉。到了早上，他就会患上癌症，死于心脏残疾。他静静地思考着这些可能性，沉浸在心碎之中，尽管他知道这仍然只是假设。她温暖了他，擦干了他，听他说话。她甚至给他唱歌。在她坚持要煤之前，他的感激之情充满了爱意，用“啧啧”和“嘘”淹没了他的抗议。

As she stacked—with her bare hands—poisonous aggregates of arsenic, lead, and mercury, he was stung by the possibility that she might actually kill him. Maybe by accident. Maybe by intention. The blue haze of burned fuel could have choked the life out of the apartment and soaked into the broth, baking the apple as it saturated the fruit flesh with toxic minerals. The fumes could soften, then twist the bones, leaving him crippled, yellowing his teeth, stinging his eyes blind. He tried not to swallow a deep lungful of air and concentrated on short sharp exhalations. He would not have survived the night in there alone, asphyxiated by the pollution billowing black as death from his brick furnace. By morning he would have flourished a cancer of sores, knocked dead by a crippled heart. He brooded quietly over these possibilities, indulging in a heartbreak that he knew was still only hypothetical. She had warmed him, dried him, and listened to him. She even sang to him. His gratitude was dense with affection before she insisted on the coal, drowning out his protests with “tsk's” and “shush's.”

她的手很脏，沾满了黑色的灰尘。有毒的金属会冲破皮肤，皮肤会封住她的血液和内脏，保护她免受污染。单是砷就会冒泡，形成开放性溃疡，像腐烂一样蔓延。她也在自杀。

Her hands were filthy—caked with black dust. The poisonous metals could break through the skin that sealed her blood and guts, protecting her from contamination. The arsenic alone could bubble into open sores that spread like the rot. She was killing herself too.

当火势越来越旺，她确信煤会稳定燃烧时，她将炉子关在小金属门后面，同样熟练地照看远处房间里的第二个炉子，洗净双手，开始准备库尔特的晚餐。他仔细地看着她洗，用滑溜溜的手指轻轻搓动，把手指间网状皮肤上的颗粒弄掉。他需要确保没有致命的煤屑影响土豆和大麦汤的调味。

When the fire held strong and she felt sure the coals would burn steadily, she sealed the furnace shut behind the small metal door, tended the second furnace in the far room with equal competence, scrubbed her hands clean, and set about preparing Kurt's dinner. He watched closely as she washed, feathering her slippery fingers together to dislodge particles from the webby skin between digits. He needed to be sure no fatal flecks of coal were seasoning the soup of potatoes and barley.

她从包里拿出一个苹果放在桌上，洗净土豆切片，浸泡大麦后，阿黛尔收拾好包，用手指抚平头发。她像母亲一样抚摸着他的头发，宣告她要离开了。她张开手掌，顺着他的头型托住他的脖子，重重地吻了他冰凉的嘴唇。

After she produced an apple from her bag and placed it on the table, after the potatoes were washed and sliced, and after the barley was soaked, Adele gathered her bag and fingered her hair smooth. She announced her departure with a motherly stroke of his hair. Using her full open palm, she followed the shape of his head to cradle his neck as she kissed him heavily on his cool lips.

当门在她身后关上时，哥德尔扔出了有毒的他在垃圾堆里捡苹果，用汤把炉子熄灭，鼻子夹在弯曲的手臂里，眯着眼睛，抵御着热煤迅速冷却发出的嘶嘶声，直到他走到窗前，衣衫褴褛地挂在窗框外，在令人震惊的寒冷中喘着粗气。今天早上他醒来时，天气冷得刺骨。而他还活着。

As the door closed behind her, Gödel threw the poisoned apple in the rubbish, extinguished the furnaces with the soup, his nose pinched in the crease of his bent arm, eyes squinted against the sizzle that spewed from the rapid cooling of the hot coals, until he made it to the window, hanging raggedly out the frame gasping for his life in the stunning cold of the fresh air. When he woke this morning, it was bone-snapping cold. And he was alive.

阿黛尔左脸颊上有一块深红色的污渍。这块胎记的颜色预示着她的情绪，在性爱瞬间，她会脸红，而当愤怒从内而外地烧灼她时，她会感到十分灼热。

Adele has a stain the color of a dark port infusing the skin of her left cheek. The hue of her birthmark forecasts moods, blushing deeply in carnal moments that she is relieved pass quickly and positively scalding when rage burns her from the inside out.

她经常照镜子，找一个合适的角度来隐藏镜子里的痕迹。她的父亲是一名摄影师，教她如何摆姿势拍照，她和父亲都喜欢在最后的照片上用黑白照片记录下她完美、白皙的脸庞，仿佛他们欣赏的是另一个孩子。如果没有照片能从阴影中捕捉到紫色，也许她的一生可以没有它——她意识到，这种从母亲那里遗传下来的像瘀伤一样的瑕疵可能有点粗俗。她和丈夫（也是摄影师）重复着这个奇怪的仪式，摆出近乎侧面的姿势，她的左眼、脸颊和嘴唇神秘的，他和她一起溺爱她那完美而白皙的脸庞，仿佛他们所仰慕的是另一个女人。

She often studies herself in the mirror, striking just the right angle to hide the mark from her reflection. Her father, a photographer, taught her how to pose for cameras, and together she and he doted on the prettiness of the perfect, fair side of her face recorded in black-and-white on the final print, as though it were another child altogether that they admired. If no photographs could catch the purple color out of shadow, maybe her life could be remembered without it—a blemish like a bruise inherited from a mother she realized might be the littlest bit vulgar. She repeated the strange ritual with her husband, also a photographer, posing in near profile, her left eye, cheek, and lip occulted, and together he and she doted on the prettiness of the perfect, fair side of her face, as though it were another woman altogether that they admired.

几周前，阿黛尔穿好衣服准备上班，她的母亲来到她狭小的公寓，对她进行了严厉的言语、建议和批评，使公寓更加拥挤。阿黛尔将右脸颊贴在镜子上，凝视着她自己，而不是那个女人。她的母亲挤在阿黛尔和镜子之间，以便也研究镜子中的倒影。她们站在那里，稍微有些踉踉跄跄。阿黛尔把头发盘起来，而她母亲的闲话在玻璃上留下了一层淡淡的唾沫。当她把眼睛前面、耳朵后面、脖子后面的散落的头发盘起来、拉扯时，她注意到母亲也在做同样的事情。盘起来、拉扯、拉扯，她们齐声拨弄着头发。就在阿黛尔放慢速度打破同步时，她的母亲也放慢了速度，仿佛节奏的变化是舞蹈的一部分。

A few weeks ago, as Adele dressed for work, her mother visited her cramped flat to crowd it even more with a harsh gas of words, advice, and criticism. Adele aligned her right cheek with the plane of the mirror to contemplate the woman she was not. Her mother wedged herself between Adele and the mirror in order to study the reflection too. There they stood, slightly staggered. Adele pinned up her hair as her mother left a faint mist of spit on the glass with her gossip. As she tucked and tugged and pulled at the loose strands in front of her eyes, behind her ears, at the nape of her neck, she noticed her mother do the same. Tuck, tug, pull, they fingered their hair in unison. Even as Adele slowed down to break the synchronization, her mother slowed too as though the change in tempo were part of the choreography.

看着母亲那厚厚的下垂的下巴和嘴唇周围的皱纹，她知道她看到的是她真实的倒影。时间的缓慢流逝揭示了它的可塑性，让她跨越了几十年。她清楚地看到了自己的命运，疲惫地叹了口气，接受了它。面对镜子里的自己，还有污渍，她想，“我是个没多少时间的老妓女。”她当时就知道，现在也知道，用不了多久她就会收拾行李离开丈夫。那一天，她将成为她的母亲，也是哥德尔的母亲。这是一个她会擅长的角色。她会在库尔特真正的妈妈玛丽安的指导下，成为他的母亲。

Looking at her mother, the thick sagging jowls and carved line surrounding the lips, she knew she was looking at her true reflection. The plodding passage of time revealed its malleability and allowed her to step across the decades. She saw her fate clearly and with a weary puff accepted it. Facing her image in the mirror, stain and all, she thought, “I’m an old tart with not much time left.” She knew then, and she knows now, that it won’t be long before she packs her things and leaves her husband. That is the day she will become her mother, and Gödel's mother too. It is a role in which she will excel. She will mother him right out from under Kurt's real mummy, Marianne.

玛丽安自然讨厌她。一个舞者，胡说，在中产阶级眼中，她更像是妓女，在母亲眼中，她同样糟糕。更不用说年龄了。或者丈夫。哥德尔的母亲曾经想象那块紫色胎记是波特酒，或者更便宜的东西，是一股粘稠的酒水顺着她的脸颊滑落。玛丽安真希望自己能成为那个把酒泼到她脸上的人。

Naturally Marianne hates her. A dancer, nonsense, more like a prostitute to a middle-class eye and rather as bad to a mother's. Not to mention the age. Or the husband. Gödel's mother used to imagine that purple birthmark was port, or something cheaper, a viscous booze slipping down her cheek. Marianne would like to have been the one to throw it in her face.

更重要的是，阿黛尔滔滔不绝。她不能不说话。她不能忍受空虚的时刻，当它本可以充满活力时，她会怎么做？她警惕地攻击沉默。她试图通过释放每一个向前的想法来清理她的思绪。最好把所有的想法都放在脑外而不是脑内。脑子里满是想法有什么好处？看看库尔特。它们在里面会让人恼火，像酸牙或脏刺一样被感染。

What's more, Adele talks an ocean. She can’t not talk. She can’t bear an empty moment, what, when it could be alive with zest? She is vigilant in her offense against silence. She tries to unclutter her mind by freeing every thought that presses forward. Better to have all her thoughts outside her head and not inside. What's so good about a head full of thoughts? Look at Kurt. Inside they can irritate, become infected like a sour tooth or a dirty splinter.

科特注意到，在她向他转述关于歌舞厅里其他女孩的八卦时，她往往会在关键情节上陷入道德判断的陷阱——他怀疑她会夸大这些叙述，以加剧她的谴责，并掩盖她自己的信念。但她像收音机一样，用无害的词语和主题填满空气，从而为他创造了一个白噪音的背景景观。阿黛尔从不要求他进行任何实际对话。她似乎明白，她在那里是为了保持节奏，淹没更多个体噪音的警报。一根针掉在地上的叮当声会让他神经紧张，街道上一个人的重量压碎砾石的声音，一对情侣从他窗下经过朗格街时沉闷的谈话声，当他们走近时，阴谋论的交流声越来越大。噪音的飞溅让他他紧张又害怕。她在他的公寓里喋喋不休地闲逛，抚平了城市的喧嚣，就像一张阴沉的毯子抚平了热涡流一样。

Kurt has noticed she tends to get snared on moral judgments at key plot points in the gossip she relays to him about the other girls in the cabaret—narratives he suspects she embellishes to fuel her condemnation and fluff her own convictions. But she fills the air with harmless words and themes much as a radio would and thereby creates for him a background landscape of white noise. Adele never demands of him any actual conversation. She seems to understand that she is there to keep time and drown out the alarm of more individuated noises. The clink of a pin drop that can fray his nerves, the grinding of gravel beneath the weight of a man on the street, the spike of a dulled conversation as a couple pass beneath his window over Langegasse, the mounting pitch of the conspiratorial exchange as they approach. The splatter of noises leaves him strained and frightened. Her voluble puttering around his apartment smoothes out the clamor of the city like a dull blanket evening out the thermal eddies.

对科特来说，阿黛尔就像是一块活过来的泥土。没有花招或修饰，没有玩弄规则，没有违反逻辑原则。她简单而又不文雅，让人感到安心和清晰，透明和真实。他是他美丽的受伤的苹果，他可爱的小阿黛尔。她是一块肉，像泥土一样真实。阿黛尔是真实的。她唯一的奢侈之处是偶尔的灵异事件，偶然获取信息或超越普通感官的微妙感知——一点点超感知能力。科特昨晚在极度恐慌中求助于这种天赋。

To Kurt, Adele is like a lump of earth come to life. No tricks or embellishments, no flirting with the rules, no violations of the principles of logic. In her simple uncultured manner, she is reassuring and clear, transparent and real. His beautiful bruised apple, his sweet little Adele. She is a chunk of flesh, real as mud. Adele is real. Her only extravagance is an occasional psychic episode, an incidental plucking of information or a subtle perception beyond the ordinary senses—a modicum of ESP. It is this filament of talent that Kurt turned to last night in his colossal panic.

尽管那天晚上她点燃的篝火和烹制的晚餐都化为灰烬，但这开始还算愉快，因为阿黛尔像往常一样陪伴着他，给他温暖的毯子，给他安慰的咯咯声，给他母亲般的关怀。

And though the evening ended with the destruction of fires she had built and the dinner she had cooked, it began well enough because Adele was there for him, as she always would be, with a warm blanket, a comforting cluck, and a mothering tone.

科特床的铁架是寒气的残酷导体，今天早上他从床上爬起来时，寒气刺痛了他的手，仿佛留下了灼伤，从他潮湿的嘴里冒出的冷凝水云就像是烟雾。他花了一整天的时间准备与 Circle 的讨论，并注意表现得体。他穿了好几层衣服，就像在伤口上敷料一样，用结实的羊毛织物小心地包裹着四肢。第三条裤子很容易扣在里面的两层衣服上，阻力恰到好处。他确保穿得最近的两条裤子略短，并很好地隐藏在外套的袖口后面。他的上半身也做了类似的处理——一系列衬衫和背心形成了五件衣服厚的衬垫。即便如此，他看起来还是很瘦，尽管不那么吓人。

The iron frame of Kurt's bed was a brutal conductor of the chill singeing his hand so sharply as he hoisted himself awake this morning that it might as well have left a burn, and the cloud of condensation that escaped from his damp mouth could have been smoke. He prepared for his discussion with the Circle most of the day and took care to present himself well. He applied layers of clothes like a dressing over a wound, carefully wrapping his limbs in strong woolen weaves. The third pair of pants buttoned easily over the inner two layers with just the right amount of resistance. He made sure the two pairs of trousers he wore closest were slightly short and stayed well hidden behind the cuff of the outer suit. A similar procedure was followed for his upper half—a series of shirts and vests created a padding five garments thick. Even then he looked lean although less alarmingly so.

尽管他很超脱，但他的家庭的成熟程度却没有他完全忘记了这一点，而是从他做出的微妙选择中浮现出来，如果不是在他宽敞的公寓里，他用一些俗气的物品与母亲的设计相冲突，那么至少在他现在用来装扮自己的许多衣服上，都体现了这一点，这些衣服都参考了他父亲工厂生产的华丽纺织品。他穿上了一件织工精细的夹克，这件夹克仍然松松地挂在连接他两肩的线上，最后披上了一件漂亮的大衣。
