Despite his detachment, his family's sophistication was not entirely lost on him and surfaced in the subtle choices he made, if not in the few kitsch objects he clashed against his mother's design in the interior of his large flat, then at least it showed in the many garments that he now used to flatter himself, a reference to the rich textiles manufactured in his father's factories. He applied the finely woven jacket that still hung loosely from the line connecting the points of his two shoulders, and finally a handsome overcoat was draped over that.

哥德尔喜欢这些星期四的晚上。一周的其余时间他几乎完全与世隔绝，有时甚至忘记了白天。在最黑暗的时刻，当他感到孤独时，他会感到安慰，将逻辑符号处理成完美的序列，在他的笔记本中生成一个又一个定理。他在白纸本上写满了数学证明，这些证明引出了新的想法，而新的想法又产生了新的结果。除了书页本身，他总是找不到逻辑结论的扩散背景，书页从左到右覆盖着一侧，直到读完书，他才从右到左翻过书页的背面。在这些普通的棕色笔记本中，他构建了一个自己的逻辑宇宙，其中嵌套着私人的想法，他的秘密宝石。他用 Gabelsberger 记下了他最宝贵的见解，这是他小时候学过的一种过时的德语速记形式，肯定没有人记得。

Gödel loves these Thursday nights. The rest of the week is spent in near complete isolation, sometimes losing the sense of days. Comforted by the darkest hours when his loneliness is assured, he manipulates logical symbols into a flawless sequence, generating theorem after theorem in his notebooks. He fills the plain paper books with mathematical proofs that lead to new ideas that spawn new results. He can’t always find a context for the proliferation of logical conclusions other than the pages themselves, which are covered on one side from left to right until the book is finished and he moves back through the volume covering the backs of the pages from right to left. In these ordinary brown notebooks he builds a logical cosmos of his own in which the private ideas are nested, his secret gems. His most precious insights he transcribes in Gabelsberger, an obsolete form of German shorthand he was taught as a schoolboy and is sure no one else remembers.

虽然他经常在周一轻易迷失，试图在周二找到根基，尽管周三只是两个夜晚之间的纽带，但他总是知道周四。他喜欢早点到，每次都选择同一个地方，一把靠近墙的深色木椅，几乎隐藏在软垫沙发的花艺扶手后面他的摊位不太靠近中心，但也不至于太远，否则会变得拥挤，人们挤在一起取暖，以抵御来自中心的争论的激烈气氛。他舒适地静静地喝着一杯他从不打算喝的温热咖啡，聆听着辩论、思想和笑声，就像一个被遗弃在岛上的人收听着遥远的广播。这证明还有其他人在那里。这证明他并不孤单。这证明。

While he often loses Monday easily and tries to find root in Tuesday, and although Wednesday is a mere link between nights, he always knows Thursday. He likes to arrive early and choose the same place each time, a dark wooden chair near the wall, almost hidden behind the floral arm of an upholstered booth, not too close to the center but not too far out where it might become crowded, people pressing in to warm themselves against the heat of argument emanating from the core. Comfortably still, with an undisturbed tepid coffee he never intends to drink, he listens to the debates, the ideas, and the laughter, like a man marooned on an island tuning in to a distant radio broadcast. Proof that there are others out there. Proof that he is not alone. Proof.

他通常不同意他们的观点。不过，圆圈给了他一个清晰的联系形式，为他的私人宇宙提供了一个外部环境——现实的坚固岩石出现在幽灵的迷雾中。

He usually disagrees with them. Still, the Circle gives him a clear form to relate to, an external setting for his private cosmos—solid rocks of reality appearing in a fog of ghosts.

今天晚上他比平时来得晚。最近发生的事情让他坐立不安。他随身带着最新的笔记本，紧紧地贴在夹克上。他的指关节像带刺的铁丝网一样从书脊伸出。书页几乎都写满了，前后都盖满了；必须从第一页读到最后一页，然后再回到第一页——一条闭合的路径，一个破碎的三角形，在尖端发现了一个秘密。一个令人难以置信的秘密。他对符号流印象深刻，特别是在符号开始的地方，符号流的末端，他感到头晕目眩，而他的血液在他瘦骨嶙峋的膝盖周围汇成一滩滩。

This evening he is later than usual. Knocked unsteady as he has been by recent events. He has his latest notebook with him, pressed against his jacket. His knuckles protrude from the spine of the book like barbed-wire lacings. The pages are nearly full, front and back covered; they must be read as a loop from the first page front to the last page back, then toward the first page again—a closed path, a broken triangle, and at the pointed tip a discovery. An incredible discovery. He is so impressed by the stream of symbols that accumulate particularly at the end point, where they began, that he feels light-headed, while his blood collects in pools about his bony knees.

他站在约瑟夫咖啡馆的玻璃门前。透过玻璃窗的过滤，他的活动变成了一道不真实的光与色的痕迹。他把手放在门上，门开了，闻到了香气，他走进了房间。透过他的眼睛的过滤，他的活动仍然存在，一道不真实的光与色的痕迹。这里谁是真实的？

He's in front of the glass doors of the Café Josephinum. Through the filter of the windowpanes the activity becomes an unreal smear of lights and colors. His hand on the door, it opens, that aroma, and he moves into the room. Through the filter of his eyes the activity persists, an unreal smear of lights and colors. Who here is real?

他顶着幻影的微风，向桌子，靠在椅子上。他看起来很镇定，这很神奇。他的身体状况很脆弱。他的情绪状况也很脆弱。他用厚厚的织物和精心修剪的外表来掩饰前者。他用眼镜反射的灯光图案来掩饰后者。在这个由约瑟夫咖啡馆提供的舞台上，他看起来很轻松，仿佛他属于这里。但过去几天充其量是不规律的。首先，阿黛尔差点毒死他。今天早上，他醒来时感到极度寒冷，仿佛冲破了冰冻的湖面，喘着粗气——空气用脆弱的冰刺冲击着他的鼻子和喉咙，他的脑海里回想着过去几天的进展。一种可怕的解脱感涌上心头，这些解脱的想法本身也向他证实了他还活着。我思故我在，他想。活着的想法和状态都让他感到有趣。虽然他一遍又一遍地在脑海里回想着这些事件，但它们每次重演时都会发生改变：一位老妇人、他的死亡，然后是善良的阿黛尔，直到她往他的炖菜里撒了点东西。然后又是一个老妇人、他的死亡、雨，阿黛尔操纵他的供词，公然地堆起有毒的柴堆。一位老妇人。他的死亡。雨。阿黛尔。美丽而肮脏的阿黛尔。他因怀疑和背叛的浓稠粘液而痛苦不堪。

Pushing against a breeze of phantoms he moves toward the table, pressing into a chair. Amazing that he looks composed. His physical condition is fragile. His emotional condition is fragile. He hides the former behind thick textile weaves and a well-manicured facade. He hides the latter behind the pattern of lights reflected off his glasses. On this stage provided by the Café Josephinum, he looks at ease, as though he belongs. But the past few days have been irregular at best. For one thing, Adele almost poisoned him. He woke into the hardest cold this morning as though breaking through the surface of a frozen lake and gasped for breath—the air shocking his nose and throat with brittle spikes of ice as his mind sucked in the progression of the past days. A terrible relief flooded his system and the relieved thoughts themselves confirmed to him that he was indeed alive. I think therefore I am, he thought. Both the thought and the condition of being alive amused him. While he has run the events over and over in his mind, they permute with each replay: an old woman, his death, then Adele who is kind until she dusts something into his stew. Then again: an old woman, his death, the rain, Adele manipulates his confession and blatantly builds a toxic pyre. An old woman. His death. The rain. Adele. Pretty, stained Adele. He aches with suspicion and the thick mucus of betrayal.

他还因病而疼痛。他疲惫不堪。他的胸口疼痛。他没有呼吸。就在今天晚上，他咳血了。八岁时，他得了一次风湿热，心脏变得僵硬，留下疤痕。多年来，心房瓣膜融合并收缩。这种疾病花了整整十年的时间才宣告他所面临的具体威胁。他饱受病痛折磨。血液回流使心房扩张，使他的心脏无法动脉。他一直生活在对生命的恐惧中。每一分钟都充满恐慌。他胸口的颤动警告他可能出现血栓、窒息或心力衰竭。他不应该待在这里，空气中烟雾弥漫，温暖而有毒。但今天早上四肢的轻松感让他有一种紧迫感和雄心壮志。他需要见莫里茨。

He also aches with disease. He is fatigued. His chest is sore. He has no breath. This very evening he coughed up blood. His heart has become stiff and scarred after a bout of rheumatic fever at the age of eight. A valve in his atrium fused and constricted over the years. It took the disease a full decade to declare the specific threat intended. He is plagued by attacks. A backwash of his blood stretches the chambers, depriving his arteries. He lives in constant fear for his life. Every minute framed by panic. The flutter in his chest a warning of a potential blood clot, suffocation, or heart failure. He shouldn’t be here in the smoky air, warm and virulent. But the relief that filled his limbs this morning gave him a feeling of urgency and ambition. And he needs to see Moritz.

直到莫里茨·石里克到来，圆圈才成型。他像一阵狂风一样进入，身后留下一圈旋涡，绕过门，流入房间。他是这所大学的归纳科学哲学系主任，这个头衔声望很高，很有权威。莫里茨总是一位绅士，总是彬彬有礼、认真而令人钦佩。他摇摇晃晃地坐到椅子上，大家挥手示意，点了更多的咖啡，在越来越暗的房间里，比日落时分还要暗，他们都开始在叮当作响的盘子和碰撞的肘部中安顿下来，他们的重量都向内倾斜。桌子摇晃着，杯子上上下下，形成了一个圆圈。

The Circle doesn’t take shape until Moritz Schlick arrives. He enters like a gale, his entrance embellished by a curl of eddies in his wake that flow around the door and into the room. He is the chair of Philosophy of the Inductive Sciences at the university, a title that carries great prestige and authority. Moritz is always a gentleman, always gracious and earnest and admirable. As he rocks into a chair, hands are waved, more coffees are ordered, and in the darkening room, darker than the ebbing day, they all begin to settle amid clanking dishes, knocking elbows, their collective weight leveraged inward. The table wobbles as cups rise and fall and a circle forms.

这是莫里茨·石里克的圈子。他的邀请将人们聚集在一起，他那舒缓的语调将他们凝聚在一起。他们来到这里是为了围绕真理，摆脱几个世纪以来的误导信仰、宗教的枷锁和形而上学的催眠。他们庆祝自己坐在结实的椅子上的重量、咖啡的热度、他们在咖啡馆里发出的声音。有些人对这一天的紧迫性感到欣喜若狂，因为这才是最重要的。没有别的了。一切真理都集中在椅子、杯子和建筑物中。只有压力、热量和力量。世界就是一切。

It's Moritz Schlick's circle. Drawn together by his invitation and kept together by his soothing tones. They come here to orbit around truth, to throw off centuries of misguided faith, the shackles of religion, the hypnotism of metaphysics. They celebrate the heft of their own weight in a solid chair, the heat off the coffee, the sound their voices manufacture within the walls of the café. Some are delirious with the immediacy of this day because it is all that matters. There is nothing else. Everything true is summed up in the chair, the cup, the building. There is only pressure, heat, and force. The world is all that is the case.

莫里茨知道成员们能产生多大的伟大他选择了，所以他抚平了自我之间的尖刻边缘，使他们成为一个集体，一个由不和谐组成的折衷乐团。莫里茨是将共产主义者、数学家、经验主义者凝聚在一起的粘合剂。他精心挑选了这里的每一个人，耐心地在脑海中思考他们，用他善良的眼光研究他们。他们的自信让他们感到安慰，如果他们有幸收到邀请，他们会对周四的讨论会的邀请感到由衷的荣幸。对许多人来说，他们所期待的邀请从未到来。

Moritz knows the greatness that can emerge from the members he has chosen, so he smoothes the caustic edges between egos and makes out of them a collective, an eclectic orchestra created out of dissonance. Moritz is the glue that holds together the communist, the mathematician, the empiricist. He has selected each person here with care, patiently turning them over in his mind, studying them with his kind eyes. They are comforted by his self-assurance and are sincerely flattered by the invitation to Thursday's discussions, if they are ever fortunate enough to receive the summons. There are many for whom the hoped-for invitation never comes.

大约四年前，当莫里茨在数学研究所地下室的房间里向哥德尔发出邀请时，哥德尔脸红了，不知道是因为虚荣还是害羞，谁知道呢。当时，科特正坐在黑板前，用简练的符号整理另一个学生的思想，这些符号就像是擦得不干净的前人留下的可爱的尘埃痕迹。他总是先用纯符号逻辑记法把骨架抄录下来，然后再开始发言。尽管他只是一名 21 岁的学生，但其他人都钦佩地看着他能够看透辩论中的逻辑骨架，就像厨师熟练地去除鱼片的内骨骼，不让鱼肉粘住一样。莫里茨也看着他，被哥德尔对一个他自己也觉得非常困难的问题的清晰解决方案所感动，他最终决定邀请科特参加他周四晚上的圈子活动。

Gödel blushed with either vanity or shyness, who can know for sure, when Moritz approached him in the room in the basement of the mathematics institute and extended the invitation almost four years ago. Kurt was at the chalkboard organizing another student's thoughts in spare symbols, lovely dusty marks on a landscape of poorly erased predecessors. He always transcribes the skeleton in the pure notation of symbolic logic first and with such care before he begins to speak. Even though he was only a twenty-one-year-old student, the others watched with admiration for his ability to see through to the logical bones in their debates, like a chef skillfully removing the endoskeleton of a filleted fish without a morsel of clinging flesh. Moritz watched him too and moved by the lucidity of Gödel's resolution of a problem he himself had found distractingly difficult, he came to his final decision to extend to Kurt an invitation to his Circle on Thursday nights.

莫里茨和他一起坐在棋盘前，悄悄地在鱼脊骨中间的肋骨上分支出来的无限整数列表上添加了一条精彩的评论。他以这种流畅的方式轻松地哥德尔开始交谈。每个人要么凭直觉知道，要么通过简单的实验学会先用数学来与哥德尔会面。因此，莫里茨用关于无穷大和整数的正确话语接近了科特，赢得了感激和信任的目光。当他带着感激的惊讶握住科特的手和自己的头时，他们交谈起来。

Moritz joined him at the board, quietly adding a fine comment on the infinite list of integers that branched off the middle rib of the fish's spine. And in this smooth manner he eased Gödel into conversation. Everyone either knows by instinct or learns by plain experiment to meet Gödel with mathematics first. And so Moritz approached with the right words about infinity and integers and earned that look of gratitude and trust. As he shook Kurt's hand and his own head in grateful amazement, they talked.

“教授先生，我一直在思考说谎者悖论，说谎者说，这句话是假的。 ”

“Herr Professor, I have been thinking about the Liar's Paradox where the liar says, This sentence is false.”

“啊，说谎者的矛盾。是的，就是那个说这句话是假的说谎者。 ”

“Ah, the antinomy of the liar. Yes, that liar who says, This sentence is false.”

“这个判决不可能是错误的。”

“The sentence cannot be false.”

“因为如果它如所声称的那样是假的，那么它就一定是真的。这很矛盾。” 莫里茨研究了他年轻的学生一段时间，捋了捋嘴唇，最后回答道：“这不可能是真的。因为如果它是真的，那么它就是假的，这又是一个矛盾。这是一个悖论，也是我们粗心使用语言的产物。数学永远不会允许这样的悖论。数学命题要么是真的，要么是假的，没有矛盾。”

“Because if it is false as claimed, then it must be true. A contradiction.” Studying his young student for a time Moritz stroked his lip dry and concluded his motion with the reply, “And it cannot be true. Because if it is true, then it is false which is again a contradiction. It is a paradox and an artifact of our careless use of language. Mathematics will never allow such a paradox. Mathematical propositions will either be true or false with no contradictions.”

“如果数学不能摆脱这样的命题怎么办？”

“What if mathematics is not free of such propositions?”

“一定是的。数学一定是完整的。没有解决不了的问题。”

“It must be. Mathematics must be complete. There are no unsolvable problems.”

自从那天早上收到邀请并经历了谎言的矛盾之后，哥德尔发现莫里茨的存在本身就令人安心。如果库尔特的性格不同，更加亲切，不那么死板；如果莫里茨也稍微不同，更加自发，不那么矜持，哥德尔可能会像爱父亲一样爱莫里茨。相反，他感觉莫里茨更正式，更疏远，更合适。他感到很感激。他把这种他对自己的感受，这种情绪除了参加莫里茨的讨论之外几乎没有任何外在表现。他相信莫里茨是真实的，他存在，莫里茨分享了对无限数字列表的评论的那一刻，他的信仰就更加坚定了。有了这种洞察力，莫里茨就好像说出了一个暗语。我是真实存在的人之一，他的评论得到了证实，他从云中结晶出来并成形。

Ever since that morning of the invitation and the antinomy of the liar, Gödel has found Moritz's very presence reassuring. If Kurt was different in character, more affectionate, less rigid; and if Moritz too were just a little different, more spontaneous, less reserved, Gödel could have come to love Moritz like a father. Instead he feels something more formal, more distant, more appropriate probably. He feels grateful. He keeps this feeling to himself, and the sentiment has almost no outward manifestation beyond his attendance here at Moritz's discussions. He believes that Moritz is real, that he exists, and his faith solidified the moment that Moritz shared the comment on the infinite list of numbers. With that insight, it was as though Moritz uttered a code word. I am one of the real ones, his comment certified, and with that he crystallized from the cloud and took shape.

这不是每个星期四。这是某个特别的星期四。那天晚上，库尔特迫不及待地想见到他，咖啡馆的玻璃门打开了，莫里茨迎着一阵微风走了进来。他分别坐在圆圈的起点和终点。会议一如既往地开始了。莫里茨一边用食指抚摸着上唇的尖角，一边要求大家保持安静，深深地凝视着面前的棕褐色咖啡。他暗自微笑。

This isn’t every Thursday. This is one Thursday in particular. An evening on which Kurt is impatient to see him, on which the glass doors of the café swing wide and Moritz enters with a flourish of a curling breeze. He takes his place at the beginning and end of the Circle. The meeting begins as it always does. Moritz calls for silence as he strokes the articulated peaks of his top lip with his forefinger, looking deep into the nut-brown coffee in front of him. He is smiling to himself.

其他人等着莫里茨开始演讲，一小团安静的气氛从桌子周围弥漫开来，将他们与咖啡馆的喧闹声隔开。圈子里最年轻的成员在寂静的聚光灯下挣扎。他们雄心勃勃。他们紧张不安。他们随时准备争论和狂欢。尽管哥德尔的性格截然不同，但他仍然觉得自己属于这里，受到欢迎，这让他沉浸在一种最接近解脱的感觉中。莫里茨让这一切成为可能。他创造了寂静、聚光灯和场景。当一名年轻的新兵摆动交叉腿的脚踝时，库尔特看着莫里茨·施里克教授，寻找合适的时机来提出他的发现。

The others wait for Moritz to begin as a small quiet sphere emanates from the table and surrounds them, separates them from the clamor of the café. The youngest members of the Circle struggle in the spotlight the silence generates. They are ambitious. They are nervous. They are ready to argue and to revel. Although Gödel is quite different in temperament, he nevertheless feels as though he belongs here, that he is welcome, and it bathes him in a feeling closest to relief. Moritz makes all of this possible. He creates the silence, the spotlight, the scene. While a young new recruit swings the ankle of his crossed leg, Kurt looks to Herr Professor Moritz Schlick for an indication of the right moment to offer his discovery.

与此同时，莫里茨对库尔特没有给予特别的关注。和其他许多人一样，莫里茨被这一平凡日子的经历所吸引。他感觉到今天是如何成为一串珠子中的一颗珠子，以及它将如何交接给下一个珠子，另一个伟大而平凡的日子。就在他开始在朋友们沉默的纯净平台上讲话时，他回顾了自己一路走来的松散结点，就像翻阅一组照片一样，看到了将他带到这一刻、这张桌子、这个圈子的主要力量。他看到了自己是如何从那里走到这里的。

Moritz meanwhile pays Kurt no special attention. Like many of the others, Moritz is distracted by the experience of this single ordinary day. He feels how today has emerged as a bead on a strand of beads and how it will give over to the next in the sequence, another single great and ordinary day. Even as he begins to talk on the pristine platform of his friends’ silence, he looks back over the loose knots along his trajectory and sees, as if flipping through a collection of pictures, the primary forces that brought him to this moment, to this table, to this circle. He sees how he got here from there.

莫里茨脑海中突然闪现出一系列画面，它们始于 1914 年德国枪骑兵的情景。他看着他们从柏林出发，为头戴雕刻金属头盔的骑兵欢呼，头盔顶部有一个尖刺，本身就是一件武器。他看着自己认识的男孩加入步兵队伍，对他们没有装饰的金属头盔感到满意，光秃秃的头盔一直延伸到耳朵上。在危机时期，他们从束缚中得到安慰，接受了从肚脐到紧领口的制服，一个纽扣紧贴喉结，他们狼吞虎咽地吃着腌制的肉和陈旧的厚面包。他们从柏林出发，手里拿着沉重的枪，平衡地放在肩窝里，他再也没有见过他们。

The series of pictures that snap across Moritz's mind starts arbitrarily with German Uhlans in 1914. He watched them march out of Berlin and cheered the cavalry of sculptured metal helmets with a spike at the very crown, a weapon in itself. He watched boys he knew join the infantry and express satisfaction with their undecorated metal helmets, bald domes extending over their ears. They took comfort in restraints during a time of crisis and accepted the uniform that buttoned from navel to a tight collar about the throat, one button a nodule against the Adam's apple as they choked down rations of preserved meat and stale heavy bread. They marched out of Berlin cradling heavy guns in their hands balanced in the hollows of their shoulders and he never saw them again.

在两年的战争服役期间，他计算了弹道湿泥沟里的弹道。当他看到朋友的肉体被撕开一个洞，另一个人被割断的颈静脉流出鲜血，陌生人断裂的脊椎毫无生气时，一些形而上学的概念从他自己的伤口中流出，也从他制服的舒适感中流出。他注意到他早期的学识在最粗糙的炮火面前毫无用处。信仰、形而上学、神学——在暴行面前都是无用的韵律。空洞的咒语没有提供任何东西，没有创造任何东西，没有建立任何东西。只有子弹、弹道和风。物理的、可计算的、残酷的。

During his two years of war service, he calculated ballistic trajectories from a ditch of wet mud. As he watched a hole tear in his friend's flesh, the orbit of blood from another's severed jugular, the lifelessness of a stranger's broken spine, certain metaphysical notions drained out of his own wounds along with his comfort in the harness of his uniform. He noted the uselessness of his earlier scholarship against the crudest artillery. Faith, Metaphysics, Theology—impotent rhymes in the face of atrocity. Empty incantations that served up nothing, created nothing, built nothing. There were only bullets, trajectories, and wind. Physical, calculable, brutal.

他对失去知识遗产的失望几乎与国家战败一样深重。尽管伤口愈合后，他的不满情绪不断增长，但他的反感仍然保持着礼貌。

His disappointment over the loss of his intellectual heritage was nearly as grave as the defeat of his nation. Still his antipathy remained polite although his dissatisfaction grew even as his wounds healed.

随后路德维希·维特根斯坦出现了，莫里茨的矜持在这句话的刺痛下崩溃了：“世界就是一切事物。”

Then came Ludwig Wittgenstein, and Moritz's reserve burst under the incision made by these words: The world is all that is the case.

毫不奇怪，在他对自己来到这里的经历的回顾中，有许多关于维特根斯坦的形象。这个人让任何接近他的人都着迷，而他让莫里茨着迷。维特根斯坦是一位哲学家，一位伟大的哲学家，他来自维也纳最富有、最有文化的家庭之一，事实上，也是整个欧洲最富有、最有文化的家庭之一。有人说他是二十世纪最伟大的哲学家。他当然这么认为。圈子里的成员对他唯一的一本书《逻辑哲学论》着迷不已，这是一系列合乎逻辑的宣言，一场辩论，每个短语都没有解释或辩护，读起来就像是用韵律写的，但是一种随机节拍。Circle 的成员逐句阅读了《逻辑哲学论》。第二次阅读花了将近一年的时间。

It is no surprise that in his review of the trajectory that brought him here, there are many images of Wittgenstein. The man mesmerizes anyone who comes near him, and he mesmerized Moritz. Wittgenstein is a philosopher, a great philosopher, and progeny of one of the most extravagantly wealthy and cultured families in Vienna, in fact, in all of Europe. Some people say he is the greatest philosopher of the twentieth century. He certainly thinks so. Members of the Circle obsess over his only book, the Tractatus Logico-Philosophicus, a series of logical proclamations, a polemic, each phrase exuded without explanation or defense so that it reads as though written in meter but a kind of stochastic meter. Sentence by sentence the members of the Circle went through the Tractatus. The second time took nearly a year.

尽管编号系统赋予文本以圣经的特质，但该文件始终缺乏连贯性。但仔细阅读后，他们开始逐一被这本书所打动，然后逐渐被他的想法所打动，直到他的想法成为他们思想的中心。他是一个罕见而令人陶醉的人，他远远地统治着他们，几乎完全不感兴趣。他从不来约瑟夫咖啡馆，也许这只会加剧他们对他的痴迷，这种强烈的欲望源于单相思。

Despite the implications of a numbering system that lends a biblical quality to the text, the document persistently lacks cohesion. But on closer reading the book impresses them one by one at first and then handful by handful until his ideas sit very near the epicenter of their thinking. A man with a rare and intoxicating personality, he rules them from afar and with near complete disinterest. He never comes to the Café Josephinum, perhaps only heightening their obsession with him, the intense desire fed on unrequited love.

莫里茨是维特根斯坦唯一同意亲自见面的人。他们第一次见面是在玛格丽特的家里，她是维特根斯坦八个兄弟姐妹之一，后来由于自杀，他们只剩下五个。在那里，他痴迷地为她建造位于昆德曼街的房子。一开始，维特根斯坦只是弯腰站在房间一角测量衣服的身影。有一秒钟，他只是一个人。但随后，他伸展开来，扭动身体，向前冲去，但实际上并没有动。他用眼睛冲过去。他看起来和莫里茨见过的任何人都不一样。正直的鼻子，哥特式的眼睛，一头卷曲的硬发——明亮、敏锐、富有感染力。他似乎一直处于电击状态。整体效果是把原本才华横溢的人——包括莫里茨——变成了狂热的、不受欢迎的使徒。在莫里茨脑海中维特根斯坦的所有形象中，他们第一次面对面站在一起的那一刻是最明亮的。

Moritz is the only one Wittgenstein actually agrees to see in person. Their first meeting occurred at the home of Margarete, one of Wittgenstein's eight siblings, though suicide would eventually reduce their numbers to five. There he labored obsessively on the construction of her house in Kundmanngasse. First there was just the shape of Wittgenstein bent over a corner of the room, measuring a fitting. For a second he was just a man. But then he unfurled and twisted and lunged without actually moving. He lunged with his eyes. He looked unlike anyone Moritz had ever seen. The righteous nose, the gothic eyes, the frisson of wiry hair—bright, searching, and infectious. He seemed to be in a perpetual state of electrocution. The overall effect was to roast otherwise brilliant people—including Moritz—into fanatical, unwanted apostles. Of all the pictures of Wittgenstein in Moritz's mind, that moment they first stood face to face is the brightest.

在他们初次见面的那天晚上，莫里茨入睡时欣喜若狂，仿佛仍因救世主的炽热光芒而感到兴奋。第二天早上，莫里茨一气呵成地从床上起身，穿上衣服，度过了一天，走过街道，进入星期四晚上，大步走进约瑟夫咖啡馆，而他的嘴里还念念不忘一句话，即《逻辑哲学论》的第一行：

As he slipped off to sleep the night of their initial meeting, Moritz was ecstatic, as though still glowing from the white-hot intensity of the full fire of the savior himself. As if in one motion Moritz rose from bed the next morning, stepped into his clothes and past the day, down the street, into Thursday evening and strode into the Café Josephinum while one sentence seared his mouth, the first line of the Tractatus:

1. 世间万物皆如此。

1. The world is all that is the case.

在咖啡馆的喧闹声中，莫里茨在他的圈子里作证，在一种异常的讽刺和蔑视的驱使下，他挣脱了德国形而上学的枷锁，撕碎了“绝对”、“精神”和“上帝”等概念，看着它们蒸发后落地。信仰、神秘主义——这些想法并不假。它们毫无意义。毫无意义的陈述争夺真理的地位。可悲的污染物污染了人们的心灵。一旦斗篷被撕掉，几乎不需要解剖；但他还是进行了解剖，猛击这些有影响力的词语，把它们打成毫无生气的浆糊。幻想和自欺欺人已经一去不复返了；所以几年后的一个星期四晚上，他们在这里，被他们的胜利和莫里茨的残酷所震撼和恐惧。不管是好是坏，他们都必须艰难前行。

In the commotion of the café, with his Circle to bear witness, Moritz, animated by an aberrant sarcasm and contempt, tore off the yoke of German metaphysics, ripping down notions like “The Absolute,” “Spirit,” and “God” and watched them vaporize before hitting the ground. Faith, Mysticism—it's not that these ideas a re false. They are meaningless. Meaningless statements vying for the status of Truth. Pathetic contaminants fouling people's minds. A dissection was hardly needed once the cloak was ripped away; but he provided one anyway, bludgeoning the influential words, beating them into a lifeless pulp. There was no turning back to illusion and self-deception; and so here they are, a few years later, on a Thursday evening, charged and terrified by their victory, by Moritz's brutality. For better or worse, they have to trudge forward.

这些图像闪过，是一部由几帧不连贯的视频组成，最后一帧是莫里茨开始讨论世界事实、维特根斯坦和真理时此刻的粗略勾勒。

These images flicker past, a choppy movie of a few frames with the last one a crude sketch of this very moment as Moritz opens the table to discussion of facts of the world, of Wittgenstein, of Truth.

但这就是科特需要来这里的原因。他必须和莫里茨谈谈，莫里茨把他们聚集在一起，创造了这个他可以归属于的地方。他的心在抽搐。他的头脑在抽搐。他仍然能尝到的毒药刺痛了他肿胀的舌头。那些鬼魂。那些幻象。这就是他必须告诉莫里茨的：世界并非全部都是那样。

But this is why Kurt needs to be here. He must speak to Moritz, who brings them all together, who creates this place in which he can belong. His heart cramps. His mind cramps. The poison he can still taste pricks his swollen tongue. The ghosts. The visions. This is what he must tell Moritz, this: The world is not all that is the case.

昨天晚上 5:02，库尔特约见了一位通灵者，一位吉普赛人，一位灵媒——一位坐在一张非常古老的红色椅子上的老妇人。这些自称吉普赛人的人最近像色彩鲜艳的树叶一样飘进维也纳。他们安顿在角落里，成群结队地在城市里四处游荡。通灵者的数量之多引起了大学教授组织的一项合法研究的注意。这些罗马尼亚游牧民族虽然有贵族和失落帝国的故事，但他们根本不是埃及后裔，他们声称自己拥有魔法饰品和超感知觉。魔法和唯心论是理性思考的敌人，因此他们宣称自己是莫里茨的敌人。但诚实的扭曲说服了一些学者参加一两次降神会，尽可能开放地接受对过程的公正评价。他们说服自己接受这个简单的论点：如果只有一个人拥有嗅觉和如果他能从砖墙的另一边探测到一片薰衣草园，其他人都会对他的超感知能力感到惊讶，但这根本不涉及任何魔法，只是空气中的分子被带到鼻腔细胞。只是基本的物理、化学和解剖学。如果有一个物理过程在起作用，允许一些增强的感知，他们会尽力评估它们。库尔特加入了最早的一些邀请，为灵媒的说法作证。随着证据的积累证实了其他人对骗局的怀疑，与此形成鲜明对比的是，库尔特完全相信表演是真实的。从那时起，他就成了城里各种灵媒的偶尔赞助人。

At 5:02 yesterday evening, Kurt kept an appointment with a clairvoyant, a Gypsy, a medium—a very old woman in a very old red chair. The self-proclaimed Gypsies have recently wafted into Vienna like brightly colored leaves. They settled in nooks and corners, raked into groups that drift around the city in clusters. The sheer number of clairvoyants drew the attention of a legitimate study organized by professors at the university. The Romanian nomads, who are not at all of Egyptian descent despite stories of nobility and lost empires, bring claims of magic trinkets and extrasensory perception. Magic and spiritualism are the enemies of rational thinking and thereby have declared themselves Moritz's enemy. But a perversion of honesty persuaded some scholars to attend a séance or two with as open a mind to the fair evaluation of the proceedings as they could muster. They persuaded themselves to go with this simple argument: If only one man possessed the sense of smell and could thus detect a garden of lavender from the far side of a brick wall, all others would be amazed by his extrasensory perception, yet no magic would be involved whatsoever, just molecules carried on the air to the cells of the nose. Just basic physics, chemistry, and anatomy. If there was a physical process at work allowing some heightened perceptions, they would do their best to evaluate them. Kurt joined some of the earliest invitations to bear witness to the claims of a medium. As the evidence accumulated to confirm the others’ suspicions of a hoax, in perfect contrast Kurt was completely convinced that the performance was real. Ever since, he has become an occasional patron of the various psychics around the city.

他觉得这些拜访有点不愉快，但却是必要的，就像去看医生一样。消息并不总是好的。昨晚的约会是他第一次与自称吉普赛女王的人见面。她名声很好，而且年纪非常大。几乎可以预见的是，她的皮肤在厚度和颜色上都与老皮革相媲美，峡谷、褶皱和皱褶的华丽垂坠，迷宫般的线条可以用手相术的讽刺变体来解读。从这块纹理布上可以看到她那双鸟一样的眼睛，那双眼睛保持着一种宏伟的向上状态，仿佛是用镰刀的猛击雕刻而成的。厚重的圆眼睑一定曾经因年轻而肿胀，但现在却萎缩到眼球，上面是破碎的、有垛口的皮肤。他断定，她看起来像一只老熟的鸟。一只烧焦的鸟，稀疏的干灰毛代替了散落的羽毛。如果不是她那几乎是美丽的衣服——层层叠叠的布料、纯净色彩的微风——的优雅舞动，她看起来会像死了一样。

He finds these visits mildly unpleasant but necessary, much like a visit to the doctor. The news isn’t always good. Last night's appointment was his first with the self-proclaimed Gypsy Queen. She had a good reputation as well as the advantage of being incredibly old. Almost predictably her skin begged for comparisons to aged leather in thickness and color, a splendid draping of canyons and folds and crinkles, a maze of lines that could be deciphered in a sarcastic variant on the palm reader. From this textured cloth peered her birdlike eyes, which maintained a magnificent lift as though carved with the swoop of a scythe. The heavy round eyelids must once have been swollen with youth but were now shrunken to the eyeballs and topped with crumbled, crenellated skin. She looked like an old cooked bird, he decided. A burned bird with sparse patches of dry gray hair in place of stray feathers. She would have looked dead were it not for the graceful motions of her almost beautiful clothes—confused layers of fabric, a breeze of pure color.

她的小桌子中央放着一杯水，除了其狭窄的比例让它看起来像一个超大的化学烧杯外，它相当不起眼。水是这个媒介的媒介。她喜欢讲述她的一生，就像展示她的资历一样，她告诉库尔特：她出生后的第二天，她的母亲毫不留情地把她扔进一个洞里，凿开了封住巴伐利亚一个小池塘的冰层。她的母亲看到婴儿的眼睛透过水的镜片聚焦，知道她是一个chovihanis — 一个先知，一个女巫。冰冷的水想在她刚出生的皮肤上变硬，但她被拽了出来，擦干，包在母亲的胸前。如果她活了下来，她很坚强。如果她死了，她很虚弱，不用说，太虚弱了。她通过了这项测试和许多其他测试。小时候，水魔与她做爱，附身成一个丑陋的叔叔，在清澈的浴缸里强奸了她。他笨拙地将她的脸按入水中，透过透明的薄膜，她看到了恶魔灵魂上的黑色印记。她当时就知道自己被选中了。她是一个预言家，一个女巫——一个乔维哈尼斯。近一个世纪后，她已经完美地运用了薄薄的水，这是她神秘的光学仪器，液体的厚度与冰层相符，在她漫长生命的第二天，她接受了水的考验，那层冰水将她盲目的新生眼睛与上方的空气隔开。在向他解释了精心测量的体积后，她观察了库尔特·哥德尔的扭曲，他的黑色护目镜模糊不清，他的身体在水中倒映成一条细丝。然后，她通过从起伏的图像中读出他的命运来吓唬他。

At the centerpiece of her small table was a glass of water, rather unspectacular except for its narrow proportions that gave it the appearance of an oversized chemist's beaker. Water was this medium's medium. She liked to tell the story of her life as though presenting her credentials, and she told it to Kurt: The day after her birth, her mother plunged her without remorse in a hole, chipping open the crust of ice sealing a small pond in Bavaria. Her mother saw the infant's eyes focus through the lens of water and knew she was a chovihanis—a seer, a witch. The icy water wanted to harden onto her newborn skin but she was yanked out, dried, and wrapped to her mother's breast. If she survived, she was strong. If she died, she was weak, too weak, needless to say. This test she passed and many others. As a child the water demon made love to her, possessing the form of an ugly uncle and raping her in a clear bath. He pushed her face below the water in his clumsy assault and through the transparent film she saw the black marks on the demon's soul. She knew then that she had been chosen. She was a seer, a witch— a chovihanis. Nearly a century later she has perfected the use of the thin volume of water that was her mystical, optical instrument, the liquid's thickness measured against the layer of icy water that separated her blind newborn eyes from the air above in her trial by water on the second day of her long life. And thus having explained to him the carefully measured volume, she examined the distortions of Kurt Gödel, his black goggles blurred, his body a thin filament reflected in the water. She then terrorized him by reading his fortune in the undulating image.

做完后，吉普赛人把玻璃管压扁了。一滩水里，鲜艳的色彩渗入了波西米亚挂毯覆盖着被脚啃过的地板，地板的木板就像被侵蚀的骨头碎片。地毯的颜色变化很快，仿佛经历了化学变色反应，直到沾满污渍的布似乎从破碎的玻璃中溢出，形成一滩鲜艳的蓝色。他没有等待确认，这是一个病态的预感，一个真正的不幸。

When she was done, the Gypsy crushed the glass tube. From the pool of water a vivid color bled into the Bohemian tapestry covering the foot-chewed floor, with its planks like splinters of eroded bone. The rug rushed with hues as though enduring a chemical color reaction until the stained cloth seemed to spill from the broken glass, a puddle a vibrant hue of blue. He did not wait for confirmation that this was a morbid premonition, a real misfortune.

他从房间里跌落到从四面八方涌来的雨中。与通常均匀倾斜的雨水不同，雨水变成了一道道交叉的雨流，使场景变得模糊不清，哥德尔也溶解在颗粒状的溶液中。吉普赛人默默地看着，当晚发生的事情令他惊讶不已，哥德尔被冲到大街上——一缕光亮、一个幽灵、一个鬼魂。

He fell from the room into the rain that came from all directions. Defying the ordinarily uniform slant, it was a flurry of crosshatched streams that pixilated the scene and dissolved Gödel in the grainy solution. The Gypsy watched mute, endlessly surprised by the evening's events as Gödel was swept along the Strasse—a mere wisp, an apparition, a ghost.

当阿黛尔来到他家门口时，她发现他正在雨中等她。他苍白的气息让她推迟了自己在夜总会的报道。在她收集煤炭、点燃炉子、煮汤之前，阿黛尔引导他进了屋。她在那里听着，嘴唇张开，露出了上排门牙上一层蜡质的口红，她用她那异常火热的手揉捏着他被雨水浸湿的指关节的冰冷疼痛。

When Adele arrived at his door, she found him waiting for her in the rain. His pale tincture convinced her to postpone her own report from the nightclub. Before she collected the coal, before she lit the furnaces, and before she cooked the soup, Adele guided him inside. There she listened with lips parted to reveal a waxy smear of lipstick on her top front teeth, as she kneaded the cold ache from his rain-drenched knuckles with her improbably hot hands.

他的眼镜上沾满了水珠。水珠折射出所有打在他眼镜上的图像，形成一个融化的万花筒。他想让世界恢复秩序，在阿黛尔耐心的注视下小心翼翼地移动。他试图用一只空着的手把头发梳回原位，以恢复他平时浓密光滑的头顶，但浸满水的发丝汇合成宽而扁平的带状，沉重地垂下，在一侧形成深深的分界线。

His glasses beaded with water. Liquid pebbles refracted all images that struck his spectacles to create a melted kaleidoscope. Wanting to restore order to the world, he moved cautiously under Adele's patient attention. He tried to scoop his hair back into place with his one free hand to reproduce his usual thick, smooth dome but the waterlogged strands merged in wide flat bands and fell heavily, creating a deep part down one side.

“这个世界超越了这个房间，阿黛尔。维也纳的街道，更远的欧洲，更远的太空中围绕着宇宙中的一颗恒星运转的地球。但我怎么才能确定呢？我现在和你说话的时候，看不到地球绕着轴旋转。我怎么能确定呢？我可以确定，因为它是合乎逻辑的；数学是合理的，行星的轨道也尊重数学。我可以验证它是真的，不是通过看，而是通过思考。

“This world extends beyond this room, Adele. There are the streets of Vienna and beyond that Europe and beyond that a globe in space in orbit around a star in a universe. But how do I know that for sure? I cannot see the globe spinning on its axis right now as I speak to you. How can I be sure? I can be sure because it's logical; the mathematics is sound and respected by the orbits of the planets. I can verify it's true, not by looking at it, but by thinking about it.

“我也看不见鬼魂，阿黛尔。我看不见他们。但吉普赛人透过水的镜片看到了我，看到了我身后，她看到了他们，阿黛尔。我没有产生幻觉。我如何区分幻觉和现实？我知道。不真实的虚构不符合逻辑原则。

“I also cannot see ghosts, Adele. I cannot see them. But the Gypsy saw through the lens of water into me and past me and she saw them, Adele. I am not hallucinating. How do I distinguish a hallucination from reality? I know how. Unreal figments do not adhere to the principles of logic.

“这就是这个世界。肉体和空气的结合。它们混杂在一起，真是难以驾驭。公平地说，阿黛尔，公平地说，区分真实与虚假并不总是那么容易。但这个世界之外还有另一个世界。”说到这里，他的护目镜冒出蒸汽，他自己的眼睛里充满了咸咸的鹅卵石，在睫毛上结成了水珠。“那里有另一个纯粹逻辑的世界。那里没有颗粒、沙砾、污垢或毒药。那里有完美的三角形，π，数字 1，不可能混淆真实与想象。我通过勤奋的内省到达那里。我了解这个世界，阿黛尔。我通过直接体验了解它。我可以通过思考在任何一天的任何一分钟到达那里。我的思想接触到它，这个完美无瑕的现实无法欺骗。”然后他公开地、无力地哭了起来。一个悲伤的孩子。他的脊柱呈现出优美的曲线，从木椅开始一直延伸到深深的弯腰，直到他的头发垂向地面，搔痒着他们紧握的双手，水顺着掌心的缝隙缓缓滴落。

“That is this world. Figures of flesh and figures of air. It is unruly how they mingle and in fairness, Adele, in fairness, it is not always so easy to distinguish what is real from what is not. But beyond this world is another.” With this his goggles steamed and his own eyes stormed with salty pebbles that beaded on his lashes. “There is another world of pure logic. There are no particles or grit or dirt or poison. There are perfect triangles, π, the number one, and it's impossible to confuse the real with the imagined. I get there through diligent introspection. I know this world, Adele. I know it through direct experience. I can go there any minute of any day by thinking. My mind touches it, this flawless reality incapable of deception.” And then he wept openly, limply. A sad child. His spine a fine curve beginning on the wooden chair tracing around a deep bend until his hair fell toward the earth and tickled their clasped hands, sluggishly dripping water along the seam between their palms.

她把他的头抬到她的胸前，抱着他。他的脸颊和额头紧贴着她的身体，让她想起他其实只是个男孩。当他沉入她体内时，他说：“当我死去时，我们必须记住我的灵魂将永存。即使我在转世中发现我仍然处于部分真相和幻象的混乱之中，我至少会更接近那个完美的现实。当我一次又一次死去时，我们必须记住，最终我会到达那里，到达那个纯洁、完美的地方。”

Lifting his head to her chest she cradled him. The angle of his cheeks and the swell of his forehead against her body reminded her that he was just a boy really. As he sank into her, he said, “When I die, we must remember my soul will survive. Even if I find in my reincarnation that I am still in this muddle of partial truths and phantoms, I will at least be closer to that perfect reality. And when I die again and again, we must remember that eventually I will get there, to that pure, flawless place.”

为了让他感觉好些，阿黛尔唱了一首温柔的摇篮曲，略微跑调、节奏不对，就像一个慢慢停下的美丽音乐盒。

To help him feel better, Adele sang a tender lullaby, slightly off-key and off-tempo, like a pretty music box winding down.

多塞特，1930 年

DORSET, 1930

克里斯的颈部和胸部病变恶化。淋巴结肿大，大肿块充血，钙化，乳糜状脓液几乎要爆裂。当他发烧转为寒战，失眠转为精神错乱时，他被家主紧急送往伦敦的一家医院。进行了手术以切除发炎的组织。这不是他的第一次手术，也不是最后一次——手术将在两天内进行。医生无法确定是原有的结核病、新发感染，还是切除过多组织的受损残留物杀死了他。但住院第六天，疼痛随着呼吸停止时，他没有惊讶，而是感到无法抑制的遗憾和一丝轻松。

Lesions have festered in Chris's neck and chest. Tubercles rotting his lymph nodes, large nodules engorged by a calcified, cheesy pus near to bursting. When his fever gave way to chills and his insomnia gave way not to sleep but to delirium, he was rushed, by the master of his house, to a hospital in London. Surgery was performed to harvest the inflamed tissue. Not his first surgery, nor his last—that was to come within two days. The doctors couldn’t know if it was the original tuberculosis, a fresh infection, or the compromised remains of overharvested tissue that killed him. But when the pain stopped along with his breath on the sixth day of his hospitalization there was no surprise, an irrepressible regret, and the faintest admission of relief.

自从艾伦捡起地板上被蓝色溶液弄脏的碎玻璃以来，两年过去了，他的焦虑情绪时而高涨时而平息。有时，他极度的沮丧突然被喜悦驱散。但总体而言，阴郁感越来越强烈，他无法否认，在半夜，可能就是克里斯衰弱的那一刻，他透过窗户的棱镜，看着月亮落在朋友的宿舍上空。他不安地想知道自己是否再也见不到克里斯那张漂亮的脸了。当克里斯的死讯传到艾伦的耳朵里时，他的恐惧像克里斯的感染一样可怕地爆发了。他惊呆了。他无法控制自己的脸或身体移动。他僵住了，深深地盯着带来消息的初级舍监，那个男孩感觉自己的身体被入侵了，努力抑制着把艾伦推开的冲动。

In the two years since Alan had collected the broken glass from the blue solution that stained his floor, his anxiety distended and subsided in alternating currents. There were moments of utter desolation suddenly dispelled by joy. But overall the gloom grew, and he could not deny that in the middle of the night, possibly the very moment of Chris's decline, he watched the moon set over his friend's dormitory through the prism of his window. He wondered with unease if he would never see Chris's pretty face again. Alan's dread burst as gruesomely as Chris's infection when the statement of his death touched his ears. He was petrified with shock. He couldn’t command his face or body to move. Frozen, he stared so deeply through the junior housemaster who brought the news, that the boy felt the very matter of his body invaded and struggled to stifle the urge to shove Alan away.

葬礼在 1930 年 2 月 15 日星期六清晨举行，他没有被邀请参加。黑暗中，他跪在光秃秃的、被大火烧毁的窗台下，将额头贴在冰冷的隔板上。他的睫毛轻拍着玻璃，鼻子在窗户上形成两滩蒸发的水雾。艾伦试图捕捉那些他只能勉强看见的星星，它们在视野边缘摇晃，但当他的瞳孔朝它们的方向猛地一扫时，它们就消失了。克里斯曾抓住艾伦的手，把他从图书馆的复习中拉出来，拖到黑暗的草坪中央，向他展示这个最暗淡的天体的难以捉摸的特征。

The funeral, to which he is not invited, is early Saturday morning, February 15, 1930. He kneels in the dark below his bare, fire-damaged windowsill and presses his forehead to the cold partition. His lashes tap at the glass as his nose fogs the window with two evaporating puddles. Alan tries to catch the stars that he can only barely see wobbling on the periphery of his vision, but they disappear when his pupils dart in their direction. Chris once grasped Alan's hand and dragged him away from their revisions in the library, dragged him out into the middle of the dark lawn to show him this elusive character of the faintest celestial objects.

在黎明前渐弱的黑暗中，星星顽强地闪耀了几分钟，然后升起的太阳的光芒将它们熄灭。它们好像消失了。但艾伦知道它们还在那里，在地平线上闪闪发光的黄色火球的映衬下徒劳地散发着光芒。这是一场天文葬礼。克里斯走了，但他好像还在这里。艾伦感觉到他在新的一天的光芒映衬下无形地散发着光芒。

In the weakening dark before dawn, the stars shine defiantly for a few minutes before the blanket of the rising sun's light snuffs them out. It is as if they are gone. But Alan knows they are still there, radiating in vain against the glowing yellow fireball on the horizon. It is an astronomical funeral procession. Chris is gone, but it is as if he is still here. Alan feels him radiating invisibly against the blaze of a new day.

维也纳，1931 年

VIENNA, 1931

哥德尔感觉自己被困在了这一刻。星期四。他把手放在门上。他看到自己眼睛里的蓝色在玻璃中渐渐褪去。他在外面看着里面向外看的男人。他通过空气、声音和灯光感受到咖啡的味道。他坐在圆圈边缘的一张椅子上，靠近一个摊位。莫里茨在一张原本是圆形的桌子上创造了一个尖顶。它们是一圈天体，相对于遥远的恒星旋转。它们围绕着一个可识别的真理中心旋转，这个中心似乎近在咫尺，就在它们面前，但却遥不可及，就像天空无限远处的一颗星星，就像一颗它们几乎可以分辨但又悄然溜走的星星。

Gödel feels stuck in this moment. Thursday. His hand on the door. He sees the blue of his own eyes attenuated in the glass. He is outside looking in at a man inside looking out. He takes in the taste of the coffee through the air and then the sounds and then the lights. He settles in a chair, near a booth, on the periphery of the Circle. Moritz creates a pinnacle at an otherwise round table. They are a ring of celestial bodies, rotating with respect to the distant stars. They orbit around an identifiable epicenter of truth, the epicenter seemingly near at hand, just there in front of each of them, but unreachably far away like a star in the infinitely far surface of the sky, like a star that they can almost resolve but then slips away.

科特穿着外套，毛皮领子不像他希望的那样保暖。寒冷刺痛着他的骨髓。他跛脚的心脏无法维持正常的血液循环，所以他从血管向外感到寒冷。咖啡温暖了他的双手，但喝下第一口时，他的胃开始抽搐，疼痛感一直持续到他腹部后部稍靠右的位置。剩下的深色啤酒原封不动地放在杯子里，与他勉强撑过来的近乎过量的泻药相得益彰。尽管阿黛尔吃得丰盛，他却瘦得惊人。“怎么，你不喜欢土豆？”她问。“怎么，你不喜欢炖菜？怎么，你不喜欢肉？”他被迫出于无奈吃东西——为了结束她对厨艺的质问，当然，也是为了让她感觉良好。尽管如此，包括衣服和眼镜在内，他的体重加起来刚刚超过 100 磅。他把这个秘密藏在大衣下面。

Kurt wears his coat, the fur collar not as insulating as he would like. The cold aches through to his marrow. His lame heart is unable to sustain proper circulation, so that he is chilled from the vessels outward. The coffee warms his hands, but at the first sip his stomach convulsed with that habitual pain high in the back of his gut, slightly to the right. The rest of the dark brew sits untouched in its cup, an unhappy complement to the near overdose of laxatives he has managed to survive. He is appallingly thin despite Adele's bounteous production of food. “What, you don’t like the potatoes?” she asks. “What, you don’t like the stew? What, you don’t like the meat?” He is driven to eat out of exasperation—to put an end to the interrogation over her cooking, and, of course, to make her feel good. Still, his combined weight, including clothes and glasses, is just over one hundred pounds. He keeps this secret beneath his overcoat.

从科特对阿黛尔说完最后一句话（听不清的再见）到今晚在圈子里说完第一句话（礼貌的问候），他已经沉默了二十个小时。当他打断讨论的准备工作来对莫里茨讲话时，他的声音虽然很少使用，但出奇地清晰。“我更多地考虑了说谎者悖论，考虑了说‘这句话是假的’的说谎者。”

Kurt has been silent for the twenty hours since his latest words (an inaudible good-bye) to Adele until his first words (a polite salutation) in the Circle tonight. His voice is surprisingly clear despite disuse when he interrupts the preliminaries of the discussion to address Moritz. “I have thought more about the Liar's Paradox, about the liar who says, This statement is false.”

莫里茨似乎没有听见，他继续坐下来，向他的朋友奥托·纽赖特打招呼。奥托是个大人物，有远大的理想，也有宏大的嗓门来传播这些理想——一个魁梧、迷人、热情但令人生畏的理想主义者。他在柏林短暂服刑后来到维也纳，这次服刑是为了让他对自己继续反政府的煽动有更好的认识。莫里茨的善意问候，无疑伴随着他对维特根斯坦的一贯批评，奥托却猛然回击，莫里茨假装恼怒地捂住耳朵，对奥托的坚持感到好笑。尽管奥托没有耐心抑制自己的嘲讽，但他确实听到了库尔特试图打断他们的谈话。奥托仍然摇着头，脆弱的头发末端颤动着，他试图没有特定的人，“撒谎者说，这是谎言。克里特人宣称所有克里特人都是撒谎者。”

Moritz appears not to hear as he continues to settle himself in and greet his friend Otto Neurath. Otto is a big man with big ideas and a big voice with which to spread them—a burly, charming, warm, but intimidating idealist. He came to Vienna after a short prison sentence in Berlin, a sentence imposed to make him think better of his continued agitation against the state. Otto pounces on Moritz's benign greeting, no doubt with his usual criticism of Wittgenstein, so that Moritz is holding his own ears, in mock annoyance, amused by Otto's persistence. Although Otto hadn’t the patience to hold back his gibes, he did hear Kurt's attempt to penetrate their conversation. Still shaking his head so the brittle ends of his hair vibrate, Otto projects to no one in particular, “The liar says, This is a lie. The Cretan declares that all Cretans are liars.”

“他们说的关于我的谎言有一半是真的，”奥尔加笑着补充道。她挽着莫里茨的胳膊走到桌子旁。奥托俯身点燃她的雪茄，然后往她的咖啡里加奶油。她没有面对科特，而是和他说话，而奥托则在她身边忙来忙去。“当我还是学生的时候，我对这些自我指涉的纠结印象太深刻了。首先是说谎者悖论。然后是理发师为那些不给自己理发的人理发。那么谁给他理发呢？包含所有不包含自身的集合的集合，等等。毫无疑问，这些无法解决的问题很有趣，但实际上无害。”

“Half the lies they tell about me are true,” Olga adds laughing. She takes Moritz's arm to find the table. Otto leans over to light her cigar and then adds cream to her coffee. She addresses Kurt without facing him while Otto fusses over her. “When I was a student, I was too impressed with those self-referential tangles. The Liar's Paradox, first. Then the barber who cuts the hair of anyone that doesn’t cut his own hair. So who cuts his? The set that contains all sets that don’t contain themselves, et cetera. These kinds of unsolvable problems are amusing, no doubt, but harmless really.”

莫里茨补充道：“如果我们认识到它们毫无意义，那就无害了。但如果一个人愚蠢到陷入它们的循环中，那就有害了。”

“Harmless if we recognize that they are utterly meaningless,” Moritz adds. “Harmful if one is fool enough to get caught up in their loops.”

科特友好地点点头，但说道：“我不同意。”

Kurt nods amiably but says, “I do not agree.”

“啊，好啊，真是个傻瓜。”奥托大声说道。

“Ah, good, a fool,” Otto booms.

莫里茨靠在椅子上，头发修剪得整整齐齐，垂在耳边和颈背上。他耐心地审视着库尔特。“说谎者悖论与世界事实不符。它毫无意义。是语言的滥用。纯粹的逻辑不可能允许任何这样的花招。没有无法解决的问题。”

Moritz leans back in his chair, his hair freshly clipped into a pristine edge above his ear and along the nape of his neck. He examines Kurt patiently. “The Liar's Paradox does not correspond to a fact about the world. It is meaningless. A misuse of language. Pure logic cannot possibly allow any such tricks. There are no unsolvable problems.”

Kurt 的思想同时涉及多个主题。当他思考得最清楚时，他经常看到大群体而不是连续的步骤。他可以逆向思考，重建一个更线性的形式逻辑论证，为了研讨会或文章的目的，一步一步地证明，从左到右逐个字母阅读，并按数字顺序交错方程列表。但这并不是他产生最美妙想法的方式。有时它们会毫无根据地出现，就像他的定理一样，它根本不是线性的。它是自指的，是一个纠结的循环。一条吞下自己尾巴的蛇。他希望他能向莫里茨展示他的结果，就像他看到的那样，他只要张开嘴，就可以让完全成形的形状伸展开来。他试图让莫里茨放心，“我知道这是一个伟大的抱负，”他停下来又开始说，“但有些数学问题无法解决。数字中的事实永远无法证明是真是假。”

Kurt's thoughts touch upon several themes at once. When he is thinking most clearly he often sees things in big groups and not sequential steps. He can work backward and reconstruct a more linear formal logical argument, proving one step after the other for the purposes of a seminar or an article that is read from left to right one letter at a time staggered by a numbered list of equations. But this is not how the most beautiful ideas come to him. Sometimes they emerge whole without justification, like his theorem, which is not at all linear. It is self-referential, a tangled loop. A serpent swallowing its own tale. He wishes he could present his result to Moritz as it appears to him, that he could just open his mouth and have the fully formed shape stretch out. He tries to reassure Moritz, “I realize it is the great ambition,” he stops and starts again, “But there are unsolvable mathematical problems. Facts among the numbers that can never be proven true or false.”

奥尔加尤其感到好奇。她第一次认识库尔特是通过她的哥哥，她的哥哥是数学家，也是大学的教授。他指导哥德尔学习，并把他带入了圈子。她的哥哥被这个几乎沉默寡言、极其努力的学生迷住了，他显然具有才华横溢的潜力。奥尔加经常被要求审查学生的作品，或者听取争论并寻找缺陷，所以她被要求听库尔特说话。她立刻对他产生了兴趣，尽管他们最初的几次见面很奇怪——一个盲人女人和一个沉默寡言的男人。可以肯定的是，交流很少，但无论说什么都让她印象深刻，有时甚至令人震惊。不久之后，库尔特和她说话就更自然了，两人结下了友谊。奥尔加比其他任何人都清楚，库尔特说话要么极其精确，要么根本不说话。他的措辞和解释总是相当直白。所以他不同寻常的、有点不精确的说法引起了她的注意。她也学会了留意他说的任何话，不管这给人留下的第一印象有多奇怪。她发现，他的一些最深刻、最有趣的想法创造了一个复杂的雕塑形象。它们的价值和意义只有付出一些努力才能显现出来。她一只手摸索着金属托盘，另一只手把烟灰拍进碗里，同时要求澄清。“说谎者悖论是错误使用词语的结果。它不是真的。”

Olga in particular is piqued. She first met Kurt through her brother, a mathematician and professor at the university. He advised Gödel in his studies and brought him into the fold. Her brother was fascinated by this nearly silent, intensely hardworking student whose potential for brilliance was evident. Olga was often asked to vet a student's work or to hear out an argument and search for flaws, so she was asked to listen to Kurt. She immediately took an interest in him although their first few meetings were odd—a blind woman and a silent man. Communication was minimal, to be certain, but whatever was said struck her as sharp and at times even stunning. Before long, Kurt spoke more spontaneously with her and a friendship was forged. Olga, better than any of the others, knows that it is Kurt's custom to speak extremely precisely or not at all. He is always quite literal in both his phrasing and his interpretation. So his uncharacteristic, somewhat imprecisely stated claim catches her attention. She has also learned to pay heed to anything he might say, no matter how odd a first impression it might leave. She has found that some of his deepest, most intriguing ideas create a complex sculptural image. Their value and meaning can be seen only with some effort. She feels for the metal tray with one hand and taps her ash into its bowl with the other while pressing for some clarification. “The Liar's Paradox is a consequence of wrongly used words. It isn’t real.”

莫里茨打断道，手放在心上，仿佛在宣誓效忠，“纯粹的逻辑中不会有这样的混乱。能说的都会说清楚。正如维特根斯坦恳求我们的那样，我们不能说的，我们必须保持沉默。《逻辑哲学论》第 7 章， ”他重复道。“我们不能说的，我们必须保持沉默。”

Moritz interrupts with his hand stretched over his heart as though swearing allegiance, “There can be no such confusions in pure logic. What can be said will be said clearly. As Wittgenstein implores us, what we cannot speak of we must pass over in silence. Tractatus 7,” he repeats. “What we cannot speak of we must pass over in silence.”

一名新成员穿着白衬衫，没有打领带，这种风格在年轻成员中像流感一样蔓延开来。他用拳头敲着桌子表示同意，其他人则敲着椅子的木头。莫里茨甚至有点被维特根斯坦思想的火焰所震撼，尽管他保持着自己的外在身份和正式着装，并为此感到自豪。他发现自己将自己确信是自己的想法归功于维特根斯坦，这些想法是他在昆德曼加斯那次决定性的会议之前形成的。他引用了《逻辑哲学论》第一卷：“世界就是一切事物。《逻辑哲学论》第一卷第一节，世界是事实的总和。”

One of the new recruits, wearing—in the style of Wittgenstein that has spread among the younger members like a flu—a white shirt, no tie, knocks a fist on the table to concur as others rap on the wood of their chairs. Even Moritz is melting slightly from the inferno of Wittgenstein's ideas, although he maintains his own outward identity, and formal attire, proudly enough. He has caught himself attributing to Wittgenstein ideas that he is sure were really his own, thoughts he had formulated before that fateful meeting at Kundmanngasse. “Tractatus 1,” he quotes: “The world is all that is the case. Tractatus 1.1, The world is the totality of facts.”

之前的每个星期四，库尔特都是一个沉默的旁观者。今晚，他从一个人看向另一个人，等待着合适的机会。机会来了又去，他的情绪也随之波动，直到他抛出一个他知道他们已经问过自己一千遍的问题。“你如何认识世界的事实？”

On every previous Thursday, Kurt has been a silent spectator. Tonight he looks from one person to another as he waits for the right opportunity. His temperature fluctuates while openings come and go until he throws out a question he knows they have asked themselves a thousand times. “How do you recognize a fact of the world?”

莫里茨笑了，但并不粗鲁，他点了点头，这让他放松了下来头发刚从正确位置稍微偏离，他就停了下来，看到库尔特严肃的表情，他有点为自己的反应感到抱歉。“这是一个公平的问题，”他承认道。“我如何验证一个世界事实？”这么简单的问题。他甚至无法回答这个简单的问题。尽管莫里茨宣称，但他知道有些事情是错误的。无论他多么自律地坚持逻辑，他都无法理解一种验证世界事实的方法。他得出的定义越来越狭隘，神奇地让他远离了清晰。理性思维的螺旋使他更接近理解，却又令人失望地解开了遥远的领域。莫里茨伸手去拿咖啡时，动作非常缓慢，在他看来动作很均匀，透视是望远镜。他的手指握住杯子，感觉到热气。他把杯子拉到脸上，看到了黑色的液体。“我怎么知道这个杯子存在？我不知道，”他对自己承认。“我不知道。”

Moritz laughs, but not rudely, and nods, which loosens his hair only marginally from its proper place before he stops himself, slightly sorry for his reaction as he takes in Kurt's serious expression. “It is a fair question,” he confesses. “How do I verify a fact of the world?” Such a simple question. He cannot even answer this simple question. Despite his proclamations, Moritz knows something is wrong. No matter how disciplined he is in his adherence to logic, he cannot make sense of a method to verify facts of the world. He comes to ever narrowing definitions that magically take him farther from clarity. Spirals of rational thinking thread him closer to understanding only to unravel disappointingly far a field. As Moritz reaches for his coffee his motion is very slow, and it seems so even to him, the perspective telescopic. His fingers surround the cup and feel the heat. He pulls the cup to his face and sees the dark liquid. “How do I know this cup exists? I don’t,” he admits to himself. “I don’t.”

说实话，他可以肯定只有他看到了。他可以肯定只有他触到了。他看着奥尔加抽着一支巨大的雪茄。她总是一副平静的样子，总是很放松。烟雾飘散成卷曲的缕缕，从她的睫毛间穿过。她似乎并不介意，甚至倾向于将燃烧的余烬垂直地放在眼睛附近，这让她感到不舒服。她的头发松散地聚集在颈背上，凌乱的框架衬托着她那双又大又宽的破碎的眼睛。

Being honest he can be sure only he sees. He can be sure only he touches. He watches Olga pull on a mammoth cigar. She has a calm about her, always at ease. The smoke drifts in curly plumes sifting through her lashes. She doesn’t seem to mind and even tends to hold the burning cinder vertically and uncomfortably close to her eyes. Her hair is collected loosely at the nape of her neck, a rumpled frame for her big and broad broken eyes.

她看不见雪茄。她说手指间有一支雪茄是什么意思？这句话的意思是，她感觉到了塞满烟草的包装纸。她尝到了汁液和烟雾。她感觉到了。它存在吗？这不是一个有意义的问题。

She cannot see the cigar. What does it mean for her to say there is a cigar between her fingers? The meaning of the statement is that she feels the tobacco-stuffed wrapping. She tastes the juice and smoke. She senses it. Does it exist? That is not a meaningful question.

但真正吸引莫里茨的是，是什么让他的手指冰冷的手握着杯子，咖啡悬浮在下巴附近，他问的是：奥尔加存在吗？他似乎在那里呆了很长时间。谈话停滞了，与咖啡一起停滞了。

But what really arrests Moritz, what keeps his fingers in a frozen clutch around the cup, coffee suspended near his chin, is this question: Does Olga exist? He hangs there for what seems like a very long while. The conversation stalls, suspended along with the coffee.

“奥尔加？”

“Olga?”

“是的，莫里茨。我在这里。”

“Yes, Moritz. I’m here.”

她伸出手，用食指勾住他的大拇指。其余手指也伸过去握住他的手。但莫里茨只承认，他能感觉到他所知道的压力，他知道那只手是他的。

She reaches over and hooks his thumb with her forefinger. The rest of her fingers scramble over to clasp his hand. But all Moritz concedes is that he can feel what he has learned to describe as pressure on what he believes to be his hand.

奥托占据了哥德尔右边的空间。他全身浸满红色——红色的胡子、头发和脸颊——这种颜色给人一种他永远处于红肿状态的印象。他身材高大，像个大山一样。他的胡子干枯而杂乱，从下巴一直延伸到很远的地方，形成了一个长长的网状结构。胡子的天然红色使他的整个形象都显得火热，这是他喜欢的活力。他确实在炫耀自己的力量，但不是隐喻。他用手臂敲打桌子以示强调，并用全身的力量来支持他洪亮的笑声。为了表彰他强大的气度，他在信的结尾画了一头大象来代替签名。给他夸张的气度注入活力所需的丰富燃料部分来自深刻的道德和政治信念。他确实背负着沉重的原则，仿佛这些思想本身已被吸收并转化为他的身体。

Otto occupies the space to Gödel's right. He is doused in red— red beard, hair, and cheeks—a coloring that gives the impression that he is perpetually inflamed. He is a mountainous man of impressive physical stature. His beard grows in a dry and unruly tangle, a long web woven far out from his chin. The beard's natural red stain adds a fiery hue to his whole presence, a verve that he enjoys. He throws his weight around literally, but not metaphorically. He bangs his arms on the table for emphasis and backs up his resonant laugh with all his mass. In recognition of his formidable bearing, he draws an elephant to conclude his letters in lieu of his signature. The abundant fuel needed to energize his exaggerated bearing comes in part from deep moral and political convictions. He is literally heavy with principles as though the ideas themselves had been ingested and converted to the stuff of his body.

奥托的第一任妻子安娜·沙皮尔在生下他们的儿子时去世。如果他们允许，他会在悲痛中吞噬她。他会一把抓住她，生吃她的肌肉、脂肪和骨头。他会拒绝吐出她的一丁点肉。他会紧紧抓住她的肉体，将她永远储存在脂肪和腺体中。事实上，他被蛮力所束缚；需要几个男人和女人才能哄骗他。所以他吞噬了她的理想——她的女权主义、她的社会批评、她对政治变革的愿景。

Otto's first wife, Anna Shapire, died giving birth to their son. In his grief he would have consumed her if they had let him. He would have grabbed her by the handfuls and eaten her raw— muscle, fat, and bone. He would have refused to expel a morsel of her flesh. He would have hung on to her corporeal self, storing her in fat and glands forever. As it was he was restrained by brute force; it took several men and women to coax him down. So instead he gobbled up her ideals—her feminism, her social criticism, her visions of political change.

她能流利地说几门语言，但他无法记住，这些语言他没能消化。但他完整地吸收了她对社会和经济改革的看法，并与自己的观点保持一致，因此，当他继续担任具有社会和政治影响力的职位时，他能从自己的决定中感受到她的主动性。

Her fluency in several languages he could not retain, and those languages passed through him undigested. But her vision of social and economic reform he absorbed intact and aligned solidly along his own so that he felt her initiative in his own decisions as he went on to positions of social and political influence.

他的社会理想让他的内心焦躁不安，这种焦躁偶尔会表现为性格缺陷，削弱他丰富的智慧和魅力。在这种情况下，他似乎过于敏锐地发现良心犯罪，并且过于草率地执行判断。

His social ideals leave his large proportions restless, an agitation that occasionally manifests as a character flaw, one detraction from his generous portion of wit and charm. In those instances, he seems too keen to detect crimes of conscience and too quick to execute judgment.

举个例子：奥托对维特根斯坦一直心存疑虑。他总是像舌头在寻找疼痛的牙齿一样探究《逻辑哲学论》中的几行，比如《逻辑哲学论》第 6.522 节：确实，有些东西无法用语言表达。它们自己显现出来。它们是神秘的。每次他说“神秘”时，他都会不由自主地唱出这个词，它挂在他的嘴唇上，是一种尴尬，一个下流的笑话，一首粗俗的打油诗，其他人设法忽略了。

Case in point: Otto harbors an unfading suspicion of Wittgenstein. He always probes a few lines of the Tractatus like a tongue in search of a sore tooth, such as Tractatus 6.522: There are, indeed, things that cannot be put into words. They make themselves manifest. They are what is mystical. Each time he says “mystical,” he sings the word involuntarily and it hangs from his lips, an embarrassment, a blue joke, a crude limerick the others manage to ignore.

另一个例子是：他觉得库尔特很奇怪。如果不是因为奥尔加，他可能更倾向于把他描述为同事，奥尔加对科特的评价是：“科特几乎像一个陌生人，而不是朋友。科特对奥托热情洋溢的幽默感毫无抵抗力，这也令人失望。反过来，奥托也觉得科特的幽默太聪明、太学术了，所以人们花在思考设置和妙语上的时间会破坏笑话的时机，尽管奥尔加经常会由衷地、自发地笑出科特。她对科特产生了好感，就好像他是一只翅膀折断的娇弱的小鸟，但有幸掉进了她的花园。他的数学天赋给她留下了深刻的印象，所以她对他不仅仅是怜悯。她对他怀有真正的钦佩，最终是友谊。在奥尔加的指导下，奥托比平时更耐心地听他说话，并有意识地决定仔细思考科特的任何评论，以寻找其中的微妙之处。”

Another case in point: He finds Kurt odd. If it weren’t for Olga, he might be more inclined to describe him as an associate, a stranger almost, than as a friend. Kurt's immunity to Otto's ebullient sense of humor is also a disappointment. In return, Otto finds Kurt's humor too clever and academic, so that the time one spends mulling over the setup and the punch line spoils a joke's timing, although Kurt often gets a genuine and spontaneous laugh from Olga. She has taken a shine to Kurt, as though he were a delicate bird with a broken wing but had the good fortune to fall into her garden. And he has impressed her deeply with his mathematical aptitude, so that it is more than pity he inspires. It is genuine admiration, and finally friendship, she feels toward him. Under Olga's instruction Otto listens to him more patiently than he might otherwise and has made a conscious decision to think over any of Kurt's comments carefully for subtleties of meaning.

他思考着库尔特的问题，思考着莫里茨的回答。奥托怎么知道什么是真实的？他知道自己膝盖因旧伤而疼痛。他了解儿子的胳膊、手、脸和正在长出的腿。当他们一起穿过公园时，他占据了空间并撞到了儿子。奥托知道一种隐匿的悲伤，这种悲伤像他儿子新陈代谢的激增一样幼稚而戏剧性地爆发，但现在已经消退为一个悲伤的回忆。最重要的是，他了解奥尔加。他怎么知道的？他不知道自己怎么知道的，但这种对现实的柔弱敏感让他很恼火。奥尔加是真实的吗？她是奥托的全部现实。她是他的爱，他的生命。他的向导。

He considers Kurt's question. He considers Moritz's response. How does Otto know what is real? He knows the ache in his knee from an old injury. He knows his son's arms and hands and face and growing legs. He occupies space and knocks into him as they walk together through the park. Otto knew an insidious grief that grew in spurts as childish and dramatic as the surges in his son's metabolism, but that has now abated to a sorrowful memory. And above all else he knows Olga. How does he know? He doesn’t know how he knows, but this effete delicacy around reality irritates him. Is Olga real? She is Otto's whole reality. She is his love, his life. His guide.

奥托·诺伊拉特和奥尔加·哈恩于 1912 年结婚。他仍然向她描述他干枯胡须的日常变化，花时间讨论似乎随着季节变化的各种红色。当她抚摸粗糙的头发时，她想象着姜黄色和玫瑰色的稻草色。她对这些干燥颜色最极端的样本的华丽感到惊讶，比如古斯塔夫·克里姆特画作中的金色。当她看到克里姆特 1904 年为维特根斯坦姐妹之一所作的肖像画时，她想知道这幅拥有如此惊人财富的女继承人的结婚照上所有的金色都去了哪里。巧合的是，在她看完这幅肖像画后不久，她因一种罕见的感染而失明，当时她只有 22 岁。她越来越少要求奥托向她描述颜色，在黑暗的二十年里，记忆逐渐消退，直到她几乎无法想象出一幅与奥托肖像相媲美的复制品描述。但她总能想象到他胡子上的鲜血和琥珀色。

Otto Neurath and Olga Hahn were married in 1912. He still describes to her the daily permutations of his parched beard, taking time to discuss the variety of reds that seem to alter with the seasons. When she fingers the coarse hair, she imagines ginger and rose-painted straw. She was amazed by the opulence of the most extreme sample of these dry colors, like the gold of Gustav Klimt's paintings. When she saw Klimt's portrait of one of the Wittgenstein sisters in 1904, lots of white and blue and green, she wondered where all the gold had gone from this wedding picture of an heiress to such a staggering fortune. By mere coincidence, it was not long after she viewed the portrait that she was blinded by a rare infection when she was just twenty-two. Less and less frequently she asks Otto to describe colors to her, the memories fading over the twenty dark years until she can barely conjure up a reproduction to match against his description. But she can always picture the blood and amber of his beard.

失明后，她尝试用以前在纸上计算的方式在脑中计算，想象着头骨表面的白色粉笔痕迹。但随着列表越来越长，最初的方程式逐渐模糊，她发现自己想得太快了，就像一个疯狂的科学家在与即将消失的墨水赛跑。几年后，她放弃了旧方法，也有些苦涩，找到了自己小时候抛弃的一项才能，当一段出乎意料的生动记忆将其从休眠状态中唤醒时，她意外地恢复了这种才能。

After she lost her sight, she tried to calculate in her head the way she used to calculate on paper, visualizing cool white marks like chalk on the bone surface of her cranium. But the initial equations would fade as the list became long and she found herself trying to work too quickly, a mad scientist racing against disappearing ink. After some years she abandoned her old methods along with some bitterness and found an aptitude she had discarded as a girl, reviving it accidentally when an unexpectedly vivid memory knocked it from dormancy.

她的方向感无可挑剔。她和女朋友们会手拉手旋转，太阳俯视着她们逆时针旋转的轨迹，她们的双脚交叉旋转的速度比她们协调的速度要快，直到她们晕眩迷茫地摔倒。但奥尔加随时都可以闭上眼睛，用摆动的手臂冲破空气阻力，指向东方，弥补她跌倒时的踉踉跄跄。即使她摇摇晃晃地走着，但只要食指清晰地指向北方，她就能毫不费力地指向北方。

She had an immaculate sense of direction. She and her girlfriends would clasp hands and whirl, the sun looking down on their counterclockwise orbits, their feet crossing and looping faster than they could coordinate until they’d fall over dizzy and disoriented. But at any moment Olga could close her eyes and point east with swinging arm cutting through the air's resistance, compensating for her stumbling. Even as she tottered on wobbling legs, with clear articulation of her index finger she could effortlessly point north.

她放弃了空间灵活性，转而从事数学研究，追求更出色的分析能力。即使双目失明，她仍试图用钢笔和墨水记录自己的想法，尽管她知道自己会弄得一团糟，很快就会失去对纸张的控制，也不确定残留物中会出现什么疯狂的断言。

She abandoned this spatial dexterity for a more analytic facility in her mathematical studies. Even blind, she still tried to record her ideas with pen and ink, knowing the mess she was making, quickly losing control of the page, and unsure of what wild assertion emerged from the residue.

然后她又想起了。在维也纳第九区波尔兹曼街 5 号，阳光照在她的脸颊上，清爽的空气中有一小片温暖，数学研究所的气味很普通，她的手臂就像一根与地球磁场对齐的针。

Then it came back to her. On Boltzmanngasse 5 in Vienna's Ninth District, the sun on her cheek, a small mask of warmth in a sea of crisp air, the plain smell of the mathematics institute, and her arm a needle aligned with the earth's magnetic field.

她的牙齿将阳光反射到地理北极。她发现她可以在数学对话中提供这项技能，就像其他人迷路时的任何指南针一样有用。在广阔的开放空间中，黑暗提供了她看到其他人错过的转弯和联系。用夜视仪俯瞰鹰的鸟瞰图。

Her teeth reflecting sunlight to the geographic North Pole. She found she could offer this skill in mathematical conversation, as useful as any compass when the others were lost. In the vast open space the darkness provided she saw turns and connections that the others missed. An aerial view of the hawk with night vision.

她利用自己内心的空间地图在漆黑一片的房间和街道中穿行；她的灵巧让她的动作显得有些漂亮，所以她可以轻盈地飘进咖啡馆，滑进椅子里，让奥托点燃她的雪茄——这是她敏捷的自信展示。她的空间天赋让她觉得这是一种生物磁现象，她已经学会了控制和改进这种现象，只要她集中注意力，她就能非常准确地绘制出她周围的地形、她的咖啡杯、她的同伴的位置。

She uses her internal map of space to navigate in the solid darkness through rooms and streets; and her dexterity allows her some prettiness in her movements, so that she floats smoothly into the coffeehouse and glides into her chair, allowing Otto to light her cigar—a confident demonstration of her agility. Her spatial aptitude strikes her as a kind of biological magnetic phenomenon that she has learned to control and refine to the extent that, if she concentrated, she could map out her immediate terrain, her cup of coffee, the location of her companions, all with great accuracy.

今晚，她坐在奥托身边，抽着一支新雪茄，全神贯注于烟草的浓郁味道和她眼中记忆中燃烧的余烬点燃的橙色余烬的灼热形象。

Tonight she sits close to Otto, drawing on a fresh cigar, preoccupied with the juicy tang of the tobacco and the hot image of orange embers the burning cinder ignites in the memory of her eyes.

莫里茨倾身向她，他的好朋友，隔着夹克衫密谋似的说着话。他倾身靠近她，吸入了她的烟雾。“我并不是觉得你不是真的，奥尔加。你确实似乎在这里。我承认这一点。”

Moritz leans in toward her, his good friend, speaking conspiratorially over the ridge of his jacket. He leans near enough to inhale her smoke. “It's not that I think you are not real, Olga. You do seem to be here. I’ll give you that.”

“好吧，莫里茨，谢谢你。”

“Well, Moritz, thanks for that.”

“尽管如此，无论如何，我对你的现实提出任何断言都是毫无意义的。这不是应该说的话。”

“Nonetheless, it is meaningless for me to pose any assertion of your reality either way. It's not something that ought be said.”

奥尔加一边卷着散落的头发，一边听着奥托的哼哼声（他的鼻孔擅长颤音），她的大大象。他大块大块地移动着，以保持精致椅子的平衡。他那笨拙而又方正的动作就像一场分散注意力的孤立地震。“当我们坐在桌边，默默地翻阅一切时，世界就分崩离析了。”他扯着胡子，用电线拉出叉状的火焰形状，音量也随之增大。“我们坐在这里不说话，能做出什么贡献呢？”

Olga winds the curly end of a loose strand of her hair as she listens to Otto snort (his nostrils have a flair for vibrato), her big elephant. He shifts in chunks about the balance of his delicate chair. His square and lumbering movements are a distracting, isolated earthquake. “The world falls apart as we sit at the table passing everything over in silence.” He pulls at his beard to form forked fiery shapes from the wire as his volume rises. “What can we contribute as we sit here not saying things?”

莫里茨对奥托的好辩情绪并不在意。“从某种意义上说，哲学家没有新的真理可以提供给科学家。但这并不令人失望。科学描述是一幅世界图景。我们的贡献是从天文和生物世界图景中提取意义。”

Moritz is unperturbed by Otto's contentious mood. “In a sense the philosopher has no new truth to offer the scientist. But this isn’t a disappointment. The scientific description is a world picture. Our contribution is to extract meaning from the astronomical and biological world picture.”

奥尔加倾身说道：“为什么科学描述还不够？这些是世界的事实：经验发现。这份清单就是世界。这就是现实。”

Olga leans in. “Why isn’t the scientific description enough? Here are the facts of the world: empirical discoveries. That list is the world. That is reality.”

“当然，人们可以争论自然主义者的观点，即心灵体验着它参与的外部现实。但是，奥尔加，这种说法怎么能真正让我们满意呢？人们同样可以争辩说，所有的经验都是高度主观的，我们真正拥有的唯一东西是形象、气味、味道，我们对宇宙的所有断言都是人类心灵的构造。”

“Sure, one could argue the naturalist's case that the mind experiences an external reality in which it participates. But how can this account really satisfy us, Olga? One could equally well argue that all experience is highly subjective, that the only thing we really have is the image, the smell, the taste, and all of our assertions about the universe are constructions of the human mind.”

奥尔加从嘴里吐出一根烟丝。“这个说法让你满意了吗？你觉得是真的吗？”

Olga peels a stray feather of tobacco from her lips. “And this account satisfies you, strikes you as the truth?”

“争论哪种世界图景是正确的解释是毫无意义的。说爱因斯坦相对论的英文描述比德文描述更正确，这毫无意义。抽象结构是相同的，从这个意义上说，两者都是正确的。”

“It is rather that it is senseless to argue over which world picture is the correct interpretation. It makes no more sense than it does to say that the English description of Einstein's relativity is more correct than the German. The abstract structures are the same and in this sense both are correct.”

“在某些时候，我们难道不必说出我们所相信的是真实的事情吗？”

“At some point don’t we have to declare what we believe to be true?”

“如果我们的命题与世界具有相同的结构，那么它们就是真实的。真理是通过结构的对应。”

“Our propositions are true if they have the same structure as the world. Truth is a correspondence through structure.”

奥尔加呼出一口气，又争取了一秒钟的时间才找到这句话。“莫里茨，我们真的要说我们不能宣称什么是真实的吗？”

Olga exhales, buying an extra second to find the phrase. “Moritz, are we really going to go so far as to say that we cannot lay claim to what is real?”

哥德尔歪着脖子插话道：“数字是真实的。”

Gödel angles his neck forward to interject, “Numbers are real.”

“请您原谅，”奥托转动着宽阔的肩膀，生气地说道，他对自己略显拘谨的措辞感到很有趣。

“I beg your pardon,” Otto huffs with a pivot of his big shoulders, amused by his own slightly prissy phrasing.

莫里茨的金属丝眼镜仿佛为了营造效果一样晃动着咖啡馆的灯光，然后他大声说道：“数字不是真实的。它们提供了一种反映世界结构的抽象语言，但它们不是物质的，不是真实的。”

Moritz's wire glasses swing the café lights around as if for effect before he enunciates, “Numbers are not real. They provide an abstract language that reflects the structure of the world, but they are not material, not real.”

“数字是真实的。一、三和π。我有经验证实数字的存在。我做了一个实验，比如想象一个完美的圆。我用这个圆除以其直径来发现π 。你可以重现这个实验。大脑对数字的感官体验是它们存在的确凿证据。π是真实的。”

“Numbers are real. One, three, and π. I have empirical confirmation of the existence of numbers. I perform an experiment, such as imagining a perfect circle. I divide that circle by its own diameter to discover the number π. And you could reproduce the experiment. The mind's sensory experience of numbers is conclusive evidence of their reality. π is real.”

“真的吗？”奥尔加问了他这个问题，这是他最后一次收回或至少掩盖真相的机会。

“Real?” Olga offers this to him as a last opportunity to retract, or at the least to obscure.

“是的，真实。最真实。”

“Yes, real. The most real.”

她将手肘撑在桌子上，弯曲的手指托住雪茄：“科特，那可能意味着什么，最真实的吗？”

With her elbow planted on the table and her fingers crooked to perch her cigar: “Kurt, whatever could that possibly mean, the most real?”

在他们之前多次的数学讨论中，Olga她用盲眼模糊地感觉到他的脸，徒劳地掠过他的空间，就像只是在锻炼肌肉一样。但这次她看着他。她完美地放回了茶杯，用手肘支撑住身体，然后猛地转过身，将护目镜的镜片固定在他的蓝眼睛上。有原则、公理和精确的规则可以将它们转化为物理可能性。奥尔加违反了这些规则。科特认为奥尔加不可能存在。

Many times before in their mathematical discussions, Olga has felt his face vaguely with her blind eyes, uselessly skimming over his patch of space as though merely exercising the muscles. But this time she looks at him. She replaces her cup of tea flawlessly, anchors her elbow, and turns her profile sharply to pin the goggle lenses onto his blue eyes. There are principles, axioms, and precise rules for transforming them into physical possibilities. Olga violates those rules. Kurt considers the possibility that Olga isn’t possible.

科特想告诉她，这个世界不值得信任。这个世界充满了幻影和规则的漏洞。这个世界充满了背叛和欺骗、细菌和毒药。他想告诉她，在这个逃避现实的世界之外，有一个更好、更真实的现实，一个柏拉图式的现实，我们的思想通过清晰地遵循逻辑，能够感知到那个仅由圆圈和线条、数字和几何图形组成的独立现实。没有疾病，没有声音，没有欺骗——只有真相。就好像一个混乱的镜头截取了所有真实的线条，并将光线重新定向到视野之外的焦点。

Kurt wants to tell her this world is not to be trusted. There are phantoms, slips in its rules. It is full of betrayal and deception, germs and poison. He wants to tell her that beyond this fugitive world is a better, truer reality, a Platonic reality, and our minds, through clear adherence to logic, are able to perceive that separate reality composed only of circles and lines, numbers and geometry. There is no disease, no voices, no deception—only truth. It is as though a lens of confusion intercepts all true lines and redirects the rays to a focal point beyond their vision.

奥尔加热心地建议道：“库尔特，你的意思是真实吗？或者你想说一些关于真理的事情？”他考虑向她坦白，“只有当我知道什么是真的时，我才知道什么是真实的。”但他回避了她的问题，尽管他确实开始用可爱的清晰度对她说话。他讨论了逻辑的基础和数学证明的形式。他那冰冷的表情融化了；他越深入逻辑语言，他就越慷慨——也越有感觉。奥尔加听着，惊叹于这个男人的独特聪明才智，他一秒钟前还很坚强，就像一根火柴点燃了他的温暖，烧掉了寒意。他讨论了不同之处证明与真理之间的矛盾，他靠在桌子上画了一些她看不见的符号，并叙述道：“在公理系统中，证明有一个正式的定义，但真理却没有。”当库尔特恢复他一贯的正式、技术风格时，奥尔加放松了下来。“人们通过变换规则来证明公理。真理则略有不同。”当他继续说下去时，他知道他正在向她提供一件珍贵的东西，一颗炽热的宝石，极其神圣。他正在向幻影提供一些坚实的东西。

Olga suggested helpfully, “Kurt, do you mean real? Or do you mean to say something about truth?” He considers confessing to her, “I know what is real only if I also know it is true.” But he evades her question, although he does begin to speak to her with lovely clarity. He discusses the basis of logic and the form of mathematical proof. His frozen look melts; and the deeper into the language of logic he delves, the more generous he becomes—and feels. As Olga listens, she marvels at the unique cleverness of this man who was hard and sealed not but a second earlier, as though a match were struck to ignite his warmth and burn away the chill. He discusses the difference between proof and truth and narrates over the spare symbols that he has leaned to the table to draw but that she can’t see. “There is a formal definition of proof within an axiomatic system but not of truth.” Olga relaxes as Kurt resumes his usual formal, technical style. “One takes axioms through transformation rules to prove theorems. Truth is subtly different.” As he continues, he knows he is offering her something precious, an incandescent gem, utterly sacred. He is offering something solid to a phantom.

数字 1 是存在的。它是真实的，即使 Olga 不是。

The number 1 exists. It is real, even if Olga is not.

维也纳，1931 年

VIENNA, 1931

Kurt 沿着 Währingerstrasse 跑去。天色已晚，他低着头跑着，眼镜从鼻梁上滑落。他追上了一个矮胖的女人，手里拿着沉重的黑面包和一袋蔬菜。他差点把她撞倒，他瘦削的臀部撞到了她圆润的臀部。他说对不起。他的道歉太过诚恳。他跑起来笨手笨脚。他把脚往一边踢，几乎把所有他想超越的人都绊倒了。天空是钴蓝色的。人行道上挤满了下班回家的人。他跑到了第一个拐角处。Josephinum 咖啡馆就在他身后半个街区。他希望它走开，消失。他转过身去看。Otto 仍然站得笔直，打开咖啡馆的门，看着他跑。Otto 叫他的名字。

Kurt is running down Währingerstrasse. It is late evening and his glasses are slipping off the bridge of his nose as he runs with his head down. He overtakes a stocky woman carrying heavy brown bread and a bag of vegetables. He nearly knocks her over, his thin hip colliding with her doughy round one. He says he is sorry. His apology is too ardent. He is clumsy as he runs. He kicks his feet out to the side so that he trips nearly everyone he tries to pass. The sky is cobalt dark. The sidewalks are crowded with people returning from work. He makes it to the first corner. The Café Josephinum is only half a block behind him. He wants it to go away, to disappear. He turns to look. Otto is still standing squarely, holding open the door of the café, watching him run. Otto calls his name.

今晚是库尔特第一次未经邀请就发言。他在圈子里的参与通常不过是点头或耸耸肩，几乎没有什么明显的迹象同谋或怀疑。但今晚，透过桌子上闪闪发光的白月，隔着天文数字般的距离，科特几乎是低声说：“我一直在思考说谎者悖论。”

Tonight was the first time Kurt had taken the floor without invitation. His participation around the Circle is usually no more than a nod or a shrug, barely noticeable indications of complicity or skepticism. But tonight, over the glowing white moon of the table, across that astronomical distance, Kurt nearly whispered, “I have been thinking about the Liar's Paradox.”

莫里茨从容不迫地重复道：“库尔特，说谎者悖论是对语言的滥用。数学中没有无法解决的问题。”

Moritz repeated with measured, deliberate timing, “Kurt, the Liar's Paradox is a misuse of language. In mathematics there are no unsolvable problems.”

“但确实有。有些真理永远无法被证实。而我可以证明这一点。”

“But there are. There are some truths that can never be proven. And I can prove it.”

科特双手交叉在胸前，努力保持步调。雨已经开始了。男人们都把头埋在帽檐后面。他们像暴风雨中的物质一样在他周围流动。即使在寒冷的天气里，他也无法摆脱莫里茨那双充满责备的蓝色眼睛，他盯着科特的双筒望远镜，损害了他的视神经。“不，”莫里茨摇了摇头，双手交叉放在膝盖上。“不，”他说。

Kurt wraps his arms across his chest as he tries to maintain his pace. The rain has started. Men are tucked behind the brims of their hats. They flow around him like the matter of the storm. Even out in the cold he can’t shake the accusing blue of Moritz's eyes as he stared into Kurt's binoculars, damaging his optic nerve. “No,” Moritz shook his head and folded his hands on the podium of his knees. “No,” he said.

哥德尔穿过一条又一条街道时，他试图抑制自己的情绪。他什么感觉也没有，就像一根干涸的软管。他想逃避接下来发生的事情，但他和莫里茨的对话就在眼前，一段录音在不断重播，随着每次循环而不断增强。莫里茨屈服于他的朋友中唯一可能提到的不礼貌倾向时，科特感到讨论朝着不祥的方向发展。他用手指把头发往后梳，扬起眉毛，和邻居们一起假笑。这只是有点贬低，但足以让科特苍白的脸颊红起来。他试着不慌张。科特被困在其他人中间的座位上，他向奥尔加提出了莫里茨拒绝的。“撒谎者说，这个陈述是假的。有一个数学等价的陈述，也使一个关于其本身的无法解决的主张。翻译过来就是，这个说法是无法证明的。 “

As Gödel crosses one street and then another he tries to strangle off his emotion. He feels nothing, a hose twisted dry. He is running away from what happened next, but his exchange with Moritz is in front of him, a recording replaying, enhancing with each circuit. Kurt felt the discussion take an ominous direction when Moritz gave in to the only impolite tendency any one of his friends might mention. He brushed his hair back with his fingers and lifted his eyebrows to share a smirk with his neighbors. It was only slightly demeaning but enough to burn color into Kurt's pallid cheeks. He tried not to panic. Trapped where he was in his seat between the others, Kurt offered to Olga what Moritz rejected. “The liar says, This statement is false. There is a mathematical equivalent, a statement that also makes an unsolvable claim about itself. It translates to, This statement is unprovable.”

他找来墨水笔，在茶碟和茶杯之间，在桌子上写下一排数字，奥尔加则读着他伸展的背部和弹性的安静中流露出的紧张感。他向她概述了他的编号系统。

He searched for the inky pen and wrote a spire of numbers on the table between the obstacles of saucers and cups as Olga read the tension in the stretching backs and elastic quiet. He outlined for her his numbering system.

“我将‘这个陈述是无法证明的’这句话编码成数字——没有文字，只有数字。”

“I encode the sentence, This statement is unprovable, into numbers—no words, just numbers.”

“你将这句话翻译成数字代码吗？”

“You translate the sentence into a numerical code?”

“是的，纯数字的代码。”

“Yes, a code of pure numbers.”

奥尔加扮演着好姐姐的角色，身体前倾，眼睛向上看，仿佛在等待药膏。她试图跟上科特的论点，比其他人跟得更快，但还是不够快。“然后你证明这个关系是真的？”

Playing the part of the good big sister, Olga pitched forward in her seat, her eyes looking up as though waiting to receive a salve. She tried to catch up to Kurt's argument, keeping pace better than the others, still not quite there. “And then you prove the relation is true?”

“不，我证明关系的真假不能通过遵守算术规则来决定。”

“No, I prove that the truth or falsity of the relation cannot be decided by adhering to the rules of arithmetic.”

“因此它没有数学证明。”

“And so it has no mathematical proof.”

“确实如此。但这正是关系所断言的：这个陈述是无法证明的。”

“Exactly. But this is precisely what the relation asserts: This statement is unprovable.”

“所以这是真的吗？”

“So it is true?”

“是的，这是真的。我们可以清楚地认识到它的真实性，不是通过数学规则，而是从数学之外。这个陈述的真实性不是来自僵硬的逻辑关系链，不是来自将一个数学事实与另一个数学事实联系起来的环节。而是来自一瞥。”

“Yes, it is true. We can recognize its truth plainly, not through mathematical rules, but from outside of mathematics. The truth of this statement does not follow from the inflexible chain of logical relations, the links that cleave one mathematical fact to another. It comes instead from a glance.”

奥托对今晚的意外发展感到欣慰。今晚他们离开公寓前，奥尔加穿着高领毛衣，穿着白色上衣的奥托站在门口，帮他穿上大衣，鼓励他要有礼貌。“去吧，要有礼貌，要留下来抱怨，”她一边劝说，一边帮他拉上外套，她知道他会选择“去吧，抱怨吧”的组合。他对维特根斯坦的厌恶具有传染性，已经蔓延到对所有权威的普遍烦躁，包括莫里茨的。她把脸贴在覆盖他大心脏的发痒的布料上，然后抓住他的手肘，跟着他把他推到门外，他们去了约瑟夫咖啡馆，度过了一个晚上，最后以奥托说的这段对话结束：“你是说莫里茨错了吗？”

Otto could not help a certain amount of hopeful gratification with tonight's unexpected developments. Before they left their apartment this evening, Olga, cinched up in her high collared white blouse, stood at the door bundling Otto into his overcoat, encouraging him to be civil. “Go and be civil, or stay and grumble,” she advised even as she pulled his coat closed and knew he would opt for the go-and-grumble combination. His annoyance with Wittgenstein is contagious and has spread to a general irritability with all forms of authority, including Moritz's. She rested her face on the itchy fabric cloaking his big heart before holding his elbow and following as she pushed him out the door and they made their way to the Café Josephinum to spend an evening that culminated in this conversation as Otto said, “Are you saying Moritz is wrong?”

“是的。”

“Yes.”

奥托深吸一口气，让肚子鼓起来，然后，像巴伐利亚手风琴一样，笑声在客厅里响起，他拍着肚子站起来去吧台点了一块蛋糕。奥托被肾上腺素的刺激所吸引，兴奋不已。这个可能性让他吃了一惊，本能地感到震惊。但莫里茨对这个消息的反应就没那么好了。他交叉双腿，双臂，仿佛要阻止这个想法，莫里茨几乎要生气了，他收起下巴，把话指向库尔特，语气意在强调荒谬之处。“维特根斯坦错了吗？”

Otto drew a deep breath, making room for his belly to expand and then, like a Bavarian accordion, wheezed laughter into the parlor, slapping his stomach as he rose to order a cake from the bar. Otto was wholly entertained, elevated by adrenaline. The possibility gave him a start, an instinctive jolt. But Moritz took the news less well. Crossing his legs and arms as if to bar the very idea, coming as close to anger as Moritz ever gets, he tucked in his chin to point his words toward Kurt, the tone meant to highlight the ridiculous. “Is Wittgenstein wrong?”

哥德尔从大衣里伸出双手，削掉尖刺，懊悔地挡住了自己的回答。“是的。”

Gödel's hands sprung out from within his overcoat, whittled down spikes ruefully warding off his own reply. “Yes.”

学生们几乎爆发出一阵咆哮，但奥托却愉快地鼓掌。“如果科特是对的呢？这有什么不好的？”

There is nearly a roar from the students, but Otto applauded merrily. “What if Kurt is right? What is so bad?”

莫里茨用力摇了摇手指。“这是最令人绝望的原因。理性必须占上风。为此，数学必须完美且完整。它必须从逻辑上能够回答所有有意义的问题。它必须有可能。”

Moritz shook his finger vigorously. “It is cause for the greatest despair. Reason. Must. Prevail. And for that, mathematics must be perfect—and complete. It must be logically possible to answer all meaningful questions. It must be possible.”

库尔特回答说：“数学是完美的。但它并不完整。要看到一些真理，你必须站在外面往里看。”

To which Kurt replied, “Mathematics is perfect. But it is not complete. To see some truths you must stand outside and look in.”

“不，”莫里茨几乎吼叫道。他接着反手一拍空气，举起上臂，仿佛在挥舞旗帜。“不。”

“No,” Moritz nearly bellowed. He followed with a backhanded swat at the air, holding his upper arm as though waving a flag. “No.”

科特重温着那场对话，每次重温时，对话都会稍微变形，他沿着下一条街向左拐，然后又沿着两条街拐。风从排水沟里掀起纸屑。一块玻璃从人行道裂缝中一个紧密的楔子上闪闪发光。他的嘴周围雾蒙蒙的。一个身材魁梧的男人正在清洗他那间没有灯光的商店的窗户。泡沫在冒泡成白色泡沫之前，先把街上最鲜艳的颜色都洗掉了。这个男人已经清洗过这些窗户数百次，还会再清洗一千次，而再清洗一千次，它们就会被一层细小的污垢覆盖。一对夫妇在上面窗户的灯光下小声争吵，他们看起来像是在舞台上，他们误以为那是私人避难所。她试图理解他的论点，他试图理解她的坏脾气。他们更接近了，但他们还没有完全接近。从来没有完全接近。

Reliving the conversation, deforming it slightly with each replay, Kurt turns left along the next street, then down two more. The wind kicks up paper garbage from the gutter. A piece of glass flashes from a tight wedge in a break in the pavement. The air is foggy around his mouth. A heavyset man is washing the windows of his unlit shop. The suds catch the brightest colors off the street before bubbling to a white foam. This man has washed these windows hundreds of times and will wash them a thousand more times, and a thousand more times they will be coated with a fine dirt. A couple argues quietly beneath a light from the window above so that they appear as though on stage on a corner they mistook for a private shelter. She is trying to understand his argument and he is trying to understand her bad temper. They are closer but they are not quite there. Never completely there.
