Turing has become the focus of the philosopher's campaign to shake the idolatry for science out of people's eyes, so his course on mathematics has become a live debate between them. Alan is unaccustomed to philosophical methods of argumentation. The course that Alan teaches happens to have the same title but by contrast is a forceful lesson in mathematical methods, an impressive demonstration of logical manipulations of symbols, and nearly opposite Wittgenstein's in every way. Still, Alan does his best to defend mathematics in Wittgenstein's course while attempting to adhere to more philosophical forms of discourse.

他参加的上一堂课是在艾伦跨过门槛时（迟到了五分钟）开始的，维特根斯坦向他讲话，仿佛在继续一场私人讨论。他经常把人当成书，翻到一页就放在一边，直到他选择参考纸上的某个观点。“想想说谎者的例子，”艾伦在座位间穿梭时，他说。艾伦和维特根斯坦之间的对话如下。

The previous lecture he attended began as Alan's foot crossed the threshold (five minutes late) and Wittgenstein addressed him as if continuing a private discussion. He often treats people like books, flicking to a page and laying them aside until he chooses to consult a point on the paper. “Think of the case of the Liar,” he said as Alan scooted through the seats. And the following dialogue between Alan and Wittgenstein ensued.

“想想撒谎者的例子，”维特根斯坦说。“这很奇怪，任何人都应该对此感到困惑——比你想象的还要奇怪：这应该是人类担心的事情。为什么，事情是这样的：如果一个人说“我在撒谎”，我们说他没有撒谎，由此可以得出他撒谎，依此类推。好吧，那又怎么样？你可以一直这样下去，直到你脸色发青。为什么不呢？没关系。

“Think of the case of the Liar,” Wittgenstein said. “It is very queer in a way that this should have puzzled anyone—much more extraordinary than you might think: that this should be the thing to worry human beings. Why, the thing works like this: If a man says ‘I am lying’ we say that it follows that he is not lying, from which it follows that he is lying and so on. Well, so what? You can go on like that until you are black in the face. Why not? It doesn’t matter.

“一个人说‘我在撒谎’，我说‘因此你不是，因此你是，因此你不是……’——有什么错？没什么错。只是它毫无用处；这只是一个无用的语言游戏，为什么有人会兴奋呢？”

“A man says, ‘I am lying,’ and I say, ‘Therefore you are not, therefore you are, therefore you are not … ’—what is wrong? Nothing. Except that it is of no use; it is just a useless language game, and why should anyone be excited?”

图灵： “让人困惑的是，人们通常用矛盾作为做错事的标准。但在这种情况下，人们找不到任何错误。”

TURING:“What puzzles one is that one usually uses a contradiction as a criterion for having done something wrong. But in this case one cannot find anything done wrong.”

维特根斯坦： “是的——而且，什么事都没有做错。危害又在哪里呢？”

WITTGENSTEIN:“Yes—and more: nothing has been done wrong. Where will the harm come?”

图灵： “真正的危害不会发生，除非有应用，在这种情况下，一座桥梁可能会倒塌或发生类似的事情。”

TURING:“The real harm will not come in unless there is an application, in which case a bridge may fall down or something of that sort.”

维特根斯坦： “啊，现在如果存在矛盾，桥梁就会倒塌的想法非常重要。但我太笨了，现在无法开始；所以我下次再讲。”

WITTGENSTEIN:“Ah, now this idea of a bridge falling down if there is a contradiction is of immense importance. But I am too stupid to begin it now; so I will go into it next time.”

艾伦穿着破旧的蓝色外套和两只不同颜色的袜子，一边坚持，一边调整坐姿，坐在椅子上。“人们最担心的是，这种事情不应该发生在数学上。但哥德尔证明，这样的事情确实发生了。”

In his ratty blue blazer and two different colored socks Alan rearranged himself to sit higher in the chair as he persisted. “One is most concerned that this should not happen in mathematics. But something like this does happen as Gödel demonstrated.”

维特根斯坦： “问题是：为什么人们害怕矛盾？很容易理解为什么他们应该害怕数学之外的秩序、描述等等中的矛盾。问题是：为什么他们应该害怕数学内部的矛盾？图灵说，‘因为应用可能会出错。’但什么都不必出错。如果真的出了问题——如果桥梁倒塌——那么你的错误就是使用了错误的自然法则。”

WITTGENSTEIN:“The question is: Why are people afraid of contradictions? It is easy to understand why they should be afraid of contradictions in orders, descriptions, et cetera, outside of mathematics. The question is: Why should they be afraid of contradictions inside mathematics? Turing says, ‘Because something may go wrong with the application.’ But nothing need go wrong. And if something does go wrong—if the bridge breaks down—then your mistake was of the kind of using a wrong natural law.”

图灵： “严格来说，数学中没有矛盾。相反，数学是不完整的。数字中有一些事实我们永远无法确定是真是假。”

TURING:“Strictly speaking there are no contradictions in mathematics. It is rather that mathematics is incomplete. There are facts among the numbers that we can never decide are true or are false.”

维特根斯坦： “那又怎么样？这有什么意义呢？”

WITTGENSTEIN:“And so what? What could be the significance?”

图灵： “这意味着并非每个适定问题都有解决方案。我们不可能知道一切。”他耸耸肩膀，环顾着班里盯着他的学生。

TURING:“This means that not every well-posed problem has a solution. We can’t know everything.” He shrugged his shoulders as he looked around the class of pupils staring at him.

维特根斯坦没有继续这个方向。他没有解释他的观点是如何改变的（他确实在《逻辑哲学论》中坚持他的论点，即每一个适定问题都必须 他没有解释为什么它们会改变，甚至不知道它们是否改变了。相反，他只是离题了一段，然后又重新开始辩论。“也许我们对说谎者悖论、哥德尔定理、图灵的不可计算数印象太深刻了，因为我们对这些词的含义感到困惑。当你说这个命题是真的时，你所说的‘真’到底是什么意思？在什么系统中？是有意义的吗？”

Wittgenstein did not pursue this direction. He did not explain how his opinions had changed (he had indeed pressed his thesis in the Tractatus that every well-posed problem must have a solution), or why they had changed, or even if they had changed. Instead there was a confusing digression after which he took up the argument again. “Maybe we are overly impressed with the Liar's Paradox, with Gödel's theorems, with Turing's uncomputable numbers, because we are confused about the meaning of the words. When you say the proposition is true, what do you really mean by the word ‘true’? In what system? Is it sense?”

辩论就这样一直持续着，直到艾伦说“我明白你的意思”时，辩论才突然且含糊地结束，而维特根斯坦则大声喊道：“我没有任何意义！”

And so the debate wore on until it ended abruptly and rather ambiguously when Alan said, “I see your point,” and Wittgenstein shouted, “I have no point!”

维特根斯坦在窗前停下，任由沉默持续下去。最后他热情地继续说道：“我们之间没有意见分歧。显然，关键在于我没有意见。”然后他又说了一句不那么激烈但对艾伦来说同样神秘的话：“这只能是我们在某些词语的使用上有所不同。”

Wittgenstein stopped at the window, allowing an outrageous silence to accumulate. Finally he continued ardently, “There is no difference of opinion. Obviously the whole point is that I have no opinion.” And then less intensely but no less mysteriously for Alan, “It can only be that we differ in our use of certain words.”

维特根斯坦的目光在灰色云层中辨别出一条黑线，锁定了一只打破队形的鸟。其他鸟落地后，这只鸟仍长时间漂浮在空中。维特根斯坦可以看到翅膀下方，直到这只鸟落在一股气流中，露出背部的黑色羽毛。

Resolving a dark thread against the gray clouds, Wittgenstein's gaze locked onto one bird that broke formation. The bird stayed afloat long after the others touched down. Wittgenstein could see under the wings until the bird fell around a swell of air to show the black feathers of his back.

艾伦坐在教室深处的座位上，从不同的角度观察着这只鸟，它的左侧，羽毛上的一个瑕疵，侧面的喙。当他研究这只鸟的孤独飞行时，他发现这只鸟的目的是飞翔。它的大脑执行着一串指令，它的翅膀、胸部和脚协调着它们的机械任务。这只鸟用眼睛收集光线，用羽毛探测风向，发现鸟群中的其他鸟或失去它们。鸟与艾伦只是程度不同。鸟是一台机器。它没有灵魂。没有精神。但它有一个目的。鸟提醒他，无论是他，还是维特根斯坦，还是其他任何人都没有那么重要。这不是一种苦涩的情绪。他有时能找到目的、乐趣，甚至意义。当他这样做时，他就像那只找到空气并歌唱的鸟。他和那只鸟一样重要。

From his seat deeper into the classroom, Alan had a different angle on the bird, its left side, a flaw in the feathers, a beak in profile. As he studied the solitary flight of the bird, he saw the bird's purpose is to fly. Its brain executed a list of instructions and its wings and chest and feet coordinated their mechanical task. The bird collected light with its eyes, detected the wind with its feathers, spotted the rest of the flock or lost them. The bird is different from Alan only in degree. The bird is a machine. It has no soul. No spirit. But it has a purpose. The bird reminded him that neither he, nor Wittgenstein, nor any other person is so significant. This isn’t a bitter sentiment. He can find purpose and pleasure and even meaning sometimes. When he does this, he is like the bird that finds the air and sings. He is every bit as significant as that bird.

在自己无法改变的私密思想中，维特根斯坦默默地反驳图灵对数学的崇拜，反驳他的机械论观点。他穿着皮夹克站在窗边，头发盘起，仿佛被一阵穿过墙壁和玻璃的风吹倒了。他双脚稳稳地站在原地，以平衡头部的倾斜，试图追随那只孤零零的鸟儿的轨迹，而天空中却充满了鸟群。小时候，他一看到哪怕是最卑微、最寒酸的鸟儿，心跳就会加速。在他发声和运动功能还未成熟时，他试图说出它们的名字，给它们一个词。那是一种喉音，而不是鸽子的鸣叫。在他学会了熟悉的“沃格尔”这个词很久之后，每当他看到一只鸟儿抛弃他和他沉重的声音，它们沉重地落在地上时，他仍然在努力克制自己发出那种喉音的冲动。

In the irrevocable privacy of his own thoughts, Wittgenstein argued silently against Turing's admiration for mathematics, against his mechanistic outlook. He stood at the window in his leather jacket with his hair screwed up as though caught in a wind that penetrated the walls and glass. His feet were firmly planted to balance the tilt of his head as he tried to follow the path of the one lone bird while the sky filled with the rest of the flock. As a boy his heart raced at the sight of even the lowliest, shabbiest of birds. He tried to say their name, to give them a word, before his vocal and motor functions were actually able. It was a guttural thump, not the warble of a dove. Long after he acquired the familiar word Vogel, he still fought the urge to call out that guttural thump each time he watched a bird abandon him and his heavy sound, weighed as they were to the earth.

维特根斯坦小时候就渴望飞翔。这始于航空学理念，然后是纯粹的永不满足的飞行梦想。小时候，他手工制作的空气动力学装置的吸引力让他身体疲惫。起初它们什么都不是，只是木棍和纸，他把它们打造成机器零件，组装成一个简单的模型，根据前一个模型成功升空的几次瞬间，然后是微弱的颤动和迅速的纸片坠落，对设计进行了微小的改变。他看到最初的骨架如此清晰地知道如何从位移的空气中升起，如何驾驭湍流掠过维特根斯坦宫的花园。有时，他会将原型固定在一根细绳上，就像一只精巧的风筝，用拇指和食指捏住线头，伸长脖子迎着风，然后松开，双脚固执地抓住地面。他看着自己精致的结构活了过来，摆脱了手指的轻微粘性。他最喜欢的作品逃离了修剪整齐的巨大花园，越过了喷泉和原色花朵，越过了灌木丛和界定他家族豪宅广阔场地的墙壁。他渴望地看着自己的模型。他年轻的棕色眼睛已经英俊而明亮——这种美只会随着年龄的增长而加深，棕色的皱纹和浓密的眉毛更能表达出来。

As a child, Wittgenstein longed to fly. It began with aeronautic ideas, then pure insatiable dreams of flight. As a young boy, the appeal of his handmade aerodynamic contraptions caused him physical strain. First they were no one thing, just wooden sticks and paper that he groomed into machine parts and assembled into a simple model, changing the design fractionally based on the few successful airborne moments of its predecessor followed by a weak flutter and a swift papery crash. He saw the initial skeleton so clearly, knew how to connive a lift from displaced air and how to ride the turbulence skimming the gardens of the Palais Wittgenstein. Sometimes he would pin the prototype to a delicate string, an ingenious kite, and pinch the end of the thread between thumb and finger while craning into the flow of the wind only to let go, his feet stubbornly gripping the earth. He watched his delicate structures come alive and escape the slight stickiness of his fingers. His favorites escaped the confines of the enormous manicured gardens, past the fountains and the blooms of primary colors, past the shrubbery and the walls defining the extensive grounds of his family's elaborate mansion. He watched his models with longing. His young brown eyes already handsome with brilliance—a beauty that would only deepen with age, enunciated by umber creases and thickening brows.

他在工程学方面的特殊才能包括有条不紊地集中他在所有物理问题上的一般才能。外部世界呈现在他面前，就像他得到了一张完整注释的力、作用和反作用的示意图一样。这种才能定义了维特根斯坦的一个方面，许多人都钦佩他。非常理性的思想家。但维特根斯坦年轻的生命中有一个裂缝，一个断层将他的生命一分为二：之前和之后。在那条裂缝的尖端，太尖太细，无法确定时间的长短，闪着白热的光——只是那不对，那是光的缺失，但不是黑暗。那是空间、时间、光和物质的完全缺失，最接近于刺眼的白色，只是这些话是无效的，不诚实的。它们是谎言。它没有颜色。它最接近于虚无，他无法用普通语言描述的。它最接近于虚无。只是它是一种令人眼花缭乱、闪闪发光、充满狂喜的虚无。它不是一个事物；而是一个发生，一个事件。他一生中最伟大的事件。只是它没有在时间上被解析出来，也没有在空间中可识别的位置。在之前和之后的边缘，维特根斯坦飞了起来。不完全是他的身体。也不只是他的思想。他——无论他是谁，无论他是什么——从那一刻，从那个地方脱离了肉体的物质，体验了飞翔，漂浮在那种非能量、非光、非物质、非白色、非黑暗的纹理中。当他恢复过来时，就好像他的身体被披在身上，四肢重新接上，这是极好的假肢。在内心深处，不是在某个地方，而是在一个他无法命名的非地方，他被狂喜所灼烧。

His specific acumen in engineering involved a methodical focusing of his general acumen in all matters physical. The external world presented itself to him as plainly as if he had been given a fully annotated schematic diagram of forces, actions, and reactions. This talent defined an aspect of Wittgenstein that so many admired. The intensely rational thinker. But there was a fracture in Wittgenstein's young life, a crisp break that split his life into two: Before and After. On the cusp of that fissure, too sharp and thin to assign a duration in time, blazed a white-hot light—only that's not right, it was the absence of light, but it wasn’t dark. It was the complete absence of space and time and light and matter and it was closest to an eye-sizzling white, only these words were ineffectual, dishonest. They were lies. It had no color. It was closest to nothing he could describe in ordinary language. It was closest to nothing. Only it was a dazzling, shining nothing pregnant with ecstasy. It wasn’t a thing; it was a happening, an event. The greatest event of all of his life. Only it was not parsed out in time and had no identifiable location in space. On the edge between Before and After, Wittgenstein flew. Not his body exactly. Not just his thoughts either. He—whoever, whatever he is—disengaged from the material of his flesh, from that moment, from that place, and experienced flight floated by the texture of that not-energy, that not-light, not-matter, not-white, not-dark. When he recovered himself, it was as though his body had been draped over him and the limbs reattached, superb prosthetics. Somewhere deep inside, only not in a place, but in a non-place he couldn’t name, he was seared by rapture.

他从未大声讲述过这件事，尽管他渴望将它框定下来。他尝试的每个词都失败了。在语言中，他找不到使他变形的崇高神秘真理。然后他意识到。描述他的飞行的所有尝试都失败了。没有足够准确的词语。没有足够精确的图片。他唯一能希望的就是框定它的缺失，一个从世界上雕刻出来的负空间。他只能描述它不存在的东西。因此，他开始用一种完美的逻辑语言对世界上的一切进行完整的描述，希望在剩下的负空间里，他能默默地指向他的宝藏。世界的伟大建筑和普通语言将为最珍贵的东西——无法言说的东西——创造一个框架。我们不能谈论的事情，我们必须保持沉默。

He never spoke of the event aloud, although he crumpled with a desire to frame it. Every word he tested failed. Nowhere in language could he find the sublime mystical truth that disfigured him. Then he realized. All attempts to describe his flight would fail. There were no words accurate enough. No pictures precise enough. All he could ever hope for was to frame its absence, a negative space carved out of the world. He could only describe what it was not. So he embarked on a complete description of everything in the world in a perfect logical language with the hope that in the negative space remaining, he could point silently to his treasure. The great architecture of the world and ordinary language would create a frame for the most precious of all—that which cannot be said. What we cannot talk about we must pass over in silence.

维特根斯坦背对着房间站着，课堂上剩下的漫长几分钟。学生们坐在那里，越来越焦躁不安，因为这个下午的时间一分一秒地过去，就像维特根斯坦呼吸的燃料。透过窗玻璃，他看到一群学生从演讲厅飞出来，然后组成交叉在草坪上的团体。他们的动作起初似乎有组织，然后变得混乱，然后又变得有序。也许课已经结束了。他决定，该看电影了。他打算坐在电影院的前排，让闪烁的灯光洗去今天讲座的汗水和挣扎。他从窗边转过身，大步迈出六步，从厚重的门框里走出去。

Wittgenstein stood with his back to the room for the remaining long minutes of the class. The students sat in growing agitation as that afternoon was burned heavy minute after heavy minute like a fuel to power Wittgenstein's breath. Through the windowpanes he watched a swarm of students fly out of lecture halls and then form groups that crisscrossed the lawn. Their motions seemed organized at first, then disordered, then ordered again. Maybe class was over. It was time for the movie, he decided. He planned to sit in the front row of the cinema and allow the flickering lights to wash away the sweat and struggle of today's lecture. He turned from the window and took six big strides to exit through the heavily framed door.

这是艾伦听的最后一堂课，第七堂课他因为要去政府密码学校接受培训而缺席了。他决定去听下一堂课。语言有缺陷，但数学是完美的——这就是他要争论的。他将试图说服维特根斯坦，数学不是人类的发明，数学有待发现，它是自然法则最纯粹的形式。数学创造了我们，而不是我们创造了数学。

That was the last lecture Alan attended, missing the seventh lecture owing to his training session at the Government Code and Cypher School. He resolves to attend the next lecture. Language is flawed but mathematics is perfect—this is what he will argue. He will try to convince Wittgenstein that mathematics is not a human invention, that it is there to be discovered, that it is the purest form of natural law. Mathematics has made us, not the other way around.

维特根斯坦在门口的挂钩上挂了两件大衣。他决定原谅图灵今天的缺席。他决心说服图灵，数学是一项发明，不要与自然法则混淆。

Wittgenstein hangs two overcoats on the pegs in his entrance. He decides to forgive Turing his absence today. He resolves to convince him that mathematics is an invention and not to be confused with natural law.

双方都无法说服对方。

Each will fail to persuade the other.

第八讲之后，艾伦就完全不再听课了。当被问及维特根斯坦时，艾伦会解释维特根斯坦的评论，以及他为何觉得这些评论完全令人费解。他还会说，他觉得维特根斯坦非常奇怪。

Alan stopped attending the course altogether after the eighth lecture. When asked about Wittgenstein, Alan will explain Wittgenstein's comments and how he found them completely baffling He will also say that he found him very peculiar.

艾伦甚至不会试图表达在格兰切斯特的那一刻当他发现机器时，他是在梅多斯，而维特根斯坦甚至不会试图描述他在童年花园中的那一刻。

Alan will not even try to articulate that moment in Grantchester Meadows when he discovered his machines, and Wittgenstein will not even attempt to articulate that moment in his childhood garden.

每当艾伦回想起维特根斯坦，总会有一段记忆浮现。他会记得曾经一起看到过一只黑色的鸟从鸟群中飞出来，飘浮在窗户的另一边。

When Alan thinks back on Wittgenstein, one memory will always recur. He will remember having shared the sight of the black bird that broke from the flock to float on the other side of the window.

英国白金汉郡。1940 年

BUCKINGHAMSHIRE, ENGLAND. 1940

英国正处于战争之中，而艾伦却正处于相当幸福的时期。我们可以从这里了解他的故事，那是一个难忘的夜晚，他用致命的刀片刮胡子，看到血就晕了过去。当然，他割伤了自己——实际上伤得相当严重。不是用剃刀，剃刀沿着他方下巴的骨头划出一道干净的薄片，而是用第三块瓷砖，中间偏左，他倒在地上，坚硬的陶瓷与他坚硬的头骨相接。就在眩晕之前，他看着血顺着下巴流下来。这一视觉，加上昨晚晚餐时下巴碰到从叉子上流下的鸡汁的感觉，幸运的是，他在被地板震晕之前昏了过去。

England is at war and Alan is in the middle of a reasonable happiness. We can pick up his story here on a night made unforgettable during a shave with a lethal blade as he faints from the sight of the blood. Of course he cuts himself—injures himself rather badly actually. Not with the razor, which cuts a clean thin slice tracing the bone of his square chin, but with the third tile, left of center, as he crumples to the floor and the hard ceramic connects with his hard skull. Just before the vertigo, he watches the blood slide down his jawline. The visual, along with the sensory recall of the feel of last night's dinner when his chin caught the chicken juice sluicing off his fork, mercifully knocks him unconscious before he is concussed by the floor.

在他头脑昏迷之前的那一瞬间，但在他因刺痛而退缩并看到深红色的汁液渗入伤口后，他平静地看着自己。血液逐渐填满伤口，就像水银在温度计上攀升一样。我接下来会晕倒他想，这不是一种意图的陈述，而是对因果关系不变的观察。按下打字机上的一个键，一个字母就会以墨水的形式出现在纸上。结果是确定的，是按下键的初始结果。他的思维也一样。按下一个杠杆，结果就会随之而来。下巴被割破，刺痛，流血，然后他晕倒了。他试图坚持这个想法，但他的双腿发软，周边视觉逐渐消失，他闭上了眼睛。

For that brief moment before his mind goes dark but after he flinches from the sting and sees the deep red sap oozing into the cut, he calmly watches himself. The blood fills the split progressively like mercury climbing a thermometer. I will next faint from the sight of my own blood, he thinks, not as a statement of intention but as an observation of the unfaltering order of cause and effect. Push a key on a typewriter and a letter appears in ink on a page. The outcome is determined, a fixed consequence of the initial push of the key. His mind is no different. Press a lever and an outcome follows. Cut his chin, the sting, the blood flows, and he faints. He tries to hang on to this thought as his legs give way and his peripheral vision fades, closing down his eyes.

当他苏醒过来时，他正盯着自己丢弃的鞋子的鞋底。他毫不犹豫地伸手去拿，坐起来，系好鞋带，然后去捡邻居丢弃的旧婴儿车。

When he revives he is staring into the soles of his cast-aside shoes. Without hesitation, he reaches for them, sits up, laces them on his feet, and goes to collect the old baby carriage a neighbor has discarded.

作为战时投资，他以 250 英镑的价格购买了两块银条。第一次世界大战期间，在其他一切东西都跌到英国人难以忘怀的毫无价值的水平时，银价却成功上涨。大多数投资者将银条存入银行，而艾伦决定将银条埋入地下。他把银条塞进脏兮兮的婴儿车，推着它走进附近的树林，引来市民们担忧的目光，他们知道，看到一个邋遢的年轻人，迈着奇怪的步伐，推着毫无生气的婴儿车，是不应该忽视的。他像马一样腾跃，将瘦腿的膝盖抬到臀部高，动作敏捷。尤其是在剑桥演讲时，或者独自沉思时，或者推着装满银条的婴儿车时，他总是腾跃。

As a wartime investment, he bought two bars of silver bullion at the price of 250 pounds. During the First World War, silver managed to rise in value even as everything else sank to a level of worthlessness that England finds hard to forget. While most investors place theirs in a bank, Alan has decided to place his in the ground. Tucking them into the dirty pram, he wheels the bounty into a nearby woods, drawing concerned looks from citizens who know better than to dismiss the sight of a messy young man with a peculiar stride and a lifeless pram. He prances like a horse, lifting the knees of his skinny legs hip-high and in a sharp motion. He prances especially when he is delivering a lecture in Cambridge or when alone with his thoughts, or when he pushes a pram heavy with silver bars.

给当地警察打电话的人并非只有利太太，因为她住的地方比任何人都更靠近森林，她觉得，也许这有点不合情理，就好像森林由她来照管，如果不是，实际上是她的财产。当警官们准备进行正式审讯时，他们被毫不含糊地告知不要打扰这个年轻人时，他们感到有些困惑和尴尬。有传言说，这些命令来自人们能想象到的最高层——来自首相本人。白金汉郡的一些当地居民已经怀疑布莱切利庄园（山上的豪宅）正在发生一些事情——是为英国皇家服务局或军情五处准备的。

It isn’t only Mrs. Leigh who places a call to the local constables, living as she does closer than anyone to the woods and feeling, perhaps unreasonably, as though it is in her care if not actually her property. There is some confusion and embarrassment when the officers, ready for a proper interrogation, are told in no uncertain terms to leave the young man alone. There are rumors that these orders come from as high up as one could imagine—from the prime minister himself. Several of the local residents of Buckinghamshire already suspect something is going on at Bletchley Park, the mansion on the hill—something for His Majesty's Service or MI5.

图灵几乎完全误解了普通人类的互动，他认为婴儿车并不显眼——是一种伪装。一位年轻的父亲带着他的孩子散步。旁观者永远不会想到，这个小包裹是珍贵的银子，很快就会有宝藏埋在树林里。他没有想到，他们会怀疑，一位推着婴儿车进入森林却没带走的年轻父亲埋藏了更珍贵的东西。

Turing in his near total misunderstanding of ordinary human interactions thinks the pram inconspicuous—a disguise. A young father on a walk with his baby. The casual observer would never suspect that the little bundle is precious silver and that there would soon be a treasure buried in the woods. It hasn’t occurred to him that they would suspect instead that a young father who entered the woods with a pram and left without it had buried something rather more precious.

一根金条埋在森林地表的一个浅坟里。他花了一些时间在脑海中记下这些自然地标，这样就不需要明显的人造标记了。他特别注意到了溪流、坟墓和一棵树之间的几何形状，这棵树的树枝形成了一系列均匀的分叉，他花了一段时间研究它们，把它们画成一张图，在数值关系中寻找一个特殊的序列——偶尔会发现至少一组树枝维持的规则，但却找不到一条适用于整棵树的规律。

One bar is buried in a shallow grave in the forest floor. He spends some time inscribing mental notes on the natural landmarks so no obvious human-made marker will be necessary. He takes note especially of the geometry between stream, grave, and a tree that seems unique with its branches forming a sequence of even bifurcations that he dwells on for some time, drawing them out as a graph and searching for a special sequence in the numerical relations—occasionally finding a rule sustained for at least a cluster of branches but failing to find one law that applies to the tree as a whole.

第二块银块埋在人行桥下，就在溪流的石床上。他用自己设计的代码加密了两块银块的走向，把它们卷成苯丙胺吸入器，并按照说明将管子滑入下一座桥的基础的一个狭窄缝隙中。

The second bar is buried under a footbridge, right in the stony bed of the stream. He encrypts the directions to the two silver bars in a code of his own design, rolls them into a Benzedrine inhaler, and slides the tube with instructions into a narrow gap in the foundation of the next bridge along.

当他赤脚涉过泥泞，鞋子和袜子都放在婴儿车里时，天并没有下雨。也就是说，水不是从云层落到地面的。水被困在泥土和云层之间的半空中，如果真的有这种东西的话，它就是一种冷蒸汽。他很容易就被淋湿了，就好像雨是垂直落下的一样。当他穿过雾气时，水滴落在他的脸上和头发上，直到满满一杯的雨水沿着他的毛孔弹跳，勾勒出他前额、鼻子和下巴的轮廓。刺骨的寒冷使他的手指发红，他的鼻子滴水，但这可能只是冷蒸汽凝结得足够厉害，在尖端产生了一颗小葡萄。当图灵搅拌泥土、测试记号笔和发明押韵时，阴天的灰色渗透到阴天的夜晚。他把温暖的空气吸入嘴里，里面夹杂着树上的糖浆和地上腐烂的物质。在他的肺脏深处，森林的乙醚变成了他的呼吸。他是由与植物、泥土和空气相同的分子构成的。他吞下它们，它们变成了他。他把空气和一些唾液一起排出，这些唾液渗入森林地面，他的呼吸飘散开来，被风吹向高高的云层，直到他只是下面一只孤独的小动物，群山一直绵延到五十英里以南的伦敦，首都正处于关闭状态，躲在黑暗中，感谢雾气。

As he wades through the mud in bare feet, his shoes and socks stored in the baby carriage, it doesn’t exactly rain. That is, the water is not raining from clouds down to earth. The water is trapped in midair between mud and cloud, a kind of chilled steam if such a thing could exist. He is easily as wet as if the rain were coming down vertically. Droplets collect on his face and hair as he moves through the fog until cupfuls of rainwater bounce along his pores tracing the contours of his forehead, nose, and jaw. The raw cold irritates his fingers pink and his nose drips, but it might just be the chilled steam condensing heavily enough to produce a small grape at the tip. As Turing churns mud, tests markers, and invents rhymes, the gray of the overcast day saturates into an overcast night. He takes the balmy air into his mouth, sugared with syrup from the trees and rotting matter from the earth. Deep in his lungs the forest ether becomes his breath. He is made of the same molecules as the plants and the dirt and the air. He ingests them and they become him. He pushes out the air along with some spittle which soaks into the forest floor while his breath drifts and is caught on a wind that takes his vapors high into the clouds until he is just a small, solitary animal below and the hills roll all the way to London, fifty miles south, where the capital is shutting down, hiding in the dark, grateful for the fog.

他只是数十亿粒子组成的庞大系统中的一个粒子。他通过不可逆转的交叉点、接触点、因果关系与所有其他粒子相连。他感到孤独，但从这个高高在上的鸟瞰视角来看，从历史的角度来看事实上，他是某种更宏大机制的一部分。虽然他无法从森林中离地面的距离、从伦敦、牛津和剑桥的大气视角，以及白金汉郡森林中的阿兰·图灵的视角看出这一点，但他与岛上其他地方的命运紧密相连。反过来，他们的命运也与他息息相关。因此，伦敦人（包括不止一位因恐惧而长满溃疡的舍伯恩学校毕业生）承担着生存的重担，却没有意识到他们的生命取决于一位年轻的数学家，尽管这个大首都的灯火管制严格，但他仍在泥地里挖洞。

He is just one particle in a vast system of billions of particles. He is connected to all the others through irrevocable crossings, points of contact, of cause and effect. He feels alone, but from this bird's-eye view high above and far away, and from history's view for that matter, he is part of some greater mechanism. Although he cannot tell from his proximity to the ground in the forest, from an atmospheric view that encompasses London, Oxford, and Cambridge, along with Alan Turing in the woods in Buckinghamshire, he is sewn tightly to the fate of the rest of the island. In turn, their fate is tied to his. And so Londoners (including more than one graduate of Sherborne School with a sorry bloom of ulcers seeded by a pit of dread) go about the burden of surviving, unaware that their lives depend on a young mathematician who digs in the mud even as the blackout is strictly enforced over the grand capital.

当艾伦在五十英里外的树下揉着泥巴时，防空警卫在伦敦东区巡逻，他们努力沿着蜿蜒的人行道忠实地前行，避免脚踝扭伤，或膝盖受伤。他们凭着记忆和直觉，沿着弯道和连接处前行，经过死胡同，沿着覆盖着他们脑海中手绘地图的街道迷宫的拱门和小巷前行，敲打窗户的框架，这些窗户又矮又歪的旧框架，透过遮光布的缝隙，明亮的光线勾勒出它们的轮廓。防空警卫们享受着他们在老城区夜晚的伦敦口音，他们敲打着窗户，大喊着：“你家有灯光！”直到里面的灯灭了，或者遮光窗帘被烦躁地钉回原位。

As Alan kneads sludge under the trees fifty miles away, air-raid wardens patrol the East End of London, trying to steer faithfully along the winding pavement and not to stumble in the dark with a twisted ankle or to fall atop a perpetually reinforced injury of the knee. They navigate by memory and intuition along turns and connections, past dead ends, along arcs and alleys covering the maze of streets in the hand-drawn map in their head to pound on the frames of windows, short and cockeyed old frames, outlined in bright shards of light shining through gaps in the blackout sheeting. The wardens, enjoying their cockney authority over the nights in the old city, pound and holler, “You’ve a light showing!” until the light inside is extinguished or the blackout curtain is irritably tacked back into place.

德国空军发动攻击，天空中云朵一朵朵地蒸发，没有人习惯这种宁静。装有三十六枚燃烧弹的燃烧弹爆炸开来，喷出厚厚的火花和火焰，橙色闪光四溅。一些炸弹无力地落在鹅卵石上，就像一只被剥皮的动物，仍然很烫，但很快就被几铲沙子掩埋了。其他炸弹卡在屋顶的拐角处或两座建筑物的交界处，或设法穿透窗户，它们会疯狂地蔓延火势，随着易燃疾病的蔓延，整个街区都会被烧毁。现在几乎没有人会向小火山块上泼水，因为最初的几个火山块在被浇水后爆炸，向四面八方发射出二十英尺远的致命水柱。今晚的情况也是如此。天空被橙色的闪光照亮，直到城市的一片片区域燃起火焰，伦敦在闪电战的野蛮打击下屈服和呻吟。

No one grows accustomed to the quiet just before the clouds evaporate one at a time across the sky as the Luftwaffe attacks. Molotov breadbaskets of thirty-six incendiary bombs burst open to spew thick trails of molten sparks and flame and a splatter of orange glitter. Some bombs thud lifelessly on cobblestone, like a flayed animal, still dangerously hot but quickly buried with a few shovelfuls of sand. Others stick in the crook of a rooftop or the join of two buildings or manage to penetrate a window, and these spread fire with vengeance, taking out entire blocks as the flammable sickness catches. Hardly anyone ever throws water on the small volcanic lumps anymore, not after the first few exploded upon being dowsed, projecting murderous lobs twenty feet in all directions. Tonight is more of the same. The sky lights up in orange flashes until swatches of the city shine with flames and London buckles and moans under the savage beating of the blitz.

每天晚上，伦敦人都会抱怨停电；但到了黎明，他们更加害怕阳光，因为雾气过滤后阳光很微弱，他们不得不评估损失。每天，从西区到泰晤士河，再到东边的圣保罗大教堂，他们的眼睛都带着悔恨垂下，因为白天考验着他们对家乡的记忆。经过五十七夜无情的轰炸，每个人都不得不问自己，自己的记忆是否能胜任这项任务。

Each night, Londoners grumble about the blackout; but by dawn they dread the sunlight even more, weak as it is through the filter of fog, as they are forced to take stock of the damage. Each day eyes sag with remorse, from the West End to the Thames, along east past St. Paul's Cathedral as the day tests their memory of their home. After fifty-seven nights of relentless bombardment each is forced to ask if his memory is up to the task.

在黑暗中，人们更容易想起东边老城周围的罗马城墙，以及黑衣修士车站外街角的小鞋匠店，这家店在大教堂巨大圆顶的阴影下忙碌，并受益于河水的吹拂。西区的剧院仍然开放，一些花园也幸存了下来。数百人睡在地铁站里，或者睡在菲利克斯和莱恩服装公司地下室的公共避难所里，哈多克斯夫人在那里经营着一家小卖部，供应豆子、吐司和淀粉汤，这些汤能即便牛肉和汤料的短缺会让他们失去肉食，他们仍然会吃掉这些肉。从黄昏到黎明，他们要忍受着空气污浊、拥挤不堪、卫生不堪的环境，但他们仍然对破晓时分感到不满，因为他们醒来后发现，大地的焦灼让他们的记忆变得混乱，而昨天，红砖维多利亚式建筑还像石头一样坚固。他们的眼睛里充满了可怕的城市截肢，直到他们被刺痛得流泪。只要天黑了，整个伦敦可能就完好无损——就像他们记忆中的那样。

In the darkness it is easier to recall the Roman wall around the old city in the east, the small cobbler's shop on the corner outside Blackfriars Station that labors in the shadow of the great dome of the cathedral and benefits from the cleansing draft off the river. The theaters that stencil the West End are still open and some gardens survive. Hundreds sleep in the underground stations or in public shelters in the basements of Felix and Lane's clothing firm where Mrs. Haddox runs a canteen serving beans and toast and starchy soups that manage to get eaten, even when shortages eliminate beef and flavor from the stock. Twelve hours from dusk until dawn pass in the stale air in cramped, unsanitary conditions, but still they resent the break of day when they emerge to have their memories confused by the scorch of earth where a redbrick Victorian had lived solid as stone just yesterday. Their eyes suck in a rash of hideous civic amputations until they water from the sting. As long as it stays dark, the whole of London might be intact—just as they remember it.

西北五十英里处，艾伦·图灵在树林里玩耍，哼着童话故事《白雪公主》中的童谣。对于防空警卫、平民和幸存者来说，他是谁？一个同性恋、一个基佬、一个教授类型的怪人。一个异教徒、一个无神论者、一个同性恋者。一个天才。一个英雄。但他们并不了解他，正如他不了解他们一样。对他来说，战争已经成为一场痴迷的游戏，他要从一串串毫无意义的代码中寻找模式，起初只是凭眼睛观察，然后通过符号逻辑和数字定律。他玩这个游戏时非常任性，如果输了，他就会摔门而出。他想赢。这项工作很耗费精力。它很有挑战性，甚至可能是不可能的。还有其他值得强调的事情。这让他很开心。

Fifty miles northwest, Alan Turing plays in the woods humming rhymes from the fairy tale “Snow White.” Who is he to the air-raid wardens, the civilians, the survivors? A homosexual, a fag, an eccentric of the professor type. A heathen, an atheist, a queer. A genius. A hero. But they are no more aware of him than he is of them. For him, the war has become an obsessive game of searching meaningless strings of code for patterns, by eye at first on a lark and then through symbolic logic and the laws of numbers. He plays this game with bratty intensity, storming out of a room with a slam of the door if he loses. He wants to win. The work is consuming. It is challenging, maybe even impossible. There is something else worth emphasizing. It makes him happy.

他总是在工作，即使是在散发着芳香的黑暗森林里。当他用手挖土铲去土块时，他发现了一棵树的根。一条穿越空间的路径。一条穿越地球的可能路径。然后一个想法充满了他的脑海，仿佛凭空而来。他认为这是原创的。然后他思考这个想法。然后他思考这个想法，思考原创性，关于这是他的想法意味着什么。这是他思想的产物，神经元的激发，他眼中的画面，按下按钮的固定结果。对泥土的反应。由机器执行的算法。

He is always working, even here in the sweet-smelling dark of the woods. As he digs his hands in the earth shoveling away clumps of dirt he comes upon the root of a tree. A path through space. One possible path through earth. Then an idea fills him, presents itself to him, as if from nowhere. It is original, he thinks. And then he thinks about the thought. And then he thinks about thinking about the thought, about originality, about what it means that it's his thought. A product of his mind, a firing of a neuron, a picture in his eye, a fixed consequence of the push of a button. A reaction to mud. An algorithm executed by a machine.

下棋、想点子或思考本身一定存在某种算法。按下按钮，机器就能执行精确的指令，给出答案，或下棋，或破解密码。但每个人的行为都大不相同。他们对相同的输入做出出乎意料的反应。也许其他人会在这里挖洞，产生完全不同的想法。也许其他人会想，泥巴很脏。或者，这里可以种西红柿。他思考偏好、倾向和欲望——这些是如何决定的。他想到他多么讨厌黄油米饭旁边的煮土豆。它们颜色相同，但一个是大块的，另一个是可怕的颗粒。这种组合足以让艾伦禁食。但他的朋友琼喜欢黄油米饭上浇着煮土豆。他和琼执行不同的算法。他们是不同的人，有不同的品味。想到这些，他又有了另一个想法：有许多不同的算法可能会产生一些类似人类的反应。但正确序列肯定比错误序列少得多——这些序列无法产生类似人类的反应。也许可以以某种方式丢弃大量错误算法，以便保留一小部分正确序列。但这就像他最初的想法一样，促使他思考思想。德国密码传输只有一个密钥。几乎不可能将其分离出来。但显然，大量可能的组合毫无用处；它们只是一堆空洞的泥土。如果他能制造一台机器来运行所有可能的组合，当组合出错时机器就会停止，那么他们就可以丢弃所有坏钥匙，把它们铲走。他们才有机会筛选剩下的，可能性要小得多。他们不应该试图找到一个正确的代码；他们应该试图铲除所有错误的代码。

There must be an algorithm for playing chess or for having an idea or for thinking itself. Press a button and a machine could execute the precise instruction and produce an answer or a move in a game of chess, or break a code. But then people all behave so differently. They respond so unexpectedly to the same input. Maybe someone else would dig here and have an entirely different thought. Maybe someone else would think, Mud is filthy. Or, Tomatoes could be grown here. He thinks about predilections, tendencies, and desires—how these are determined. He thinks about how he loathes boiled potatoes next to buttered rice. They are the same color but one comes in big lumps and the other horrid grains. The combination is enough to prompt Alan to fast. But his friend Joan loves her buttered rice topped with boiled potatoes. He and Joan execute different algorithms. They are different people with different tastes. Thinking about these thoughts he has another: There are many different algorithms that might produce some humanlike response. But surely there are many fewer right sequences than there are wrong sequences—sequences that could not produce a humanlike response. Maybe huge chunks of these wrong algorithms could be discarded somehow so that a smaller vein of correct sequences remain. But this is just like his original thought that precipitated the thought about thought. There is only one key to the encoded German transmission. It is nearly impossible to isolate. But huge possible combinations clearly lead nowhere; they are empty lumps of earth. If he could build a machine to run through possible combinations, a machine that stops when the combination goes wrong, then they could discard all of the bad keys, shovel them out of the way. They’d have a real chance of sifting through what's left, a far smaller number of possibilities. They shouldn’t be trying to find the one right code; they should be trying to shovel away all the wrong ones.

伦敦的天空开始塌陷，而他知道自己找到了答案。这让他胸中燃烧着一种兴奋。这让他感到一阵灼痛。

The sky is caving in over London and he knows he has an answer. It burns his chest—a kind of elation. It scalds him.

回家的路上，他感觉纳粹法典变得像丝绸一样柔软，他等不及第二天早上实施他的想法了。他浑身沾满泥巴——泥巴深深地印在指甲下，突出了每根手指被啃过的红色表皮，头发上露出了树林的痕迹——他开始奔跑。他自由地跑回家，没有婴儿车，也没有银块的负担。他的四肢松弛而纤细，他的手腕啪啪作响，他的双腿交替地向左、向右、向左、向右移动，他瘦削的身体皮肤微微摇晃，他放松下来，步履轻快。

As he starts home, he feels the Nazi code yield supple as silk and he can’t wait until morning when he can implement his idea. Covered in mud—mud rubbed deep under his nails emphasizing the gnawed, red cuticle of each and every finger, evidence of the woods poking from his hair—he begins to run. He runs home freely without the pram or the burden of the silver bullion. His limbs are loose and lank, his wrists snap as his legs reach in alternating scissors, left, right, left, right and the skin of his lean body jostles slightly as he relaxes into the rhythm of his stride.

他会永远记得自己这样奔跑。用他瘦削有力的四肢奔跑。奔跑时仿佛世界的命运都取决于他。

He will always remember running like this. Running with his lean strong limbs. Running as if the fate of the world depends on him.

艾伦已经订婚了。和一个女人订婚。自从他被政府密码学校征召入伍以来，她一直是他最好的朋友，这一点很重要。他记得她在 8 号小屋里，弯腰看着毫无意义的字母，脖子紧绷，水平地趴在桌子上，希望她的眼睛里能出现某种图案。他对她最清晰的记忆开始于那天早上，他从树林里醒来，他的想法几乎完全成形——一个彩色的幻象。中午，他来到 8 号小屋，脸上戴着防毒面具，松垮的裤子用一根绳子系着。她说：

Alan is engaged to be married. To a woman. She has been his best friend since he was drafted by the Government Code and Cypher School and this counts for something. He remembers her in Hut 8, bent over meaningless groups of letters, her neck tense and horizontal over the table hoping some pattern might stick in her eye. His clearest memory of her begins that morning after the woods when he wakes with his idea nearly fully formed—a Technicolor vision. He makes it to Hut 8 at noon with a gas mask strapped to his face and his sagging pants held up by a piece of string. And she says:

“说真的，艾伦，你戴着防毒面具骑着自行车过来会吓到白金汉郡的居民的。”

“Really, Alan, you are going to terrify the residents of Buckinghamshire riding your bike in here with that gas mask of yours.”

“防止花粉进入，琼。”

“Keeps the pollen out, Joan.”

“人们会认为我们在这里设计毒弹。”

“People will think we’re designing poison bombs in here.”

“但我们不是。我们正在解密。”

“But we’re not. We’re decrypting codes.”

“艾伦，最好让他们永远不知道我们在这里做什么，这样我们就不会引来这么多的关注。”

“Better that they should never think of what we’re doing in here, Alan, than draw such attention to ourselves.”

在布莱切利园被改造为英国密码破译中心的初期，人们在园内周围的灌木丛中安装了用于拦截德国无线电信号的天线，因此这座山上的豪宅和它的一系列小屋看起来就像一个精致的针垫。或者，必须承认，它看起来像一个密码破译中心。由于这违背了他们的秘密目标，当权者很快就质疑了自己的判断，将天线移到了岛上更小、更不显眼的拦截站。所有往返于 U 型潜艇的无线电传输都由德国海军恩尼格玛密码机加密，这台密码机只不过是一台精致的打字机。按下这台工业打字机上的一个键，一系列有线轮和反射就会将字母旋转到灯泡上的另一个字母上，然后读取并复制到加密信息中。恩尼格玛密码机能够产生大约一万亿亿种可能的组合。令人惊讶的是，竟然有人有胆量去破解每天都在变化的加密。随后，加密的海军通讯被转交给艾伦·图灵在 8 号小屋的负责人，他在那里负责对最新拦截的信息进行分析。他们在布莱切利拥有一个关键优势，那就是拥有一台近乎复制的恩尼格玛密码机。这台密码机是在 1925 年从德国购买的，当时并没有经过深思熟虑，被一家英国银行用于商业用途，直到波兰密码分析员给他们一台精确的复制品。如果他们找到转子和反射的排列，他们就可以输入加密文本并读出德国信息。

In the earliest days of Bletchley Park's conversion to the British center for code breakers, aerials to intercept German radio transmissions were planted in a thicket around the grounds so the mansion on the hill with its series of huts looked like an elaborate pincushion. Or, it had to be admitted, it looked like a center for code breaking. As this was counter to their secretive aims, the powers that be soon questioned their own judgment and the aerials were moved about the island to smaller, more inconspicuous intercept stations. All radio transmissions to and from the U-boats are encrypted on the German Naval Enigma machine, not much more than an elaborate typewriter. Press a key on the industrial-looking typewriter and the series of wired wheels and reflections rotates that letter to another on a bulb, which is then read and copied into the encrypted message. Enigma is capable of something like a hundred thousand billion billion possible combinations. It's a wonder that anyone has the audacity to approach a solution to the encryptions, which change daily. The coded naval transmissions are then relayed to Alan Turing's charge in Hut 8, where he oversees the dissection of the latest intercepts. They had the critical advantage at Bletchley of possessing a near-replica Enigma machine bought in Germany without conscious foresight for commercial use in a British bank in 1925 until that was replaced with an exact replica given to them by the Polish crypt-analysts. If they find the arrangement of rotors and reflections, they can type in the coded text and read off the German message.

艾伦的主意即将成型的那天早上，琼加班加点。她划掉一堆毫无意义的字母，尝试其他组合，充分利用她纤细白皙的手腕和修长、几乎像男人一样的手指的灵活性。她的手腕有十美分硬币那么大，从那里长出一双巨大的手，骨头和静脉密布。这些十美分硬币的底部是她的手臂，猎户星座的图案自然而然地被纹在朴素的棕色雀斑上。（艾伦解除婚约的那一天，这些肢体会像干枯的树枝一样挂在她身上，或者可能只是木棍。她巨大的手用沉重的重量把它们拉下来。他会觉得她纤细的手腕可能会断掉，一边期待地盯着它们，一边背诵奥斯卡·王尔德的话。）

The morning of Alan's nearly fully formed idea is Joan's double shift. She crosses out meaningless clots of letters and tries other combinations, making ample use of the flexibility of her thin white wrists and long, almost manly fingers. Her wrists are the size of dimes and from them sprout immense hands of bone and vein. At the base of these dimes are the stems of her arms where the constellation Orion was naturally tattooed in plain brown freckles. (The day Alan will break off the engagement, those limbs will hang from her like dry branches or maybe no more than sticks. Her huge hands pulling them down with dead weight. He will think her tiny wrists might break, and stare at them expectantly as he recites Oscar Wilde.)

她的头发又黑又卷。他曾经问过其他密码分析员琼是否漂亮，但他自己也不知道。答案并不重要，因为艾伦永远无法确定。她姿态完美，脊柱挺直，就像一个专注的孩子，举止中带着一种深深的吸引力，一丝早熟女孩的痕迹仍然依稀可见。她不是非常优雅，但也不笨拙。她在解密机周围操作时效率很高，甚至很自信。

Her hair is dark and wavy. He once asked one of the other cryptanalysts if Joan was pretty, being unable to decide for himself. The answer is irrelevant because Alan can never be sure. She has impeccable posture, her spine straight as an attentive child's, and she carries something deeply appealing in her mannerisms, a trace of the precocious girl still faintly visible. She isn’t extremely graceful but she isn’t clumsy either. She is efficient, even confident, as she maneuvers around the decryption machines.

她很高兴来到这里，并享受与艾伦的秘密订婚。虽然他们的订婚比他的性取向更为隐秘，但这并没有让她感到惊慌。她是一个接受和开放的人，这是她自己在社会中的地位强加给她的宽容。虽然英国公务员将她的头衔降为“语言学家”，但她被录用的原因与其他数学家完全一样，因为她的聪明才智和数学技能。她一直在研究射影几何，并且当她引起政府密码学校的注意时，她确信她的进步是相当有希望的。不久之后，她就发现自己住进了白金汉郡山上的布莱切利园的一座古老的维多利亚式豪宅，位于伦敦西北 50 英里处，工资比其他允许他们获得密码分析员头衔的数学家要低。艾伦和其他一些人试图安排将她的头衔改为 WRNS 军官，以提高她的薪水。皇家海军女子服务队的女士们在场外照看艾伦机器的转子，当机器完成任务并且咔嗒作响的开关安静下来时，她们就会打电话到 8 号小屋。但是在 8 号小屋工作，解密德国海军传输的琼宁愿接受较低的薪水也不愿做更丰厚的工作。

She is glad to be here and enjoys her secret engagement to Alan. Although their engagement is rather more covert than his sexuality, this foolishly hasn’t alarmed her. She is accepting and open-minded, a tolerance forced on her by her own position in society. Although the British civil service downgraded her title to “linguist,” she was recruited for the exact reason that the other mathematicians were, for her cleverness and mathematical skill. She had been studying projective geometry and was quite sure her progress was more than promising when she came to the attention of the Government Code and Cypher School. It wasn’t long before she found herself in the old Victorian mansion at Bletchley Park on the hill in Buckinghamshire, fifty miles northwest of London, earning rather poorer pay than the other mathematicians whose gender allowed them the title cryptanalyst. Alan and some of the others tried to arrange for her title to be changed to WRNS officer to enhance her pay. The ladies of the Women's Royal Naval Service tend the rotors of Alan's machines off-site, telephoning to Hut 8 when a machine concludes its task and the clattering switches fall quiet. But Joan, working in Hut 8, deciphering German naval transmissions, prefers the poorer pay in favor of the richer work.

艾伦确实向她提到过他的同性恋倾向。她很容易接受这个消息，主要是因为她不完全确定自己是否理解了“倾向”这个词。她选择了一个古怪的天才，而一个古怪的天才也选择了她。处理他凌乱的倾向、他奇怪的饮食倾向、他的强迫倾向并不容易——同性恋倾向并不是她最担心的。当然，她错了。艾伦应该更有力，比平时更坦率。他应该说，“我绝对没有异性恋倾向”，这样就可以澄清他的同性恋倾向比他最初的用词所暗示的更为绝对。

Alan did mention to her his homosexual tendencies. She took the news easily, mostly because she wasn’t completely sure she understood the term “tendency.” She chose an eccentric genius and an eccentric genius chose her. It will not be easy to deal with his unkempt tendencies, his peculiar dietary tendencies, his obsessive tendencies—the homosexual ones are not her most serious worry. Of course, she is wrong about this. Alan should have been more forceful, even more frank than usual. He should have said, “I have absolutely no heterosexual tendencies,” which would have clarified that his homosexuality is rather more absolute than his original word choice suggested.

在他把财宝埋进树林后的第二天早上，琼看着他，其他一切都似乎遥远了，伦敦炸弹的气味，被大海淹没的 U 型潜艇的吱吱声和嗡嗡声，机器的吱吱声。一切都安静了下来，甚至连恩尼格玛密码机按键的咔嗒声都听不见。她最喜欢他的脸当它静止如照片时。他那浓眉突出的眼睛看起来不像典型的英国人，也许这分散了人们的注意力，使他们没有注意到他的口音有多么英俊，尤其是当他不动、不说话、不笑的时候。她看着艾伦打开茶杯，他把茶杯可笑地拴在暖气片上，好像有人可能会把主人误认为艾伦以外的人，好像其他密码破译员会把嘴唇凑到他的私人杯子上，杯子的内壁被他总是泡得过头的茶染成了可怕的锈褐色。当他跪在暖气片前打开他的物品时，他的脚后跟张开了，她看到他试图洗掉裤子下摆的泥巴，而不是把衣服整件洗干净。当她顺着他的腿望去时，她不禁感到惊讶，尽管他今天早上可能在他房间的水槽里洗了袖口，但他并没有注意到裤子后面有两片沾满灰泥的树叶。

Joan watches him the morning after he buried his treasure in the woods, and everything else seems far away, the smell of the London bombs, the creak and drone of the U-boats stifled by the ocean, the cricketing of machines. It all goes quiet, even the click of the keys of the Enigma machine. She likes his face most when it is as still as a photograph. The way his dark eyebrows accentuate his eyes does not look typically English and maybe this distracts people from noticing how handsome the accent can be, especially when he isn’t moving or talking or laughing. She watches Alan unlock the tea mug he ludicrously keeps chained to a radiator, as though someone could possibly mistake the owner for someone other than Alan, as though any of the other cryptographers would put their lips to his personal cup, the inside walls horribly stained a rusty brown from the tea he always over-brews. As he kneels at the radiator to unlock his possession, his heels splay open and she sees where he tried to wash the mud from the bottom hem of his trousers instead of laundering the garment in its entirety. As she looks along his leg she can’t help but marvel that even as he washed the cuffs, probably in the sink of his room this morning, he didn’t notice the two leaves matted with gray mud into the seat of the trousers.

阿兰和他的计划。除了用钢链固定在加热装置上的杯子和他的安全藏银计划外，他还戴着政府发放的防毒面具来防过敏。他把闹钟系在腰上，用来计时他从布莱切利跑到伦敦的全程。还有他想在遇到困难时从手提箱里卖掉的剃须刀片，因为他不能透露他为国家服务的性质，所以他无法找到工作。他有机器来机械化思维和破解密码。她也是他的计划之一吗？有一个家和一个妻子来洗衣服，生孩子，照看房子。他偶尔会给她一个惊喜这些传统的社会观念，保留了他的家庭背景的遗迹。也许这些观念尽管他有许多其他怪癖，但仍然留存下来，因为它们与他的实际生活完全无关。

Alan and his schemes. In addition to the mug secured by steel links to the heating apparatus and his plan for the safe hiding of silver bullion, there is the government-issue gas mask he wears to defend himself against allergies. There is the alarm clock he tied to his waist to time his run from Bletchley nearly all the way to London. As well as the razor blades he wants to sell out of a suitcase if times get tough and he is unable to secure a job because he is unable to reveal the nature of his service to his country. There are his machines that mechanize thought and crack code. And she too, is she one of his schemes? To have a home and a wife to wash his clothes, bear his children, tend his house. He occasionally surprises her with these conventional social ideas, preserved relics of his family background. Maybe they survive despite all his other eccentricities because they are so utterly irrelevant to his actual life.

他用受伤的手指拍打她的试卷，皮肤被咬得生疼，留下一道长满老茧的疤痕，并在她那几页数学纸上寻找昨晚问题的答案，这时，世界轰然崩塌的喧嚣再次降临到她头上。

He brings the noise of the world crashing back upon her as he slaps his mangled fingers atop her papers, his cuticles bitten raw into a calloused scar, and scratches her pages of mathematics for a solution to last night's problem.

“艾伦，你割伤了自己。”他下巴上的剃须刀伤痕被凝结的血液封住了，看起来更加糟糕。

“Alan, you’ve cut yourself.” The shaving cut on his chin is sealed with congealed blood, making it look worse.

“是的。然后我就晕过去了，”他抱着自己的躯干笑着。

“Yes. And I fainted,” he hugs his torso as he laughs at himself.

他避开了她的目光，尽管他们共同经历了这场小小的灾难。琼让这种失望只触动了她一秒钟，然后她同样被加密的好奇心和艾伦的好奇心所吸引，她也在笑，虽然更害羞，下巴缩进肩膀的杯中，使她那串串的珠子呈现出柔和的曲线，这串珠子勾勒出了她坚强的脊柱。

He avoids her eyes, even as they share this minor calamity. Joan lets this disappointment touch her only for a second before she is equally swept up in the curiosity of the encryptions and the curiosity of Alan and she is laughing too, if more shyly, chin tucked into the cup of her shoulder, introducing a gentle curve to the string of beads that define her strong spine.

这场不幸的订婚并不完全是艾伦的错。

The ill-fated engagement isn’t entirely Alan's fault.

他的大脑里缺少了一些东西，一个过滤器，一个解释器，一种简单的机制，可以解释微笑的含义或控制面部数百块肌肉的情感流。即使是布莱切利园住宅里照看房子的老妇人，在扫地时也像是普通事情的先知，她一边扫着人行道，一边在他来来往往时发表一些讽刺的评论。“你的琼小姐想要的不仅仅是一场棋局，图灵大师。”这些话出自一个爱管闲事的管家之口，显而易见，却又毫无意义，但对艾伦来说，这些话出自一位圣人的妙语，他知道一些无论他多么专注都无法从生活中获取的东西。她对他真正的忘却感到恼火，说：“她想成为你的新娘，图灵大师。”她一边扫地一边用力地甩着她那一头卷曲的头发，力气之大让艾伦想起了印度保姆过去在洗澡时把他擦得通红的样子。他的父亲是一名英国公务员，驻扎在次大陆。

Something is missing in his brain, a filter, an interpreter, a simple mechanism that explains the meaning of a smile or the current of feeling directing the hundreds of muscles in a face. Even the old woman who tends house at his residence in Bletchley Park seems a prophet on commonplace matters as she sweeps the walkway and makes wry comments as he comes and goes. “Your Miss Joan is looking for more than a chess game, Master Turing.” Obvious, inane reflections of a meddling housekeeper but to Alan they are words of brilliance from a sage who knows things he cannot extract from life no matter how intently he focuses his attention. Exasperated with his genuine oblivion she says, “She wants to be your bride, Master Turing,” and shakes her wiry shroud of hair as vigorously as she sweeps, with such punishing force it reminds Alan of how the Indian nannies used to scrub him red raw in the bath when his father was stationed on the subcontinent as a British civil servant.

那天他在 8 号小屋比前几天更笨手笨脚。下午，在清理了转子设置、收集了信息、测试了婴儿床之后，他和琼订婚了。你不能说他已经向她求婚了，至少不是按照传统意义上的。但是，当他回到寄宿公寓，在满是灰尘的台阶上踩着大块的泥土时，他已经订婚了。所以，订婚在一定程度上是管家的错。这也是琼的错。但大部分，必须承认，这是艾伦的错。

All that day he was even clumsier at Hut 8 than he was all the days before. By the end of the afternoon after rotor settings were cleared, messages were collected, and cribs were tested, he and Joan were engaged to be married. You couldn’t claim he had asked her to marry him exactly, not in any conventional sense. But still, by the time he retraced his steps to the boardinghouse and tracked chunky lumps of mud across dusted steps, he was engaged. So, in part, the engagement is the housekeeper's fault. It is Joan's fault too. But mostly, it has to be admitted, it is Alan's fault.

十一小时的轮班结束了，连续数月紧张的战术、加密和机器轮班也结束了。现在是半夜。艾伦和琼还醒着，但已经累得可以下盘棋了。

It is the end of an eleven-hour shift, the end of too many months of tense turns in tactics and encryptions and machines. It is the middle of the night. Alan and Joan are still awake but just exhausted enough for a game of chess.

“你是一位英雄，艾伦。”

“You’re a hero, Alan.”

他没有从比赛中抬起头，但他的头几乎与肩膀齐平。他很尴尬。

He doesn’t look up from the game, but his head sort of bobs about nearly level with his shoulders. He is embarrassed.

“我们都是英雄，琼，”他对她的白皇后说，身体过分倚在棋盘上；他敞开的海军蓝夹克下口袋里有两个棋子从格子里滑出来，他看着棋子移动。他喜欢从空中俯瞰棋盘和他们上演的静态战争。

“We’re all heroes, Joan,” he says to her white queen, leaning too far over the board; the lower pocket of his open navy jacket slides two pawns out of their squares as he looks over the moves. He likes to get a nearly aerial view of the checked board and the static war they enact.

“要知道，我是个女英雄，”她模仿一个任性的青少年说道。她眯着眼睛瞪着他，有点失望，因为她的判决竟然是指控。

“If anything, I’m a heroine, you know,” she says in imitation of a petulant adolescent. She glares at him with narrowed eyes, a bit disappointed that her sentence landed on an accusation.

“对我来说，你永远都是英雄，”艾伦从鼻子里窃笑道，并没有完全意识到他刚才所造成的困境的转折。

“To me you’ll always be a hero,” Alan sniggers through his nose, not fully realizing the twist in the pinch he just delivered.

琼知道自己会赢得这场比赛，这让她有些满意。她已经看到，只需要再走两步，艾伦不太可能会阻止。他又在寻找一个整体模式，试图发明一条规则来制定正确的策略，这样他就会特别忽略这个简单的现实。棋盘是她的，是一个破旧的纸板口袋游戏，不是为了经受艾伦自制棋子的交通而设计的。当棋子最初排列在相对的两侧时，棋盘中间向上起皱，然后随着游戏的进行，棋盘中间向下凹陷。艾伦戴着防毒面具，在布莱切利附近的一个裸露的粘土坑里挖土，然后试图保持平衡，骑车回家，方向盘边缘挂着一把粘土，这一定很壮观。他在自己的房间里塑造了这些棋子，并在自己的炉灶上烘烤它们。他做了额外的棋子，但还不够，他们不能用一套完全没有损坏的棋子来玩。三分之一的人在某种程度上受到了伤害，但他们的身份仍然很容易确定，尽管她的一个骑士可以兼作棋子。

Joan takes some satisfaction in knowing she is going to win this game. She can already see it will take only two more moves that Alan is not likely to obstruct. He is looking for a global pattern again, trying to invent a rule for generating the right strategy so that he misses in particular this one reality, simple as it is. The board is hers, a worn cardboard pocket game not intended to weather the traffic of Alan's homemade pieces. It puckers upward in the middle when the pieces are initially aligned on opposing sides and then dips downward in the middle as the game advances. Alan must have looked quite a sight wearing a gas mask, digging in an exposed clay pit near Bletchley, and then attempting to balance as he cycled home with fistfuls of clay hanging over the rim of the steering wheel. He molded the pieces in his room and baked them on his own hob. He made extras, though not enough that they can play with an entirely undamaged set. One-third are broken to some extent but their identity is still pretty easy to ascertain, although one of her knights could double as a pawn.

艾伦迈出了一步。谁知道他在想什么？经过深思熟虑之后，这一步看起来是随机的。他仍然悬在棋盘上，所以她必须伸手到他的头发下找到主教，然后毫不犹豫地将棋子移到位。

Alan makes a move. Who knows what he is thinking? It looks random after all that deliberation. He still hangs over the board so that she has to reach under the fringe of his hair for her bishop as she shifts the piece into place with neither deliberation nor hesitation.

艾伦觉得她没有认真考虑自己的策略，这让他很惊讶，他大叫道：“琼！”他伸长脖子看着她，但眼睛没有直视她。他的嘴难以置信地睁大了双眼，他低头看了看比赛，又抬头看了看她几次，然后再次喊道：“琼！”然后他困惑地笑了起来。

Amazed by what he perceives as her lack of considered thought over her strategy, Alan shouts, “Joan!” and cranes his neck to look up at her, though not square in the eyes. His mouth hangs open with disbelief and he looks down at the game and up at her a few times before shouting again, “Joan!” and then he chuckles, bewildered.

“我知道自己在做什么，”她说道，并且她也确实这么做了。

“I know what I’m doing,” she says, and she does.

他们可能会赢得这场战争。她发现自己焦虑地担心战争将要发生什么。她既有希望和解脱，又担心艾伦为她制定的计划会失败，她将孤身一人。她希望艾伦能和她一起担心。“战争结束后，我们就会自由。我们会在其中发挥一些作用。”

They might win this war. She catches herself fretting anxiously over what will happen then. There's hope and relief but also fear that Alan's scheme for her will fail, that she will be alone. She wants Alan to fret with her. “When the war ends, we’ll be free. We’ll have played some part in that.”

虽然她可能想到了最终结婚的自由，但他的脑海中并没有出现这样的迷宫。一个人同时想到了这么多图像。有这么多不同的想法和不同的意识水平。很难沟通或见证。“自由”这个词出现在他的脑海中，这是冲动和转变的连锁反应后的最终产物，直到它成为唯一幸存的想法。他的表情变得阴沉，但他假装专注于他的战术，摆弄着他亲手塑造的干枯碎片。这些小雕像就是他自由意志的证明吗？“我们永远不自由，琼。”

While she may have in mind the freedom to finally marry, this is not where he is led through the labyrinth of his mind. So many images occurring to a person at once. So many different thoughts and different levels of awareness. So hard to communicate or to witness. The word “freedom” emerges in his mind, the final output after a chain reaction of impulses and transformations until it is there, the one surviving thought. His expression darkens but he pretends to concentrate on his war tactics, fidgeting with the dry broken pieces he molded with his own hands. Are these very figurines proof of his free will? “We’re never free, Joan.”

“艾伦，你是故意挑起争端，只是为了搞笑吗？”

“Alan, are you contentious on purpose, just to be ridiculous?”

“我们并不自由。我们都不自由。没有自由意志这回事。我不知道。我不这么认为。如果一台机器可以机械地添加一串数字，那么它完全是被决定的，根本没有行使自由意志。”

“We’re not free. None of us. There's no such thing as free will. I don’t know. I don’t think so. If a machine can mechanically add a list of numbers, it is entirely determined and not at all exercising free will.”

“但这只是一种死记硬背的过程，没有表现出任何思考的证据。”

“But that's just a rote process; it shows no evidence of thought.”

“就因为它简单吗？Enigma 是一台机器；结果加密完全由配置决定，更加复杂，但不再自由。”

“Just because it's simple? Enigma is a machine; the outcome of an encryption is completely determined by the configuration, more elaborate, but no more free.”

“这仍然不是思想，艾伦，不是人类的、独立的、自由的思想和行动。Enigma 只是一台打字机。我按下一个键，这个键会变成哪个字母是完全固定的。”

“It's still not thought, Alan, not human, independent, free thought and action. Enigma is just a typewriter. I strike a key and it is entirely fixed which letter that key transforms into.”

“是的，完全确定。”

“Yes, it is entirely determined.”

“谜团是一台机器，不是活生生的人，”就像我一样，她快要哭了。就像我一样。

“Enigma is a machine, not a living, breathing person,” like me, she is getting near to crying. Like me.

“我们也是机器，琼。比这复杂得多，但仅此而已。总有一天会有机器，像人类的计算机一样，只是电子的。机电计算机。战后我打算造一台，也许会借鉴我们机器的一些东西，但我心里有一个更通用的设计。它可以加、除或计算任意数量的任务。它将是通用的，就像回答数学问题的通用机器一样。只有这台机器是真实的，而不仅仅是一种逻辑上的可能性。”他笑着，仿佛在自言自语，简单地说：“我要造一个大脑。”

“We are machines too, Joan. Far more elaborate but that's all. One day there will be machines, like human computers, only electrical ones. A mechanical-electrical computer. I’m going to build one after the war, maybe taking something of our machines but I have a more general design in mind. It will add or divide or compute any number of tasks. It will be universal, like the universal machine that answers mathematical questions. Only this one will be real, not just a logical possibility.” And grinning as if to himself he says simply, “I’m going to build a brain.”

“它会活着吗？”她指责这个荒谬的建议。我是，她现在想纠缠他，她的脸颊因怨恨而刺痛，我是活着的，是一个人，一个自由的人。她沮丧地知道艾伦不会认出她的恶意。

“It will be alive?” She accuses with the absurdity of the suggestion. I am, she wants to badger him now and her cheeks are prickling with resentment, I’m alive, a human being, a free person. In frustration she knows Alan will not recognize her venom.

“它会有电。我不知道。它不是活的？它是活的？你问我什么，琼，它有灵魂吗？没有灵魂，没有这种东西。”

“It will have electricity. I don’t know. It's not alive? It's alive? What are you asking me, Joan, does it have a soul? There is no soul, no such thing.”

琼没有争辩这一点。她和他一样虔诚地信奉无神论。她的父亲是牧师，她永远无法假装。他的女儿甜美、聪明，举止彬彬有礼，坚强即便在她很小的时候，他就已经将这种存在感带到了现代。她端坐着，听着他的布道，她的海军蓝连衣裙的白领子上方露出了脊椎骨，苍白的皮肤间露出了小珠子。他的女儿很敏锐，总是问“为什么”，直到他希望她完全无礼，然后可以惩罚她。但她并不无礼，只是相信自己思维的有效性，无法相信一个不理性的上帝。无法相信上帝。她可怜他，希望自己可以撒谎，欺骗他。她可怜她的父亲，因为他为她没有的灵魂而深感悲痛。“纳粹认为人类很弱，但他们的机器是无敌的。但我们打败了他们的机器。”

Joan does not argue the point. She shares his devout atheism. Her father the minister could never get her to pretend. His sweet, brilliant daughter with the polite manner and strong presence, even as a very young girl. She listened to his sermons, sitting tall, the vertebrae poking above the white collar of her navy blue dress showing as little beads through her pale skin. His perceptive daughter, always asking “why” until he wished she were downright insolent and he could punish her. But she wasn’t insolent, just convinced by the effectiveness of her own thinking, unable to believe in a God who wasn’t rational. Unable to believe in God. She pitied him, wished she could lie, deceive him. She pitied her father as he mourned so heavily for the soul she didn’t have. “The Nazis think humans are weak but their machines are invincible. But we beat their machines.”

“但我们是机器。机器只是打败了其他机器。有一天，计算机会像我们一样思考。它们会自由吗？还是它们只是坚定的机器，执行它们被配置来执行的复杂过程？我们自由吗？还是我们只是坚定的机器，注定要执行我们每个人被配置来执行的复杂过程？”仿佛在举例说明，他终于移动了他的棋子。他认为他距离实施他的游戏计划只有三步之遥。他在这场游戏中以及在生活中的弱点是，他从不为别人的行为做好准备。它们是预先确定的，但太复杂了，无法解决或预测，而且有些规则他根本不擅长应用。

“But we are machines. Machines just beat other machines. One day the computers, they’ll think just as we do. Will they be free? Or are they just determined machines carrying out the elaborate processes they are configured to execute? Are we free? Or are we just determined machines, bound to carry out the elaborate processes that each of us is configured to execute?” As if in illustration, he finally moves his pawn. He thinks he is just three moves from implementing his game plan. His weakness in this game, and in life, is that he is never prepared for how others will act. They are predetermined but too complex to solve or predict, and there are rules that he is just no good at applying.

“但我们的机器都不会思考。它们不会做出任何实际决定。”

“But none of our machines think. They don’t make any actual decisions.”

“还没有，还没有。但我们才刚刚开始。没必要为每项任务建造不同的机器。一台通用机器将管理所有任务。这将是一个编程问题通用机器可以做不同的工作。布莱切利的一万名工作人员，在字母亮起时写下字母，机械地改变转子，将被一台机器取代。齿轮的机械变化将对应一台电子机器的不同指令。而且不仅仅是那些不需要动脑的工作，还有密码分析员的工作。最终指令本身将成为机器的领域。然后，琼，它们就会思考。”

“Not yet, not yet. But we’ve just gotten started. It won’t be necessary to build a different machine for each task. One universal machine will manage all tasks. It will be a matter of programming the universal machine to do different jobs. All these ten thousand people working at Bletchley writing down letters as they light up, mechanically changing the rotors, will be replaced by one machine. A mechanical change of the wheels will correspond instead to different instructions for the one electronic machine. And not just the mindless jobs but the jobs of the cryptanalysts too. Eventually the instructions themselves will be the domain of the machines. And then, Joan, then they will think.”

“你所说的‘思考’是什么意思？它怎么能思考？你怎么知道机器是否在思考？”

“What do you mean ‘think’? How can it think? How would you even know if a machine was thinking?”

“问吧。”

“Ask it.”

“问它？”

“Ask it?”

“是的，如果它能够模仿有意识的思考，那我们又有什么资格说它没有这样做呢？”

“Yes, if it can imitate conscious thinking, then who are we to say it is not doing so.”

琼在心里测试着自己的无神论，她停顿了一下。“如果我们只是在执行程序，那么是谁编写的程序？”

There is a pause as Joan internally tests her own atheism. “And if we are just executing programs, who did the programming?”

“自然选择。天文和化学力量促使大脑发生变异。我们理解数学，因为我们是由服从数学的力量创造的。这就是为什么我们能够发现数字及其关系，不是因为我们感知到了另一种现实——哥德尔就是这么认为的。但因为这是我们编程的一部分。”然后他补充道，“有人告诉我哥德尔有点奇怪。”

“Natural selection. Astronomical and chemical forces prodded the brain to mutate. We understand mathematics because we are created by forces that obey mathematics. That is why we can discover numbers and their relations, not because we perceive another reality—that's what Gödel thinks. But because it is part of our programming.” And then he adds, “I am told Gödel is a little strange.”

“噢，他有点奇怪是吗？”

“Oh he's a little strange is he?”

“是的。几年前，我差点在普林斯顿见过他，但他精神崩溃了，在我在高等研究院的那一年。当时我希望见到的一些逻辑学家都没有来，但除了哥德尔，我想我并不介意缺席任何一个人。”

“Yes. I almost met him once in Princeton a few years ago but he had a nervous breakdown and returned to Vienna during my year at the Institute for Advanced Study. Some of the logicians I hoped to meet then were absent but I don’t think I minded very much missing any of them except Gödel.”

坦率。他就是这样，坦率。这让琼既喜欢又怨恨。“我猜他天生就很奇怪。就像我认识的其他人一样。”

Guileless. That's what he is, guileless. This stirs Joan's fondness as much as her resentment. “I guess he is just programmed to be strange. Like some others I know.”

“是的。” 浑然不知。艾伦很坦诚，也很无知。

“Yes.” Oblivious. Alan is guileless and oblivious.

“艾伦，你向我解释哥德尔不完备定理时说过，有些真陈述永远无法被证明。对吗？所以哥德尔证明了，即使无法从逻辑上证明，我们也能识别真陈述？”

“Alan, when you explained Gödel's incompleteness theorems to me, you said that there were true statements that could never be proven. Isn’t that right? So Gödel proved that we can recognize true statements even if they can’t be logically proven?”

“是的。”

“Yes.”

“所以，如果一台机器被编程为完全合乎逻辑，如果它只能遵循一个又一个的逻辑步骤，它怎么可能识别出这些真实但无法证明的陈述呢？如果它不能像你我一样清楚地看到真相，因为它盲目地遵循一系列指令，那么我们怎么能称它为智能呢？我想我是想问，哥德尔定理，以及你自己的定理，是否意味着机器永远无法思考？”

“So if a machine is programmed to be perfectly logical, if it can only follow one logical step after another, how could it ever recognize one of these true but unprovable statements? And if it can’t see a truth as plainly as you or I can because it blindly follows a series of instructions, then how can we call it intelligent? I guess I’m trying to ask if Gödel's theorems, and indeed your own, imply that machines can never think?”

艾伦情不自禁地微笑着，他快速地点头，在膝盖上坐立不安。当琼这样的时候，他爱她。他真的以他的方式爱她。“我想说，必须公平对待机器。我们想要的不是一台万无一失的机器，而是一台智能机器。如果一台机器被期望是万无一失的，它就不可能同时是智能的。哥德尔定理几乎完全暗示了这一点。当我们为一台机器编程时，我们只想让它启动。我想，我们真正想要的是建造一台能够适应的机器，这样它就像任何从简单开始的生物一样编程并进化出复杂的智能。然后我们就会拥有它们——像我们一样有生命的机器。像我们一样自由或不自由。”

Alan smiles uncontrollably as he nods rapidly and fidgets about on his knees. He loves Joan when she is like this. He really loves her in his way. “I would say that fair play must be given to the machine. It is not an infallible machine we want but an intelligent machine. If a machine is expected to be infallible, it cannot also be intelligent. Gödel's theorem implies almost exactly this. When we program a machine, we only want to get it started. What we really want, I suppose, is to build a machine that can adapt so that it is like any living thing that starts from a simple program and evolves a complex intelligence. Then we will have them—machines that are as alive as we are. As free or as not free as us.”

他停下来咬着手指。“必须允许机器与人类接触，以便它能够适应人类的标准。国际象棋游戏可能更适合这个目的，因为对手的举动会自动提供这种接触。”

He stops to chew on his fingers. “The machine must be allowed to have contact with human beings in order that it may adapt itself to their standards. The game of chess may perhaps be rather suitable for this purpose, as the moves of the opponent will automatically provide this contact.”

“作为你的人类对手，艾伦，我很荣幸能够为你提供一些适当的标准。”当他这样的时候，她也爱他。她爱他，打结的头发，黏糊糊的肤色，肮脏的衣服，等等。这么晚了，她自己的头发也比艾伦的头发打理得好不了多少。它卷曲，卷发散落，但她知道他和她一样不在乎。“你怎么能写出让机器适应的指令呢？也许这是不可能的，正是我们的这种适应和改变的能力让我们自由。”

“As your human opponent, Alan, I’m honored to be able to provide you with some proper standards.” She loves him too when he is like this. She loves him, knotted hair, sticky complexion, filthy clothes, and all. Her own hair is not much better kept than Alan's at this late hour. It is frizzy and the curls have fallen loose but she knows he doesn’t care any more than she does. “How could you write instructions that allow a machine to adapt? Maybe this won’t be possible and it's exactly this ability of ours to adapt and change that makes us free.”

“是的，我们会改变，但改变的方式是确定的。我们的内部配置会读取一些输入，从而产生改变我们内部配置的输出。所以我们会改变。这不是自由。我们从讨厌西兰花变成喜欢西兰花。这不是自由意志。”

“Yes, we change, but in a determined way. There is some input that is read by our internal configurations to produce an output that changes our internal configuration. So we change. This isn’t freedom. We go from hating broccoli to liking broccoli. This isn’t free will.”

“那么创造性的飞跃、直觉的飞跃呢？”

“What about creative leaps, leaps of intuition?”

“神经元在其他神经元附近发射，发送物理信号。创造性飞跃是不可避免的，固定在内部配置中并接收输入。”

“Neurons fire near other neurons, sending physical signals. The creative leap was inevitable, fixed in an internal configuration and the input received.”

“如果有人能改变你的配置会怎么样？给你一种可以改变你感觉的药物。”

“What if someone could change your configuration? Give you a drug that changes how you feel.”

“如果我的结构发生改变，那么，是的，我会有不同的欲望，会做出不同的选择。但那样就不是我了。我会死而复生。你被设定为琼·克拉克。你所做的选择实际上只是一系列复杂的内部转子的输出。你感觉自由，但你并不自由。我也不自由。”

“If my very construction were changed, then, yes, I would have different desires, would make different choices. But then it wouldn’t be me. I would be dead and gone. You are configured to be Joan Clarke. The choices you make are really just the output of a complex series of internal rotors. You feel free, but you are not. And neither am I.”

她愤怒地抓起骑士，将棋子移到合适的位置，用断开的力量将小雕像的顶部掰掉，然后得意洋洋地说：“将军。”

Angrily, she grabs her knight, shifts the piece into position, snapping the top off the figurine with the force of her disconnect as she gloats, “Checkmate.”

他惊讶地抹了抹额头，嘴巴张得大大的，扫了一眼棋盘，寻找他想象到的所有失败步骤。他咧嘴笑着，实际上很高兴，他仍然高高地跪在地上，接受了这个结果。然后他跪下来，说：“我的英雄。来吧，琼，我们织毛衣吧。你可以教我如何完成我做的手套。”

He smears his forehead in amazement and his mouth drags open as he scans the board for all the lost moves he imagined. Grinning, actually delighted, he comes to grips with this outcome, still perched high up on his knees. Then he drops onto his heels and says, “My hero. Come, Joan, let's knit. You can show me how to finish the gloves I’ve made.”

英国威姆斯洛，1952 年

WILMSLOW, ENGLAND. 1952

1 月 23 日，霍利米德缺少了以下物品。一瓶已打开的雪利酒、一件干净的衬衫、一条破旧的裤子、一双不起眼的鞋子、一套还算不错的剃须刀、几把未曾使用过的渔刀和一个深受喜爱的指南针。霍利米德是一座半独立式维多利亚式住宅，位于中产阶级小镇威姆斯洛，位于曼彻斯特以南十英里处，环境舒适。艾伦·图灵在这里继续他的战后生活，并受邀监督曼彻斯特大学一台大型计算机的设计。

Here's what was missing from Hollymeade on January 23. An opened bottle of sherry, a clean shirt, a worn pair of trousers, unspectacular shoes, a reasonable set of razors, underused fishing knives, and a much-loved compass. Hollymeade is a semidetached Victorian house in the middle-class town of Wilmslow, located a comfortable ten miles south of Manchester, where Alan Turing continues his postwar life with an appointment to oversee design of a massive computer at the University of Manchester.

2 月 3 日，艾伦亲自去了警察局。他从线人那里得知了窃贼的名字。与此同时，线人坐在街对面的长椅上等待。

On February 3, Alan went to the police station in person. He had discovered the name of the burglar, given to him by an informant. Meanwhile the informant waited on a bench across the street.

阿诺德·默里。告密者。十九岁时，他的皮肤已经很薄，头发稀疏，信念也很薄弱。他脸色苍白眼睛和头发都泛着淡色，仿佛颜色无法粘附，就像他无法坚持任何东西一样。他无法维持工作。他无法维持与女人的关系。他无法维持与男人的关系。不幸的是，他所维持的，是一个男孩的表情，他目睹了母亲被他并不太喜欢的父亲殴打。他曾试图搭便车从曼彻斯特贫民区逃到伦敦，在那里他继续与饱受虐待的母亲和偶尔打工的父亲生活在一起。但是在一次拙劣的盗窃导致缓刑后，他很快又回到了这个似乎无法逃脱的贫民窟，那里充满了寒冷、阴雨、失业和绝望。由于缺乏更好的想法，他只能在曼彻斯特的牛津街上漂泊，过着漂泊的生活，希望能坚持一些东西。

Arnold Murray. The informant. At nineteen his skin is already thin, his hair is thin, his convictions are thin. He is pale with pale eyes and pale hair as though color won’t adhere, just as he won’t adhere to anything. He can’t maintain a job. He can’t maintain a relationship with a woman. He can’t maintain a relationship with a man. What he does maintain, unfortunately, is the expression of a boy who watched his mother get a beating from a father he never much liked. He once tried to escape by hitchhiking to London from the Manchester ghetto in which he continues to live with his battered mother and occasionally employed father. But he was swiftly returned to the cold and rain, unemployment and hopelessness of this same seemingly inescapable slum after a poorly executed theft resulted in a probationary sentence. Lacking better ideas, he drifts along Oxford Street in Manchester as he drifts through life, hoping to stick to something.

艾伦在剑桥大学读书时，维特根斯坦经常被人说起他在曼彻斯特大学学习航空学时，经常在牛津街散步。牛津街上酒吧、商店昏暗，行人寥寥，在街角和十字路口，很容易遇到一些粗鲁的、甚至可能是胡子拉碴的年轻小伙子。但实际上，维特根斯坦在街上散步是因为偶尔看到性感的男妓而感到既着迷又害怕。他从不勾引男妓，但他会跑回家，用幼稚的密码记录下自己的经历和欲望（以防有人偷看他的笔记本）。维特根斯坦的才华被夸大了，这让曼彻斯特的肮脏街道变得神话般，艾伦不时想亲自去牛津街散步，希望能遇到一个胡子拉碴的年轻小伙子。他真的这么做了。

When Alan was at Cambridge, gossip used to circulate around Wittgenstein and the walks he would take along Oxford Street when he studied aeronautics at the University of Manchester. With its dark pubs and shops and anonymous pedestrians, Oxford Street provides corners and intersections at which to cruise for a bit of rough, maybe a poorly shaven young bloke. But really Wittgenstein's laps along the street were encouraged by fascination and terror at the occasional sight of a sensual boy prostitute. He never picked one up but he would race home to record his experiences and his desires in a childish code (in case anyone should steal a look over his notebooks). The exaggerations of Wittgenstein's prowess mythologized the sordid strip in Manchester so that from time to time Alan thought he would try a walk along Oxford Street himself with the hopes of meeting a poorly shaven young bloke. And so he did.

阿诺德假装欣赏商店橱窗，引起了艾伦的注意。他本以为艾伦会邀请他到废弃的铁路拱门进行一次短暂的私下约会，但这并不在艾伦考虑的选项之列。相反，艾伦邀请他到家里吃一顿正经的午餐，餐桌在艾伦的管家的帮助下布置得漂漂亮亮。尽管艾伦长期不善社交，但他出生于中上阶层，甚至继承了阶级的某些特征，随意选择生活方式、道德和举止，随意拒绝他人。他的地位和成就使他成为阿诺德在街头所希望的更好的伙伴。这是对他糟糕生活的补偿，阿诺德认为这至少是他应得的。他们的恋情就这样开始了。

Having caught Alan's eye while pretending to admire a shop window, Arnold might have expected an invitation to the abandoned railway arches for a brief, illicit encounter but that was not among the short list of options Alan had considered. Instead Arnold was invited for a visit to Alan's home for a proper lunch, the table arranged handsomely with the help of Alan's housekeeper. Despite his chronic social tactlessness, Alan nonetheless had been born into upper-middle-class privilege and even adopted certain trappings of his class, randomly selecting modes, morals, and mannerisms and randomly rejecting others. His status and accomplishment made him better company than Arnold could have hoped for on the streets. This was the compensation for his crummy life that Arnold believed was at least his due. And so their affair began.

我们一起吃了两次晚餐。喝了茶。晚上在壁炉前的地毯上聊天。一起度过了几个夜晚。虽然钱确实易手了（从艾伦到阿诺德），但严格来说，这并不是卖淫。

There were two dinners together. Some tea. Late evening talks on a throw rug in front of the fire. Some nights spent together. Though money did change hands (from Alan's to Arnold's), it was not, strictly speaking, prostitution.

然后艾伦的钱包里又少了钱。双方互相指责，争吵，生闷气，道歉，尝试和解。然后霍利米德被洗劫一空。虽然阿诺德可能没有抢走艾伦的雪利酒、衬衫、裤子、鞋子、剃须刀、刀具或他心爱的指南针，但可以断定盗窃是他的错。在牛津街的一家酒吧里，他确实向一位朋友吹嘘过他们的关系——除了与一位著名的大学学者有联系外，他没有什么可吹嘘的——而那个在酒吧和街头挑选不当的伙伴就是从艾伦手中抢走这些奇怪物品的罪魁祸首。个人财产。阿诺德·默里对这种喝了酒后做出的轻率行为感到十分羞愧，这种说法并不准确，但至少他感到尴尬甚至后悔。当艾伦把信息传递给当地警察局的警察时，懊悔不已的阿诺德在街对面的长椅上等着。第二天下午，两个侦探——一个是大个子威尔斯先生，另一个是小个子里默先生——按响了艾伦家的门铃。

Then there was money missing from Alan's wallet. Accusations. Some bickering. Some sulking. Apologies. A tentative reconciliation. And then Hollymeade was ransacked. While Arnold may not have robbed Alan of the sherry, the shirt, the trousers, the shoes, the razors, the knives, or the much-loved compass, it would not be unfair to conclude that the theft was in fact his fault. He did brag of their association to a friend over a third pint in a pub on Oxford Street—he had little else to boast about besides a liaison with a noted university scholar—and that rather poorly chosen associate from the pubs and the streets was the culprit who relieved Alan of this odd assortment of personal property. It would not be accurate to say that Arnold Murray was fully mortified by this beer-lubricated imprudence, but at least he was embarrassed and even sorry. As Alan passed the information on to the police at the local station, a contrite Arnold waited on a bench across the street. The next afternoon, two detectives—one big, Mr. Wills; and one small, Mr. Rimmer—rang the bell of Alan's door.

威尔斯先生在大轰炸期间曾担任防空警卫。每天晚上，他都会在伦敦东区的罗马路巡逻，那里有许多小巷和死胡同。他会对那些粗心大意地在窗户周围留缝隙的居民大吼大叫，因为灯光会从缝隙中照进来，照亮人行道，而这些灯光在看不见的城市中只是微不足道的一点光亮，这严重违反了灯火管制。他会敲窗户。“你家有灯光，”他喜欢这样喊。威尔斯的午夜巡逻经历了几个月的痛苦，直到袭击停止（很大程度上要归功于艾伦的密码破译），他的膝盖仍然疼痛不已，因为他经常在最黑暗的夜晚误判距离并从路边摔下来，导致膝盖反复受伤。

Mr. Wills had been an air-raid warden during the blitz. Each night he had patrolled Roman Road in the East End of London with its mesh of small side streets and dead ends. He’d bellow at the residents who carelessly left gaps around their windows through which lamps shone and illuminated the sidewalks, a small volume of light in the invisible city, a strict violation of the blackout. He’d rap on the window. “You’ve a light showing,” he enjoyed shouting. There were several harrowing months before Wills's midnight patrols were abruptly rendered benign as the attacks stopped (in no small part owing to Alan's code breaking), although the detective's knee continues to ache from the recurrent injury sustained when he habitually misjudged the distance and fell off a curb in the darkest nights.

另一方面，如果战争没有随着艾伦的机器中流出的纳粹传输的宝贵信息而结束，里默先生很可能会作为一名年轻、略显无能的步兵而失去生命。他们每个人的生活都感觉像是一条穿越历史的孤独轨道，但这些事件却像闪电网一样分支出一系列后果。这感觉就像他们第一次与艾伦接触，但这只是众多顶点之一。艾伦在树林里。他的想法。破解恩尼格玛密码。闪电战的结束。战争的胜利。

Mr. Rimmer, on the other hand, would likely have lost his life as a young slightly incompetent infantry soldier if the war hadn’t ended with the invaluable information on Nazi transmissions that spewed from Alan's machines. Each of their lives feels like a solitary orbit through history, but these events branch off into a cascade of consequences like a web of lightning. This feels like their first point of contact with Alan but it is just one of many vertices. Alan in the woods. His idea. The breaking of the Enigma code. The end of the blitz. The winning of the war.

一个不引人注意的案件被指派给一位经验丰富的侦探。正如里默先生和威尔斯先生与艾伦有着不为人知的联系（谢尔本学校的一名毕业生也与艾伦有着不为人知的联系，他曾在菲利克斯和莱恩的商店里度过几个晚上，喝着马多克斯夫人的汤），入室行窃的那个年轻人也与艾伦有着不为人知的联系。小偷哈利是一名刚从海军退役的军官，他曾在一条船上服役，这条船没有被 U 型潜艇摧毁，而是在艾伦翻译的拦截信息的帮助下被转移了航向。还有无数其他这样的联系和命运的曲折，很难追踪，也无法编成一份冗长的清单。所以这里我们只看到了艾伦在自己的死亡中扮演了某种角色的一小部分。

The assignment of an unspectacular case to a veteran detective. Just as Mr. Rimmer and Mr. Wills had unknown connections with Alan (as did a graduate from Sherborne School who spent some nights in Felix and Lane's shop eating Mrs. Maddox's soup), so too did the young man who burgled Alan's house. An officer just barely discharged from the navy, Harry the thief once served on a boat that was not destroyed by a U-boat but instead was diverted with the aid of the intercepts Alan had translated. There are innumerable other such connections and folds and twists of destiny that are too difficult to track and to compile in a list that would be too long to manage. So here we have only a fragment of Alan playing some part in his own demise.

威尔斯将他那强大的大腿挤进艾伦楼上办公室的椅子里，一边拍着膝盖上的旧伤，一边取出一堆写满计算结果的文件。

Wills squeezes his formidable thighs into a chair in Alan's upstairs office, removing a spray of papers covered with calculations while patting the old wound in his knee.

“很抱歉打扰您，图灵先生。很抱歉，但我们需要澄清您故事中的一些方面。您能再描述一下揭露嫌疑人身份的线人吗？”

“We are sorry to disturb you, Mr. Turing. We are sorry, but we need to clarify some aspects of your story. Could you describe again the informant who revealed the identity of the suspect?”

“他大约二十五岁，身高五英尺十英寸，黑头发。”

“He's about twenty-five years of age, five foot ten inches, with black hair.”

“我们有理由相信你的描述是错误的。我原以为默里先生是金发碧眼的，而且个子也没有那么高。你为什么要撒谎？”

“We have reason to believe your description is false. I rather thought that Mr. Murray was blond and not so tall as all that. Why are you lying?”

“噢，亲爱的。原来您认识默里先生啊。”

“Oh, dear. So you know of Mr. Murray.”

“是的，我们确实认识他。默里先生是金发，个子不高。而且年轻得多。”

“Yes indeed we do. And Mr. Murray is blond and not so tall as that. And rather younger.”

“是的，没错。他有一头稀疏的金发，一双蓝眼睛。他中等身材，完全不值得信任。”

“Yes, yes he is. He has thin blond hair, blue eyes. He's medium build and completely untrustworthy.”

“你为什么要误导我们有关告密者的身份？”

“Why did you misdirect us as to the identity of the informant?”

“因为我们有外遇。”

“Because we had an affair.”

“外遇？”

“An affair?”

“婚外情。”

“An affair.”

“你愿意告诉我们你和他之间有过什么样的关系吗？”

“Would you care to tell us what kind of an affair you have had with him?”

“同性恋关系。我们进行了三种不同的性行为。我要告诉你它们是什么吗？”

“A homosexual affair. We performed three different sex acts in particular. Shall I tell you what they were?”

“是的，好的，先生，你为什么不呢？”

“Yes, all right, sir, why don’t you.”

他确实这么做了。他提出将细节记录成一份长达五页的书面声明，文笔清晰、官方，符合侦探们对技术语言的品味。

And he does. Offering to transcribe the details in a written statement, five pages in a clear, official style that pleases the detectives’ taste for technical language.

“这真是一个很美的句子，就像散文一样，”大个子向小个子展示道，“尽管其中的一些措辞我不太明白。”

“It really is a lovely statement, like prose,” the big one says, showing the little one, “although it is beyond me in some of its phraseology.”

离开霍利米德时，威尔斯感到一丝忧伤。“我只担心教授的不知羞耻。”

As they leave Hollymeade, Wills feels the littlest bit melancholy. “I’m only concerned about the professor's lack of shame.”

“是的，”小家伙扬起眉毛说道，然后严肃地说，“我也是。”

“Yes,” the little one says with raised eyebrows, and then solemnly, “me too.”

“我们必须指控他。”

“We shall have to charge him.”

“是的。我们会的。”

“Yes. Yes, we shall.”

“耻辱。”

“Shame.”

“真可惜。”

“Shame ’tis.”

2 月 27 日，艾伦·图灵和阿诺德·默里均因严重猥亵罪被捕，违反了 1885 年《刑法修正案》第 11 条。

On February 27 Alan Turing and Arnold Murray are both arrested on the crime of Gross Indecency contrary to Section 11 of the Criminal Law Amendment Act 1885.

艾伦已经多年没见过琼了，但就连他也明白，他必须告诉她真相。和其他人一样——在工作场所的自助餐厅、曼彻斯特的电脑旁、皇家学会的科学会议上——他可以自由地甚至大声地谈论对他的指控。他的广播对任何敢于评判他的人来说都是一个过度补偿的挑战。但在故事登上报纸之前，他必须找到更微妙、更难接近的方法来告诉他的兄弟、母亲和琼。他先写信给他的兄弟。艾伦写给他兄弟的信开头是，我想你知道我是同性恋。约翰在把信塞进裤袋前只读了这么一句话，所以他错过了结尾，结尾是，当你来到曼彻斯特时，也许你会抽出时间去监狱看望我。在他的兄弟拒绝告诉他们寡居的母亲后，艾伦乘火车去了吉尔福德告诉她——不是解释，只是陈述事实。他们吵架了，但并不激烈。她所理解的一点她清理了表面的思绪，采取坚定的立场来捍卫她最有天赋的（尽管无可否认他并不正常）儿子，反驳那些模糊的、无法重复的指控。

Alan hasn’t seen Joan for years but even he understands he has to be the one to tell her. With anyone else—in the cafeteria at work, around the Manchester computer, at scientific meetings at the Royal Society—he talks freely, even loudly about the nature of the charges against him. His broadcast is an overcompensating challenge for anyone to dare judge him. But before the story makes the papers, as it will, he has to find more delicate, and hence less accessible, methods by which to tell his brother, his mother, and Joan. He wrote to his brother first. Alan's letter to his brother began, I suppose you know I’m a homosexual. That was all John read before smashing the letter into the pocket of his trousers, so he missed the close, which was, When you come to Manchester, perhaps you will find the time to visit me in jail. After his brother refused to inform their widowed mother, Alan took a train to Guildford to tell her—not explain, just state the facts. They fought, but not bitterly. What little she understood she cleaned off the surface of her thoughts and assumed a firm stance in defense of her most gifted (if undeniably not normal) boy against vague, unrepeatable charges.

现在他要把这件事告诉琼，这是一项复杂的任务。他起草了这封信：

And now he has the complex task of telling Joan. He drafts this letter:

亲爱的琼，

我知道我们已经有近七年没有通信了，所以收到我的来信可能会让你有点震惊。也许更震惊的是，当我们的订婚结束时，你为什么还记得我引用奥斯卡·王尔德的话：

Dear Joan,

I realize we have not corresponded in almost seven years so it might come as a bit of a shock to hear from me. Possibly an even greater shock to discover ‘why Do you remember ‘when our engagement ended and I quoted Oscar Wilde:

然而每个人都会杀死他所爱之物，

每个人都会听到这句话，

有的人用苦涩的眼神，

有的人用奉承的话语，

懦夫用吻，

勇敢的人用剑！

Yet each man kills the thing he loves,

By each let this be heard,

Some do it with a bitter look,

Some with a flattering word,

The coward does it with a kiss,

The brave man with a sword!

你说我背诵这首诗和退出我们的关系的时间点都很糟糕？好吧，恐怕我的诗歌水平没有提高，显然也没有解释自己。我想成为告诉你的人。我被捕了，很快就会接受审判。情况与王尔德臭名昭著的审判非常相似，尽管我希望它们没有以前那么野蛮。我告诉过你我有同性恋倾向。我应该告诉你我偶尔会这样做。

And you said I had abominable timing both in my recitation of the poem and in my withdrawal from our relationship?
