Well I have gotten no better at poetry, I’m afraid, nor apparently at explaining myself. I ‘wanted to be the one to tell you. I have been arrested and will soon go to trial. The circumstances are rather similar to those that permeated Wilde's infamous trial, although I hope they are rather less savage than they used to be. I told you I had homosexual tendencies. I should have told you that I do occasionally practice.

我在曼彻斯特的家被盗了。每个人都告诉我，我应该忘记这次入室盗窃，让这件事过去，但琼，这实在是太不对了，我无法容忍。我报了警。警方在调查过程中发现，我和其中一名嫌疑人有关系。好吧，他并不是真正的嫌疑人（尽管我对此表示怀疑）。他更像是一个线人。他有意或无意地把小偷引到了我家门口，这还有待确定。好吧，你明白了。我被抢劫了，现在我要接受审判。我想成为告诉你真相的人。

My home in Manchester was burgled. Everyone tells me I should have put the invasion out of my mind and let the incident pass, but it ‘was just so ‘wrong, Joan, and I couldn’t tolerate it. I notified the police. In the course of their investigation it came to light that I had a relationship with one of the suspects. Well, he's not really a suspect (though I have my doubts). He's more of an informant. Intentionally or otherwise, as remains to be determined, he led the thief to my door. Well, there you have it. I ‘was robbed and now I’m the one going to trial. I ‘wanted to be the one to tell you.

我的密码分析生涯很快就要结束了。我曾以平民身份协助一些密码分析员，但我相信您已经听说过几项建议政府清除同性恋者的调查。他们坚持认为同性恋者更容易受到敲诈勒索或情感和道德上的弱点。我不知道他们是如何得出这个结论的。那些参与热恋的已婚军官的道德弱点让我想起了这一点。但您可能不想听到我的轻率行为造成的相当严重的后果。

My cryptanalytic days are soon over. I ‘was assisting some cryptanalysts as a civilian but I’m sure you’ve heard the several inquiries that have advised the government to purge itself of homosexuals. They insist that the homosexual is somehow more vulnerable to blackmail or emotional and moral ‘weakness. How they came to this conclusion escapes me. The ‘weak moral fiber of those married officers engaged in torrid affairs comes to mind as a counterpoint. But you’d probably rather not hear about the rather grave consequences of my indiscretion.

他停下了写信，对无法避免的尴尬语气感到不满。这次降职让他很受伤。他从未吹嘘过战争期间或战后的成就。他从未谈起布莱切利园。没有跟他的兄弟谈过。没有跟他的母亲谈过。没有跟他为数不多的大学朋友谈过。他从未讲过那些可怕日子的悬疑故事，比如英国护卫队在他们手中拿着德国的电报时失踪，电报被锁在无法破解的密码中，而他们聪明的创意却被巧妙地付诸实践速度很快，但他们收到的回复仍然是密码，英国士兵阵亡，他们以为德国人会入侵，伦敦弥漫着灰烬的味道，他们夜复一夜地失眠，失去了希望，不知道事情是如何逆转的。这些都是艾伦从未讲过的故事。

He stops the letter, unhappy with the awkward tone he can’t avoid. This demotion wounds him. He never boasted of his achievements during the war or after. Never spoke of Bletchley Park. Not to his brother. Not to his mother. Not to his few college friends. He never told suspenseful stories of the terrible days when British convoys were lost even while they held German transmissions in their hands, locked in an impenetrable code, when their brilliant ideas were set to work with ingenuity and speed and still what they got back was code and British soldiers died and they thought the Germans would invade and London smelled of ash and they lost night after night of sleep and hope and how it all turned around. These are stories Alan never told.

但他热爱这份工作。热爱谜题。热爱问题的现实。理论解决方案变成了物质解决方案——一台机器，一台计算机。而说到密码破译，艾伦就是明星。他是最棒的。他甚至是一个领导者，尽管他是一个非传统的领导者，因为他负责整天从潜艇、陆地指挥官、气象船和元首本人发来的信息。他一生都住在那间砖房里，坚硬的地板上长满了静脉，积满了淡淡的水池。小屋里挤满了木桌，桌子以毫无意义的排列方式交错排列，桌子上铺着一张放大的纸张，上面写着一排排加密文本。WFLX 和 RTVN 的一列列连接到一列列的数字、规则和猜测，但仍然没有德语。

But he loved the work. The puzzle. The reality of the problem. The theoretical solution come alive as a material solution—a machine, a computer. And when it came to code breaking, Alan was a star. He was the best. He was even a leader, if an unorthodox one, in charge as he was of the transmissions that came in all day long from submarines, from commanders on land, from weather boats, from the Führer himself. He spent a lifetime in that brick hut with its hard floors that had grown veins and collected faint pools of water. The huts were crammed with wooden desks staggered in senseless arrangements and the desks were topped with a blanket of enlarged papers marked by rows and rows of encrypted text. Columns of WFLX and RTVN connected to columns of numbers and rules and guesses but still no German.

艾伦可以轻松地筛选出可识别的纯文本，作为三十六小时的备忘，直到最后屈服于之前未曾察觉的疲惫。他们都在拥挤的房间里神经质地工作着，淹没在清单、穿孔卡和装满传入传输但空无一物的铁丝篮中。机器零件的咔嗒声取代了谈话的轻快，每个人都靠在穿孔纸上，笔悬在空中晾干。他们看起来像是剑桥或牛津考试的学生，事实上他们中的许多人都是。头发卷曲的女人穿着宽松圆肩套头衫的雕塑。海军部称他们为教授型，他们不穿制服，手指埋在头发里，到处都是一张写着乱七八糟的字母的床单，上面写着入侵、伦敦的毁灭、纳粹的计划。他们的手指触摸到这些字母，但他们仍然不知道这些字母描述的是什么计划。大西洋上的损失不断增加，英国被扼杀了。几个月又几个月过去了，他们仍然一无所获。

Alan could easily sift for recognizable plain text to use as cribs for thirty-six-hour stretches before succumbing finally to a previously unnoticed exhaustion. They all worked neurotically in a crowded room drowning in lists and punch cards and wire baskets loaded with incoming transmissions and empty of translated transmissions. The clicking of machine parts replaced the lilt of conversation as everyone leaned on the perforated sheets, pens hanging and drying in the air. They looked like students studying for exams from Cambridge or Oxford, as many of them in fact were. Women with hair curled into sculptured shapes wearing loose jumpers with rounded shoulders. Men out of uniform, professor types they were called by the Admiralty, their fingers buried in their hair and everywhere a blanket of sheets with scrambled letters that described invasion, the destruction of London, the Nazi designs. Their fingers touched these letters and still they didn’t know what plans they described. Losses were mounting in the Atlantic, and England was choked off. Months and months and they still had nothing.

有人可能会尝试一种毫无希望的游戏，任意设置转子，然后将截获的加密信息输入恩尼格玛密码机键盘，只是为了看看会亮起什么。但是转子有数万亿种可能的搭配，因此意外找到德国海军恩尼格玛密码机使用的设置的可能性极小。后来艾伦在树林里想出了这个主意。这个主意真是太奇妙了。他们通常只知道加密信息任何部分的一小部分明文含义 — — 日期、生日快乐，元首、天气。艾伦知道他们如何使用这个小窍门来排除大部分错误的转子设置，即那些无法重现小段明文的转子设置。

A person could attempt the hopeless game of arbitrarily setting the rotors and typing into the Enigma keyboard an intercepted encrypted message just to see what might light up. But there were trillions of possible wheel combinations so that accidentally finding the setting used by the German Naval Enigma was woefully unlikely. Then Alan had his idea from the woods. It was so brilliantly weird. They often knew a small piece of the plain meaning of any part of an encrypted message—the date; Happy Birthday, Führer; the weather. Alan saw how they could use this crib to rule out the bulk of wrong rotor settings, namely those that could not reproduce the small piece of plain text.

艾伦设计了一台机电机器，将一系列恩尼格玛密码机连接在一起。他以波兰原型机的名字将其命名为 Bombe。Bombe 可以在众多转子设置中旋转，并删除大量错误设置。这为他们留下了一棵可以手动处理的剩余可能性树。有人来回奔波于 6 号小屋，德国空军的传输信息就是从那里发出的。每个人都尽其所能。其他一些密码分析员对艾伦的密码进行了巧妙的改进想法，然后他又对他们的改进进行了巧妙的改进。原型机被制造出来并进行了测试。不得不说，这让他很高兴。

Alan designed an electromechanical machine that wired together a series of Enigma machines. He named it a Bombe after a Polish prototype. The Bombe spun through the multitude of rotor settings and pruned away huge bushels of wrong settings. This left them a fine tree of remaining possibilities to work through manually. There was some running back and forth to Hut 6 where Luftwaffe transmissions were sent. Everyone came forward to do what they could. Some of the other cryptanalysts came up with ingenious improvements on Alan's idea and he in turn made ingenious improvements on their improvements. A prototype was built and tested. And it has to be said, this made him happy.

他的机器开始运转。七台炸弹在数万亿种可能性中不断搅动，以破译这些传输。丘吉尔要求每天解密，有时一天一千份，尽可能多地解密，将他最喜欢的解密内容带入内阁作战室，以启发他的战术决策。首相甚至抽出时间从伦敦赶来，站在 8 号小屋，试图握住艾伦颤抖的手。他锁定艾伦的手掌比锁定他的目光更幸运，因为艾伦四处张望，就是没有看首相的脸，他笑得如此焦虑，听起来像是尖叫和打嗝的警报。

His machines worked. Seven Bombes churning through the trillions of possibilities to decipher the transmissions. Churchill demanded the daily decrypts, sometimes a thousand a day, as many as he could get through, taking his favorites into the cabinet war rooms to inspire his tactical decisions. The prime minister even found the time to travel from London and stand in Hut 8, where he tried to clasp Alan's quivering hand. He had more luck locking onto Alan's palm than he did his gaze as Alan looked everywhere but in the face of the prime minister, laughing so anxiously it sounded like an alarm of yelps and hiccups.

艾伦和琼的订婚也许不是他幸福的主要来源。但她是他最好的朋友。当他安装 Enigma 的轮子和接线板，用拇指敲击键盘读出亮起的字母时，琼就站在他旁边。她在那里，带着难以抑制的兴奋和纯粹的焦虑问他：“艾伦，上面写的是什么？上面写的是什么？”

Alan's engagement to Joan may not have been the primary source of his happiness. But she was his best friend. She stood next to him when he set the wheels and plug board of the Enigma and stubbed his thumb into the keyboard to read off the letters as they lit up. She was there to ask him with uncontained excitement and pure anxiety, “Alan, what does it say? What does it say?”

“我不知道。我一点儿概念都没有。”她在那里聆听着他混乱的笑声，当他用粗糙的手指刺出伤口时，他发出机关枪般的笑声，“但那是德国的！”她在那里是为了这份快乐。这很重要。

“I don’t know. I have no idea.” She was there to take in his chaotic laughter, that machine-gun laugh of his as he stabbed his gnarled finger, “But it's German!” She was there for this happiness. And that counts for something.

艾伦再次开始给琼写信：

Alan starts his letter to Joan again:

这是一个有趣的故事，我想你会很喜欢。几乎可以说是经典。我和一些朋友，我的邻居格林鲍姆一家一起去了布莱克浦。海风非常猛烈，我们不得不向前倾身，这样每个人看起来都像是被冻住了，头朝下扎进了沙子里。沿着拱门下的长廊，我看到了一个算命师的标志，吉普赛女王！我们停下来躲避大风，我花了一分钟时间去拜访吉普赛人。正如你所知，我认为通灵术完全是胡说八道，但我仍然发现自己被表演所吸引。就像我们一起看过的那部美丽的动画电影《白雪公主》。当然我知道这不是真的，但我仍然喜欢一遍又一遍地看它。记得我们无法把目光从白雪公主的每一个动作上移开，我们花了整年都在吟诵“把苹果浸入啤酒中，让沉睡的死亡渗透进来”？吉普赛女王看起来就像白雪公主中扮演女巫时的女王，只是年纪更大，老得不可思议。她的口音很脏，我几乎听不清她在说什么。她把一杯水放在这张小圆桌的中央，透过饮料盯着我看了很长时间，感觉很不舒服。这真的很可怕。她眼睛的倒影在玻璃杯周围变成了巨大的鱼眼。房间太小了，这让我感到不安，我觉得没有别的地方可以看，事实上，当她终于尖叫起来，撞翻桌子，打碎玻璃杯时，我开始变得相当生气。我不知道她在叫什么，但声音很刺耳，让我脖子上的汗毛都竖起来了。我也尖叫着逃走了。我彻底慌了，简直像个傻瓜。我从她挂在门口的紫色窗帘下掉了下来，据我的朋友说，我脸色苍白得像个鬼，然后沿着海滩跑进一场暴雨中，暴雨大得让我觉得自己要融化了！我的朋友在公共汽车站找到了我，我们一起回到了曼彻斯特，但我一句话也说不出来。我自然觉得自己是个十足的傻瓜。我的邻居还没有回我的电话，我不知道他们是否会回。这件事发生在我半夜把布莱切利的所有人都吵醒的时候，因为我以为我不小心毒死了自己。还记得吗，你必须说服安全官员，我不是国家危害？我希望你在这里说服格林鲍姆一家。

Here's an amusing story I think you will quite enjoy. Almost a classic really. I went to Blackpool with some friends, my neighbors the Greenbaums. The wind off the ocean ‘was terribly fierce and we had to lean forward so that everyone looked like they were frozen in a head-first dive into the sand. Along the promenade under the arches I spotted a sign for a fortune-teller, the Gypsy Queen! We stopped to get a rest from the gale and I took a minute to visit the Gypsy. As you well know I think psychics are complete rubbish but I still find myself drawn to the performance. It's like that beautiful animated film we saw together, Snow White. Of course I know it's not real, but still I love to see it over and over again. Remember how we couldn’t keep our eyes off Snow White's every movement and we spent the whole year chanting, “Dip the apple in the brew, let the sleeping death seep through”? Well the Gypsy Queen looked just like the Queen in Snow White ‘when she ‘was cast as a ‘witch only even older, impossibly old. Her accent ‘was so polluted I could hardly make out ‘what she ‘was saying. She put a glass of ‘water in the center of this little round table and stared at me through the beverage for quite an uncomfortably long while. It ‘was terrifying really. The reflection of her eyes ‘was smeared around the glass into huge fish orbs. It ‘was agitating how small the room was so that I felt there ‘was nowhere else to look and in fact I began to get rather cross ‘when she finally shrieked and knocked the table over, smashing the glass. I don’t know ‘what she ‘was calling out but it ‘was shrill and raised the hairs on my neck. I shrieked too and fled. I was thoroughly rattled and rather made a fool of myself. I fell out from under the purple drapery she had hanging in the doorway, white as a ghost according to my friends, and ran down the beach into a rainstorm so thick I thought I would dissolve! My friends found me at the bus stop and we traveled back to Manchester together but I ‘was unable to utter a single ‘word. I felt a complete buffoon, naturally. My neighbors haven’t yet returned my call and I ‘wonder if they ever will. The incident matched the time I ‘woke everyone at Bletchley in the middle of the night because I thought I had accidentally poisoned myself. Remember, you had to convince the security officers that I ‘wasn’t a National Hazard? I wish you were here to convince the Greenbaums.

曼彻斯特计算机的研究工作正在向前推进，我确信这些机器将是有一天，机器自己也会这么想！至少你会发现在国际象棋中打败一个比打败我更有挑战性。

Work on the Manchester computer moves forward and I feel certain that these machines will be indispensable one day and that the machines will even think so themselves! At least you would find it more challenging to beat one at chess than it ‘was to beat me.

祝贺你们订婚。

Congratulations on your recent engagement.

最诚挚的问候，

艾伦·图灵

Sincerest regards,

Alan Turing

艾伦撕毁了写给琼的信，并寄了这封信：

Alan tears up his letter to Joan and sends this instead:

1952 年 2 月 4 日

亲爱的琼，

我想告诉你，我因严重猥亵罪被捕，违反了 1885 年《刑法修正案》第 11 条。将进行审判，你应该准备好在报纸上读到不愉快的消息。在战争期间，我告诉过你我的同性恋倾向。我应该告诉你我偶尔会这样做。我只能希望我的同性恋倾向比奥斯卡·王尔德时代要少一些。

February 4, 1952

Dear Joan,

I ‘wanted to be the one to tell you that I have been arrested for Gross Indecency contrary to Section 11 of the Criminal Law Amendment Act 1885. There will be a trial and you should be prepared to read of the unpleasantness in the paper. During the ‘war I told you of my homosexual tendencies. I should have told you that I do occasionally practice. I can only hope that they are rather less savage than they were in Oscar Wilde's day.

整个故事远远超过了我把银块扔进小溪后从树林里出来被暂时逮捕的时间。我记得，你对那件事相当高兴。如果我没有被监禁，我有一天我必须回到白金汉郡并收回我的投资。

The ‘whole saga rather outstrips the time I ‘was momentarily arrested upon emerging from the ‘woods after depositing my silver bullion in the stream. As I recall, you were rather delighted by that episode. If I am not incarcerated, I must go back to Buckinghamshire one of these days and recover my investment.

我确实非常怀念那些时光以及我们的友谊。

I do remember those times, and our friendship, rather fondly.

祝你们订婚顺利。

Best wishes on your recent engagement.

最诚挚的问候，

AM Turing

Sincerest regards,

A. M. Turing

美国普林斯顿。1977 年

PRINCETON, AMERICA. 1977

在普林斯顿郊外一所简陋的低矮长方形房屋里，科特每天早餐只吃一个鸡蛋，喝一茶匙茶。一天从近乎完美的排便开始。然后阿黛尔为他准备早餐，没有发生任何意外，她似乎没有像往常那样坚持用勺子喂他更多的食物，而不是他习惯的单个鸡蛋和一茶匙茶。他完美地调整了自己对特定食物的摄入量，精确地平衡了他对镁乳和 ExLax 的摄入量——平衡到了最低点。这控制了他去年出血的溃疡，并减轻了与之相关的胃痛，胃痛位于上部右侧，位于背部深处，如此之高和如此之深，几乎通过内脏内壁灼烧他的心房。精心安排的食物摄入量和泻药摄入量也缓解了他的消化不良和便秘。他花了二十年时间才制定出如此精确的时间表。他每天记录胃肠道周期的日记，他的体温和排便情况对于制定自己的处方非常有价值。

On the edge of Princeton in a simple, low, rectangular house Kurt eats a single egg for breakfast and a teaspoon of tea. The day begins well with a nearly perfect bowel movement. Then Adele prepares his breakfast without incident and seems less persistent than usual in her attempts to spoon-feed him more food than his habitual single egg and teaspoon of tea. He has perfectly tuned his intake of specific foods, balanced precisely against his intake of Milk of Magnesia and ExLax—balanced to the drop. This has controlled his ulcer, which hemorrhaged last year, and ameliorated the associated stomach pain, high up and to the right, deep in the back, so high and deep it almost burns the atrium of his heart through the linings of his organs. The carefully timed administration of morsel of food versus laxative has also tamed both his indigestion and his constipation. It has taken him two decades to work out the schedule so precisely. The diary he maintains of his daily gastrointestinal cycle, his temperature, and his bowel movements has been invaluable in working out his own prescription.

早餐后，他把自己隔离在空余的办公桌前。他几乎不再去研究所了。这样做的好处是隐私。缺点是阿黛尔的注意力不受控制地靠近他。但今天她没有阻止他躲到办公桌前。她几乎被制服了，他甚至几乎没有注意到她在四处走动、收拾东西。他不知道今天要做什么。他的想法支离破碎，没有重点。他已经很久没有找到完成计算或论文所需的雄心壮志了，他担心这真的可能要花好几年的时间。

After breakfast, he isolates himself at his spare desk. He barely goes to the institute anymore. The advantage is privacy. The disadvantage is the proximity of Adele's unmodulated attention. But today she does not resist his escape to his desk. She is almost subdued and he hardly even notices her milling about, tidying up. He doesn’t know what he will work on today. His ideas have been fractured, unfocused. He hasn’t found the ambition he needs to complete a calculation or a paper in so long he worries it might actually be years.

阿黛尔已经完成了这间房间的装修，但她喜欢待在库尔特身边，于是她弯下腰，做出一个又宽又低的姿势，开始擦拭他办公桌旁边踢脚板上的微弱灰尘。她转过身，开始温和地抱怨管家，她是一个强壮的波兰人，她很感激地和他成为了朋友，但出于连阿黛尔都无法理解的原因，她那无力的长篇大论渐渐消失了。几乎就像她今天不想说话一样。她只想靠近他。

Adele is finished with this room, but she likes to be near Kurt, so she bends over, making a wide, low shape and begins to wipe the faint hint of dust from the baseboards near his desk. Over her shoulder, she begins a mild complaint about the housekeeper, a strong Pole whom she gratefully befriended, but for reasons even Adele can’t fathom the weak tirade peters off. It is almost as though she doesn’t feel like talking today. She just feels like being near.

“几乎没有人可以和我说话了，”他指着阿黛尔的臀部说道。

“There is almost no one left to talk to,” he tells Adele, speaking toward her haunches.

库尔特今天的心情也很奇怪。“那么，跟我说话吧，”她说。她的手臂感觉沉重，颤抖不已。

Kurt is in a strange mood today too. “So, talk to me,” she says. Her arms feel heavy, wobbly.

“如果爱因斯坦在这里，我可能仍会去研究所。”

“If Einstein were here, I might still go to the institute.”

“是的，”她说道，重新找到了任务的意义。“但他已经走了二十年了。你还有奥斯卡，”阿黛尔说道。“要心存感激。”

“Yes,” she says, finding renewed purpose behind her task. “But he's been gone twenty years. You still have Oskar,” Adele says. “Be grateful.”

他很感激。库尔特把阿黛尔赶出家门，这样他就可以给他最后一位在世的朋友奥斯卡·摩根斯坦 (Oskar Morgenstern) 打电话。“阿黛拉，你能从商店给我拿个苹果吗？”

He is grateful. Kurt sends Adele out of the house so he can phone his last living friend, Oskar Morgenstern. “Adele-la, would you bring me an apple from the store?”

“是的，库尔特勒。当然。为什么不呢？一个苹果。”她站起身，用几乎干净的抹布背面擦了擦手，然后抚摸了一下库尔特的头，离开了房间，从走廊上的一个挂钩上拿起外套，关上了身后的门闩。

“Yes, Kurtele. Sure. Why not? An apple.” She pulls herself up, wipes her hands with the nearly clean back side of the rag and pets Kurt's head just once as she leaves the room, collects her coat from a peg in the hall, and closes the latch on the door behind her.

科特拨通了那个比他自己的号码更让他记忆犹新的号码。

Kurt dials the number he remembers better than his own.

“你好，”奥斯卡回答。

“Hello,” Oskar answers.

“研究所里没人尊重我。”

“No one at the institute respects me.”

为了避免妻子在接到库尔特的电话时感到厌烦，奥斯卡默默地对妻子说了句“哥德尔”，然后挥手让她走开。“库尔特，我尊重你。”

Wanting to spare his wife the taxing repetition that Kurt's phone calls demand, Oskar mouths silently to his wife, “Gödel,” and waves her away. “Kurt, I respect you.”

“我花了二十年时间才成为教授。”他的声音有些紧张。

“It was twenty years before I was made professor.” His voice is strained.

“是的，库尔特。这错了，”奥斯卡真诚地承认。“这错了。”

“Yes, Kurt. This was wrong,” Oskar concedes genuinely. “This was wrong.”

“如果我死了，你必须答应发表我的文章，反驳艾伦·图灵关于心智极限的论点。图灵机是一个概念，相当于一个机械程序或算法。图灵能够用公式的机械操作——图灵机——完全取代推理。很好，同意吗？然而，我们应该把人类灵魂等同于图灵机吗？不。图灵的工作存在哲学错误。图灵在他 1937 年的论文第 250 页中提出了一个论点，该论点应该表明心理过程不能超越机械过程。然而，这个论点是不确定的。图灵完全忽视的是心智在使用过程中并不是静止的，而是不断发展的。他们谋杀了他，你知道吗？”

“If I die, you must promise to publish my article refuting Alan Turing's thesis on the limits of the mind. A Turing machine is a concept, equivalent to a mechanical procedure or algorithm. Turing was able to completely replace reasoning by mechanical operations on formulas—by Turing machines. Good, agreed? However, are we supposed to equate the human soul with a Turing machine? No. There is a philosophical error in Turing's work. Turing in his 1937 paper, page 250, gives an argument which is supposed to show that mental procedures cannot go beyond mechanical procedures. However this argument is inconclusive. What Turing disregards completely is the fact that mind, in its use, is not static, but constantly developing. They murdered him, you realize?”

“我以为是自杀，”奥斯卡心不在焉地回答。

“I thought it was suicide,” Oskar replies absently.

库尔特继续说道：“政府在他的食物里下了毒。我也一直在研究上帝存在的正式证明。但这还没有完成。我不想让我们的同事认为我疯了。如果我死了，也许你不应该发表那篇文章。”

Kurt continues, “The government poisoned his food. I have also been working on a formal proof of the existence of God. But this is still unfinished. I don’t want our colleagues to think I am crazy. Maybe you should not publish that one if I die.”

“科特，我才是那个快要死的人！”奥斯卡恳求道。

“Kurt, I’m the one who's dying!” Oskar entreats.

哥德尔对奥斯卡的病情不以为然。“你的腿很快就会从瘫痪中恢复过来，”库尔特说，然后迅速回到了自己的泥潭中。

Gödel dismisses Oskar's illness. “Your legs will soon recover from paralysis,” Kurt says, pulled rapidly back to the indulgence of his own mire.

“库尔特，我得了癌症。癌症！我不会好起来的。”

“Kurt, I have cancer. Cancer! I will not get better.”

“癌症会消退。”

“The cancer will recede.”

“不，库尔特，不会的。它已经扩散了。不会消退的。我不能再和你的出版商谈判了。也不能和你的医生谈判。也不能和你的妻子谈判，”说实话，奥斯卡从来都不喜欢她。他觉得阿黛尔很粗俗，而库尔特对她的吸引力是一个令人讨厌的谜。他向自己的妻子抱怨道：“她是维也纳洗衣妇类型：喋喋不休、没有文化、意志坚强。”当阿黛尔笑的时候，她那肮脏的牙齿就露出来了。奥斯卡总是等着她哼一两声，不过公平地说，她哼的次数并不多，不值得他守夜。

“No, Kurt, no it will not. It has metastasized. It will not recede. I cannot negotiate with your publishers anymore. Nor with your doctors. Nor with your wife,” who, to be honest, Oskar never liked. He found Adele vulgar, and Kurt's attraction to her was an annoying mystery. He complained to his own wife, “She's a Viennese washerwoman type: garrulous, uncultured, strong-willed.” When Adele laughed her dirty teeth showed. Oskar always awaited a snort or two though, to be fair, they really weren’t so frequent as to warrant a vigil.

过了一会儿，库尔特问道：“你收到维也纳的消息了吗？”

After some time, Kurt asks, “Do you receive news from Vienna?”

“那里几乎已经没有人了。”

“There is hardly anyone there anymore.”

“是的。”

“Yes.”

奥斯卡耸耸肩膀，看着妻子冒险回到房间。他听着电话线里传来的安静的声音，“库尔特？”

Oskar shrugs his shoulders to his wife as she risks returning to the room. He listens to the quiet phone line, “Kurt?”

“再见，奥斯卡。”

“Good-bye, Oskar.”

“再见。”

“Good-bye.”

库尔特刚把听筒还给他，就又想给奥斯卡打电话，但他忍住了几分钟。他花了一段时间整理他保存的所有洗衣收据、传单、旧信件、凭证和其他杂物。这些纸条让他心烦意乱。他觉得自己被压垮了，被义务所束缚，却无法忽略哪怕是最小的细节，无法在最琐碎的任务上取得进展，除非通过最详尽的一系列逻辑步骤。他必须以牺牲工作和好心情为代价，参与每个过程的每个阶段。当文件按逻辑顺序排列好后，他给奥斯卡打电话。“你还记得奥尔加·哈恩·诺伊拉特吗？”

The urge to phone Oskar again rises as soon as Kurt returns the receiver but he resists for a few minutes. For a while he organizes all the laundry receipts, flyers, old letters, vouchers, and other random detritus he saves. The slips of paper annoy him. He feels buried, hampered by obligation but unable to ignore even the smallest detail, unable to advance in even the most trivial of tasks except through the most exhaustive series of logical steps. He has to attend to every stage in every process at the expense of his work and of his good humor. When the papers are logically ordered, he phones Oskar. “Do you remember Olga Hahn-Neurath?”

阿黛尔离开家时大喊：“即使没有天才在车里，我也很乐意开车”，但她知道她的声音不够大，他听不到。例如，当她开车送摩根斯特恩一家回家时，她喜欢这样说。“即使没有天才在车里，我也很乐意开车，你不知道，”她用德语对着后视镜里奥斯卡恼怒的形象说，而他的妻子多萝西会扬起眉毛，怒视着副驾驶座的窗户。

As Adele leaves the house, she shouts, “I’ll be happy to drive without having a genius in the car,” but knows she isn’t loud enough for him to hear. She likes to say this, for instance, when she drives the Morgensterns home after a visit. “I’m so happy to drive without having a genius in the car, you can’t know,” she’d say in German to Oskar's irritated image in the rearview mirror while his wife Dorothy would turn with raised eyebrows to glare out the passenger seat window.

但今天，不知为何，当她经过车道上的汽车时，她把钥匙放回口袋里，然后步行几个街区去当地的杂货店。她尽量避免与收银员进行任何不必要的交谈，因为她自己蹩脚的英语仍然让她感到很羞愧。她一言不发地为她精心挑选的那一个水果付了钱。几个月来，她每天的每一次选择都被拒绝了。她选择了——或者说，她认为她选择了——一个苹果，她把苹果弄得很小，以免吓到他；苹果呈淡红色，以免显得不自然或被污染；苹果毫无理由地保留着茎的残端。她从商店走回家，手里拿着苹果，大腿比以前粗了。她把街道推开，踢着身后的水泥和泥土，感觉大而圆。她的连裤袜的腰带变成了一根没有天然支撑点的惩罚性钢丝。而且，她完全无法容纳白色棉质菱形裤裆，它通常与一条大腿对齐，就像一块用得不当的巨大纱布。她的长袜每走一步，就会像针织针一样从大腿前部和后部聚拢。她的肉体滚动着，直到尼龙扭曲和切割，像钢琴丝一样锋利。她在闪闪发光的商店橱窗里看到了自己沉重的倒影。“噗”，她吹了声口哨，这首曲子既有自怜又有接受。她想：我的大腿丰满得像一个饱满的佛罗里达橙子。剥了皮。就像一个饱满、剥了皮、饱满的佛罗里达橙子。她脑子里想的都是农产品。

But today, for whatever reason, she returns the keys to her pocket as she passes the car in the drive and walks the few blocks to the local grocer. She tries to avoid any unnecessary chatting with the cashier, since her own poor English still makes her feel quite ashamed. Without a word, she pays for the single piece of fruit she has carefully selected. Every previous selection on every previous day for several months has been rejected. She chooses, or so it seems to her she chooses, an apple that is small so as not to intimidate him, that is pale red so as not to seem unnatural or tainted, and that retains a stump from the stem for no reason at all. She clomps home from the store, the apple in hand, her thighs heavier than they used to be. They feel big and round as they push the street away, kicking the cement and earth behind her. The waistband of her pantyhose has become a punishing wire with no natural resting place. And there is absolutely no accommodating the white cotton diamond crotch, which usually aligns with one thigh like a poorly applied giant gauze. Her stockings bunch over the front of her thigh and down the back with each stride like a kind of knitting stitch. Her flesh rolls around until the nylon twists and cuts, piano-wire sharp. She catches her hefty reflection in a sparkling shop window. “Pff,” she whistles, a tune of simultaneous self-pity and acceptance. She thinks: My thighs are plump like an engorged Florida orange. Peeled. Like a plump, peeled, engorged Florida orange. Produce is on her mind.

透过窗户，库尔特看着阿黛尔从街角的商店回来，蹲在前院的篱笆上，篱笆上装饰着一只粉红色的塑料火烈鸟，这是她家前院的装饰。去年 12 月，她对附近出现的耶稣诞生场景印象深刻，想做一个自己的装饰品。哥德尔同意了，这太迷人了。她放弃了花园，摇摇晃晃地走进门。她很累。她的头发从盲目的夹子上松了下来，眼镜也松了。她扯下连裤袜，把它们挂在绿色乙烯基厨房椅背上。她开始抽烟，在厨房停下来，点燃了一根完美的机器卷烟，这是她在手提包的烟草收集袋里找到的。她还没有脱掉那件深色夹克。她撅起下唇，把烟直接喷到眼睛上，一双灰蓝色的眼睛映衬着她那双灰蓝色的眼睛。她把香烟抽到冒烟的泡沫上，然后掐灭了过滤嘴。在书房里，就在她离开他的时候，她找到了科特，那个她从未有过的孩子，并把他的苹果带给了他。

Through the window Kurt watches Adele return from the corner store and squat over a hedge decorated by a plastic pink flamingo she has installed in their front lawn. She was impressed with the nativity scenes that appeared in the neighborhood last December and wanted an ornament of her own. It is awfully charming, Gödel agreed. She gives up on the garden and waddles through the door. She is tired. Her hair has come loose from the blindly placed clips and her glasses have lost their grip. She pries off her pantyhose and leaves them dangling over the back of a green vinyl kitchen chair. As she has taken up smoking, she stops in the kitchen to light an immaculately machine-rolled cigarette she finds in the tobacco-collecting pocket of her dark jacket that she has not yet removed. She extends her lower lip in a pucker to blow the smoke straight up to her eyes, a vague blue-gray complement to her definite blue gray-eyes. She smokes the cigarette down to the burning foam and stubs out the filter. In the study, just as she left him, she finds Kurt, the child she never had, and brings him his apple.

他检查了这颗小红果的厚果皮。果皮皱巴巴的，周围有从藤上撕下来的凹痕，上面有痕迹，而且变褐了。他寻找痛苦的证据、刺伤，以及店主与医生合谋毒害他的证据。那里的那个痕迹太深，太干净，不像是自然的。他把它扔掉了。他会在明天、后天和大后天向她要另一个苹果，就像他前天和大前天做的那样。每天他都会把有毒的水果扔掉。

He inspects the thick hide of the little red fruit. The skin is puckered and marked and browning around the dimple where it was torn from the vine. He looks for proof of distress, punctures, evidence that the storekeeper is colluding with the doctors to poison him. That mark there, too deep, too clean to be natural. He throws it away. He will ask her for another apple tomorrow and the day after and the day after as he did the day before and the day before that. Each day he will throw the poisoned fruit away.

“为什么，库尔特勒？”她对着被丢弃的水果喊道，双臂哀怨地伸出，手指张开，包带在她还没有脱下的深色外套里，一只手臂比另一只手臂重。

“Why, Kurtele?” She shouts at the discarded fruit, both arms extended plaintively, fingers spread, bag strap weighing one arm lower than the other in the dark coat she still hasn’t removed.

他无视她的问题。“你从西尔斯买的散热器散发出有毒气体。气味堵在我的鼻子里，还粘在头发上。我已经打电话给西尔斯，让他们把它拆下来。”

He ignores her question. “The radiator unit you bought from Sears is emanating poison gases. The smell is trapped in my nose and clinging to the hairs. I have called Sears to have it removed.”

“移除？我们整个冬天都会被冻死。又来了！你想让我们整个冬天都被冻死吗？”

“Removed? We will freeze all winter. Again! You want us to freeze all winter?”

“阿黛尔，这对我的心脏有害。”

“Adele, it is bad for my heart.”

“你的心脏没有问题，库尔特勒。医生们都发誓。他们检查了一百遍。你的心脏很好，很好，”她指着他面前，仿佛要把这个想法拂去。“而且没有人会毒害你。”

“There is nothing wrong with your heart, Kurtele. The doctors swear to it. They have checked a hundred times. Your heart is fine, just fine,” she gestures in front of him as if to dust away the very idea. “And nobody is going to poison you.”

“你在维也纳差点用煤毒死我。现在又用暖气片了？”

“You nearly poisoned me in Vienna with coal. Now with the radiator?”

“那是个意外，库尔特勒，”她带着一种无奈的语气说道，她已经重复了无数次同样的辩护，以至于这句话已经变成了一个独立的词，一个比其各个部分的总和更大的概念。“那是个意外，库尔特勒！”

“That was an accident, Kurtele,” she says with the exasperation of one who has repeated the same defense so many times that the phrase has become its own word, an independent concept emerging larger than the sum of its parts. “That was an accident, Kurtele!”

“我给你尝尝，”她一边说，一边从垃圾堆里捞出有瑕疵的苹果，用门牙咬破了果皮。阿黛尔吃掉了剩下的苹果。她一边舔干净手指，一边把果核扔回桶里。

“I will taste it for you,” she says fishing the blemished fruit from the garbage and breaking the skin with her front teeth. Adele eats the rest of the apple. As she licks her fingers clean, she throws the core back into the pail.

下午时光流逝，阿黛尔从鸡身上剥下筋肉，同时撕下一些血管和韧带，留下光滑干净的弧形软骨。紫色的肉散发着液化脂肪的臭味，当阿黛尔把鸡肉条推入热气腾腾的炖菜中时，油脂在她长满老茧的手指上闪闪发光。科特整天都在书房里。他无法忍受烹饪动物肉的气味和景象。肉在舌头上滑动的质感让他感到恶心。她必须把炖菜打成糊状，哄着他吃。首先，他会看着她尝尝热汤，以证明食物没有下毒。然后，他会看着她吃掉一整碗，等待至少一个小时，只是为了确定汤里没有慢性毒剂。如果她幸运的话，他会让她像喂婴儿一样一勺一勺地喂他。那将是一顿成功的晚餐。

As the afternoon wears on Adele peels stringy meat from a carcass and with it some veins and ligaments tear free leaving a smooth clean arc of cartilage. The purple flesh stinks of liquefied fat and the grease shines on Adele's calloused fingers as she pushes the strips of chicken into the steaming stew. Kurt has been in his study all day. He can’t bear the smell or sight of cooking animal flesh. The texture of meat sliding along his tongue repulses him. She will have to puree the stew and cajole him to eat. First he will watch her taste the hot soup to demonstrate that the food is not poisoned. Then he will watch her eat an entire bowl and wait at least one hour just to be certain there are no slow-acting agents in the brew. If she is lucky he will allow her to feed him spoonful by spoonful like a baby. That would be a successful dinner.

她趴在炉子上，汗流浃背。或许她感染了纽约流行的流感病毒。每年她都会去泽西岛。现在才七月，但这是有可能的。她不能让库尔特知道她身体不好。如果他看到她在厨房附近出汗，他会好几天不吃饭。在她叫他来见证她品尝食物之前，她用颤抖的力气擦洗双手，然后把清晰的卷发塞到头和耳朵下面和周围。她擦干脸，站在大厅里椭圆形的小镜子前，重新画眉笔，画一条直线，一边向上移动，一边向外移动。这让她看起来有点生气，但也让她的眼睛有点提升。她以四分之三的姿势站着，这样葡萄酒色的胎记几乎被隐藏起来，她想，即使胖了，我看起来也很好。她吹了声口哨，“噗”，然后轰隆隆地说，“库尔特勒。汤。”

She is sweating from leaning over the stove. Or maybe she has contracted that strain of influenza that wafts through New Jersey each year. It is only July but it's possible. She must not let on to Kurt that she isn’t well. If he sees her perspire near the kitchen he will not eat for days. Before she calls him to witness her tasting of the food, she scrubs her hands with wobbling vigor, then tucks the well-defined curls under and around her head and ears. She mops her face dry and stands at the small oval mirror in the hall to reapply eyebrow pencil in a straight line that moves up as it moves out. It makes her look slightly angry but it also gives her eyes a bit of a lift. Standing in a three-quarters pose so the port-wine-stain birthmark is almost hidden she thinks, Even fat, I can still look good. She whistles, “Pff,” and then booms, “Kurtele. Soup.”

这顿晚餐注定不会成功。库尔特努力克制自己的阴郁情绪，看着阿黛尔展示这碗纯净汤的恢复功效，她的脸上满是汗水。她试图忍住越来越强烈的恶心和疼痛，以免惊动丈夫，但在谈到奥斯卡的妻子和她对姜汁汽水的痴迷时，她中途倒下了。

It is not destined to be a successful dinner. As Kurt fights his dark mood and watches Adele demonstrate the restorative powers of the untainted soup, her face oils with perspiration. She tries to talk through the intensifying nausea and pain so as not to alarm her husband but collapses midway through a running commentary on Oskar's wife and her putative obsession with ginger ale.

接下来的一个小时简直是一场灾难。科特对她大喊大叫。他不敢碰她，也不敢碰溅到她手臂和油毡上的汤。他觉得自己老了。他感到很痛苦。有几分钟他无法忍受让别人看到他们这个样子，所以他什么也没做。最后他惊慌失措。她给奥斯卡打了好几个电话，最后多萝西从丈夫手里抢过话筒，挂断了科特的电话，叫了救护车。

The ensuing hour is a disaster. Kurt yells to her. He is afraid to touch her or the soup that has spilled across her arm and onto the linoleum. He feels old. He feels wretched. For a few minutes he cannot bear the idea of anyone seeing them like this so he does nothing. Finally he panics. There are several confused calls to Oskar and eventually Dorothy grabs the receiver from her husband, hangs up on Kurt, and calls for an ambulance.

阿黛尔被紧急送往医院，在那里进行了紧急结肠造口术，其中靠近她的小肠末端穿过腹壁，与腹部皮肤上的切口相连。她的肠壁缝在腹壁上，一个人造袋子用胶带粘在开口处，用来收集粪便，粪便比她想象的要松软。在库尔特的坚持下，她已经习惯了检查他的粪便，尽管她对自己的粪便从未有过一丝兴趣。她不让库尔特看到她的结肠造口袋，但这个想法本身就让他感到不安，所以他很高兴几天来没有排出这种恶臭的半固体食物。只要护士允许，库尔特就会花尽可能多的时间陪在她身边，尽可能地宠爱他漂亮可爱的阿黛尔。如果工作人员允许，他会睡在她身边。就这样，她的康复期过去了五个月。

Adele is rushed to the hospital where an emergency colostomy is performed in which a section of bowel tissue near the end of her small intestine is passed through the abdominal wall to join an incision in the skin of her belly. The sides of her intestine are sewn to the abdominal wall and an artificial bag is taped to the opening to collect the stool, which is looser and softer than she had imagined. She has grown accustomed to checking Kurt's stool at his insistence although she never had more than a passing interest in her own. She protects Kurt from the sight of her colostomy bag but the idea alone infests him so that he is relieved that no such foul semisolids have passed through him for several days. Kurt spends as many hours by her side as the nurses allow, doting as best he can on his pretty, sweet Adele. He would sleep by her side if the staff allowed it. And so five months of her convalescence pass.

没人知道科特是如何熬过这五个月的。阿黛尔晕倒后，很多天他都无法进食。阿黛尔竭尽全力说服他汤里没有下毒，但科特坚持说汤里有股刺鼻的气味。奥斯卡也试了试。他用医学术语解释说：“这只是肠道堵塞，高脂饮食中很常见。”阿黛尔心不在焉地强迫他吃医院的食物，但食物太难吃了，连阿黛尔都难以咽下——不过她已经开始渴望吃周二的土豆泥和豌豆。后来，他开始吃得极其少——虽然不足以维持生命，但足以延缓死亡。就这样，科特挨饿了。一种非常缓慢而痛苦的挨饿过程。

No one is sure how Kurt survives these five months. Adele's collapse makes eating of any kind unthinkable for many days. Adele tries her best to convince him the soup was not poisoned but Kurt insists an acrid breath came off the broth. Oskar tries too. He explains in medical terms, “It was a simple obstruction of the bowel, not uncommon in high-fat diets.” Adele tries halfheartedly to force him to eat her hospital food, which is so poor that even she has trouble getting it down—although she has developed a hankering for Tuesday's mashed potatoes and peas. In time he begins to eat extremely modestly—not enough to keep him alive, but just enough to delay his death. And so Kurt starves. A very slow and very painful starvation.

阿黛尔的结肠造口手术破坏了库尔特对食物和泻药的调节。如果没有阿黛尔在身边叫醒他、给他洗澡、给他送药，他的排便、体温和药物摄入日记变得很古怪，无法记录。他睡着了。她那边的床空无一人，静悄悄的。他能看到曾经是阿黛尔的幽灵在粗糙的床单上打滚。他仍然可以吸入她在床上最后一次麝香睡眠的残留，他竭尽全力听她破晓时的叹息声。但她那边的床是空的。

Adele's colostomy episode has destroyed Kurt's regulation of food versus laxative. His diary of bowel movements, body temperature, and medicinal intake becomes erratic and unchartable without Adele there to wake him, bathe him, send him off to sleep. Her side of the bed is empty and still. He can see the phantom shadow that was once Adele rolling in the rough sheets. He can still inhale the remnant of her last musky sleep in their bed and he strains to hear her daybreak sighs. But her side of the bed is empty.

“给我拿氰化物！”科特在电话里恳求奥斯卡。“他们每晚都来我的房间，给我注射黄色血清。他们到底对我做了什么？奥斯卡，你必须帮我自杀。奥斯卡，求求你，我求求你帮帮我。阿黛尔的医生会把我送进精神病院。他们毒死了那只鸡。奥斯卡——给我拿氰化物！”

“Bring me cyanide!” Kurt begs Oskar over the phone. “They come into my room every night and inject me with a yellow serum. What are they doing to me? Oskar, you must help me kill myself. Please Oskar, I beg you to help me. Adele's doctors will commit me to an asylum. They poisoned the chicken. Oskar— bring me cyanide!”

“谁进了你的房间？谁？”奥斯卡对着电话大吼，却发现电话已经断了。“他来自另一个世界，”他向妻子解释道。“氰化物，他向我要氰化物。什么，给他自己的食物下毒？你知道他从哪儿弄来的吗？白雪公主的毒苹果。这是他最喜欢的电影。”突然响起的拨号音让奥斯卡更加沮丧。“多萝西，你知道他有时非常迷人。活泼有趣。这些年来，他一直是我很好的、敏锐的伙伴，你还记得爱因斯坦是多么珍惜他的友谊。

“Who comes into your room? Who?” Oskar bellows into the phone only to realize the line has gone dead. “He's from another world,” he tells his wife by way of explanation. “Cyanide, he asks me for cyanide. What, to poison his own food? Do you know where he gets that from? Snow White's poisoned apple. It's his favorite movie.” The abrupt blaring of the dial tone has further battered Oskar's spirits. “Dorothy, you know he can be splendidly charming at times. Animated and quite funny. He has been good, sharp company for me all these years, and you remember how Einstein valued his friendship.

你不知道这样的谈话对我来说意味着什么：他是我们这个世纪最杰出的人物之一，对我非常依恋。他显然患有某种偏执症，希望得到我的帮助，而我却无法帮助他。他依恋我——很明显，他没有其他人了——这加重了我的负担。”

You have no idea what such a conversation means for me: here is one of the most brilliant men of our century, greatly attached to me. He is clearly suffering from some kind of paranoia, expecting help from me, and I am unable to extend it to him. By clinging to me—and he has nobody else, that is quite clear—he adds to the burden I am carrying.”

当库尔特在当天第三次打电话后一个小时来到他家门口时，奥斯卡无法掩饰他对库尔特面容憔悴的失望，尽管他穿了好几层衣服，但还是很明显。他的皮肤最厚的地方是绿色的，紧贴着颧骨，在头骨上留有眼睛的地方，周围是一层坚硬的黄色皮肤。他的太阳穴松弛，宽如茶碟。“有趣的是，”奥斯卡曾告诉他的妻子，“如果你想吃传统的德国菜，阿黛尔是个好厨师。”

When Kurt arrives at his door an hour after the third phone call that day, Oskar is unable to camouflage his dismay at Kurt's cadaverous appearance, obvious despite the padding of several layers of clothes. His skin is green where it's thickest and pulled tautest against his cheekbones, paling to a tough yellow hide around the holes in the skull where a space is left for his eyes. His temples are flaccid and broad as saucers. “The funny thing,” Oskar once told his wife, “is that Adele is a good cook if what you crave is traditional German fare.”

库尔特的主人在他面前的桌子上放了一杯加冰的嘶嘶作响的姜汁汽水。杯子里半满着姜根糖浆和气泡水，还有许多黄色的果肉，是之前装在杯子里的橙汁汽水留下的。玻璃杯的上半部分盛满了阳光，从窗户射进来的炎热而沉重的阳光，仿佛星星沿着光线将液体滴入杯子。热量使姜根和气泡水起泡。上次他们作为夫妻拜访摩根斯特恩家时，阿黛尔喝了三杯他们自制的姜汁汽水。她的脸被玻璃杯捂住，她把嘶嘶作响的果汁吸到了厚厚的玻璃杯底部。饮料变成了一种令人口渴的糖浆，粘在她的牙齿和舌头上，以及她渴望喝水的胃里的所有管子里。当她表示口渴时，摩根斯特恩太太误解了，把她带到了又喝了一杯加冰的自制姜汁汽水。然后又喝了一杯。她的贪吃给摩根斯顿夫妇留下了不好的印象，而她的主人无法提供一点淡水，这也没有给阿黛尔留下什么好印象。两个女人面对面坐着，开始摆出一连串令人精疲力竭的女性姿势，每个人都想胜过对方。阿黛尔拉长裙子的下摆，扭动着身子爬到沙发边上，她想象自己坐在那里更像猫。多萝西则以一个古怪的脚踝交叉来回应。阿黛尔把她的大手放在膝盖上，低下下巴，试图把她所有的肥胖都吸成一个更修长的形状，甚至满怀希望地把手放在腰上。多萝西将手腕轻轻地倾斜到膝盖的一侧。夜晚就这样继续着，两人都模仿对方的姿势，然后一步步提高赌注。

Kurt's hosts place a sizzling ginger ale over ice on the table in front of him. The glass is half full of ginger root syrup and sparkly water with lots of yellow pulp from the previous occupant of the glass—an orange juice spritzer. The top half of the glass is loaded with sun, hot heavy sun coming in from the window, as though the star drooled a liquid along its rays into the cup. The heat is causing the ginger root and sparkling water to froth. The last time they visited the Morgensterns as a couple, Adele drank three of their homemade ginger ales. Her face muffled in the glass, she sucked the sizzling juice down to the heavy glass base. The beverage became a thirst-enhancing syrup that lined her teeth and tongue and all the tubing down to her longing-for-some-water stomach. When she expressed her thirst, Mrs. Morgenstern misunderstood and brought her another homemade ginger ale over ice. And then another. Her gluttony made a bad impression on the Morgensterns, and her hosts’ inability to supply a little fresh water made no great impression on Adele either. The two women sat across from each other and began an exhausting volley of feminine poses, each intending to outdo the other. Adele stretched the hem of her skirt as she wriggled to the edge of the sofa in what she imagined to be a more feline perch. To which Dorothy responded with a quaint crossing of the ankles. To which Adele rested her big hands on her knees and tucked in her chin, trying to suck all of her corpulence into a more elongated shape, even pushing her hand hopefully on her middle. To which Dorothy angled her wrists delicately to the side of her knees. And so the evening went on, each matching the other's posture and then raising the stakes one ridiculous step at a time.

几个月来，阿黛尔一直设法从姜汁汽水事件中寻找谈话素材。在阿黛尔不在的情况下看到同样的饮料，只会加剧科特的孤独。因此，这次拜访开始得并不顺利。奥斯卡和他的妻子建议，鉴于七十华氏度的气温，科特应该脱掉毛衣，而他没有想到毛衣下面还穿着另一件毛衣。但科特无法摆脱寒冷，而是接受了奥斯卡妻子送的另一件针织衫。然后是一件外套。然后是另一件外套。还有一条暖和的披肩。然后，奥斯卡尽管自己也感到不舒服，还是费了好大劲才生了火。给来访的尸体披上布料的过程占据了他们会面的大部分时间。

Adele managed to eke conversational material out of the ginger-ale episode for months. The sight of the very same beverage in Adele's absence only magnifies Kurt's loneliness. Thus the visit does not begin well. Oskar and his wife suggest that, what with the seventy-degree weather, Kurt should remove his sweater, not suspecting the presence of another sweater under that. But Kurt can’t shake the chill and accepts instead another knit from Oskar's wife. And then a coat. And then another coat. And a warm wrap. And then, with difficulty, Oskar lights a fire despite his own discomfort. The process of draping fabrics over the visiting cadaver consumes the better part of their meeting.

Kurt 非常透明。“你很担心。你有一双忧虑的眼睛，”Oskar 说着，用食指和拇指勾起在他的眼睛周围画着，以说明担忧的目光所在。“是的。我累了。”绝望之色浮现在他的脸上。奥斯卡皱起眉头，他看到风暴正在形成，他的脸几乎和库尔特一样透明。

Kurt is incredibly transparent. “You’re worried. You have worried eyes,” Oskar says and scoops his forefinger and thumb around his own to illustrate the locus of worried eyes. “Yes. And I am tired.” Desperation blows across his face. Oskar frowns, as he sees the storm forming, his own face nearly as transparent as Kurt's.

科特鼓起勇气，准备面对痛苦的自我意识。他是一个穿着华丽服装的骷髅木偶，被一团压倒黄色阳光的火光戏剧性地照亮。“奥斯卡，”他说道，以引起奥斯卡的注意，仿佛奥斯卡迷失在自己思绪的危险迷宫中。“奥斯卡，我从来没有发挥出自己的潜力。在我来到美国之后就没有了。”

Kurt steels himself for a painful moment of self-awareness. He is a skeletal puppet in abundant costume, theatrically lit by a fire that manages to overpower the yellow sunlight. “Oskar,” he says to get his attention, as if it is Oskar who is lost in a dangerous maze of his own thoughts. “Oskar, I never lived up to my potential. Not after I came to America.”

奥斯卡抚摸着额头，想找些安慰的话，但什么也没找到。

Oskar strokes his forehead and searches for some consoling words. He finds none.

“如果我没有发现不完备定理，也会有别人发现。”

“If I had not discovered the incompleteness theorems, someone else would have.”

“我对此表示怀疑。”奥斯卡屏住呼吸，重新调整双腿。

“I doubt that.” Oskar holds his breath as he readjusts his legs.

“是的，有人会这么做，因为数学独立于我们任何人而存在。”

“Yes, someone would have because mathematics exists independently of any of us.”

“我认识很多聪明人，库尔特，才华横溢的人。我不知道有谁能做到你所做的。我敢肯定我们还没有完全理解其中的含义，我敢肯定我们没有。但我们都知道你发现了最终的极限。爱因斯坦表明，没有什么能比光传播得更快，海森堡意识到我们永远无法超越量子不确定性，而你告诉我们，数字，甚至是数字，永远超出了人类的理性范围。”

“I know many clever people, Kurt, brilliant people. I do not know anyone who could have done what you did. I’m sure we still haven’t fully understood the implications, I’m sure we haven’t. But we all know you discovered the ultimate limit. Einstein showed that nothing can travel faster than light, Heisenberg realized that we can never transcend quantum uncertainty, and you taught us that numbers, numbers even, are forever beyond human reason.”

“我没那么出名。”

“I am not so famous.”

“这有那么重要吗？”

“Does that matter so much?”

“如果这些想法不为人所知，那就很重要了。”

“It matters if the ideas are not well known.”

“但你的想法是众所周知的。你改变了一切。现在有了机器，也许有一天会有智能，人工智能。”如果说“对我们的未来产生了多大的影响”这句话听起来有些陈词滥调，奥斯卡之所以这么说，只是因为他是真心实意的，而且他几乎是自言自语。

“But your ideas are known. You have changed everything. And now there are machines and maybe one day intelligence, artificial intelligence.” If it sounds trite to add, “What an impact to have on our future,” Oskar does so only because he means it and he says it almost to himself.

“维特根斯坦说我的定理不过是把戏。把戏。艺术品！”

“Wittgenstein said my theorems were no better than tricks. Trickery. Kunststücke!”

“维特根斯坦，”奥斯卡笑道。他的名字仍然勾起了人们对维也纳的回忆。尽管最近这种回忆已经逐渐消失，但奥斯卡还是忍受了许多关于维特根斯坦的长篇大论——关于他拥有莫里茨、他的想法，以及最糟糕的是他对库尔特成就的漠视。“你很清楚，”他敲着椅子，强调他无数次提出的观点；“你很清楚，”他重复道，“很多人认为你的证明是数学史上最重要的成果。”

“Wittgenstein,” Oskar laughs. His name still stirs memories of Vienna. Although they have petered off as of late, Oskar has tolerated many a tirade about Wittgenstein—about his possession of Moritz, his ideas, and worst of all his disregard of Kurt's achievements. “You well know,” here he pounds on his chair to instill a point he has made countless times; “you well know,” he repeats, “that there are many who consider your proof to be the most important result in the history of mathematics.”

他们安静了好一会儿，直到太阳明显改变了角度，科特才说：“我还能完成一些壮举。我仍然有这个能力。”

They are quiet just long enough for the sun to perceptibly change angles before Kurt says, “I am still capable of some feats. I still have that ability.”

“我毫不怀疑。”

“I have no doubt.”

“我正在做出真正的选择，不可思议的选择。”

“I am making real choices, incredible choices.”

“你做出的这些选择让我害怕。”

“It's these choices you make that scare me.”

“我的这些行为是力量的展现，是自由的体现，是自由意志的证明。”

“These actions of mine are a show of strength, you know, a demonstration of freedom. A proof of free will.”

“具体是哪些选择？”

“Which choices exactly?”

“我已经一个多星期没吃东西了。”

“I haven’t eaten in over a week.”

“天啊，库尔特。”

“Jesus, Kurt.”

“宇宙中的每一种力量都把我们推入这些看似无法逃脱的循环。每一种力量都得到了解释。我正在做不可能。我选择违抗这些力量，做出与他们指示不同的反应。”

“Every force in the universe drives us into these seemingly inescapable cycles. Every force accounted for. I am doing the impossible. I am choosing to disobey these forces, to react differently than they instruct.”

“天啊，库尔特，”奥斯卡重复道。

“Jesus, Kurt,” Oskar repeats.

这是库尔特陷入幻觉之前他们最后一次真正的交流。奥斯卡试图在库尔特的脑海中找到一条路径，让他找到他那位才华横溢的朋友的藏身之处。他会牵着他的手，带他走出眼睛的门户，穿过圆形黑框的双目镜片，走向这个简单的现实。这场谈话是一种折磨。（还会有许多其他可怕的谈话，主题重复。库尔特会不停地打电话两个星期，直到心碎的多萝西接电话的那一天——奥斯卡去世的那一天。哥德尔会一言不发地挂断她的电话。他不会跟任何人提起这件事。谁知道什么是真实的？）奥斯卡无法用他那双无力的腿站起来，坐在那里，听着库尔特关门的声音，库尔特带着摩根斯特恩家的两件外套和一件毛衣走进了潮湿的天气，披肩掉在地上。奥斯卡从轮椅上拿起一根熨斗，把火扑灭了。

That was their last real exchange before Kurt was lost among hallucinations. Oskar tries to find a path through Kurt's mind that will lead him to where his brilliant friend is hiding. He would take him by the hand and bring him forward out the portals of his eyes, through the binocular lenses in the round black frames, to this simple reality. The conversation is torture. (There will be many other terrible conversations with repeating themes. Kurt will phone relentlessly for two more weeks until the day a heartbroken Dorothy answers—the day Oskar dies. Gödel will hang up on her without a word. He will speak of it to no one. Who knows what's real?) Unable to get up on his useless legs, Oskar remains seated as he hears the door close after Kurt, who departs into the humid day with the Morgensterns’ two coats and one sweater, leaving the wrap where it falls on the floor. From his wheelchair, Oskar reaches for a flat iron poker and snuffs out the fire.

圣诞节前夕，阿黛尔回到家中，身体虚弱，卧床不起。她无法照顾科特萎缩的身体和过度热情的头脑，因此，一个身体膨胀，另一个则受损。他的骨头上的肉被烧掉，骨髓干涸，只剩下脆弱的骨骼外壳。她歇斯底里地哀嚎，直到科特终于同意以急救为由入院。

Adele returns home near Christmas, enfeebled and confined to bed. She cannot nurse Kurt's atrophied body and overzealous mind, so that one swells at the cost of the other. The meat burns off his bones and the marrow dries inside until all that is left is the fragile skeletal shell. She wails in hysterics until Kurt finally concedes to admit himself to the hospital as an emergency case.

他生命中最后的日子，一直直挺挺地坐在医院的椅子上，痛苦不堪。他误诊了关节疼痛、胸部收缩、侧腹绞痛。他怀疑心脏因童年发烧而受损，溃疡因喝茶而加重，器官因食用有毒食物而受损。但实际上，这只是他身体所有部位发出的疯狂恳求——向凶手求饶。

He spends his last days sitting upright in a hospital chair, mortified by the agony. He misdiagnoses every joint-crunching ache, every contraction in his chest, every cramp in his side. He suspects a heart damaged by childhood fever, an ulcer aggravated by tea, organ damage from poisoned food. But really it is just the frantic pleas from all of the elements of his body— appeals for mercy from their murderer.

他在医院的椅子上坐了三天，体重六十五磅，倔强又沉默，直到因长时间的折磨而死去。自我绝食。他认为这次自杀是他自由意志的胜利，是强加于所有正当力量的不可能的选择。但从外表来看，他的自杀似乎是两种驱动力找到均等力量的唯一可能结果：生存的决心和死亡的决心之间的最终僵局。难道他的选择不是选择，只是幻觉？

For three days he sits in that hospital chair at sixty-five pounds, recalcitrant and taciturn, until death comes from prolonged self-starvation. He believes this suicide to be a triumph of his free will, an impossible choice imposed against all rightful forces. But from the outside, his suicide could seem to be the only possible outcome of two drives finding equal strength: the ultimate impasse between the determination to live and the determination to die. Could it be that his choice is not a choice, only an illusion?

在这三天里，他一直在与怀疑和恐惧作斗争，他们说没有灵魂，没有来世，心灵只不过是一种生物机制，死亡后就会死亡，仅此而已。在这三天里，他全神贯注于内心，全神贯注于他那病态的心灵。

For these three days he fights off doubts and fears that there is no soul, no hereafter, and the mind is no more than a biological mechanism that dies when it dies and that is that. He spends these three days turned inward, focused with the full effort of his ailing mind.

威姆斯洛，1954 年

WILMSLOW, 1954

艾伦对人们行为背后的原因几乎不感兴趣。我们很少对自己不擅长的事情感兴趣，艾伦也不擅长解读别人，甚至不擅长解读自己。今天早上，当他登上从曼彻斯特开往伦敦的早班火车，打算在白金汉郡下车时，他从未停下来考虑自己的动机，因此他从未停下来担心后果。两年前，他清楚地记得自己决定是时候回到森林里寻找他的战时投资了。他甚至还弄到了合适的工具来寻找丢失的赏金，但它们和他的战功勋章一起被搁置在他的棚子里。昨晚，当他睡不着觉，发现他的电镀实验太无聊，无法缓解他的情绪时，去森林旅行的想法突然浮现在他的脑海里。谁知道为什么？也许他只是对那段他最快乐的时刻有点伤感。

The reasons behind people's actions interest Alan very little. We are rarely interested in things we are no good at and Alan is no good at deciphering people, not even himself. When he boards an early train from Manchester to London this morning with the intention of alighting in Buckinghamshire, he never stops to consider his motives and so he never stops to worry over the implications. Two years ago he distinctly remembers deciding it was time to go back to the woods and find his wartime investment. He even went so far as to acquire proper tools for locating the lost bounty but they languished in his shed along with his war medal. When sleep deserted him last night and he found his electroplating experiment too boring to alleviate his mood, the idea of the trip to the woods came to him all at once. Who knows why? Maybe he was the littlest bit sentimental for that time when he was the littlest bit happy.

清晨的旅程很轻松，他的疲劳几乎令人愉快，因为他摇摇晃晃地走过一排排相连的砖房。艾伦走进树林，开始寻找银块。中午时分，他开始在泥地里挖东西。他很放松，但有点沮丧。他的身体让他感到恶心。他肥胖无能。最可怕的是，他因为荷尔蒙而长出了乳房。他终于承认这些变化是永久的，也是不可能发生的。他们毒害了他。他们几乎要了他的命。如果他们不完成任务，他会自己完成。

The early morning trip is easy, his fatigue almost pleasant, as he rocks past rows of attached brick houses. Alan makes his way to the woods and sets his expedition for the silver bars under way. By noon, he is digging in the mud. He is relaxed, if depressed. His body disgusts him. He is obese and impotent. Most horrid of all, he has developed breasts from the hormones. These have been changes that he finally admits are both permanent and impossible. They have poisoned him. They’ve as good as killed him. If they don’t finish the job, he’ll do it himself.

经过这么多年，这辆婴儿车仍然在树林里。它积累了数季的雨水和碎石，几乎没有机会干燥。它创造了自己的小气候，生长着丰富的霉菌和植被。琼会知道这些物种叫什么。海军蓝帆布现在变成了黑色和绿色，有些地方有粉蓝色的斑点。大轮子的金属辐条从长满青苔的中心伸出，就像完美、闪亮的金属树枝。它的大部分人工特征已被磨损，因此看起来像是自然生长的东西。这辆婴儿车是一个奇特的地标，某种意义上是一块墓碑。

After all of these years the pram is still in the woods. It has collected seasons of rain and detritus, rarely having a chance to dry out. It created its own microclimate and grows a rich culture of mold and vegetation. Joan would know what these species are called. The navy blue canvas is now black and green with speckles of powdery blue in places. The metal spokes of the big wheels stick out from mossy centers like perfect, shiny, metal twigs. Much of its artificial character has been worn down so that it looks like something grown naturally. The pram is a peculiar landmark, a gravestone of sorts.

这是他第三次也是最后一次寻找金条。第一次他设法找到了他与银条一起埋藏的 200 英镑战前钞票。钞票虽然脏了，但还能用。第二次他带着自己设计和制造的金属探测器。它工作得很好，可以探测到土壤下的几个金属碎片，但甚至无法探测到他埋第一根金条的树林地底的浅坟那么深的地方。他相当肯定第二根金条是在溪流的河床下找到的。那里由于冰冷的水太深而无法进行挖掘，因此遗留了下来。

This is his third and final expedition to recover the bars. The first time he managed to locate 200 pounds in prewar notes that he buried alongside the silver. The notes were soiled but usable. The second time he came with a metal detector of his own design and manufacture. It worked well enough to call up several metal bits and bobs just under the soil but not well enough to see even as deep as the shallow grave in the floor of the woods where he buried the first bar. The second bar he was fairly sure he had located under the bed of the stream. There it remained when digging was discouraged by the depth of the icy cold water.

这次他带着工业金属探测器回来了，探测器发现了更多的导电碎片（它们都是从哪里来的？天空？），但仍然无法分离出第一根银条。第二根银条真的丢失了。原来的桥被拆除，取而代之的是一座新桥，现在河床两旁铺满了混凝土。带有加密说明的苯丙胺吸入器与原来的桥一起倒塌了。当其中一名建筑工人惊讶地发现它时，他把这个谜团和他的好奇心一起扔进了废墟。第二根银条从未被发现，一定还躺在那里，既没有腐烂也没有施肥。一根不自然地闪闪发光的骨头。

This time he comes back with an industrial metal detector that turns up yet more conducting debris (Where does it all come from? The sky?), but still fails to isolate the first silver bar. The second bar is truly lost. The original bridge has been torn down, replaced with a new structure, and concrete now lines the streambed. The Benzedrine inhaler with the enciphered instructions fell along with the original bridge. While one of the builders spotted it with amazement he discarded the mystery in the rubble, along with his curiosity. The second bar was never found and must still lie there, neither rotting nor fertilizing. An unnaturally shiny bone.

艾伦并没有太失望。当他放弃搜索时，他决定变得非常脏。他像孩子一样爬、挖、跳、嬉戏。他一直寻找蠕虫和分形根，直到天色渐晚。

Alan isn’t too disappointed. When he abandons the search, he commits to getting really filthy. He climbs and digs and skips and romps like a child. He searches for worms and fractal roots until the day is gone.

他长途跋涉回到曼彻斯特，火车在乡间疾驰而过，摇摇晃晃，他背对着后方。树木和山丘像雨水从伞上滑落一样流逝。玻璃泡沫的另一边，风景模糊不清。在玻璃的倒影中，他看到了自己那双蓝眼睛的玻璃窗，他觉得自己站在那块无法穿透的靛蓝色大理石窗外，那块大理石窗将他与世界隔开。他从那双永远被锁在里面的眼睛后面向外看，徒劳地盯着那双永远被锁在外面的眼睛。

He travels the long way back to Manchester, facing backward as the train rocks and sways while it tears past the countryside. The trees and hills stream away like rain sloughing off an umbrella. The scenery smearing on the other side of the bubble of glass. In its reflection he sees his own blue-eyed window-panes and he feels himself on the outside of the impenetrable indigo marbles that separate him from the world. He looks out from behind these eyes, permanently locked in, to stare with futility into those eyes, permanently locked out.

审判两年后，他第一次从那双没有因荷尔蒙变化而改变的眼睛里认出了自己，脂肪和乳房。顺便说一句，审判迅速而果断。艾伦和他的同伙都对十二项严重猥亵罪名表示认罪。（是的，艾伦承认，他做了。不，他不认为这是错的。）从被捕到审判的几个星期里，艾伦一直饱受神经紧张的折磨，尽管在艾伦看来，这只是他本已不寻常的举止的轻微加深。他尽可能在家工作，偶尔出现在大学或伦敦参加会议。排斥和尴尬对他来说是熟悉的状态，他似乎继续生活，甚至嘲笑——几乎吹嘘——他的罪行。但私下里，恐慌已经笼罩了他——这种恐慌将逐渐蔓延到他的整个身体。

For the first time in the two years since the trial he recognizes himself in those eyes, unchanged as they are by hormones, fat, and breasts. The trial, incidentally, was quick and decisive. Alan and his accomplice both pleaded guilty to the twelve charges of Gross Indecency. (Yes, Alan confessed, he did it. No, he did not believe it was wrong.) The several weeks between his arrest and trial were a torment of nervous agitation although in Alan this surfaced as only a mild deepening of his already unusual manner. He worked at home as best he could, occasionally appearing at the university or in London for a conference. Ostracism and embarrassment being familiar states for him, he seemed to go on with life and even laugh—almost boast—of his crimes. But privately panic had seized him— a panic that would spread steadily throughout his system.

他的律师解释说，根据 1885 年《刑法修正案》第 11 条，对严重猥亵罪的判决要么是阉割，要么是监禁。艾伦仍然对自己的割礼心怀怨恨。失去压舱物（也就是罪魁祸首）的前景是完全不可能的。他肯定会选择坐牢。他可以承受监狱——残忍、欺凌、虐待等级制度——他在多塞特的谢尔本男子学校接受过这方面的训练。他承受不了。他会是一场灾难——但他会活下来，而且会保持男子气概。

His lawyer explained that the sentence imposed for Gross Indecency contrary to Section 11 of the Criminal Law Amendment Act 1885 was either castration or prison. Alan was still resentful over his circumcision. The prospect of losing the ballasts, the primary culprits as it were, was entirely impossible. He would definitely opt for prison. Prison he could handle— cruelty, bullying, abusive hierarchies—he had been trained for this at Sherborne School for boys in Dorset. He wouldn’t handle it well. He’d be a disaster—but he’d survive and with his manhood attached.

一开始，当他听到律师使用这个词时，他感觉自己被人捅了一刀。判决还没结束，他就被击倒了。他的膝盖一软，血液疯狂地涌向腹股沟，嘴唇和毛孔却没有从失血中获益。“他们能做到吗？”他努力说道。在心血管狂躁的金属管弦乐中，他几乎能听出那些平淡无奇的案件清单通过阉割，这种技术在美国被广泛应用，更不用说《纽约时报》最近发表的一篇文章，提倡广泛实施这种做法来矫正变态者和变态者。他几乎听不到耳朵里的轰鸣声。确切的措辞并不重要。这不是诗歌。他明白自己又一次没有理解。这一次他们不会直接把他推到地板下面。

At first, when he heard his lawyer use the word, it was as though the incision had been made. He was felled before the sentence's end. As his knees gave way, the blood raced to his groin in hysterical support, his lips and pores not benefiting from the blood loss. “Can they do that?” he managed. Through a metallic orchestra of cardiovascular mania he could almost make out the matter-of-factly recited catalog of cases resolved by castration, the technique applied liberally in America not to mention the recent article in the Times advocating the broad implementation of the practice to rectify perverts and deviants. He could barely hear over the roar in his ears. The precise phrasing didn’t matter. It wasn’t poetry. He understood that once again he hadn’t understood. And this time they weren’t just going to shove him below the floorboards.

“他们还不如杀了我。”他从律师的肩膀上方的窗户里看着自己。灯光的反光使他的下巴变色，让他想起了那一滴滴的血，多年前战争期间，他一看到那一滴血就昏了过去，他居然咯咯地笑了起来——声音尖锐、刺耳、可笑。“你知道我一看到血就晕过去，”他脱口而出。笑声继续着，他试图压抑自己的紧张情绪，但成功程度与压抑自己的性欲一样，从他紧闭的嘴里挤出来。

“They might as well kill me.” He watched himself in the window over the lawyer's shoulder. The reflection of the lights tinted his jaw and reminded him of the drool of blood, the sight of which had knocked him unconscious all those years ago during the war, and he actually cackled—high, piercing, and ridiculous. “You know I faint at the sight of blood,” he blurted. The laugh continued, pinched through his sealed mouth as he tried to repress his nervousness, about as successfully as he repressed his sexuality.

最后，他没有接受手术阉割，而是接受了化学阉割，注射了大量的雌激素，导致他阳痿，乳房发育异常。根据刑期，他必须定期接受治疗，在曼彻斯特皇家医院接受药物治疗，并植入最后一次激素，据说激素可持续三个月。艾伦不想冒任何风险，在刑期结束时通过手术取出了植入物，这样他终于自由了，至少在法律眼中。虽然他并不经常自怜或愤世嫉俗，但他怀疑事实并非如此。

In the end he was not surgically castrated but chemically castrated with massive doses of estrogen that left him impotent and with notably developed breasts. His sentence required he submit to treatments at regular intervals, receiving his pills at the Manchester Royal Infirmary with a final hormone implant that was reputed to last for three months. Not taking any chances, Alan had the implant surgically removed at the end of his sentence and with that he was finally, at least in the eyes of the law, free. Although he wasn’t often given to self-pity or cynicism, he rather suspected that this was not exactly true.

试验两年后，以及激素植入物移除一年后，效果似乎不可逆转。他的性欲从未完全消失，偶尔也会有外遇。在国外，巴黎或挪威，他经历了灾难与喜剧的结合，这总是让人欣慰。但事实上，器官疗法已经腐蚀了他。他的肉体软化了，他的欲望也软化成了果冻。

Two years after the trial and one year after the removal of his hormone implant, the effects feel irreversible. His libido was never entirely obliterated and there was the occasional affair he managed abroad, in Paris or Norway, with the usual gratifying combination of disaster and comedy. But in truth, the organotherapy has corroded him. His flesh is jelly and his desires have softened to a jelly too.

他不知道如何表达自己的耻辱，甚至不知道如何去体验它。耻辱像一个破碎的部件一样在他体内晃动，从他的金属框架中脱落并松动。耻辱不会在一个地方安顿下来，沉入其中，毫无疑问它会恶化，但至少可以被隔离，甚至可能被治疗。如果没有被时间的无形冲击波逐渐侵蚀，那么也许会更有针对性地被他的荣格分析师切除。但耻辱就是不会潜入并束缚他。

He doesn’t know how to voice his humiliation or even how to experience it. It rattles around in him like a broken part, dislodged and loose in his metal frame. The humiliation won’t settle on one place, sink in where it would no doubt fester but at least could be quarantined and possibly even treated. If not steadily eroded by the imperceptible buffing waves of time, then maybe more aggressively targeted, excised by his Jungian analyst. But the shame just won’t burrow and bind.

火车将他送回曼彻斯特，这是他最后一次试图找回银条的失败尝试。在威姆斯洛的家中，他把沾满泥巴的衣服扔进洗衣篮，拧开浴缸的水龙头，浴缸发出吱吱声，然后温水滴入浅浅的浴缸。他尽可能地将身体浸泡在浴缸中。他的膝盖仍然高高地暴露在凉爽的空气中，上面布满了鸡皮疙瘩。当他看着自己柔软的皮肤、陌生身体边缘的黄色褶皱、多余皮肤的起伏、油腻的猪油不自然堆积时，终于发生了这一切。他的羞辱感生根发芽，深深地扎入他肿胀的乳房脂肪中，从那个堡垒中发出一股红色的羞耻感。嫩粉色需要整整一天才能褪去，即使到了那时，也只有在他的身体变冷、死亡时，它才会不情愿地消散。

The train returns him to Manchester from his final, failed attempt to recover his silver bars. In the isolation of his Wilmslow home, he discards his muddy clothes in a laundry hamper and twists the taps to the bath, which squeak and complain before dribbling tepid water into the shallow tub. He immerses as much of himself as he can. His knees, still high in the cool air, are covered with goose pimples. As he looks over his limp flesh, the yellow folds at the edges of his unfamiliar body, the undulation of the excess skin trapping an unnatural accumulation of oily lard, it finally happens. His humiliation takes root, furrows deep into the fat of his engorged breasts, and from that stronghold emits a pulse of red raw shame. It takes one full day for the tender pink to fade and even then it disperses only reluctantly when his body goes cold and dead.

他走出水面，擦干一半身体，一边哼着他最喜欢的童话，一边默默地开始策划自杀，“把苹果浸入汤汁中，让沉睡的死亡渗透进来。”

He steps out of the water, half dries himself, and silently begins the design of his suicide as he hums his favorite fairy tale, Dip the apple in the brew, let the sleeping death seep through.

他没有想到要写一张便条。他没有打扫卫生，也没有打任何不祥的电话。对母亲的悔恨让他有些不知所措，他允许自己在黑暗中思考这个问题。那天深夜，他设法解决了母亲的问题，几分钟后，他变得像黄油一样柔软，并愉快地沉入了昏昏欲睡之中。他很早就醒了，期待着他需要准备的化学实验。他醒得很早，但从沉睡到生命结束，他都流畅而轻松。

It doesn’t occur to him to write a note. He doesn’t clean up or place any ominous phone calls. Remorse for his mother hinders him for a bit and he allows himself to wonder about this on into the darkness. Late that night he manages a solution to the problem of his mother and within minutes he is supple as butter and deliciously succumbs to woozy sleep. He wakes early with anticipation over the chemistry experiment he needs to prepare. He wakes early, but from his slumber to the end of his life he is fluid and at ease.

他手头上有的是氰化钾。这是他电镀实验中的一种元素。氰化物摄入体内后会导致细胞窒息。每个细胞都会窒息，而他只是细胞的集合，因此也会和它们一起窒息。一袋矿物质渗透进历史的土壤。没有来世。没有灵魂。没有上帝。

It is potassium cyanide that he has on hand. It is an element in his electroplating experiment. Ingested, cyanide induces cellular asphyxiation. Each cell will suffocate and as he is just a collection of cells, he will suffocate with them. A bag of minerals seeped in history's soil. No hereafter. No soul. No God.

当他在舍伯恩上学时，他尝试过类似的电镀实验。即使在那时，这些材料也激发了他一个病态的自杀计划，用氰化物、苹果和电流自杀。这在某种程度上会很有趣，至少实验的执行过程很有趣，即使不是真正的死亡部分。他想知道如果他在舍伯恩上学时选择自杀会发生什么。宇宙中大大小小的所有事件是如何合谋将世界变成现在的样子的。他所有的想法和行动，无论大小，都是一个更大机制的必要步骤。但他不可能做出任何与他所做的不同的选择，因为没有自由意志这回事。世界就是现在的样子。

When he was a student at Sherborne, he tried a similar electroplating experiment. Even back then, the materials inspired a morbid plan to kill himself, using cyanide, an apple, and an electric current. It would have been fun in a way, at least the execution of the experiment, if not the actual dying part. He wonders what would have happened if he had chosen suicide as a schoolboy in Sherborne. How all the events in the universe, big and small, collude to make the world exactly as it is. How all of his ideas and actions, big and small, are necessary steps in an even bigger mechanism. But then he couldn’t have made any choices different from the ones he made, because there is no such thing as free will. The world is exactly as it is.

但他仍对自己在做出选择的感觉感到十分震惊。

And still it astounds him how much he feels that he is making choices.

几周后，最严重的忧郁情绪消退，他感觉自己几乎稳定了，但还是差点在谢尔本自杀。从地板下被释放的第二天，他在化学课上坐在克里斯旁边，开始告诉他如何重现碘实验，尽管颜色似乎不太对劲，烧杯摔在地板上。（克里斯不禁对艾伦每次上课都坐在他旁边的巧合发表评论。艾伦没有辩解的余地，害怕受到责备。但下课后，当他跟在克里斯后面去宗教课时，他感觉好多了，因为克里斯用眼神示意他跟着他。）当他坐在克里斯旁边的宗教课上时，艾伦邀请他去观看他更复杂的氰化物电镀金属实验。在自己的房间里和另一个学院的男孩交往是被严格禁止的，但也不是被严格禁止的。到了午夜，他承认克里斯不会像他被邀请的那样在晚饭后回家。在他柔软的手臂的舒适下，他的脸上流着水果大小的泪水，这些泪水在他刺痛的下巴上沸腾并变干成矿物盐。艾伦沉浸在如此强烈的孤独之中，他不敢相信这不是一种真实的东西。

He almost did succeed in killing himself at Sherborne quite by accident several weeks after the worst gloom ebbed and he felt almost stable. The day after his release from beneath the floorboards, he took the seat next to Chris in chemistry instruction and began to tell him how he had reproduced the iodine experiment even though the color never seemed quite right and the beaker smashed on the floor. (Chris could not help but remark on the coincidence of Alan's appearance on the seat next to him in each and every lecture. Alan had no defense and feared some reproach. But after class, when he trailed behind Chris on their way to religious instruction, he felt better, since Chris beckoned him to follow—he did so with his eyes.) When he then took the seat next to Chris in religious instruction, Alan invited him to see his more elaborate cyanide experiment for electroplating metal. It wasn’t strictly allowed to fraternize with boys of another house in one's room, but then it wasn’t strictly forbidden either. By midnight he admitted that Chris was not going to call around after supper as he had been invited to do. In the comfort of the soft fold of his arm, his face sizzled under fruit-sized tears that boiled off and dried to mineral salt on his stinging jaw. Alan was drenched in loneliness so viscous he couldn’t believe it wasn’t an actual substance.

除了那天晚上和随后的十一个晚上，他在学校的每个晚上都会吃一个苹果。相反，他拆开了实验装置，把零件（包括他习惯性的深夜水果）重新组装成一个自杀机器——一种带电毒药苹果。在接下来的几周里，他多次拆解并重新组装这个病态的装置。每隔几天，他就会摩擦这个变酸的水果的波纹状果皮。房间里空无一人，直到第二天早上，他把有毒的苹果扔进了垃圾桶，在早餐时捡到一块新的，用来重新组装这个装置。

Every night at school he ate an apple, except that night and the subsequent eleven nights. Instead, he dismantled his experiment and reassembled the pieces, including his habitual late-night fruit, into a suicide machine—an electrified poison apple. Several times over the coming weeks he dismantled and reassembled the morbid contraption. Every few days he would rub the rippled skin of the souring fruit. Blank hours moved past the room until morning when he threw the toxic apple in the rubbish, recovering a fresh piece at breakfast with which to rebuild the apparatus.

十一天后，克里斯来到图灵的房间，带了一篇新的数学论文，他要和老图灵分享。艾伦迅速拆开他发明的死亡装置，把苹果扔到一边。那天晚上，他想到了克里斯、证据、真理、意义和信仰，他感觉不那么空虚了。这就是为什么他觉得特别好笑，当他在床上用品堆里发现一个苹果时，他心不在焉地把它举到嘴边咬了一口。洗手，他妈妈过去常常责备他。不要把它们放进嘴里，她会警告你。总有一天你会毒死自己。

After eleven days, Chris came to Turing's room with a new article on mathematics that he had to share with old Turing. Alan quickly dismantled his inventive death appliance, tossing the apple aside. That night he thought about Chris and proof and truth and meaning and faith and he didn’t feel quite so hollow. Which is why he found it particularly hilarious that, when he found an apple in his pile of bedding, he absentmindedly lifted it to his lips to take a bite. Wash your hands, his mother used to scold. Don’t put them in your mouth, she’d warn. One day you’ll poi-son yourself.

每当他有这种感觉——茫然、空虚、麻木、愚蠢——他就会想起在地板下的那一小时和克里斯。这是他大脑不由自主的反应，就像一个不受欢迎的苦乐参半的记忆，在对一种感伤的气味——他童年的气味——的反应中侵入他的思想。每次，这几乎让他笑了起来。

Anytime he feels like this—blank, empty, numb, dumb—he thinks of that hour under the floor and of Chris. It is his brain's involuntary response, like an unwelcome bittersweet memory that invades his thoughts in reaction to a sentimental odor—the smell of his childhood. And every time, it almost makes him laugh.

他盯着装着毒药的透明烧杯，直到克里斯的记忆渐渐消失。他把苹果浸在毒药里，放回桌上。这只需要几分钟。他不知道自己是该躺下还是倒下。他宁愿先躺下，然后躺在床上。他在那里躺了一会儿。感觉确实不错。他腹部的新沉重感和当他像这样陷在床上时，手臂不会对他造成任何影响，多余的肉会将他推入弹簧深处。他躺在那里很长时间。

He stares into the clear beaker of poison until the memory of Chris has come and gone. He dips the apple in the brew and returns it to its place on the table. It will take only a few minutes. He doesn’t know if he should lie or fall. He rather wants to lie down first and arranges himself on the bed. He lies there a while. It does feel good. The new heaviness in his belly and arms doesn’t bother him when he's sunk in the bed like this, the extra flesh pushing him deeper into the springs. He lies there a long while.

时间似乎到了，他被无情的洪流冲刷着，坐在金属床边，伸手去拿苹果，用牙齿咬破漂亮的红皮。果皮很粉。他再次咬了一口，嘴里还塞满了咀嚼过的水果。他试着站起来。他蹒跚着，吞咽着，然后跌倒了。

When the time comes, as it seems to, flowing by until he is carried on its relentless current, he sits on the edge of the metal-framed bed, reaches for the apple, and breaks the pretty red skin with his teeth. It is mealy. He bites again with a mouth still full of masticated fruit. He tries to stand. He lurches and swallows as he falls.

他的细胞不会同时死亡。每个细胞都会单独死亡，就像一只被两根长满老茧的手指夹住的虫子。有些系统会立即关闭，而其他系统则会剧烈震动。他能感觉到自己的背部与地板相连，直到皮肤变得冰冷，他觉得皮肤一定已经消失了。他能感觉到左大腿上一阵剧痒，右脚抽搐。

His cells don’t die in unison. Each cell perishes separately like a bug squashed between two calloused fingers. Some systems shut down immediately while others kick and jolt. He can feel his back connected to the floor until the skin is so cold he thinks it must be gone. He can feel a vicious itch on his left thigh and his right foot jerks.

他想象自己会有一个最后的想法，并想知道它会是什么。它以 Bold Blue、Chris、An Ache of Love 和 Crushed Glass 开头。然后他的思想像一个失调的管弦乐队一样折叠起来，虽然他仍然保持意识并意识到自己，但他的思想开始分解成组成部分，直到语言消失，只剩下抽象。他的最后一个想法不是一个词或一个图像；它是他脑海中的一道闪电，他的大脑释放出来，他灰质的每一个领域都发出最后一个音符，只要化学物质能够维持它，它就会响起，就像管弦乐队停止演奏后歌剧的共鸣一样。

He imagined he’d have one last thought and wondered what it would be. It starts with Bold Blue, Chris, An Ache of Love, Crushed Glass. Then his mind folds up like a de-tuning orchestra and while he remains aware and aware of himself, his thoughts begin to disintegrate into component parts until language is gone and there is just abstraction. His last thought isn’t a word or an image; it is a bolt in his mind as his brain releases and every dominion of his gray matter throws out a last note that rings as long as the chemicals can sustain it like the resonance of an opera long after the orchestra stops playing.

他的唇边聚集起泡沫，并在他最后一次呼气的微风中轻轻冒泡。

A froth gathers around his lips and bubbles delicately in the breeze of his last exhalation.

纽约市

NEW YORK CITY

现在，我来到了纽约市。现在是二十一世纪。这里是个好地方，这个时代也是个好时代。

Here I am, in New York City. It is the twenty-first century. This place is as good a place, this time as good a time, as any.

我正从路边走下来。地铁入口就在街对面。巨大的绿色球体表示市中心入口已开放。人造光与太阳争光。公园里有孩子；一个银发女人，穿着一件旧长外套；一对夫妇坐在长椅上。街道上挤满了黄色的出租车。我走在一些出租车的后面，走在另一些出租车的前面。我们都沿着固定的轨迹，按照规定的弧线移动。当我沿着古老的台阶走进地铁时，出租车消失在石墙后面。

I am stepping off a curb. The subway entrance is just across the street. Big green orbs signify that the downtown entrance is open. Artificial light competing against the sun. There are children in the park; a woman with silver hair and a long, old coat; a couple on a bench. A yellow plague of taxis infests the streets. I walk behind some and in front of others. We all move along fixed trajectories, following our prescribed arcs. The plague disappears behind the stone wall as the old steps take me down into the subway.

我在城市地下。在地下的恶臭中，各种液体从街道上涌出，从格栅上流到铁轨上。一列火车来了。车厢是空的。我可以从C列车的窗户看到我的眼睛。一只大大的黑眼睛。我在里面看着从外面向内看。我盯着不透明的圆盘上的一台生物机器。

I am under the city. In this stink of an underground, miscellaneous liquids pour from the streets off the grating and onto the tracks. A train comes. The car is empty. I can see my eye in the window of the C train. A big black eye. I’m inside looking out and outside looking in. I stare into the opaque disk at a biological machine.

没有结局。我曾试图编造一个结局，但那是一个谎言，我不想撒谎。这个故事的结局将在它开始的地方结束，在中间。一个三角形或一个圆圈。一个由三个点组成的闭环。一段寻找埋藏在树林里、街道上、书中、空火车上的宝藏的旅行纪事。渴望护身符、宝石、理由、目的、真理。我几乎可以在边缘看到它，就在他们说的地方，从我搜索的每个角度的远处闪闪发光。

There is no ending. I’ve tried to invent one but it was a lie and I don’t want to be a liar. This story will end where it began, in the middle. A triangle or a circle. A closed loop with three points. A wayfaring chronicle searching for a treasure buried in the woods, on the streets, in books, on empty trains. Craving an amulet, a jewel, a reason, a purpose, a truth. I can almost see it on the periphery, just where they said it would be, glistening at me from the far edges of every angle I search.

笔记

NOTES

阅读历史人物的记述时，自然会想知道哪些核心事实（如果有的话）被改变了。构成本书的场景取自库尔特·哥德尔和艾伦·图灵的技术著作、他们的存档文件和传记。关于传记信息，我特别感谢三本书：安德鲁·霍奇斯的《艾伦·图灵之谜》 ；约翰·道森的《逻辑困境：库尔特·哥德尔的生平和工作》；以及雷·蒙克的《路德维希·维特根斯坦：天才的责任》。

It is natural when reading an account of historical figures to wonder which, if any, central facts have been changed. The scenes that structure the present work were drawn from the technical writings of Kurt Gödel and Alan Turing, their archived papers, and their biographies. For biographical information, I am indebted to three books in particular, Alan Turing The Enigma, by Andrew Hodges; Logical Dilemmas: The Life and Work of Kurt Gödel, by John Dawson; and Ludwig Wittgenstein: The Duty of a Genius, by Ray Monk.

本书中刻意更改的事实很少。大部分都是对次要人物的改动。例如，奥托·诺伊拉特和奥尔加·哈恩·诺伊拉特确实是维也纳学派的成员。奥托有着红头发和红胡子，性格热情而魁梧。奥尔加是盲人，抽雪茄。但我不知道他们与哥德尔的友谊细节，这里讲述的他们友谊的故事大部分都是虚构的。当哥德尔乘坐尚普兰号返回欧洲时，挥手告别的不是奥斯卡，而是另一位同事——尽管奥斯卡后来成为哥德尔最后一位在世的朋友，这段友谊的其他细节这个故事中叙述的事件都有历史依据。图灵第一次去看白雪公主是和一个剑桥的朋友一起去的，而不是琼，为了连贯，他去森林里找银子的时间以及他去拜访吉普赛女王的时间都做了调整。还有一点值得一提：图灵 1936 年的杰出论文《论可计算数及其在判定问题中的应用》经常在停机问题的背景下被讨论。然而，图灵并没有使用这种语言——这个表达是在 20 世纪 50 年代创造的——所以这本书没有明确使用这种语言。图灵和哥德尔思想的深度和广度在这里只是略微触及。我只能参考许多关于他们工作的优秀著作。最后，本书有很多遗漏，哥德尔和图灵生活中的迷人细节超出了本书的范围。这些细节包括哥德尔与爱因斯坦的友谊、图灵在战争期间在美国的工作以及战后对曼彻斯特计算机的开发。

The number of facts that were intentionally altered in this narrative is small. The most liberty was taken with secondary characters. For instance, Otto Neurath and Olga Hahn-Neurath were indeed part of the Vienna Circle. Otto had red hair and a red beard and a warm, burly personality. Olga was blind and smoked cigars. But I am not privy to the details of their friendship with Gödel, and the story of their friendship as told here is largely invented. It was not Oskar who waved good-bye as Gödel traveled on the Champlain back to Europe but another colleague—although Oskar was to become Gödel's last living friend and the other details of that friendship recounted in this story have historical support. Turing first went to see Snow White with a Cambridge friend, not Joan, and the timing of the trips to recover the silver in the woods, as well as his visit to the Gypsy Queen, were altered for cohesion. Another point worth mentioning: Turing's remarkable 1936 paper, “On Computable Numbers, with an Application to the Entscheidungsproblem,” is often discussed in the context of the Halting Problem. However, Turing did not use this language—the expression was coined in the 1950s—and so that language is not used explicitly in this book. The depth and magnitude of both Turing's and Gödel's ideas are only barely touched upon here. I can only defer to the numerous excellent volumes devoted to their work. Last, there are many omissions, fascinating particulars of Gödel's and Turing's lives that are beyond the scope of this book. A list of such particulars includes Gödel's friendship with Einstein as well as Turing's work in the United States during the war and his postwar development of the Manchester computer.

至于所包含的细节和整个故事，它们是对记录的历史事件的回应。图灵至少有一次被困在舍伯恩学校的地板下。他破解了恩尼格玛密码，在战争期间将银块埋在树林里，与琼·克拉克订婚，与阿诺德·默里有过那段不幸的恋情，忍受了随后的激素治疗，拜访了吉普赛女王，并咬了一口含有氰化物的苹果自杀。哥德尔确实娶了阿黛尔，她也确实用勺子喂他自制的德国菜。他确实相信灵魂轮回，在各种疗养院呆过一段时间，患有偏执和妄想症，保存了纸片和一卷正反面都盖着的笔记本，最终绝食而死。

As for the included details and this story as a whole, they are a response to documented historical events. Turing had been trapped beneath the floorboards at Sherborne School at least once. He cracked the Enigma code, buried silver bullion in the woods during the war, was engaged to Joan Clarke, had that ill-fated affair with Arnold Murray, endured the subsequent hormone therapy, visited the Gypsy Queen, and committed suicide with a bite from a cyanide-laden apple. Gödel did marry Adele and she did spoon-feed him homemade German fare. He did believe in the transmigration of the soul, spent time in various sanatoria, suffered from paranoia and delusions, saved scraps of paper and volumes of notebooks covered front and back, and ultimately starved himself to death.

本作品中有几处地方出现了直接引文，尽管上下文可能已经改变。这些注释会识别并恢复所有完整引文，并将它们与参考文献一起放入其原始上下文中。在大多数情况下，会引用主要参考文献以及可以找到引文的次要参考文献。这绝不是参考资料的完整列表。

There are several places in the present work where direct quotations appear, although the context may have been changed. These notes identify and restore any full quotes and place them into their original context with references. In most cases a primary reference is cited as well as a secondary reference in which the quote can be found. This is in no way a complete list of sources consulted.

16 “不可否认，他不是一个‘正常’的男孩。”谢伯恩学校韦斯科特宿舍舍监杰弗里·奥汉隆对图灵的学校报告作出了这样的评价。安德鲁·霍奇斯，《阿兰·图灵之谜》（纽约：西蒙与舒斯特出版社，1983 年）。

16 “Undeniably he is not a ‘normal’ boy.” Comments on Turing's school reports from Geoffrey O’Hanlon, the housemaster of Westcott house at Sherborne School. Andrew Hodges, Alan Turing The Enigma (New York: Simon & Schuster, 1983).

27 “我无法原谅他对《新约》的理智讨论所持的愚蠢态度。”阿兰·图灵的班主任 AH Trelawny Ross 的评论。霍奇斯，阿兰·图灵。 71 “他们对我说的谎言有一半是真的。”雷蒙德·斯穆里安列出了几句自我毁灭的句子，这些句子最初由索尔·戈恩博士在他的《罕见陈词滥调汇编》中编纂而成。雷蒙德·斯穆里安，《公元前 5000 年和其他哲学幻想》 （纽约：圣马丁出版社，1983 年）。

27 “I cannot forgive the stupidity of his attitude towards sane discussion on the New Testament.” Comments of Alan Turing's form-master, A.H. Trelawny Ross. Hodges,Alan Turing. 71 “Half the lies they tell about me are true.” Raymond Smullyan lists several self-annihilating sentences first compiled by Dr. Saul Gorn in his “Compendium of Rarely Used Clichés.” Raymond Smullyan, 5000 B.C. and Other Philosophical Fantasies (New York: St Martin's Press, 1983).

99 “我亲爱的莫尔康夫人，我很高兴在复活节来到钟楼。我总是喜欢特别想到与克里斯有关的复活节。它提醒我们克里斯现在在某种程度上还活着。人们可能过于倾向于只考虑他在未来某个时候我们再次见到他时还活着；但实际上，把他想象成现在只是与我们分开，这更有帮助。”艾伦·图灵致莫尔康夫人。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

99 “My dear Mrs. Morcom, I was so pleased to be at the Clockhouse for Easter. I always like to think of it specially in connection with Chris. It reminds us that Chris is in some way alive now. One is perhaps too inclined to think only of him alive at some future time when we shall meet him again; but it is really so much more helpful to think of him as just separated from us for the present.” Alan Turing to Mrs. Morcom. Hodges, Alan Turing.

101 “科学界曾经认为，如果在某一特定时刻，我们了解了宇宙的一切，那么我们就可以预测宇宙在未来会是什么样子。这个想法实际上源于天文预测的巨大成功。然而，更现代的科学已经得出结论，当我们处理原子和电子时，我们完全无法知道它们的确切状态；我们的仪器本身就是由原子和电子构成的。那么，能够知道宇宙确切状态的观念在小范围内确实会崩溃。这意味着，认为日食等都是命中注定的，我们的所有行为也都是命中注定的理论也崩溃了。我们拥有一种意志，它能够决定原子的活动，可能在大脑的一小部分，也可能是整个大脑……当身体沉睡时，我无法猜测会发生什么，但当身体死亡时，身体的“机制”——支撑灵魂的机制——就会消失，灵魂迟早会找到一个新的身体，也许会立即找到。”艾伦·图灵对莫尔科姆夫人说。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

101 “It used to be supposed in Science that if everything was known about the Universe at any particular moment then we can predict what it will be through all the future. This idea was really due to the great success of astronomical prediction. More modern science however has come to the conclusion that when we are dealing with atoms and electrons we are quite unable to know the exact state of them; our instruments being made of atoms and electrons themselves. The conception then of being able to know the exact state of the universe then really must break down on the small scale. This means then that the theory which held that as eclipses etc. are predestined so were all our actions breaks down too. We have a will which is able to determine the action of the atoms probably in a small portion of the brain, or possibly all over it… . When the body is asleep I cannot guess what happens but when the body dies the ‘mechanism’ of the body, holding the spirit, is gone and the spirit finds a new body sooner or later perhaps immediately.” Alan Turing to Mrs. Morcom. Hodges, Alan Turing.

112 “咖啡太难喝了。”哥德尔在回答奥斯卡关于维也纳的问题时对奥斯卡的评论。《奥斯卡·摩根斯坦日记》，杜克大学珀金斯纪念图书馆。约翰·W·道森，《逻辑困境：库尔特·哥德尔的生平和作品》（马萨诸塞州韦尔斯利：AK Peters，1997 年）。

112 “The coffee is wretched.” Gödel's comment to Oskar in response to Oskar's query about Vienna. Diaries of Oskar Morgenstern, Perkins Memorial Library of Duke University. John W. Dawson, Logical Dilemmas: The Life and Work of Kurt Gödel (Wellesley, Mass.: A. K. Peters, 1997).

112 “您为何来美国，伯格曼先生？”库尔特·哥德尔向古斯塔夫·伯格曼发问，伯格曼转述给约翰·道森。道森，《逻辑困境》。

112 “What brings you to America, Herr Bergmann?” Kurt Gödel to Gustav Bergmann as relayed by Bergmann to John Dawson. Dawson, Logical Dilemmas.

118 “你让我想起一个人透过一扇关闭的窗户往外看，无法向自己解释路人奇怪的动作。他不知道外面正刮着什么样的暴风雨，而这个人也许只能费很大力气才能站起来。”路德维希·维特根斯坦对他的妹妹赫敏·维特根斯坦说。赫敏·维特根斯坦，《我的兄弟路德维希》，《路德维希·维特根斯坦：个人回忆录》，拉什·里斯主编（牛津：巴兹尔·布莱克威尔，1981 年）。 123 “迷信会带来厄运。”雷蒙德·斯穆里安列出了索尔·戈恩博士首次整理的几句自我毁灭的句子。这句话是该列表中的第 13 条。斯穆里安，《公元前 5000 年和其他哲学幻想》。

118 “You remind me of someone who is looking through a closed window and cannot explain to himself the strange movements of a passer-by. He doesn’t know what kind of storm is raging outside and that this person is perhaps only with great effort keeping himself on his feet.” Ludwig Wittgenstein to his sister Hermine Wittgenstein. Hermine Wittgenstein, “My Brother Ludwig,” in Ludwig Wittgenstein: Personal Recollections, ed. Rush Rhees (Oxford: Basil Blackwell, 1981). 123 “Superstition brings bad luck.” Raymond Smullyan lists several self-annihilating sentences first compiled by Dr. Saul Gorn. This expression is number 13 on that list. Smullyan, 5000 B.C. and Other Philosophical Fantasies.

134—3 5 维特根斯坦 1939 年在《数学基础》课程中与图灵的对话，第 21 讲学生笔记中有记录：
