134—3 5 Conversation between Wittgenstein and Turing in Wittgenstein's 1939 course Foundations of Mathematics, as recorded in students’ notes during lecture XXI:

维特根斯坦： “想想撒谎者的例子。这很奇怪，任何人都应该对此感到困惑——比你想象的还要离奇：这应该是人类担心的事情。因为事情是这样的：如果一个人说“我在撒谎”，我们说他没有撒谎，由此又得出他在撒谎，等等。那又怎么样？你可以一直这样下去，直到你脸色发青。为什么不呢？没关系……现在假设一个人说“我在撒谎”，我说“因此你不是，因此你是，因此你不是……”——有什么错？没什么错。只是它没有用处；它只是一个无用的语言游戏，为什么有人会兴奋呢？”

WITTGENSTEIN:“Think of the case of the Liar. It is very queer in a way that this should have puzzled anyone—much more extraordinary than you might think: that this should be the thing to worry human beings. Because the thing works like this: if a man says ‘I am lying’ we say that it follows that he is not lying, from which it follows that he is lying and so on. Well, so what? You can go on like that until you are black in the face. Why not? It doesn’t matter… . Now suppose a man says ‘I am lying’ and I say ‘Therefore you are not, therefore you are, therefore you are not … ’—What is wrong? Nothing. Except that it is of no use; it is just a useless language-game, and why should anyone be excited?”

图灵： “让人困惑的是，人们通常用矛盾作为做错事的标准。但在这种情况下，人们找不到任何错误。”

TURING:“What puzzles one is that one usually uses a contradiction as a criterion for having done something wrong. But in this case one cannot find anything done wrong.”

维特根斯坦： “是的——而且，什么事都没有做错。危害又在哪里呢？”

WITTGENSTEIN:“Yes—and more: nothing has been done wrong. Where will the harm come?”

然后在讲座的后面：

And then later in the lecture:

图灵： “除非有应用，否则不会产生真正的危害，在这种情况下，桥梁可能会倒塌或发生类似的事情。”

维特根斯坦： “啊，现在，如果存在矛盾，桥梁就会倒塌的想法非常重要。但我太笨了，现在无法开始；所以我下次再谈。”

TURING:“The real harm will not come in unless there is an application, in which case a bridge may fall down or something of that sort.”

WITTGENSTEIN:“Ah, now this idea of a bridge falling down if there is a contradiction is of immense importance. But I am too stupid to begin it now; so I will go into it next time.”

然后在第二十二堂课中：

And then during lecture XXII:

维特根斯坦： “问题是：为什么人们害怕矛盾？很容易理解为什么他们应该害怕数学之外的秩序、描述等的矛盾。问题是：他们为什么要害怕数学内部的矛盾？图灵说：“因为应用可能会出错。”但什么都不必出错。如果真的出了问题——如果桥梁倒塌——那么你的错误就是使用了错误的自然法则。”

WITTGENSTEIN:“The question is: Why are people afraid of contradictions? It is easy to understand why they should be afraid of contradictions in orders, descriptions, etc., outside of mathematics. The question is: Why should they be afraid of contradictions inside mathematics? Turing says, ‘Because something may go wrong with the application.’ But nothing need go wrong. And if something does go wrong— if the bridge breaks down—then your mistake was of the kind of using a wrong natural law.”

路德维希·维特根斯坦，《维特根斯坦数学基础讲座》，剑桥 1939 年版，摘自 R. G. 博桑奎特、诺曼·马尔科姆、拉什·里斯和约里克·斯迈西斯的笔记，科拉·戴蒙德编辑（纽约：康奈尔大学出版社，1976 年）。

Ludwig Wittgenstein, Wittgenstein's Lectures on the Foundations of Mathematics, Cambridge 1939, From the Notes of R. G. Bosanquet, Norman Malcolm, Rush Rhees, and Yorick Smythies, ed. Cora Diamond (New York: Cornell University Press, 1976).

166 “教堂当然还在，但去年在这里的哥德尔、克莱尼、罗瑟和伯内斯已经离开了。除了哥德尔，我想我并不介意想念他们中的任何一个人。”图灵在从普林斯顿寄回家的一封信中写道。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

166 “Church is here of course, but Gödel, Kleene, Rosser and Bernays who were here last year have left. I don’t think I mind very much missing any of these except Gödel.” Turing in a letter home from Princeton. Hodges, Alan Turing.

166 “我认为必须公平对待机器。与其让它有时不给出答案，不如让它偶尔给出错误答案。但人类数学家在尝试新技术时也会犯错。我们很容易认为这些错误不算数，再给他一次机会，但机器可能不会得到宽恕。换句话说，如果一台机器被期望是绝对可靠的，那么它就不可能是智能的。有几条定理几乎完全说明了这一点。但这些定理并没有说明如果一台机器不假装绝对可靠，它可能会表现出多少智能……。必须允许机器与人类接触，以便它能够适应人类的标准。国际象棋游戏可能更适合这个目的，因为对手的举动会自动提供这种接触。”图灵在伦敦数学学会的演讲中说道。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

166 “I would say that fair play must be given to the machine. Instead of it sometimes giving no answer we could arrange that it gives occasional wrong answers. But the human mathematician would likewise make blunders when trying out new techniques. It is easy for us to regard these blunders as not counting and give him another chance, but the machine would probably be allowed no mercy. In other words then, if a machine is expected to be infallible, it cannot also be intelligent. There are several theorems which say almost exactly that. But these theorems say nothing about how much intelligence may be displayed if a machine makes no pretence at infallibility… . The machine must be allowed to have contact with human beings in order that it may adapt itself to their standards. The game of chess may perhaps be rather suitable for this purpose, as the moves of the opponent will automatically provide this contact.” Turing in a talk to the London Mathematical Society. Hodges, Alan Turing.

173— 74 “他大约二十五岁，身高五英尺十英寸，黑头发。”

173— 74 “He's about twenty-five years of age, five foot ten inches, with black hair.”

“我们有理由相信你的描述是错误的。你为什么要撒谎？”

“We have reason to believe your description is false. Why are you lying?”

“你愿意告诉我们你和他之间有过什么样的关系吗？”

“Would you care to tell us what kind of an affair you have had with him?”

“非常精彩的表述……流畅的文风，几乎像散文一样。”

“a lovely statement … a flowing style, almost like prose.”

“在某些措辞上超越了他们。”切斯特档案馆的文件中记录了艾伦·图灵与侦探威尔斯先生和里默先生之间的交流片段。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

“beyond them in some of its phraseology.” Pieces of the exchange between Alan Turing and the detectives Mr. Wills and Mr. Rimmer as recorded in documents of Chester Record Office. Hodges, Alan Turing.

175 “我想你知道我是同性恋。”阿兰·图灵在写给他弟弟约翰的信中说道。霍奇斯，阿兰·图灵。

175 “I suppose you know I’m a homosexual.” Alan Turing in a letter to his brother John. Hodges, Alan Turing.

175 “当你来到利物浦时，也许你会顺便去监狱看望我。”艾伦·图灵在写给他剑桥朋友弗雷德·克莱顿的信中写道。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

175 “When you come to Liverpool perhaps you will stop off to see me in jail.” Alan Turing in a letter to Fred Clayton, a Cambridge friend. Hodges, Alan Turing.

176

然而每个人都会杀死他所爱之物，

每个人都会听到这句话，

有的人用苦涩的眼神，

有的人用奉承的话语，

懦夫用吻，

勇敢的人用剑！

Yet each man kills the thing he loves,

By each let this be heard,

Some do it with a bitter look,

Some with a flattering word,

The coward does it with a kiss,

The brave man with a sword!

奥斯卡·王尔德，《雷丁监狱之歌》。艾伦·图灵在解除婚约时向琼·克拉克引用了这段话。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

Oscar Wilde, The Ballad of Reading Gaol. Alan Turing quoted this passage to Joan Clarke on the occasion of the dissolution of their engagement. Hodges, Alan Turing.

176 “……偶尔会练习……他们不像以前那么野蛮了。”艾伦·图灵在写给琼·克拉克的信中谈到他被捕的事。霍奇斯，艾伦·图灵。

176 “… do occasionally practice … They’re not as savage than they used to be.” Alan Turing in a letter to Joan Clarke concerning his arrest. Hodges, Alan Turing.

189 “图灵工作中的一个哲学错误。图灵在 1937 年的论文第 250 页（1965 年第 136 页）中提出了一个论点，该论点被认为是表明心理过程不能超越机械过程。然而，这一论点尚无定论。图灵完全忽视的事实是，心智在使用过程中并不是静态的，而是不断发展的…… ” 《关于不可判定性结果的一些评论》，《库尔特·哥德尔文集》第二卷，1938-1974 年出版，由所罗门·费弗曼、约翰·W·道森、小斯蒂芬·C·克莱恩、格雷戈里·H·摩尔、罗伯特·M·索洛维和让·范·海耶诺特编辑，（纽约：牛津大学出版社，1990 年）。

189 “A philosophical error in Turing's work. Turing in his 1937 paper, page 250 (1965, page 136), gives an argument which is supposed to show that mental procedures cannot go beyond mechanical procedures. However, this argument is inconclusive. What Turing disregards completely is the fact that mind, in its use, is not static, but constantly developing… .” Some Remarks on the Undecidability Results, in Kurt Gödel: Collected Works, Volume II, Publications 1938-1974, ed. Solomon Feferman, John W. Dawson, Jr., Stephen C. Kleene, Gregory H. Moore, Robert M. Solovay, Jean van Heijenoort, (New York: Oxford University Press, 1990).

190 “维也纳洗衣妇类型：喋喋不休、没有文化、意志坚强。”奥斯卡·摩根斯坦对阿黛尔的评论。道森，《逻辑困境》。

190 “a Viennese washerwoman type: garrulous, uncultured, strong-willed.” Oskar Morgenstern's comments on Adele. Dawson, Logical Dilemmas.

“我很高兴没有天才在车里。”阿黛尔每次开车送客人回家时都喜欢这样说，尤其是数学家。这是维雷娜·胡贝尔-戴森博士在《哥德尔与数学真理的本质 II》（在线发表于www.edge.org）中转述的轶事。

“I’m so happy to drive without a genius in the car.” Adele liked to say this to visitors, especially mathematicians, whenever she drove them home. An anecdote relayed by Dr. Verena Huber-Dyson in Gödel and the Nature of Mathematical Truth II (published online at www.edge.org).

193 “非常迷人”，库尔特·哥德尔在一封家庭信件中这样描述阿黛尔在他们普林斯顿家中花园里放置的粉红色火烈鸟雕像。道森，《逻辑困境》。

193 “awfully charming,” Kurt Gödel's description in a family correspondence of a pink flamingo statue Adele placed in the garden of their Princeton home. Dawson, Logical Dilemmas.

201 “很难描述这样的对话……对我意味着什么：他是我们这个世纪最杰出的人物之一，对我依恋有加……[他]显然精神失常，患有某种偏执症，期待我的帮助……而我却无法帮助他。即使我行动自如，试图帮助他……我也没能做到任何事情……[现在，]他依赖着我——而他没有其他人，这一点很明显——这增加了我的负担。”奥斯卡·摩根斯坦的备忘录，杜克大学珀金斯纪念图书馆。道森，《逻辑困境》。

201 “It is hard to describe what such a conversation … means for me: here is one of the most brilliant men of our century, greatly attached to me, … [who] is clearly mentally disturbed, suffering from some kind of paranoia, expecting help from me,… and I [am] unable to extend it to him. Even while I was mobile and tried to help him … I was unable to accomplish anything… . [Now,] by clinging to me—and he has nobody else, that is quite clear—he adds to the burden I am carrying.” A memorandum by Oskar Morgenstern, Perkins Memorial Library of Duke University. Dawson, Logical Dilemmas.
